They correspond to the three earthly corporeal hudud: in extension of the Speaker (Natiq) and the Foundation (Asas), namely the Imam, the Hujjah, (1) and the Lahiq, who together also form six divisions corresponding to the six pronunciations of the first determination, which we have already mentioned. Together they make twelve letters, like the twelve hujjas already mentioned. Thus the testimony to Allah Almighty is the highest degree — the usul — and the testimony to the Messenger (peace be upon him) is the lowest degree — the furu'.

The upper and lower hudud are contained within the letters of the testimony. So the outward of

---

(1) In the (e) recension: "the Lahiq."

<!-- page 46 -->

testimony is a statement with the tongue; its inner meaning is statement and knowledge; and its substance is action. Its outward form is Islam, and at its core is faith. On this, al-Sadiq (may the blessings of Allah be upon him) said — as we have established in the book "Pillars of Islam," when he was asked whether faith is speech or action — he said:

"Faith is all action, and speech is only a part of it."

So preserve, O believers, the testimony to which you have been called. Be sincere in it. We have shown you the sincerity due to it — that for which Allah Almighty has appointed reward by His saying: "And the witnesses do not refuse when they are called." Whatever you have been called to, be faithful to it in word and deed. Fulfill His promise to you, in the words of the Almighty:

"And fulfill My covenant and I will fulfill your covenant."

Allah has promised you, through the tongue of His Messenger, Paradise if you are sincere in your testimony. Know this, then believe and do not doubt. Act and do not stray. Do not be complacent, do not be discouraged — and you will receive what Allah has promised you of Paradise, outward and inward, as He said, Almighty:

"And for him who fears the standing before his Lord, there are two gardens."

It is wise to know that you will not leave its gardens, and you will receive with it its fruits and its spouses. And you will enter the Garden of Eternity in the abode of permanence in the hereafter, and you will gain therein the reward of Allah, which He promised you. And you will be safe from His punishment, with which He warned you should you disobey what He has commanded and commit what He has forbidden — should you neglect what He has enjoined upon you and to which He has called you to be sincere, by the testimony in which He gathered together all that with which you worship Him.

What we have mentioned in this chapter — the chapter on faith — should suffice as an explanation of the testimony and what it indicates of the hudud. We will mention in the chapters of this book all of them in like manner. When mentioning the obligatory prayers, you will know that this testimony has descended

upon her, and has encompassed the totality of that with which you worship Allah. That is why the call of the Prophet (peace be upon him) was directed to it, and why he took upon you the covenant that you would testify with sincerity after him. You have

borne witness to it with your tongue; you bear witness to it as a testimony of belief in your hearts; and you act upon it as a ruling next to a deed.

<!-- page 47 -->

(1) Take notice that you have been appointed to be encompassed by the hudud that have been set for you, and the proofs that have been shown to you,

upon the right path by which you have been saved — may Allah aid you in that, and guide you to it. May Allah's blessings be upon the Prophet Muhammad and upon the righteous of his descendants

who succeed one another until the Day of Judgment. And praise be to Allah, Lord of the Worlds.

---

(1) In the (e) recension: "and your informants."

<!-- page 48 -->

Chapter One

(In which is the interpretation of the stories of the prophets and the Imams — Adam and Idris, peace be upon them)

In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful.

Praise be to Allah, Lord of the Worlds, and may the blessings of Allah be upon Muhammad, the faithful Prophet, (2) and upon the Imams from his pure descendants.

To proceed:

We have already mentioned the interpretation of faith and Islam, which is the opening of the chapters of "The Pillars of Islam" — the book in which we have undertaken to simplify the interpretation of what it contains. The door of wilayah is recited for the Messengers and for the first of those in authority (3) whose obedience Allah has joined to obedience to Himself. The Almighty said:

"Obey Allah and obey the Messenger and those in authority among you."

So we have gathered the interpretation of what is said about them, for Allah (glory be to Him) has gathered them together in

---

(1) In the (e) recension: "the part," and in the (X) recension: "the chapter," which is the correct reading.
(2) "al-Amin" has been dropped from the (e) recension.
(3) In the (S) recension: "and for the first."

<!-- page 49 -->

the duty of obedience, even if their degrees and ranks differ. The pronouncement is a single matter of knowledge.

They are: Adam, Noah, Abraham, Moses, Jesus, Muhammad, and the seventh of them — the Qa'im of the Age. Then there follow, in their virtue, the Asas-foundations that He established from among them in their lifetime, to carry out the inner meaning. The Asas rises after the Natiq and succeeds him after him, becoming an Imam, and establishing for himself a Hujjah to take his place — likewise to circulate his cycle until that Natiq passes away. Then another Natiq comes after him with another shari'a, and so it occurs first, because the earth is never devoid of a Wali of Allah with His proof, even for the twinkling of an eye. Al-Sadiq (peace be upon him) was asked: when is the second in the last hadith? He said: "In another minute that remains from the same past" — so that full credit may be given to the two of them. And it is only ever one after one, a proof of the unity of the Almighty.

He said:

"If there were gods in them other than Allah, they would both be corrupted."

The companion of the age — whether he is a prophet, a messenger, or an imam — is called the Natiq, because he pronounces what is apparent and carries it out. His Hujjah is called the Samit (the silent one), because he

is silent from the outward. This is the reason for the twelve hujjas that Allah Almighty has mentioned in His Book when He says:

"And We sent forth from among them twelve pure ones."

We have mentioned in the foregoing their testimonies of testimony and other scholars of the greater world. The smaller ones are like them. So we said it; further than that

we come to mention this: the Imam and the Hujjah are successive like day and night, and what

is also like them, so the day is like the Imam and the night is like

the Hujjah and the concealment of the inner and its hiddenness, in which Allah Almighty says:

---

(1) In the (e) recension: "the owner of the age who was."

<!-- page 50 -->

"And We have made the night and the day two signs."

We have mentioned that the verses of Allah, in the inner meaning, are His proofs against His creation. They are the inner ones whom obedience to them is obligatory and bound to obedience.

The name of the Imam falls upon the Natiq, and the name of the Natiq falls upon the Imam. Allah Almighty said:

"And when his Lord tested Abraham with words and he fulfilled them, He said: 'I will make you an Imam for the people.' He said: 'And from my descendants?' He said: 'My covenant does not extend to the wrongdoers.'"

The Imam was called Natiq because he speaks what the prophet used to speak — in his turn — from the apparent shari'a with which he was sent. He was called Imam because the servants follow his example. He is also called the one prayed behind in congregation as their imam, to follow his example. And because he is ahead of them — that is, in front of them in their hands — and they follow him behind him, so he was called the leader (al-ra'is). The imam of misguidance is an imam who is not to be followed. Allah Almighty said:

"And We made them leaders inviting to the Fire."

The name of prophecy was given only to those who were connected to the upper substance without an intermediary — no lower hadd between him and it. So the imamate is one hadd below the hadd of prophecy, even though their obedience is equal in obligation, and it is likewise coupled with obedience to Allah.

We must first mention the origin of the Imamate in the lower hadd, which is Adam (peace be upon him). Then we will coordinate what follows and recite it little by little, as much as one can bear of this limit of speech that we say — and by Allah we seek help:

Allah says:

"And when your Lord said to the angels: 'I am placing upon the earth a successor,' they said: '

<!-- page 51 -->

Will you place therein one who will corrupt it and shed blood, while we glorify You with praise and sanctify You?' He said: 'Indeed, I know what you do not know.'"

And the Almighty said:

"And when your Lord said to the angels: 'I am creating a human being from clay. So when I have proportioned him and breathed into him of My spirit, fall down to him in prostration.'"

The first thing that must be mentioned in this statement is the origin of the knowledge of the saints of Allah. The words and speech attributed to Allah refer to what happens to those who hear,

not as you see and hear from the speech of those who speak — sounds that arise about the bodies and cavities, exiting from their outlets, broken by

the playthings, tongues, and lips, and the like — nor like the voices that come from

the friction between created bodies. Allah is exalted above being likened to anything that He has created, infinitely high. It may be permissible in the language to call something "speech" or "saying"

without it being speech with audible sound or known pronunciation. For the Arabs say: "the money

is gone," (1) "the wall has fallen," "the man has been struck," "the world has preached to its people and addressed them

with her sermons," "time has reproached so-and-so," and other such sayings. So He addressed them —

Allah knows what they know of it. A man may see in his dream what he did not see with his eyes,

and he hears speech without a speaker, and the voice is heard without a voicer. And it is within the power of

Allah Almighty to do what He says without it being done in this way (that is, by ability), as He commands it to the one He commands as He wills.

He has no partner. He has said:

---

(1) In the (M) recension: "said."
(2) In the (5) recension it also comes: "he said."

<!-- page 52 -->

"Indeed, We are mighty; if We wish, We say to it: 'Be,' and it is."

He said: "Be," and it becomes — as the created things say. Speech is performed; one of them is movable, which is the first, and the second is stationary, and so on.

There are many parables of this in the mystery of God's relation with His angelic guardians,

those whom Allah mentioned when He said to them what He said concerning the command of Adam — not

all the angels, but when Allah wanted to create Adam (the second creation, which is

the creation of knowledge), as the Almighty said: "Then We brought him forth as another creation,"

and: "And He will form you in the wombs of your mothers, creation after creation,"

and to appoint him as an Imam, He delegated from among the angels twelve kings to establish him for them as

leader. They take from him and report him to the people of the earth. When He knew that He

would create him from clay — and clay in the inner is the outward, the dense bodily knowledge —

He created the angels in the creation of the gentle and subtle spiritual knowledge.

They had already been taught that gentle knowledge is not connected to matter, and dense

knowledge comes only by teaching. And that gentle spiritual knowledge is not connected to works;

rather, it is a science without work or assignment, just as the apparent knowledge is — as the saying of the Commander of the Believers,

when he mentioned the Qur'an, attests:

"The outward is a knowledge that is apparent, and the inward is a knowledge that is hidden."

Therefore, (2) the angels were not tested by deeds. They already had

the knowledge that the one who is charged must be humbled and held short. They said:

"Will You place therein one who will corrupt it and shed blood, while we

---

(2) "Then" has been dropped from the (e) recension.
(1) In the (5) recension: "I have received them."


"I will be with you and will sanctify You. He said: I know what you do not know."

What the Almighty meant is that Adam was permitted whatever the angels had been permitted, and was warned against the same things — lest he fall short, err, or be ruined. Iblis was among them, and he saw himself as better than Adam. He claimed for himself Adam's rank, refused to be his follower, and grew arrogant before the command of his Lord. He wanted God to see the angels in their incapacity, so He created Adam, as He said, from clay. That is, He began with apparent knowledge (al-zahir), as is the established custom which He set down for His servants. Adam remained in that state for a long time, knowing nothing other than what he had learned.

This is what is mentioned in the hadith: that when God formed his image from clay, it remained a lifeless body for a long stretch before the spirit was breathed into it — meaning the inner, spiritual knowledge (al-batin). Iblis, in that interval, would come to him and speak to him of knowledge that Adam did not possess. He found in him only the apparent knowledge, in which Adam took delight, and Iblis reported back that Adam was hollow — that is, empty of any inner or esoteric content. This was before the angels, and Iblis among them, were commanded to obey him. The Almighty had said to them:

"When I have proportioned him and breathed into him of My spirit, then fall down to him in prostration."

That is, submit to him in obedience once I have endowed him with spiritual knowledge. At that, the devil among them turned against him — out of the enmity he harbored, the envy that had taken hold of him, and the arrogance he felt toward him. He saw himself as better than Adam and had taken pleasure in what he had observed of Adam's lagging behind in inner knowledge — until now he was filled with regret and pride.

When God willed to bring Iblis low, He extended Adam's reach and taught him with that inner knowledge, as the Almighty said: "And He taught Adam the names — all of them." That is, the names of every thing that human beings need to know, since each thing has a name. He taught him this and then summoned the angels, whom He had permitted to call upon him, and began questioning them about what He had taught Adam. They had nothing to answer, and said exactly what God reported of them:

"Glory be to You! We have no knowledge except what You have taught us. Indeed, it is You who is the All-Knowing, the All-Wise."

He said: "O Adam, inform them of their names." And when he had informed them of their names, He said: "Did I not tell you that I know the unseen of the heavens and the earth, and I know what you reveal and what you have been concealing?"

Al-Sadiq (peace be upon him) said: "One day I argued with my father, and he set out to walk around the House. I walked with him one night, and then he leaned toward the stone and prayed there until I had finished and sat down — while he was still standing in prayer. A man came and sat beside him, and he too was praying. I looked at him: a man of perfect build, large-boned, dark in color and hair, with two thick white garments on him. When my father saw him sitting beside him, he cut his prayer short, then greeted him and said, 'Do you have any need?' He said: 'I have come to ask you about the beginning of the creation of this House.' My father said to him: 'Yes. When God created Adam' — and he recounted his story, and the command given to the angels, and what they said to him, and what He said to them:

"I know what you reveal and what you have been concealing."

"He said: But what did they reveal? It was what they said:

'Will You place upon it one who will spread corruption in it and shed blood, while we declare Your praise and sanctify You?'

As for what they concealed, they said within themselves: We did not think that God would create any creation more honorable in His sight than we are."

He commanded us to prostrate to him, and when He said that to them, they recognized that they had fallen into disobedience. They took refuge at the Throne and circled it for a week to seek their Lord's pleasure. He said to them: "Descend to the earth and build a house at which to seek refuge — to which the sinner from the children of Adam may come, and they will circumambulate it as you have circled the Throne, and I will be pleased with them as I was pleased with you." So they built this House. Then God raised it up at the time of the flood, so that even now, from the fourth heaven, the angels make pilgrimage to it until the Day of Resurrection. Ibrahim al-Khalil rebuilt this house upon its foundations — and he related the rest of the hadith, which is a long one, from which we have taken only what is needed.

Then God Almighty commanded the angels to prostrate to Adam — that is, He commanded them to obey him, to call upon him, and to accept him — as the Almighty said:

"Do you not see that to God prostrates whoever is in the heavens and whoever is on the earth, and the sun, the moon, the stars, the mountains, the trees, the animals, and many of mankind — and many are deserving of punishment?"

And they prostrated, as the Almighty said: "Except Iblis: he was arrogant and became one of the disbelievers."

He was called Satan only after this — that is, once Iblis had said what he said. The people of the language hold that *shaytan* follows the pattern of words meaning ruined or perished: it is said *shata fulanun* when a man perishes, and likewise Iblis was called Satan once he was destroyed by the limit at which he had become Satan. It is also said that the *shaytan* is the man who is cut off and has no proof, and it is said *ibn abi sad* and *iblis* when one is dejected and brought low. All these conditions were gathered in Iblis. God spoke, and He is the most truthful of those who speak:

"And the Hour is their appointed time, and the Hour shall be more calamitous and more bitter."

The Almighty said: "What prevented you from prostrating when I commanded you?" He said: "I am better than him. You created me from fire, and You created him from clay."

That is: You raised me up in knowledge through spiritual cultivation, and granted me brilliant supportive knowledge (al-ta'yid) that carries no dense physical body with it, and You created Adam with a thick, heavy, corporeal knowledge fitted to a physical body — so how should I prostrate to one whom I am better than? In this way he exposed what he had been concealing and openly declared his disobedience. God was angered with him and cursed him — that is, expelled him — saying:

"Get out of it: you are accursed, and indeed upon you is My curse until the Day of Recompense."

So He brought him out of the bounds of supportive knowledge (al-ta'yid), cut him off from it, expelled him from it, and cursed him — and curse, in the language, is expulsion.

God created Eve (Hawwa) from Adam, because He said: "And from it He created its mate." The creation here is the creation of support (al-ta'yid), not a physical creation. That is, God Almighty took her up and supported her, taught her, illuminated her, and joined her to Adam in marriage, made her his wife, and made her his proof. God Almighty compensated Adam with her in place of Iblis. It is not — as the common folk claim — that God Almighty cast Adam into sleep, and that while he slept God took one of his ribs and created Eve from it. They heard a fragment of the interpretation which they did not grasp and did not truly know: they heard that God exchanged for Adam one of his ribs and made that rib Eve.

This is not so. Rather, God compensated Adam with Eve in place of Iblis — who had been qualified to be a proof for Adam, as we have said — and made her one of the twelve chiefs (al-nuqaba'). For their likeness, in the apparent creation of the human being, is the ribs of the body: a human being has twelve ribs on each side, and just as the right side resembles the inner knowledge, and the left side the apparent knowledge, so the chiefs (al-nuqaba') of inner subtle knowledge are twelve, and likewise their counterparts for the knowledge of the apparent.

Then God Almighty settled Adam and his wife in the Garden — which inwardly is the ranks of the messengers of support (al-ta'yid) and, beneath them, the chiefs. Our saying this, and the like of it concerning what is subordinate, is not a denial of the outer reality — namely that the Garden is itself a created entity — because the Almighty has said:

"And of every thing We created pairs, that perhaps you may remember."

Paradise is among the greatest of the things God Almighty has created, and He has prepared it, and the Almighty has said:

"On the Day God will not disgrace the Prophet and those who believed with him: their light will proceed before them and on their right hands…"

"…and give them glad tidings of gardens beneath which rivers flow, abiding therein forever. That is the great triumph."

The Almighty said: "And for him who fears the standing before his Lord are two gardens."

Then He said: "And give glad tidings to those who believe and do righteous deeds that for them are gardens beneath which rivers flow. Whenever they are provided with fruit from them, they will say: 'This is what we were provided with before,' and they will be given things in likeness."

So He made Paradise a glad tiding for the believers, and He said in another place: "Their reward is with their Lord — gardens of eternity beneath which rivers flow." He told them that for them is Paradise in this world and in the Hereafter, and He said: "Whenever they are provided with fruit from them, they will say: 'This is what we were provided with before.'" That is what He supports.

So let the listener not be misled into thinking that when we mention the inner meaning of Paradise we deny that there is an eternal Paradise and an abode of bliss, or that when we mention the inner meaning of the Fire we deny that there is a fire and a torment that has come to pass, or that when we mention a subtle inner interpretation of something we annul its outer reality — we seek refuge in God from that. For He does nothing except that it has an inner aspect, and we do not see in this world a soul rising in a human being except within a body, nor an inner reality except within an outer one — and if it were not for the outer, the name "inner" would not even apply to it. So understand this, O company of believers, with full understanding, and let your hearts feel that many among the people of this knowledge have perished by this very point. It was for this same reason that Adam fell into sin, as we shall mention at the proper place. So believe in what God has revealed outwardly and inwardly, believe in it, and act upon it. God Almighty said:

"And forsake the outwardness of sin and its inwardness."

He said: "And He has lavished upon you His bounties, outward and inward." The outward lawful is lawful, and the inward is lawful; the outward forbidden is forbidden, and the inward is forbidden. Everything, as we have said, has an outer and an inner.

As for the parables that God Almighty has struck for His servants — when He says: "And these parables We strike for the people, but none understand them except those who know" — and when He says: "Indeed, God is not ashamed to strike a parable, even of a mosquito or what is above it. As for those who believe, they know it is the truth from their Lord; and as for those who disbelieve, they say: What did God intend by this parable? He misleads many by it and guides many by it — and He misleads not by it except the corrupters who break the covenant of God after its ratification."

And the Almighty said: "And We have struck for the people in this Qur'an from every parable."

The way of these parables is not that of the outer-and-inner symbolism in which what is symbolized and what symbolizes are both real, established things. Rather, the established and obligatory thing represented by the parable is like the parable of His saying:

"Guide us to the straight path — the path of those upon whom You have bestowed favor, not of those who incurred wrath, nor of those who are astray."

The path, in the language, is the road. The Imam here stands in the place of the road, for whoever is bound to follow the Imam will not go astray, and whoever needs guidance will not be misled. What is meant by "road" here is the Imam, not a road taken on the ground.

Let us return to the mention of Adam (peace be upon him) and to the inner meaning of the Garden, which is supportive knowledge (al-ta'yid) with its true, pure, spiritual content — for the bliss in it surpasses every other bliss, and the pleasure in it exceeds every other pleasure. For this reason whoever attains it renounces all worldly attachments; they shrivel in his eye, every thing in this world is diminished in his sight, and he comes to make light of his attachment to anything but that knowledge. His union with it he finds to be the perfect bliss and the glory that knows no humiliation thereafter — as in the hadith of the Commander of the Believers (peace be upon him) to Kumayl ibn Ziyad, in which he said: "Knowledge is the ruler, and wealth is the ruled. Wealth runs out as it is spent, while knowledge purifies as it is spent. Wealth's storage decays, but the scholars endure as long as time itself endures. Their persons are absent, yet their traces remain in the world." It is a long hadith, of which we have mentioned only what is needed.

The Almighty said: "O Adam, dwell — you and your wife — in the Garden, and eat freely from it wherever you wish, but do not approach this tree, or you will be among the wrongdoers."

He warned him against Iblis by saying: "Indeed, this is an enemy to you and to your wife, so let him not drive you both out of the Garden so that you become miserable."

And He entrusted this to him by saying: "And We had already taken a covenant with Adam before, but he forgot, and We found no firm resolve in him."

So He permitted to them the ranks of the messengers in accordance with their conditions and the duties He had laid upon them — which include declaring lawful what is lawful, declaring forbidden what is forbidden, warding against what is forbidden, and warning of it. He made the tree which He forbade Adam to approach, prevented him from, and made unlawful for him, a likeness for the Master of the Time — the Possessor of the Resurrection (Sahib al-Qiyama) — within whose limits the obligations of charge lie, and before whose appearance they do not yet apply, as the Almighty said:

"No soul will be benefited by its faith if it had not believed before, or earned good through its faith. Say: Wait — indeed we too are waiting." From such a soul no recompense will be accepted, no punishment exacted, and no intercession received.

Then the inner (al-batin) will be stripped away, the outer (al-zahir) will fall, and the inner will become apparent. The Master of the Resurrection stands beyond the bounds of the messengers who preceded him, because the inner knowledge entrusted within their ranks is paid out to their proofs (hujjas), concealed from them, carried from one to the next — a deposit and a knowledge by which he is illuminated until it reaches its rightful holder, namely the Master of the Day of Resurrection, who will then make it openly manifest and strip away its outer covering. That manifest disclosure was forbidden and unlawful before him. So God forbade Adam at the outset of the matter — so that the unalterable custom of God might be carried out upon him — and Iblis asked for respite until the appointed Day, meaning the Day of Resurrection, and he said:

"Grant me respite until the Day they are resurrected" — so that I may have a little reach into his offspring.

He said: "Go, and whomever of them you can rouse with your voice — meaning by stirring them to remember you — and assault them with your cavalry and your foot — meaning whoever of them follows you in your falsehood, so press them into your command — and become a partner with them in wealth and offspring."

That is: a partner with them in the knowledge of wealth, if your doubt and falsehood enter them.


<!-- page 62 -->

He means the children born through faith, because they are like the people of the call in the inner sense. Concerning His children, Allah Almighty said: "It is the religion of your father Ibrahim. It is He who named you Muslims" (Quran 22:78). The one who calls the believers is like a father, and the proof (hujja) is like a mother, because she carries them, nurses them, and raises them with knowledge.

Therefore the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) said: "I and you, O Ali, are the two fathers of this nation."

So Iblis wished to say: share with them in their sons who believe in your falsehood — those who became, by right, their sons — and whoever among them you have overcome with your falsehood, you have transferred from their birth (which is the birth of faith) into your birth (which is the birth of disbelief); share with them in this, having promised them your arrogance and your falsehood. And Allah made it a trial for them. Then He told them about His servants who are loyal to Him — that Iblis does not prevail over them, that He returns them to Himself in full, and that they are of His party and His sons. The Almighty said: "Indeed, over My servants you will have no authority."

He made for Himself a party from among them, and said, describing the party of Satan: "Have you not considered those who make allies of a people upon whom Allah has placed His wrath" — meaning the nation of misguidance — "they are neither of you nor of them, and they swear to falsehood while they know. Allah has prepared for them a severe punishment; evil indeed is what they used to do. They took their oaths as a cover and averted people from the way of Allah, so for them is a humiliating punishment. Never will their wealth or their children avail them against Allah at all. Those are the companions of the Fire; they will abide therein eternally — on the Day when Allah will resurrect them all, and they will swear to Him as they swear to you, thinking that they are upon something. Unquestionably, it is they who are the liars. Satan has overcome them and made them forget the remembrance of Allah. Those are the party of Satan. Unquestionably, the party of Satan — they will be the losers" (Quran 58:14–19).

<!-- page 63 -->

Then He described His own party, the Almighty saying: "You will not find a people who believe in Allah and the Last Day having affection for those who oppose Allah and His Messenger" — meaning the imams of injustice and their followers — "even if they were their fathers or their sons or their brothers or their kindred. Those — He has decreed faith within their hearts and supported them with a spirit from Himself. And He will admit them to gardens beneath which rivers flow, wherein they will abide eternally. Allah is pleased with them, and they are pleased with Him. Those are the party of Allah. Unquestionably, the party of Allah — they are the successful" (Quran 58:22).

Allah Almighty made clear that His party are those who cling to Him and who have taken His guardians (awliya') as their own. And the party of Satan are those whom Iblis has acquired and cut off for himself: he shared with them in their guardians among them, so they took as their guardians his enemies — who are also their enemies — and disowned His guardianship and theirs, and took as their guardians Satan and his guardians. But whoever was abased by Satan and regretted his abasement, who resigned from his stumbling and turned back to his Lord — that one is not of Satan, nor of his party. Allah Almighty says: "And whoever does evil or wrongs himself but then seeks forgiveness of Allah will find Allah Forgiving and Merciful" (Quran 4:110).

Al-Sadiq (peace be upon him) said: "Do not consider as a guardian one whom Satan has abased entirely; rather, consider as a guardian a man who turns back, relying on his Lord." The cursed Satan abased Adam and Hawwa (peace be upon them) when he said to them — as Allah Almighty has reported concerning him in His Book: "Your Lord did not forbid you this tree except that you might become kings,

<!-- page 64 -->

or that you might become among the immortals," and he swore to them: "Indeed I am to you among the sincere advisors" (Quran 7:20–21).

He made it clear to them that the limit of the permissible was what Allah Almighty had warned them about, and said to them that the limit of obligatory action is the limit of effort and exertion, and that if they were to leave it they would end up among the gentle spiritual angels and be stripped of the dense material world — that they would be two kings eternal in what they desired. As the Almighty said: "But if they had not been beguiled, they would not have tasted of the tree, and it appeared evil to them." That is, they transgressed¹ the limits of speech that had been permitted to them, into the limit belonging to the Lord of the Resurrection — that of which Allah Almighty had warned them — and they extended their hands to what was not theirs. So they ate from it; they ate from the tree, and they fell into sin and disobedience, and that which supported them was cut off. That support is the garment of piety which Allah mentioned in His Book, saying: "And that is from the signs of Allah" (Quran 7:26).

He was stripped bare of it, and there appeared to them what was reprehensible — the intensity of the natural image — because of the nakedness of the garment of piety, which is the word, by which she saw, by its light, all the darkness in which she was compounded. For support does not accompany sins, and extending one's hand to what does not belong to one is, by ruling, obligatory to cut off. When the support for it ceased, as Allah Almighty said: "They began to stitch upon themselves leaves from Paradise" (Quran 7:22) — meaning that they joined together what remained to them of the light of wisdom in order to cover some of the shame

¹ In one copy: "and they overstepped."
² In one version: "Mustajana."

<!-- page 65 -->

that had appeared in them. What was revealed about their condition was the disappearance of support, and through ignorance many of those attached to this matter perished, and it became permitted.

"And they cried out to their Lord" — as the Almighty said: "Did I not forbid you that tree and tell you that Satan is to you a clear enemy? They said: 'Our Lord, we have wronged ourselves; if You do not forgive us and have mercy on us, we will surely be among the losers'" (Quran 7:22–23).

Adam did not turn aside as Iblis turned aside; rather he repented to Allah the Almighty and prayed to Him, asking for His mercy and forgiveness. "Then Adam received from his Lord words, so He turned to him in forgiveness; indeed He is the Accepter of Repentance, the Merciful" (Quran 2:37).

This means that he drew close to Him and found Him repenting from the side of the higher limits, so He turned to him in mercy, as the Almighty said. And Satan had no authority over him to drag him to himself and take possession of him, so that he might become of his party — rather, he was of the Party of Allah. The Almighty turned to him in mercy, forgave him, and received his words. Likewise those of his descendants who did evil and then repented from it — He turned to them in forgiveness, and they were of His party. But whoever persisted in his sin and did not repent of it, and to whom no words came from his Lord, was of the party of Iblis and his soldiers. The Almighty said: "If, when they wronged themselves, they had come to you and asked forgiveness of Allah, and the Messenger had asked forgiveness for them, they would have found Allah Accepting of Repentance and Merciful" (Quran 4:64). The repentance of the repentant is not accepted except by His receiving His words for them, and they are not forgiven until after

<!-- page 66 -->

the seeking of forgiveness for them and the seeking by the words on their behalf. This is a statement parallel to the tree which Allah Almighty forbade to Adam (peace be upon him), of which he ate nothing, but was exposed; and the beginning of his evil — which is an esoteric interpretation (ta'wil al-batin), and that is in the elaborate punishment treated in this book — and not as the general interpretation took it on its face: that that tree was a wheat tree, while others said a fig tree, and others said a grape tree; and that its clothing was made of a nail-like material, so it was forbidden to them, and they repented, and what remained of it remained in their fingertips, and that remained in their children; and that this is why most animals have nails and the like — like the hooves of beasts, of cows and sheep, and the claws of predators and birds — and that those born to Adam are not inspired with what he received, so it remains in their limbs, but as a wisdom in their composition with which al-Bari (the Maker) was familiar, such that He was able to recall it, even though if the garment had been of nail it would have been the same in interpretation — a claim which the minds do not accept and which is not correct on examination.

The same applies to what they claimed: that Adam and Eve had their sins exposed, so they sewed for themselves a covering of fig leaves. This too is something that is not proven, because it did not happen; and Allah has remembered him, and he is too noble for that, being a prophet whom He has chosen and honored — even granting that he is one of the followers — that He would look at him as a man would look at a slave who had angered him, then strip him of his clothes and leave him naked, beginning with the figure of his disgrace by that act. They attribute this to their idol, but Allah is exalted above that.

Most of those who took up this interpretation took it from those who became Muslim from among their Jewish ancestors, such as Ka'b al-Ahbar, Abdullah ibn Salam, and others, because they claim it was thus in their tradition: that Adam and Eve remained naked in Paradise, and they sensed that God was walking among its trees, so they hid from Him among its trees, and He called to them, "Where are you?" They said: "We sensed You among the trees of Paradise while we were naked,

<!-- page 67 -->

so we were ashamed before You, and we hid." And He said to them: "Did you eat from the tree?" Adam said: "The woman fed me." The woman said: "The serpent commanded me." And the serpent said: "Iblis. He entered me through the underground."¹

May Allah Almighty interpret this interpretation — that the lands contain it, or that it is seen with the eyes — for in the Torah and the Gospel,² as in the Qur'an, there are proverbs, signs, and symbols, and an outward that needs interpretation, which is the stored knowledge. Allah Almighty says: "Say: O People of the Book, you stand upon nothing until you uphold the Torah and the Gospel and what has been revealed to you from your Lord" (Quran 5:68).

From this it is known that they do not establish this except by interpretation. And therefore it has been said in interpretation that the Torah is like the outward and the Gospel is like the inward; so Allah Almighty has commanded — and the Almighty will establish them all, as we have mentioned, with what Allah Almighty has sent down of the knowledge that Adam deposited and transmitted in the word — the foundations, the imams, and their successors among their descendants, upon them all be the prayers and peace of Allah.

As for the saying mentioned above, "And their Lord called them": His call, the Almighty, to them is a call from Him to them — not that it was a call like the call that is heard from those who call out. The same applies to what we mention concerning His sayings, blessed be His name — we have explained this at length before. But the servants engage with that the same way, attributing to Allah Almighty what is contrary to Him and not appropriate for Him; what is customary among worshippers is that a voice comes only from a voice, from a hollow and a passageway, and that speech is the same only with lips and tongue. The same applies to what is

¹ In one version: "in [a] hollow."
² In one version this passage reads: "the Torah."

<!-- page 68 -->

in conflict with crimes — and Allah is exalted above that.

When Allah Almighty turned in repentance to Adam, He did not remove him from the rank of the caliphate and the imamate which He had set up for him, nor did He deprive him of his substance, his word, and his wisdom in general; rather, He brought him down — and Hawwa with him — from the limits of interpretation without a veil. He said: "Go down from it together (from the light which was good for you on earth), and you will have therein dwelling and enjoyment for a time" (Quran 7:24). He said: "Therein you will live, and therein you will die, and from it you will be brought forth" (Quran 7:25). He said: "O children of Adam, We have bestowed upon you clothing to conceal your private parts, and as adornment. But the clothing of righteousness — that is best. That is from the signs of Allah, that perhaps they will remember" (Quran 7:26).

So Allah brought Adam down from the limit of interpretation without a veil; yet He did not deprive him of substance. What was connected to him of material descended with him from the upper celestial limits, and this was connected to the signs of Allah, as He mentioned. And likewise has it been done in the word of his son.

The Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) said: "I take the revelation from Jibril, and Jibril takes it from Mikael, and Mikael takes it from Israfil, and Israfil takes it from the Tablet (al-Lawh), and the Tablet takes it from the Pen (al-Qalam)." So the support is connected to the word of the Five Upper Limits, and they are connected to those who respond by the Five Lower Limits. The Upper Limits are those we have mentioned, and the Lower Limits are the Foundations (al-asas), the Imams, the Pilgrims (al-hujaj), the Captains (al-nuqaba), the Lords of the Islands (ashab al-jaza'ir), and the Wings (al-ajniha) — and they are the preachers (al-du'at).

<!-- page 69 -->

The sixth of the two ranks of limits is the rebel — and Satan became an enemy to Adam and against him, from Allah Almighty and against Allah Almighty — whether he is a Speaker (natiq), a Silent One (samit), an imam, or a Proof (hujja). And whoever takes them as guardians and is loyal to them is from the party of Adam, which is the party of Allah Almighty; and that includes all those who are obedient to the guardianship of Allah and the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him). And whoever¹ has dismissed their command or claimed their place is from the party of Iblis — who was possessed by Satan and forgot the remembrance of Allah, and forgot here that the matter is delayed by His saying that the last of them is the remembrance of Allah, and the remembrance of Allah here is, in the inner sense, His guardians who are remembered, and they are those who have remembered Him.

The same thing that happened to Adam and Eve happened in their descendants — and their descendants, even if they were numerous, did not differ in their kinds, I mean from male and female, as it was with Adam and Eve. And so it happened in all of obedience and disobedience, as happened in Adam and Eve. The beginning of Adam's creation and what happened to him is parallel to what happened to the creation of his son in the beginning of his command and his dwelling in this house. And the dwelling of Allah Almighty Adam and Eve in Paradise — after what happened to them — is parallel to the dwelling of Allah Almighty those of their descendants who have believed and reconciled, who are of their party; and the repentance of those who repent is like their writing, and the destruction of those of them who perished in disobedience and came to the punishment of Allah by disbelief and by committing what He forbade — this is because of Iblis's possession of them and the fact that they were of his party, and their cessation from Adam, and their departure from his lineage. So they entered the entrance of those who became from him, and they became other than him — that is, from Adam, because they were cut off from him. Allah Almighty said: "And whoever takes them as allies among you, then indeed he is of them" (Quran 5:51).

Whoever takes Iblis as ally is from him, and they are his sons by calling, and his family by calling, and they became other than Adam. For Allah Almighty said concerning the son of Nuh when he disobeyed him:

¹ In one version: "and if."


<!-- page 70 -->

"He is not one of your family."

He named them the party of Satan (Shaytan) and called them by his name. He said:

"Indeed, Satan is a clear enemy."

And He said:

"Over My servants you shall have no authority."

This refers to those who follow Adam through his son.

"Except for those of the deviators who follow you, even if they know not their promised time. It has a number of gates; to each gate is an allotted portion."

By "the gates" I mean the messengers, who are the gates of the pure outward truth — for each of them there is a known sacred law (sharia). Some of those who repaid that law gave themselves over to the Fire. Of this the Prophet (Allah's blessings upon him) said to Ali: "You are the Guardian of the Fire," for he will say to it on the Day of Resurrection:

"This one is yours, take him; and this one is mine, leave him."

This means that Iblis's opposition to Adam and his enmity toward him are like the opposition of the enemies of the messengers, and like their hostility toward them. Allah Almighty says:

"And thus We have made for every enemy of the prophets a host — devils from among humankind and the jinn."

The sinner is the son of Adam who persists in his sin — neither repenting of it nor casting it off. He is like Satan in his persistence: he has departed Adam's party and entered Satan's, taken his entrance, and arrived at the punishment of Allah alongside Iblis. The repentant who turns back from what he has committed, and the obedient born of Adam, are Adam's party,

(1) In copy (M): "You are the Guardian of the Fire."

<!-- page 71 -->

which is the party of Allah (Hizb Allah).

Allah Almighty says:

"And those who, when they commit an immorality or wrong themselves, remember Allah and seek forgiveness for their sins — and who can forgive sins except Allah? — and they do not persist in what they have done while they know. Their reward is forgiveness from their Lord, and gardens beneath which rivers flow, wherein they shall abide forever. How excellent is the reward of those who labor."

Allah Almighty benefited Adam through His will: He settled him on the earth and made him a successor over those whom He placed there. Adam's descendants multiplied with him, Allah's argument was established against them, and Adam was the bearer of the message to them. He entrusted (awsa) his son Abel; his brother Cain envied him and killed him, as Allah Almighty has described. That occurred during Adam's lifetime, so that the lesson of the will (wasiyya) would be made plain to him. Whoever entertained evil thoughts, persisted in disobedience, and did not repent of his sin was of Satan's party.

Allah then granted Adam, from among his descendants, [a son] whom he named Hibat Allah ("the Gift of God"). To him Adam entrusted the inner knowledge; he took him into his confidence and commanded him to keep the secret, fearing that Cain would kill him as he had killed Abel. The custom (sunna) was thus established of guarding the secrets of the covenant and preserving them.

Allah prepared Adam for the reward He had set aside for him in the Abode of Decision, and after him the matter of the Imamate passed to the will of Seth. Things came to pass with his son in the manner we have described: remembrance after remembrance, station after station, Imam after Imam — until the matter reached the one whom Allah Almighty mentioned in His Book concerning Idris (peace be upon him). This was within the Cycle of Adam, may Allah's blessings be upon him; then it concluded with the era of Noah.

Allah sent Noah as a messenger speaking a sacred law (sharia) different from the law of Adam. Allah Almighty says:

<!-- page 72 -->

"For each of you We have appointed a law and a way."

Adam's cycle ended when Noah's era came upon them. None of them rose to messengership until he had first held fast to the law of those who came before him; the predecessor's covenant was taken up, and he bound himself to it. Allah Almighty says:

"And when We took from the prophets their covenant — and from you, and from Noah, Abraham, Moses, and Jesus, son of Mary — We took from them a solemn covenant."

We have mentioned this above; so understand what we have recited to you of the interpretation of what Allah has revealed to you. Know the truth of what it contains, so that you may worship Him by it, and grasp the inner revelation (al-tanzil al-batin) of which the Almighty informed you in His Book — that none knows it but He and those firmly rooted in knowledge: His friends (awliya'), whose authority Allah has favored you with, and whose following has placed you in His party. He has promised you His reward, and through it has removed you from the party of Satan — whose punishment you dread. Carry out what Allah Almighty has prescribed; be sincere before His face. Perform what Allah has obligated upon you, outwardly and inwardly. Whoever of you has committed a sin: let him repent to Allah from it, and let him take refuge in the guardian (wali) of his own time, so that Allah may forgive him and absolve him of his sin. He will thereby become one of those whom Allah has promised — the repentant, who seek forgiveness for their sins and for their guardians — that he may belong to the party of your father Adam and to the party of the friends of Allah from his progeny, which is Hizb Allah. Leave the party of Satan, who persisted in their sins as Satan persisted in his — they became satanic like him. Just as Satan despaired of his Lord, do not despair of your Lord or of His mercy upon you. The Almighty said:

"Do not despair of the mercy of Allah; surely none despair of Allah's mercy except the disbelieving people."

<!-- page 73 -->

And as I have cited from the words of the Almighty to His friend Abraham (al-Khalil Ibrahim):

"And who despairs of the mercy of his Lord but those who go astray?"

May Allah guide you to what He loves and is pleased with, protect you from violating His prohibitions and disobeying Him, and open for you the gates of obedience to His friends. May Allah bless His servant Muhammad and the pure Imams from his progeny ('itra), and peace be upon him.(1)

(1) In Ismaili belief, cycles are divided into two kinds: major cycles and minor cycles. The major cycles begin with Adam and end at the Resurrection; the minor cycles begin with each speaker-prophet (natiq) — the one sent with a sacred law — and end with the next speaker. The major cycle we are now in is divided into seven minor cycles: the cycles of Adam, Noah, Abraham, Moses, Jesus, Muhammad, and the awaited Qa'im (the Standing One). Each minor cycle contains a Resident Imam (al-imam al-muqim), a permanent Imam, a Foundation (asas), a speaker (natiq), and seven Imams. The Resident Imam is the one who instructs the speaker in his mission. The Concluder is the one who closes the cycle. The Foundation is the speaker's proof during his lifetime, and inherits the will after him; he is the master of esoteric interpretation (ta'wil al-batin), corresponding to the speaker, who holds the knowledge of the outward sharia.

The Resident Imam in Adam's era was "Hunaid," and his proofs (hujaj) were twelve, among them Iblis, who refused submission to Adam. Adam descended at Aden — perhaps Aden in Yemen — then migrated to Mecca al-Mukarrama (whose name was then "Faran"), where he died at 930 years of age and was buried at the foot of Mount Abu Qubais. Before that he had bequeathed to his son Seth, who was called Hibat Allah. Seth was born in the year 230 from Adam's descent, died in 1142, lived 912 years, and bequeathed to his son Enosh, born in 435 from Adam's descent. Enosh died in 1385, lived 950 years, and bequeathed to his son Qinan. Qinan, born in 625, died in 1535, lived 910 years, and bequeathed to his son Mahalel. Mahalel, born in 795, died in 1690 from Adam's descent, lived 895 years, and bequeathed to his son Yard. Yard was born in 960, died in 1922 from Adam's descent, lived 962 years, and bequeathed to his son Akhnukh. Akhnukh (Enoch) was born in 1122, was raised up in 1487, lived 365 years, and bequeathed to his son Mattu Shalih — whose name was also Idris, also called Hermes the Thrice-Blessed, the first to write with the pen. Methuselah was born in 1287 and died in 2242, the year of the flood; his death came just before the flood. He lived 955 years and bequeathed to his son Lamek (Lamech). Lamek, born in 1454 from Adam's descent, died in 2346 — 104 years after the flood — and lived 891 years; he completed the cycle of Adam and was the seventh of its Imams. He handed the matter to his son Noah, after the divine will decreed the change of the old law and its replacement by a new one: the Law of Noah, the Second Speaker.

<!-- page 74 -->

Chapter Two
(In which is the interpretation of the stories of Noah, Hud, and Salih)

In the name of God, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful.

Praise be to Allah, Lord of the Worlds. May Allah bless Muhammad, the Seal of the Prophets, and his guardian (wasi) Ali ibn Abi Talib, the best of the guardians; and the pure Imams from his successive progeny, from his loins until the Day of Judgment, and beyond.

Allah Almighty sent Noah, may Allah's blessings be upon him, as a prophet bearing a new sacred law, after the law of Adam (Allah's blessings upon him) had altered and corruption had increased among his descendants. So Noah called the people to his law, to worship Allah Almighty and affirm His oneness outwardly, as Allah informed him in His Book, saying:

"We sent Noah to his people, saying: 'O my people, worship Allah; you have no god other than Him. Will you not be conscious of Him?'"

Those who responded from among the weak responded; the arrogant rejected him; and those who were content with the law of Adam answered him by saying:

<!-- page 75 -->

"You are nothing but a human being like us."

— that is, you have come to us in the same outward form known to us; we hold in our hands what we inherited from those who came before you, and you began with us with the very things they began with us. You are human beings (bashar) just as we are. In the language, *bashar* refers to the appearance of the skin, and to direct skin-to-skin contact. The point is that they were saying: what he has brought us is already with us, so he is like us and has no merit over us. They said:

"None follows you but the lowliest of us, without consideration."

— they mean in knowledge.

We have mentioned above that the speaker (natiq) is a caller to the outward.

"Noah said: 'My Lord, they have disobeyed me and followed one whose wealth and child have only increased him in loss.'"

— that is, their scholars of the outward, whose knowledge increased nothing and who called him to nothing but loss. Wealth (mal), in the inner sense, is like knowledge; the child (walad) is like the responder, the one who answers his call and accepts what is preached to him, whether rightly or wrongly.

"And they devised a great plot, and they said: 'Do not forsake your gods, and do not forsake Wadd, Suwa', Yaghuth, Ya'uq, or Nasr.'"

— meaning their scholars from whom they took, and the elders among their scholars whom they revered, who misled many of the creation. So Noah (peace be upon him) called them outwardly for a long time. Then Allah Almighty entrusted him, saying:

"None of your people will believe except those who have already believed."

<!-- page 76 -->

— that is, except those who had believed in him and given him credence beforehand. "So do not grieve over what they were doing" — meaning, over those who had disbelieved. "And build the Ark under Our eyes and Our revelation." The Almighty then commanded him to build the Ark outwardly, and likewise commanded him to establish the corresponding inner reality — so that the outer would stand as an example and proof of the inner, testifying to it through its limits and signs.

He built the ship outwardly as an example of his call, set it up, and established its boundaries — to establish, by Allah's command, the inner counterpart: that it might be the means of salvation for the believers, in the life of spiritual knowledge and light, from sinking into disbelief and misguidance, just as the ship outwardly is a vessel of salvation from drowning. He laid the foundation of his call, set its boundaries, and built up the call for the believers through the hidden knowledge of the source. He made that knowledge manifest to them and informed them of what would come to pass. He gave the liars their warning, set the ship in place, and began to work on it. The Almighty says:

"And whenever the chiefs of his people passed by him, they ridiculed him. He said: 'If you ridicule us, we shall ridicule you in the same way you ridicule us. Soon you will know upon whom shall come a punishment that disgraces him, and upon whom shall descend an everlasting punishment.'"

He made the outward ship a guide for the believers — something from which to draw inference and to see the example of its inner meaning. For this reason, the ship outwardly runs upon the water and carries those who ride in it; in just the same way, the call of truth runs upon knowledge and bears those who enter it. Just as those aboard a ship take from the water only what they need for their journey and their sustenance — never to excess, lest they perish — so too are the people of the call of truth in what they take from knowledge.

<!-- page 77 -->

We have shown earlier that water is like knowledge; we have offered as evidence the outward Qur'an and the Arabs in whose tongue the Qur'an was revealed — they say of a man whose knowledge is vast that he is a "sea." Whoever rides the sea without a ship drowns in it and perishes; likewise, whoever seeks knowledge from one who is not its rightful possessor perishes within it.

The ship rests on four kinds of materials in which it is set up and made firm — the wood and the iron by which it is built and established — and these are like the two higher principles (al-aslan al-'alawiyyan)(1), which we have also mentioned. These four are the root of the sacred law; we have presented their counterparts and likenesses from the Witness (al-shahid) and other sources.

Likewise, the ship runs and anchors by seven things: two booms bound to it; a pillar — the mast — at its center; the cross-piece that opposes the mast at its head, which is the yard (alaza), through which the wind enters and drives it; an anchor that holds it when it lays anchor — the hujla; and a rope tied to it.

These seven are like the seven speakers (nutaqa')(2), and the seven Imams(3) between each speaker and the next. Likewise, the ship's twelve planks of wood are like the twelve subordinate-ranks (lawahiq)(4), four of which are the principals — paired with the two higher principles, and the ten subordinates that we have mentioned. They are, as Allah Almighty said:

(1) The "two higher principles" are the pair ((Intellect and Soul)) — or ((Pen and Tablet)) — or ((the Antecedent and the Consequent)) — and the like; in the religious order, ((the speaker and the imam)).
(2) We have enumerated the seven speakers in the preceding pages.
(3) The seven Imams are those who complete the cycle between one speaker and another. From Adam to Noah there were seven Imams; from Noah to Abraham, seven; and so on until the time of the speaker Muhammad.
(4) The "subordinate-ranks" (lawahiq), in Ismaili usage, are the senior deputies (du'at) in charge of the affairs of the Ismaili regions and islands (jaza'ir) — twelve in number. The islands are divided into seven, and the deputy of an island is no less in rank than the proof (hujja) of the region, who follows him and receives his orders from him.


<!-- page 78 -->
"The number of months with Allah is twelve months in the Book of Allah, [from] the day He created the heavens and the earth — of which four are sacred." (1)

These four correspond to the four ropes fastened at the open prow of the ship, to which the ropes of the central pillar — namely the mast — are bound, so that it stands fixed and does not tilt. The second set is twice that: the eight ropes of the ship, which are the rope of each of the two men, by which a rope is held and by which [the sail] is raised and lowered; and four ropes running from the head of the mast to the open [prow], fixed as we have described; and two ropes on the cross-spar — the rod intercepted at the head of the mast — at each end of which is a rope by which the wind-ropes are turned, and by which its furling is managed. This corresponds to the testimony, with its chapters and the number of its letters.

Likewise, as we have mentioned, the foundation of the law of Noah corresponds to the foundation of the law of Muhammad — Allah's prayers be upon them both — which is the testimony. Though their outward forms differ, the meaning unites them, as we have said. Hence the words of the Almighty:

"He has prescribed for you of religion what He enjoined upon Noah." (Quran 42:13)

For Noah was the first to establish the law, and Muhammad ﷺ the last to establish it. This is what we have set forth concerning the description of the ship — the foundation upon which it was built. Afterward, people added further instruments to it; that was an increase, but the original is what we have described.

---
(1) The Haram are the four preachers who accompany the Imam and never leave him. Among them is one who stands highest, called the Bab; if any of them is absent, one of the [next] four takes his place, and together they form the Imam's Majlis. If one of forty is lost, he is replaced by one of the four hundred respondents, and so on. They are called "the Haram of Substitution" — those without whom the earth does not endure. They are the worlds connected to the divine mysteries, who have been transformed in creation after being created. The Brethren of Purity described them accurately, saying of them that they were pure, detached, transformed souls — not of the common kind.

<!-- page 79 -->
Noah (peace be upon him) established his outward call, while the inward call of his foundation went unanswered. He, too, had a counterpart, as Allah the Almighty said: "None of your people will believe except those who have already believed." (Quran 11:36) — meaning except those who had already believed and called upon their Lord.

Allah said: "He said: My Lord, I have called my people night and day, but my call has only increased them in flight. Whenever I called them so that You might forgive them, they put their fingers in their ears and covered themselves with their garments, and persisted, and were arrogant in their arrogance. Then I called them publicly. Then I announced to them and confided to them secretly. And I said: Ask forgiveness of your Lord — indeed, He is ever a Perpetual Forgiver. He will send [rain from] the sky upon you in showers, and provide you with wealth and children, and grant you gardens, and grant you rivers." (Quran 71:5–12)

The saying "I have called my people night and day" means outwardly and inwardly. "I called them publicly" means he proclaimed himself with the outward call. "And I confided to them secretly" means he hid what he had grasped of the inward call — the call founded on the inner truths — and conveyed it to them, and that they had learned of it; he had concluded for them the full report. He gave the call in secret, distinct from the call to which he had summoned them on the surface.

And his saying, "Whenever I called them so that You might forgive them" means: that I might cover them in secret and in concealment. For forgiveness (*maghfira*) in the language is concealment — and from it the helmet (*mighfar*) is so named, because it covers the head; and the cover is so called because it is a covering; and the Forgiver is the Concealer. He says: their call comes with the outward invitation so that they may respond to it, and so become attached to its inward dimension. And his saying, "They put their fingers in their ears" means they did not hear the summons, and filled their ears with the words that rejected it. "And covered themselves with their garments" means they were content with their outward state and with what they had adorned for themselves.

It has been interpreted thus: "I called them publicly, then I announced to them and confided to them secretly."

<!-- page 80 -->
These have secret meanings. And his saying:

"I said: Ask forgiveness of your Lord — indeed, He is ever a Perpetual Forgiver. He will send [rain from] the sky upon you in showers." (Quran 71:10–11)

"Ask forgiveness" — he says: ask Him to inform you of what is hidden from him in the inward. "He will send the sky upon you in showers" — we have already mentioned that the like of the heavens is the inward, and the like of water is knowledge. The meaning is: when He reveals to you the inward knowledge, He will furnish you with knowledge, and furnish you with wealth and children, and make for you gardens, and make for you rivers. We have already mentioned that the secret of wealth, knowledge, and children in the inward [meaning] is the respondents — that is, He will make of you preachers to whom the servants respond. "And He will make for you gardens" — meaning a call in the inward dimension; "and rivers" — meaning the inner sciences.

Then He said:

"Until, when Our command came and the oven boiled forth." (Quran 11:40)

It means: the knowledge of support came, the foundation spoke of it, and from it issued the science of interpretation. The Possessor of Light [continued]:

"So I carried in it of every kind two of a pair." (Quran 11:40)

He says: agree on the guardianship of the foundation and his call — those who unite in him on the basis of duality — that the foundation is paired with you, the forward [figure] with the argument, and the captains with the preachers. He holds them to the high ranks corresponding to what has occurred in the impact of wisdom in the duality of creation, so that this becomes one of the proofs of the unity of the Creator.

Do likewise in the outward arrangement of the outward ship, so that the action becomes outward as our action is inward. This also takes place within the boundaries of the Apostles until work with the outward ceases at [the coming of] the Master of the Resurrection. We have mentioned snippets of what has been said on this, and we will mention exactly what is needed,

<!-- page 81 -->
to be presented in this book to the extent that we have laid out — Allah willing — when we come to it.

He said:

"Embark in it; in the name of Allah is its course." (Quran 11:41)

His saying "in the name of Allah" comprises two names, like the two upper-world origins, which together carry seven letters — like the letters of "Pen and Tablet," "Muhammad and Ali," "Front and Argument." Thus the call was made and settled with those with whom it was settled: "My Lord is indeed Forgiving, Merciful." (Quran 11:41) — we have already shown that forgiveness and mercy from Allah are what He grants to His servants and bestows upon them, and He is merciful in that. His greatest mercy is the support and the influence in inward knowledge. And mercy (*rahma*) is derived from the womb (*rahim*); the equivalent of this is the impact of wisdom in the inward of the supporter, like the occurrence of sperm within the womb, where it is implanted, [taking shape] little by little until creation comes to be.

"And it runs with them on a wave like mountains." (Quran 11:42)

I mean the foundation of his call — that those who respond to him [advance] in knowledge from one [level] to the next, until they stop at the limits of knowledge and its ranks. The wave here is like the one who has conceived [a claim to] knowledge: he labels himself one of the scholars of the outward, but he is devoid of knowledge, and it slips from his hands. Just as a wave, when it gathers, appears like a mountain to the eye, so too does the one who clothes himself in apparent knowledge: when one follows him, he turns out to be no true Imam — his command does not subdue, his rank does not endure, and his knowledge fades.

The call of truth runs upon the heads of those who imitate the [outward] scholars, contradicting them, just as the ship cuts through the waves and runs upon them while they are terrified of their falsehood. They are broken, and they collapse as the waves stir and agitate. Those who respond to the call are at rest in

<!-- page 82 -->
imitating him, and safe from their misguidance, as those in the ship are safe from the waves of the sea.

"And Noah called out to his son" (Quran 11:42) — meaning his son from his loins — "and he was apart from him" (Quran 11:42) — that is, he had withdrawn from him, hoping the matter would fall to him. So when Noah arose, he envied him and refused to enter under his command and his rule. This is as it was with Iblis toward Adam, and as with Cain toward Abel, the son born to Adam — so Noah called him until he would come under the rule of his foundation. But he refused to do so and said:

"I will take refuge on a mountain that will protect me from the water." (Quran 11:43)

That is: I take refuge with one of the scholars of al-Zahir, taking from him, and seeking shelter with him from an argument — your foundation that overwhelmed me (1) with its knowledge.

"He said: There is no protector today from the command of Allah except for one upon whom He has mercy." (Quran 11:43)

That is: those whom you have mentioned are not your refuge, but rather your protection is from the mercy of Allah. We have already shown the meaning of mercy — which is the people of support — and so pity took hold of him. He asked Allah to guide him.

"My Lord said: My son is of my family, and Your promise is true, and You are the Most Just of judges. ... except an ambush." (Quran 11:45 and context)

I mean: You promised me to carry my family with me in the ship — that is, in a call of truth and a ship of salvation. The Almighty said:

"He is not of your family; he is [a deed] other than righteous." (Quran 11:46)

That is: when he did as he did and persisted in it, his lineage was cut off from you, and he was instead attributed to those who respond to his [false] call and adhere to it — as we have mentioned above and summarized.

---
(1) In copy (e), the reading is "extinguished."

<!-- page 83 -->
We have already shown its meaning.

"And the wave came between them, and he was among the drowned." (Quran 11:43)

By the waves are meant the scholars of misguidance (1) — as we have explained their case — for he differed with them in outward [matters], and we are in doubts, suspicions, and ruin.

"And it was said: O earth, swallow up your water, and O heaven, withhold!" (Quran 11:44)

The earth here is like the foundation that Noah laid for his inward call, having commanded him to conceal what had come to him of inward knowledge and to safeguard it from any but his family — to take hold of it and gather it with himself. The sky is like the speaker (*natiq*), as we have presented; and here Noah (peace be upon him) commanded — when he had established the foundation for the performance of the [inward] task — that he should yield it and hand it over to the one for whom it had been established, and accept the outward that had been established for him. "And the water subsided" (Quran 11:44) — that is, the inward knowledge was concealed within the argument, which is the foundation of the Shari'a. The analogy is the earth into which water seeps, hiding from the eyes; so too is hidden knowledge — safe in its place and stationed in its station — and he was content with it.

"And it came to rest on al-Judi." (Quran 11:44)

It means: the call ended with the respondents.

That is: the introduction to the call and to the inward knowledge was done by the speaker to the foundation, and it did not settle in him, but was drawn from him to those affiliated with him — namely the Imams. Likewise it did not settle in them; it passed on to the arguments (*hujaj*), and did not settle with them either; then it passed to the captains, who are their preachers; then to the wings (*ajniha*), who are below them; then it ran to the respondents, and it settled with them and did not leave them, and it came to rest

---
(1) In version (M) the reading is "the people of misguidance."

<!-- page 84 -->
and settled upon them.

"And it was said: Away with the people who did wrong!" (Quran 11:44)

That is: they remained outside it and had no portion in it.

And when Allah the Almighty said to Noah, in answer to what he had appealed of His promise to save his son and to save his family, it was said to him:

"He is not of your family; it is a deed other than righteous, so do not ask Me about that of which you have no knowledge. I admonish you, lest you be among the ignorant." (Quran 11:46)

Noah (peace be upon him) knew that he had erred in his question, and in his appeal to what had previously been promised. So he took refuge in Allah and asked His mercy by saying:

"My Lord, I seek refuge in You from asking You about that of which I have no knowledge; and unless You forgive me and have mercy upon me, I shall be among the losers." (Quran 11:47)

"It was said: O Noah, descend with peace from Us and blessings upon you and upon nations from those with you. And nations We shall give enjoyment, then a painful punishment from Us shall touch them." (Quran 11:48)

The "descent" here is not the descent of deficiency, for the Almighty made his lot peace and blessings — which is the opposite of what He said to Adam and Iblis:

"Descend, one of you an enemy to another." (Quran 2:36)

That is: descend from Paradise. But here it means: descend to what is below you with peace from Us — that is, with Our support — and with their support, [coming] to you with the support of the wisdom that has come to you. Convey the message with which We have sent you. He singled out Noah for peace and blessings; the nations of those with him — I mean those who hold fast to the rope of Allah the Almighty —

<!-- page 85 -->
are the foundations, the imams, the arguments, the captains, the wings, and the respondents — the sincere ones whom Allah the Almighty singled out for peace and blessings.

"And nations We shall give enjoyment, then a painful punishment shall touch them from Us." (Quran 11:48)

I mean: those who enter the call but are not those who sit firmly within it — He will let them enjoy outwardly in their hour, by which their blood is spared and their wealth is protected, on the condition that they pay the small tribute and its humiliation. Then in their [appointed] time He will touch them with a painful punishment — for their failure to follow the truths of faith, for breaking the covenant and the bond, and for their disbelief in the unseen and in the establishment of the outward and the inward, and for their lack of being supported by wisdom and by inward knowledge — the spiritual and the secure.

The Almighty said:

"And We sent Noah to his people, and he stayed among them a thousand years less fifty." (Quran 29:14)

He meant the duration of his cycle and the dissemination of his law — because his law, however long it endures, is attributed to him in practice: it is the one he is invoked through, and no other name is acknowledged in it. Rather, He is called upon in his name, and its limits, duties, and rulings are established by his Sunna and his wisdom.

As for his body, his person, and his frame, it was only one hundred and twenty-five years for his normal lifespan. Allah did not make the bodies and natures of human beings such that they remain (1) for the duration of this [longer] cycle, but set for it an end —

---
(1) In copy (e), the reading is "He set them up with it."

without which one can scarcely pass, and which one does not exceed — because it would be ruined. Rather, Allah the Almighty has made the complete subsistence of souls to be in the abode of the Hereafter.

<!-- page 86 -->


<!-- page 86 -->

—after the dissolution of this dwelling and the parting of the bodies bound to it in the abode of this world.

And among what befell the people of Noah, and the nations that followed them after him: Allah Almighty has elsewhere in His Book mentioned about them that those who first answered the call were the lowliest among them and the foolish among them. (1) That is what they said:

"I will not follow you, since only the lowliest among us, those of weakest opinion, have followed you."

And He said:

"Nor do I say to those whom your eyes despise that Allah will not grant them any good."

That is, Allah Almighty did indeed grant them that. And upon this same pattern the nations after them passed: when their prophets began calling them to the apparent and so on, the Sunnah of Allah among the nations was that they would say to their prophets what Noah's people said to him (peace be upon him):

"This is nothing but a human being like yourselves, who wishes to gain superiority over you. And if Allah had willed, He would have sent down angels."

We have already explained, in the first two books, the meaning of "human beings" and the direct apparent interpretation of that word, and their saying "angels." By "angels" they mean those who deliver the spiritual subtlety — as if to say, "if only the messengers were purely spiritual." And their saying "we did not hear of this among our forefathers" refers to their fathers, from whom they inherited what they inherited. We have already explained how this paternity is understood, and how they came to assert that their messengers were only outwardly with them while practicing the subtle teaching in their name.

(1) In copy (S) it reads "their greatest."

88

<!-- page 87 -->

They were the ones preoccupied with the angels, and this was before Noah established his foundation to undertake the work entrusted to him. When he raised that foundation up, they clung to their disbelief just as their father Iblis had entered into his. Allah Almighty said:

"And it was no more than that they disbelieved in what was given to them, and Allah denied the disbelievers. They said, 'Shall we believe and be deprived of what Allah has bestowed on us? And Allah brings down His favor on whomever He wills of His servants, so they returned with wrath upon wrath.'"

They disbelieved in them — in the first and the second — and the same occurred in the nations that came after, as Allah, most truthful of speakers, said:

"Their hearts have grown alike. We have indeed made plain the signs to a people who are certain."
