Every nation says to its messenger something similar, as Allah Almighty has reported about them:

"This is nothing but a human being like yourselves, who eats what you eat and drinks from what you drink."

That is, what they perceived outwardly, since nothing else was disclosed to them — just as they say:

"Should we believe in you when only the lowliest follow you?"

The same words of the people of Noah were uttered by the rest of the nations — the liars, the deniers, the ungrateful — concerning the verses of their God, atheists in His names. Then Allah Almighty commanded Noah (peace be upon him) to stand firm in what He had entrusted to him, and Allah said:

"Stand fast, you and whoever has turned in repentance with you, and say, 'O Allah, You who are the one who is satisfied.'" (1)

(1) In copy (M) it came as "tollwa."
(2) In copy (M) it came as "ethtwit."

89

<!-- page 88 -->

—and the second the oppressed people."

He commanded him in this both outwardly and inwardly: outwardly, that he should be upon the apparent ship and be delivered in it — whoever boards it is saved, and whoever lags behind it perishes. And likewise inwardly: that he should be steadfast in his esoteric call, and that its command be set straight, run upon its boundaries, and be completed and made upright.

And He said: "Say, 'Praise be to Allah,'" — yes, praise Him, who has bestowed upon you that grace, and thank Him for what He has conferred upon you of the rank between sunnah and bayan (between the way and the elucidation). For the supplication of the Messenger, who speaks to the apparent, is a prayer of imitation, which the people are commanded with and which they bring as imitators of him. And so, when they are tested by it and respond, they are believers, and an invitation has been extended to them.

He established the foundation for that, and He said:

"And say, 'My Lord, cause me to land at a blessed landing place, and You are the best of those who bring to land.'"

That is: make my arrival and my settling, with what You have bestowed upon me of Your grace, a blessed support — that is, his rank at that time. Then Noah was commanded to ask Him to keep that station with him. And He commanded all the believers likewise to ask Him for guidance to the straight path — which is the Imam of the time. They have already been guided to him, yet the command is to ask Him for steadfastness upon guidance, because perfect guidance is by remaining steadfast in it; whoever is guided and then strays is among those who have gone astray. This is what He said:

"Guide us to the straight path, the path of those upon whom You have bestowed grace, not those upon whom is wrath, nor of those who are astray."

Noah commanded them to make supplication in the way we have described, and the believers in what we have mentioned, so that they would remain in a state of fear, anxious about slipping, aware of it, never feeling safe from it. They were therefore commanded to ask Him for it in every rak'ah of

90

<!-- page 89 -->

their prayers, offered by day and night, lest they neglect it or forget it.

The nations followed the saying of the people of Noah (peace be upon him), as Allah Almighty said:

"The people of Noah denied before them, and they denied Our servant and said, 'A madman,' and he was repulsed."

That is: just as Muhammad (peace and blessings be upon him) was denied by his people who said he was a madman and rebuked him, following the example of those who had denied before them — and likewise in the descriptions Allah Almighty has given of others, the nations resemble one another. We have already mentioned the congruence of the nations in this same way, including the saying of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ:

"You shall follow the ways of the nations before you, footstep by footstep and span by span. Even if they entered a lizard's hole, you would enter it after them."

We have mentioned this in the book *Da'a'im al-Islam* (Pillars of Islam). And in another hadith: "You shall follow the path of those before you, arm's length by arm's length, cubit by cubit, until even if they took a `khashram` you would take one too." For the `dabb` is a creature that takes shelter in stones and catches them by surprise, eating them while they are unaware; and the `khashram` is the shelter of wasps — a hole in clay that they construct, take refuge in, and breed in. The management of their colony is

(1) the opposite of bees, from whom honey is produced and who build their homes of wax for benefit. With wasps there is no benefit from the building of their homes — no good in them, no usefulness — and it is an example for the people of error who imitate the people of truth, whose likeness is the bees. And the stone of the `dabb`, which is like the stone of the jerboa (al-yarbu')—

it has been said that hypocrisy (`nifaq`) is derived from `nafiqa'`, because the jerboa has a stone (a side burrow) by which the hypocrites are likened: if he stops up the door of his burrow on one side, he comes out from the other. So the Messenger of Allah ﷺ wanted to show that this ummah would follow the nations before it upon misguidance and hypocrisy, since they enter the `khashram` or the burrow of

(1) In copy (S) it came as "ants."

91

<!-- page 90 -->

wasps.

It is not permissible for the Messenger of Allah ﷺ to give as a likeness something that does not in fact occur. The Almighty said in the story of Noah (peace be upon him):

"So We opened the gates of heaven with pouring rain, and caused the earth to gush forth with springs, so the waters met for a matter already decreed."

Within this is the opening of the gates of the `natiq` (the speaking-prophet) — that is, those whom he has appointed for the apparent with the knowledge of the apparent. And He said:

"And caused the earth to gush forth with springs."

Meaning the gushing forth of knowledge from the lower limits — that is, the meeting of the twelve who establish the foundation for the knowledge of the esoteric, one on each island of a `naqib` (captain) who follows him, and so on. And He said in the story of Moses (peace be upon him):

"Strike the rock with your staff, and twelve springs will gush forth from it. Each tribe of the people knew its drinking place."

And the Almighty said:

"So the waters met for a matter already decreed."

That is: the knowledge of the outward and the knowledge of the subtle — each of them appointed to the matter that was decreed for it, neither exceeding it to the other. The traditional knowledge belongs to the Messenger, and the bayan (elucidation) belongs to the foundation, and so it becomes after the traditional messenger the Imam, and the elucidation belongs to the proof (hujja), according to what we have already presented from the predetermination of Allah Almighty — that is, according to what He has ordained, arranged, and brought about by His wisdom among His servants.

"And We carried him upon a thing of planks and nails."

92

<!-- page 91 -->

That is, the ship.

We have already mentioned the interpretation of the planks — that they are twelve planks — and the ship, which is the assembly. It is like the twelve captains (`nuqaba'`), and the foundation unites them. The `dusur` (nails) are the nails by which the planks are tightened — they are the high celestial benefits connected with them. We have already presented that iron in its entirety resembles one of the higher principles, and that the benefits of dominion below it are based, as we mentioned, upon their running through the upper and lower limits. And the saying of the Almighty:

The Book is a craft to which one is guided, and some among them are wrongdoers:

"And We sent Noah and Abraham, and placed in their descendants prophethood and the Book, and We sent in their footsteps with Our Messengers and supported them with 'Isa ibn Maryam."

The meaning is that the elite of Adam (peace be upon him) passed from one to the next of his descendants until it settled in Noah, then after him in his descendants, until it reached Abraham, and then after him among his descendants. So too was it passed on to the Prophet after them. And by "descendants" He means the offspring here — the extract drawn from the lineage of Noah and Abraham, peace be upon them — who are the prophets, the messengers, the imams, and their `hujjas` (proofs), from them and from other descendants, drawing forth the propagation of the call as we have mentioned in the interpretation of religion, prophethood, and support.

And "the Book" here is the knowledge that is established through the Imams — it is called "a book" when it is established through writing — and "the Book" in the inner sense is the Imam, according to what we have said about naming the thing by the name of what accompanies its station. Endorsement is the knowledge in the offspring drawn from the lineage of Noah and Abraham, and those who were raised up for their causes from her esoteric descendants — who are

(1) In copy (S) it came as "our case."

93

<!-- page 92 -->

the offspring of religion. Many of this offspring and of the offspring of the lineage are not loyal to them — they are corrupt. We have shown that they are cut off from their offspring and lineage because of disbelief and debauchery and misguidance — if they persist in it, without remorse, without repentance from it. As for whoever among them repents, he remains as he was. And the elite of the offspring of the lineage is free from impurity, sound of garment, pure and purified — and that is Muhammad ﷺ and the Imams from his descendants who were born of Ali and Fatima, may Allah's prayers be upon them — in a single chain of mention of the descendants of Noah and Abraham among whom Allah Almighty has placed support and knowledge. And those who shared in the birth of the lineage, the son of the call, other than the people of the elite among them, are obedient and disobedient as in all of creation. Ali and Fatima were both born of the descendants of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ — by Fatima — just as 'Isa was a descendant of Abraham by his mother Maryam. Allah Almighty said:

"And that was Our argument which We gave to Abraham against his people. We raise in degrees whom We will. Your Lord is Wise, Knowing. And We bestowed on him Ishaq and Ya'qub, all We guided; and Noah We guided before, and of his descendants Dawud and Sulayman and Ayyub and Yusuf and Musa and Harun. Thus do We reward the doers of good. And Zakariyya and Yahya and 'Isa and Ilyas — all of the righteous."

So the Almighty established 'Isa as among the descendants by way of his mother, in a way that does not contradict that the descendants be made of a particular root — so He attributed the descendants to Noah and Abraham, and after them to Musa and 'Isa. The Imamate was not carried forward among their descendants before the birth of the lineage (1), since there was no trace of them, and so it returned through the footsteps of Ibrahim.

(1) In copy (S) it came as "the cross."

94

<!-- page 93 -->

Noah (peace be upon him) said:

"My Lord, do not leave upon the earth from the disbelievers any dwellers."

He says: do not grant those who have disbelieved in You any share of truth.

"For if You leave them, they will mislead Your servants and will not beget except disbelievers."

He says: if You make that fair-seeming to them, You will have prepared them to mislead Your servants from the truth, and only those like themselves will be born from their call.

"My Lord, forgive me and my parents, and whoever enters my house as a believer, and the believing men and the believing women, and do not increase the wrongdoers except in destruction."

We have already mentioned the interpretation of forgiveness above. By "parents" He means those who took up his call and his upbringing.

"And whoever enters my house as a believer."

That is: whoever was among them before him and whoever is among them after him — they all share in this supplication.

"And do not increase the wrongdoers except in destruction."

Destruction. "Injustice" (`zulm`) in the language means placing a thing other than in its proper place — meaning those who placed the Imamate other than in its proper place. And this was the role of Noah (peace be upon him). After him, of those who warned by his law and called to his call, came Hud and Salih, peace be upon them.

95

<!-- page 94 -->

Hud (peace be upon him)

As for Hud (peace be upon him), he called his people, as Allah Almighty has related in His saying:

"And to 'Ad [We sent] their brother Hud."

So He attributed him to their brothers in terms of birth, since he was one of them outwardly and inwardly. As for outwardly, he was of their clan, joined with them by a single father, and so he was their brother in the apparent birth. As for the inward, however, he was from him and they from him — the nation of Noah (peace be upon him) and the people of his call, he is their father (that is, Noah) in the inner world, as Allah Almighty said:

"The religion of your father Ibrahim."

Whoever among them believes, He calls to him; and whoever disbelieves, he is cut off from him and goes out of the attribution we ascribe to him. So Allah attributes him with brotherhood to those of them who believe, as the Almighty said:

"The believers are but brothers."

He said:

"And in 'Ad, when We sent against them the barren wind. It did not leave anything that it came upon, except that it made it like decayed ruins."

He said about them:

"And when they saw it as a cloud approaching their valleys, they said, 'This is a cloud—'"

96


<!-- page 95 -->
"It rained upon us" — but it was the wind he had been promising them, a wind carrying a torment that destroyed everything by command of its Lord, so that nothing of them could be seen but their dwellings. Thus do We recompense the criminal people.

The deeper sense of the "barren wind" is the supreme knowledge through which God's substance reaches His friends with proofs (1) against His enemies, while He prolongs them in their pretense of falsehood against the people of truth. It is not knowledge of the kind by which the believers are raised and brought to new birth; rather it strikes and crushes the disbelievers, because they had gathered around the guidance, examined it, and challenged it on its outer side, and so they raised their objections against it and were intimidated by it. It became for them only a token, under the pretext of knowledge, and they were given an appointment with its appearance.

They said: "What do you promise us, if you are one of the truthful?"

He said: "Knowledge is with Allah; I only deliver to you what I was sent with. But I see that you are an ignorant people."

He is saying: what he symbolizes to you rests with God, and he shows it only within its proper limits. "I have informed you of the knowledge with which I was sent, but you are a people who do not know the limits of knowledge and learning." So support came to him from Allah the Almighty, suppressing them and breaking their falsehood and overturning their doubts. When he opened up something of that to them, they thought he wanted to bring them some benefit they could recognize, and so they said to him:

"When they saw it as a cloud advancing toward their valleys, they said, 'This is a cloud bringing us rain.'"

(1) In version (e), "(al-Dafqah) came."
97

<!-- page 96 -->
We have already mentioned that water is like knowledge, and rain is like the sustenance that flows from it.

"Rather, it is what you sought to hasten — a wind in which there is a painful torment, destroying everything by command of its Lord." He is saying: this is the very thing of which you said:

"So bring us what you have promised, if you are of the truthful."

It is a punishment for you, not a knowledge from which you would benefit — and that was when their destruction had drawn near, and Allah the Almighty had grown angry with them. So He sent upon them the wind that appeared and destroyed them in their bodies, so they should not depart from this world while still standing on a sound argument for themselves in their misguidance, since they had not responded to the outward call as they should have responded. They should have followed the master of the outward call and then entered under the ruling of the argument of the master of the esoteric, as we have mentioned in that regard. So the punishment of Allah came upon them, outwardly and inwardly, and destroyed them, as the Almighty said:

"And nothing was to be seen of them but their dwellings. Thus do We recompense the criminal people."

Salih (peace be upon him).

He came in the cycle of Noah (peace be upon him) and was among those who warned in his sharia and called to his summons. His people were named Thamud, as Allah the Almighty narrated of him when He said:

"And to Thamud, their brother Salih. He said, 'O my people, worship Allah; you have no god other than Him.'"
98

<!-- page 97 -->
He was their brother on the same principle we mentioned in the story of Hood (peace be upon him) — by birth, because he was one of them outwardly, and by his teaching inwardly. His words, and the words of Hood and Noah and all those who call their people, from among the prophets, to the worship of Allah the Almighty — by saying "O people, worship God" — are a call to the worship of Allah the Almighty by affirming His oneness. And His oneness can only be properly arrived at from the inner side, because whoever seeks to know Allah the Almighty without ta'wil (interpretation) cannot escape one of two outcomes: either he likens Him to something, or he falls into ta'til (negation) (1) if he denies Him with mere suspicion and the measure of his own limited knowledge, without evidence. And if he takes that from his own opinion, or from a book that has come down to him, or from eavesdropping on someone who was not given permission to convey it, Allah the Almighty will not accept it from him. He said in His praise:

"And do not eat from that over which the name of Allah has not been pronounced, for it is a transgression. And indeed the devils inspire their friends to dispute with you, and if you obey them, you will be polytheists."

But whoever affirms the oneness of Allah the Almighty without taking that affirmation from the side of ta'wil drawn from evidence (2) — he has lost the limit in it. For man is created in his outward, his inward, and his intellect; in this he is intact, rewarded if he obeys and punished if he disobeys. He does not cease to be an originated being (hadith — caused) in all of this, and whoever is described by these descriptions does not refer to a Speaker who is on his level in being originated. If one were to say "He is," they would say:

"He enters under number and counting." And if he says, "He is a thing," then "the thing is a thing, and the thing said: there is nothing like Him" — because He has made Himself like it.

(1) In version (e): "(al-Ta'til)." (2) In copy (X): "(Evidence)."
99

<!-- page 98 -->
He argued from language and said that when the Arabs say, "He is not like so-and-so doing this," they mean by this that they do not want a likeness to him — and this is the most eloquent kind of negation in this chapter.

"So-and-so is a creature, and likewise the one who says of him 'he was created' — they have likenesses." And if you said that about the Maker of creation (al-Bari al-Baraya), you would have given Him a like and a counterpart. If you say He is something, you make Him an originated being; and if you say He is nothing, He would be suspended in nonexistence. Rather, in respect of His names: His names have limits beneath Him, and the name does not fall on Him as names fall on other names, because names fall only on perceived qualities. This discussion has its own place where it is established in full, for its length, and it should not be placed within the limits of this knowledge. When we reach it, we will set it out, God willing.

And a good saying of his to his people:

"O my people, this is the she-camel of Allah, a sign for you — so let her eat in the land of Allah."

He gave the she-camel as a parable for the hujja (argument), as the cow of the Children of Israel will be mentioned later, in its place, God willing — and not in the sense in which the Jews claim it in their fabrications, nor in the sense in which the Christians claim it in their Gospel — namely the news about the she-camel — for they do not know its significance in what is mentioned in the story of Salih, either outwardly or inwardly. Male camels are like the imams, and female camels are like the hujjas; the same applies to cattle.

The Arabs in whose language the Qur'an was revealed call the noble man "qarm," and he is the stallion camel (1). So Allah the Almighty struck parables for them in terms that

(1) In version (5): "(al-Nahl)."
100

<!-- page 99 -->
they would understand and recognize. He said:

"So let her eat in the land of Allah."

He meant: let her be, and let her take what Allah has appointed for her, by way of her share in the earth, from what animals eat.

"And do not touch her with harm."

He is saying: do not deny her, and do not alter her actions, for We have appointed her for a subtle hujja and the conveying of the call — and a near punishment will overtake you if you do that.

"And remember when He made you successors after Aad."

He is saying this to those who followed Hood and became his successors after him in his sciences and his teachings.

"And settled you in the land."

I.e., I brought you down into the ta'wil of the foundations.

"So you take palaces from its plains."

He meant that they had not given him what was due to him within the limit of clear teaching and opening — i.e., "you have set up wings for the da'wah."

"And you hew out the mountains as houses."

He meant: you have ascended from the limit of being a supported one (mustajib) onward, for these "houses" are the shelter of the guides, who began their origin from dense bodily speech that is compounded — like houses that appear to bodies — dense.

"So fear Allah and obey me, and do not corrupt the earth, spreading mischief."
101

<!-- page 100 -->
Otherwise, this has already been mentioned — but here he was addressing a people who were from the people of Hood's cycle and from the remnants of his descendants who had followed him without holding to what he had taught. So Salih came to revive his command among them, to guide them, and to set their condition right.

"And do not roam about the earth spreading corruption."

He is saying: do not subject yourselves to the limit of altering ta'wil by changing and substituting.

"They were arrogant, and they said, 'O Salih, bring us what you promise us, if you are one of the messengers.'"

The argument (hujja) drove them away from his rank, and he overcame them on the outward face — so, in another way, they killed him. And the Messenger of Allah likened Ali (peace be upon him) to the houghing of the she-camel, where he said: "The first of them are the most wretched of the ancients, and the latter of them are the most wretched of the latter ones — they shall hough you, O Ali."

It is reported in the narration that those who houghed the she-camel were among the faction of Salih — namely his son whom he had appointed in his place after him — just as this community killed Ali and Hussein (may the prayers of Allah be upon them).

The Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) said: "You shall surely follow the ways of the nations before you, footstep by footstep, hand-span by hand-span — even if they entered a hole of a lizard, you would enter it." So Salih's killers killed him from among the imams: they killed him "by houghing," in that they prevented him from his task and overcame him on the outward face as well. And he said:

"This is a she-camel: for her is a share of water, and for you is a share, on a known day."

It was said in the tafsir that the camel drank their water one day and they drank none of it, but they would come to her and she would yield to them, and they would milk her and drink her milk on that day in place of water. And they would drink from the water on the other day. This is a tafsir given by some of the men of the
102

<!-- page 101 -->
ta'wil, brought into the open by the general scholars.

We have mentioned that water is like knowledge, and milk is like esoteric knowledge — because it comes out of a hidden udder; it is from the inner knowledge of the subconscious as a symbol and a sign. And it is the first of the limits of the subordinate (ta'wili) ranks for the respondents, just as breastfeeding is the first food of the newborn.

We have mentioned that the Speaker (al-Natiq) brings the apparent knowledge of the sharia, and the hujja brings the ta'wil based on it. He intended for the share of water to be divided between the Speaker and the Silent One: the Speaker has the knowledge in bulk, and the Silent One benefits in the inner knowledge of the Speaker. So he informed me that the knowledge of the Speaker has been divided between his hujja and the general people of his da'wah, for he benefits the general people of his da'wah on the outward face, while his hujja benefits in his inner; and the hujja benefits the lahiqs (suffixes, the "trailing ones") and the lahiqs benefit the wings, and the wings benefit the believers.

So the knowledge of the Speaker came to be divided into two parts, in the manner we have described. Milk is only for the females, and the like of them are the hujjas, and the male and the like of them have no right to it. The Almighty said:

"So they denied him and houghed her, and their Lord destroyed them for their sin."

He meant: the enemy of the master of the time, and that they gathered against him and colluded with him in the leap upon the hujja of Salih — in some accounts they killed him, in others they removed him and overcame his rank. The overcoming of the outward command of the friend (wali) — by those who do not know it — is as the death of the dead is to those who do not know it; with the people of knowledge he is alive. For the overcoming of the command of the friends of Allah is only the overcoming of those who overcome them on the outward face of this worldly affair, and that is what has no weight for them. As for the command of Allah the Almighty, and what Allah has appointed for them, it is in their hands, and it is not violated and not
103

<!-- page 102 -->
plundered. But those who overcome on the outward face seek to remove them, in order to establish an imamate of those who are invalid in the religion of Allah, and to bring His servants to life by their own wisdom (so they imagine); otherwise they would not turn their attention to overpowering anyone whose outward they overpower. He said:

"And in Thamud, when it was said to them, 'Enjoy yourselves for a while.' Then they were insolent against the command of their Lord, and the thunderbolt seized them while they looked on."

"They could not stand up, and they were not victorious."

I.e., those who made the argument of falsehood — they were not victorious over the master of their time, who repelled them with his supporting arguments, before they perished by the lesser ruin through paradox; then they will perish by the greater ruin, as Allah the Almighty said:

"When We willed their destruction, We destroyed them and all who were with them."

The Almighty said:

"And in the city were nine clans (raht) who corrupted the land and did not bring about reform."

The inner meaning of the city is the sanctuary of the inner (haram al-batin), and the sanctuary was divided into nine ranks; so each one of them, in his opposing counterpart, corrupts the limits of the call.

The first rank of the raht is the Speaker (al-Natiq) (1); the second is the Foundations (2); the third is the Imams (3); the fourth is the Hujjas (4); the fifth is the Naqibs (Captains) (5); the sixth is the Hands (Aydi) (6); and the seventh

(1) Singular: (Speaker).
(2) Singular: (Foundation).
(4) Singular: (Hujja).
(3) Singular: (Imam).
(5) Singular: (Naqib).
(6) Singular: (Hand).
104

<!-- page 103 -->
is the Wings (Ajniha) (1); the eighth is the Authorized (Ma'dhun) (2); and the ninth is the Respondents (Mustajibun) (3). Each people stands opposed to its enemy, as Allah the Almighty said:

"And thus We have made for every prophet an enemy from among the criminals."

We have established what we have demonstrated within this limit which we have set out in the story of Noah (peace be upon him), and we have spoken of those who were in his cycle among the Speakers and Imams whom Allah mentioned in His book. He has informed us that Noah (peace be upon him) was the first of the Messengers to abrogate the laws of those who came before him and to inaugurate his own sharia. We have mentioned some of what his community said in opposing him, and what the nations after him followed of the same pattern — so that this would be a knowledge for those who hear it, and a warning to those who pause to understand it. So follow the path of the believers from those who have gone before you among the righteous, and do not follow the deeds of the deniers; you must obey your imams, and the witnesses of Allah upon you. And know how the imamate was carried out in those who were before you, age after age.

Allah the Almighty has appointed in every nation a messenger to carry the outward form of its sharia and a foundation (asas) for the inward of its call. And between every messenger and the next, a community appears in plain sight — lest it be as Allah the Almighty said:

"So that the people would have no argument against Allah after the messengers; and lest they say, 'No bringer of good news has come to us, and no warner.'"

And know that the practice continues uninterrupted in the imamate, until the rising of the Qa'im of the Resurrection, the conqueror by Allah. May He bestow His blessings on you, and make you of those who give thanks for the favor of what is bestowed upon you.

(3) Singular: (Respondent).
(2) Singular: (Authorized).
(1) Singular: (Wing).

These are the orders of the esoteric call (da'wah batiniyya) in the time of concealment (satr).
105


<!-- page 104 -->
He is brought to him to fulfill the promise made to him before — even more fully than he himself can. May God bless the Prophet Muhammad and his pure and peaceful family.

(1) Nuh was born 1642 years after the birth of Adam, and the Flood came when Nuh was 600 years old. He died 350 years after the Flood, having lived 950 years in all; his grave is on Jabal al-Judi at Mosul. The Flood began on the tenth of Rajab in the year 2242 from the birth of Adam and lasted six months, ending on the tenth of Muharram in the year 2243. Seventy men boarded the ark with him. His son who was left behind was called Yam. His sons Sam, Ham, and Yafith were born before the Flood and were among the seventy men of the Flood who rode with him in the ark. Nuh, as is known, had bequeathed the succession to his son Sam during his own lifetime; Sam is his foundation.

Sam ibn Nuh was born in the year 2142 after the birth of Adam — a hundred years before the Flood — and died 500 years after the Flood, having lived 600 years. His successor was his son Arfakhshad ibn Sam, born 2 years after the Flood and died 467 years after the Flood, having lived 465 years. He bequeathed to his son Shalakh.

Shalakh ibn Qaynan ibn Arfakhshad — his father's name (Qaynan) fell out of the line of succession because he had taken to sorcery and was thereby deprived of the station of the Imamate. Shalakh was born in the year 276 and died 567 after the Flood, having lived 460 years. He bequeathed to his son Abir.

Abir was born in 466 and died 830 after the Flood, having lived 364 years. He bequeathed to his son Falaj.

As for Falaj, he was born in 540 and died 879 after the Flood, having lived 339 years. He bequeathed to his son Ra'u — titled, like his father Falaj, Dhu al-Qarnayn, also mentioned in the Holy Quran. Ra'u was born in 670 and died in 1009 after the Flood, having lived 339 years, just as his father had. His hujja was Salih (peace be upon him). He bequeathed to his son Sarugh.

Sarugh was born in 802 and died in 1132 after the Flood, having lived 330 years. He likewise bequeathed to his son Nahur, who was born in 932 and died 1140 after the Flood, having lived 205 years. Nahur handed command on to his son Tarah, born in 1011 and died in 1316 after the Flood. He is the resident Imam (al-imam al-muqim) of the third Natiq, Ibrahim al-Khalil. He lived 315 years.

As for Hud, he is the son of Abd Allah ibn Rajah ibn al-Khulud ibn Ad ibn Awad ibn Aram ibn Sam ibn Nuh. He was the hujja to the Imam Abir. He used to reside in Hadramawt, calling his people to the law of Nuh. After God destroyed his people, he returned to Mecca and was buried there.

As for Salih, he is the son of Ubayd ibn Asif ibn Mashij ibn Ubayd ibn Hathir ibn Tamud ibn Ayr ibn Aram ibn Sarim. He was the hujja for the Imam (peace be upon him), and he used to guide his people, Thamud, who were dwelling at al-Hijr. After their destruction he emigrated to Mecca and died there at the age of fifty-eight.

<!-- page 105 -->

## Chapter Three

(Containing the interpretation of the stories of Ibrahim, Isma'il, Ishaq, Ya'qub, Yusuf, and Ayyub.)

### The Story of Ibrahim

In the name of God, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful.

Praise be to God, Lord of the worlds. May God bless Muhammad the faithful Prophet, and his wasi Ali ibn Abi Talib, and the Imams from their descendants until the Day of Judgment and afterward.

When the turn of Nuh (peace be upon him) ended and the number of his Imams was complete, God sent Ibrahim (peace be upon him) as a prophet. He sent him and singled him out with intimate friendship (khulla):

> "And God took Ibrahim as an intimate friend (khalil)."
> (Quran 4:125)

For he fulfilled what Adam and Nuh, peace be upon them, had not brought to completion. Of this fulfillment God said:

> "And Ibrahim, who fulfilled [his covenant]."
> (Quran 53:37)

<!-- page 106 -->

This fulfillment is the completion of the words with which God tested him, as He says:

> "And when his Lord tested Ibrahim with words and he fulfilled them."
> (Quran 2:124)

These are the same words that Adam received from his Lord after his fall, when he repented to Him and remembered God Almighty.

Ibrahim's knowledge of the kingdom of heaven and earth: God Almighty grants such vision only to those who please Him through what He has created. So the Almighty said of Idris (peace be upon him):

> "And We raised him to a high station."
> (Quran 19:57)

He said of Isa (peace be upon him):

> "Rather, God raised him to Himself."
> (Quran 4:158)

And He said of Muhammad (peace be upon him):

> "Glory be to Him who took His servant by night from the Sacred Mosque to the Farthest Mosque, whose surroundings We have blessed, that We might show him some of Our signs."
> (Quran 17:1)

The Messenger of God (peace be upon him) told of the Isra' and his ascent through the heavens, of the angels, prophets, and messengers who had passed before him whom he saw there, of what he did and commanded, and of what was said to him — in the long and well-known hadith.

In just this way, God Almighty shows him the pure and virtuous souls — souls He had described to him, that had been disciplined in obedience to Him, which He had drawn out, ranked, singled out, and accepted. He showed Ibrahim the kingdom of heaven and brought him into contact with the heavenly upper bodies, without the dense bodies in which the earthly density takes shelter.

It is therefore reported of the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) in the hadith of the Isra' that he was held back from his own self: in some of the reports from women in his household it is said that on that night —

<!-- page 107 -->

— she said, "He did not leave between my couch and my couch," meaning his body did not leave the bed but his soul rose into the kingdom, and there he saw what he saw and came to what he came to.

In it is what has been narrated about it, and so it was at the beginning of what the Revelation brought to him. It is also narrated of him (peace be upon him) that he would see it as a vision in his dream. God grants this to many of His saints as well; hence the saying of the Messenger of God (peace be upon him), "The good vision is part of the Revelation." When the Revelation came upon him, sleep would overtake him, cover him, and bear down on him until it grew oppressive, and he would be drenched in sweat. That is why, at the start of what came upon him, his people said he was struck — for the burden of the message and the meeting of the lower spirits with the upper spirits carries weight and hardship. From this is the word of God Almighty:

> "We shall cast upon you a heavy word."
> (Quran 73:5)

It is in human nature that when a person sees someone he has never seen before — one who carries an aura about him — he is at first repelled and afraid until he becomes familiar with that person and grows at ease with him.

In just this way Ibrahim (peace be upon him), when he first saw the upper boundaries (hudud) of the heavenly kingdom, said, "This is my Lord," and he said the same of the second and the third. When he saw what stood above each, he left the finite limit behind and clung to what was higher, on and on, just as God Almighty has described in His Book — until he ended at the Bari, the Originator, the Subduer of the heavens and the earth, who is beyond every limit and limitation. He is transcendent above the boundaries, and the boundaries themselves are within His dominion. The kingdom of heaven that God Almighty mentioned Ibrahim (peace be upon him) saw is the upper boundary, whose support flows down into the lower boundaries beneath it. We have also mentioned what he saw at the beginning of his command and the emergence of his calling in religion, according to what we have said about it, and that —

<!-- page 108 -->

— every one whom God has singled out for prophethood and chosen for the message and the Imamate is, before that, like all human beings, nothing of significance. He is brought into being by the power of the Bari, as He brings every human being into being from despised water. Then he is shaped in the womb, carried, born — first an unreasoning infant, then a discerning boy, then he reaches the age of responsibility — and all of that takes its time.

God Almighty has set up in His earth, for human beings, boundaries that He has appointed for His religion, as we have already explained. So whoever is appointed to bear responsibility (taklif) must have, from among these boundaries, a teacher who teaches him, a guide who guides him, and a blessing upon him, until — when he reaches the point of being assigned — God Almighty makes him fit for the place He has qualified him for, and he becomes that. So it was with Ibrahim (peace be upon him); so it was with every prophet and Imam before him and after him, and so too with those below them among the earthly boundaries we have mentioned elsewhere.

He looked first at the nearest of the earthly boundaries, which is the da'i and his like. We have already mentioned that the planets in the sky stand for this rank. And this is what God said:

> "When night came upon him, he saw a planet (kawkab)."
> (Quran 6:76)

Like the night, as we have said: when the da'i took the covenant upon him for the noble (lord) and ordered him to conceal and keep it secret, he was forced to do so — that is, to veil it from view. The da'i had not yet informed him of any of the other boundaries; he had only opened to him such things as ought to be opened for one of his kind. Ibrahim heard from him what was to be heard, magnified it, and thought that this was the end and that there was no boundary above it. So he said to himself, "This is my Lord," meaning the one in charge of my affair, the cause between me and the Almighty.

(1) In manuscript (e), "Muhaymin." (2) In manuscript (e) it is given as "they are blessings."

<!-- page 109 -->

The educator and the blessed (mun'im) is the wali, as Yusuf (peace be upon him) said:

> "Return to your lord and ask him about the case of the women who cut their hands."
> (Quran 12:50)

This usage is known in the speech of the Arabs, who say of a man "the lord of the favor," "the lord of the slave," and "the lord of the house" — meaning the owner of that thing and the one charged with it.

> "But when it set, he said, 'I do not love those that set.'"
> (Quran 6:76)

That is, the da'i — having let him hear and shown him the boundary above himself, which is the hujja — recognized that the one above himself stood between Ibrahim and his goal. So he connected Ibrahim with the hujja and let him see what stood above what the first had shown him. Ibrahim was again deluded as he had been the first time, taking the ultimate cause to be this one, as he said:

> "And when he saw the moon rising, he said, 'This is my Lord.'"
> (Quran 6:77)

The hujja then lowered the matter for him and showed him the boundary above himself — namely, the Imam. He looked at this second one with more awareness than at what he had seen before, and saw in what the hujja said the proof of it:

> "If my Lord does not guide me, I shall surely be of the people who go astray."
> (Quran 6:77)

He says: if I do not receive guidance from the Owner of the Time (sahib al-zaman), I am one of the misguided.

We have mentioned above that the moon is like the hujja. So when he saw the Imam, he said:

> "When he saw the sun rising, he said, 'This is my Lord, this is greater.'"
> (Quran 6:78)

(1) In manuscript (x) it is given as "the people who go astray."

<!-- page 110 -->

— meaning he confessed that this one was his guardian and the greatest of those who tend to him. And so, when he had stood upon the rank of the Owner of the Time and described him by what stood above him among the upper boundaries, he said:

> "O my people, I am innocent of what you associate. I have turned my face to the One who originated the heavens and the earth, as a pure monotheist (hanif), and I am not of the polytheists."
> (Quran 6:78–79)

So he disowned the shirk his people had been doing and was sincere to God alone, who has no partner.

> "And We have already given the family of Ibrahim the Book and the Wisdom, and We have given them a great kingdom."
> (Quran 4:54)

Then, when God raised Ibrahim (peace be upon him) to the rank of prophethood and singled him out with the message, He lifted him up to the kingdom of heaven to show him — in some manner like what we have already mentioned of the raising of the simple, gentle soul to souls like itself: simple, without the dense body, which is not composed in such a way that it can rise and ascend, but whose composition, identity, imprint of frailty, and lasting destiny belong to the earth, from which it was created and to which it returns.

When Ibrahim saw the nearest upper boundaries, he supposed at first that they were the ultimate, and he was filled with magnification of God's command in himself and with awe of what he had met, faced, drawn support and power from. The same happened with the second and third boundaries — which is the limit of the boundaries. When he saw the support of the Almighty bestowed upon him, and what He withheld from him — great is His might — and the kalima called him about him, he saw the kingdom of heaven —

(1) In manuscript (e) it is given as "and he is acquitted."

<!-- page 111 -->

— and he saw also the kingdom of the earth. He took in the virtue and obtained it outwardly and inwardly. So it was as the Almighty said of him, describing him:

> "And he is among those who are certain (al-muqinin)."
> (Quran 6:75)

As for what the literalists have interpreted — that there was a king of that time who saw in a dream that one would be born who would take away his kingdom, and so he ordered the killing of every newborn; and that the mother of Ibrahim (peace be upon him) fled with him into the wilderness and sheltered him in a cave after she had given birth to him; and that he did not come out of it and saw neither sun, moon, nor star until he had grown up; and that, when he came out and saw these things, he said what he said — the very face of this interpretation testifies to its falsehood.

For if he were in a cave, as they say, in such a way that he could not see the sky from it, no air would have reached him there, and he could not have lived. Even if he had managed to live in such a state, then to walk out into the open air all at once would have been the cause of his perishing. And his mother, when she had taken him into a cave, would not have neglected to bring him out into the fresh air and to attend to the necessities of human life — and so on. And if matters were as they claim, it would have been better for her to bring him out at night, at the close of day, when no one would see him — so that the sun, moon, and stars would not be set before his eyes. And if he had heard nothing of the Lord, he would not have known of Him at all — just as a child does not utter speech until he has heard it spoken. The boy is mute and does not speak, and the deaf does not hear and does not know what is being said; if he has not heard speech, his tongue does not move with it, and the sound comes out of his throat and chest as it does in an animal that does not distinguish speech, though it has tongue, uvula, and lips.

The corruption of this interpretation of theirs by their own opinion is clearer than to need proof or argument; the argument over it would be long, and we have not built this book upon it, nor was it our aim. When we saw that pursuing it would cut us off from what we did aim at, we cut it short. In the same way, we have not mentioned the interpretation of the general public (al-amma) and what they have brought of such things —


<!-- page 112 -->

It is easy to confuse the subjects under discussion here with what is intended by the inward, without the outward; and the outward, in such expressions, refers to the subtle inner meaning.

The Almighty said:

> "And when Abraham was tested by his Lord with certain words, he fulfilled them."

By "the words" is meant those which afflicted Adam (peace be upon him) — that is, the limits embodied by the companions of the six laws that had been permitted to him. It serves us to establish them upon the foundation of obligatory duties and assignments. Among them is the lesser, seventh matter: that Adam (peace be upon him) extended his hand to transgress what God the Almighty had forbidden him from eating — and this is what Adam (peace be upon him) received when he repented, and what he received from its upper limits, as we have already mentioned. The "word" is the author of the Sharia.

So Ibrahim (peace be upon him) completed the six words concerning the duty of obligation and action in what He had specified in His law, and he did not exceed any other; he fulfilled them, and so God Almighty remembered him as one who is complete and faithful.

Ibrahim (peace be upon him) established the upper words, which are the limits for receiving the knowledge concerning them, as well as the lower words, which are the six pronouncements for the establishment of their laws in the House of Practice. Adam and Noah (peace be upon him) had each established their own laws; Ibrahim established his and did not place after them anything beyond what God had commanded him to establish. He set up his law from the outward — by what could be inferred from the laws of those who would come after him — and he indicated these laws by their very forms. He conveyed the inner dimension to the one to whom it ought to be communicated, so that he might complete the words and fulfill them.

When he had completed them all, God raised him up as an imam, and He said in His Book:

> "I will make you an Imam for the people."

We have mentioned above the interpretation of the Imam and the Imamate. He (Ibrahim) said, "And from my descendants" — asking God to make the Imamate among his descendants — and He said:

> "My covenant will not be obtained by the wrongdoers." [p. 114]

<!-- page 113 -->

God Almighty answered him that it would be made so for those of his descendants who had not committed wrong, and excluded from it those who were wrongdoers. In the language of the Arabs, *injustice* (*zulm*) is the placing of a thing outside its proper place.

When God Almighty raised up Ibrahim (peace be upon him) as a prophet sent with a law other than the law of Noah (peace be upon him), He established for it outward principles indicating what was within them — by which God might be worshipped by his community, according to what we have mentioned. Every prophet sent with a law (1) — the foundation of Ibrahim's (peace be upon him) law was the House. So he built it and called the people to it, and gave them leave to perform Hajj to it, to circumambulate it, and he established for it rites and landmarks and your rituals. He included his son Ishmael (peace be upon him) in building it, for Ishmael is the foundation of his Shari'ah, as God says:

> "And when Ibrahim and Ishmael were raising the foundations of the House: 'Our Lord, accept it from us. Truly You are the All-Hearing, the All-Knowing.'"

He also said:

> "And We covenanted with Ibrahim and Ishmael, that they purify My House for those who circle around it, and those in retreat, and those who bow and prostrate."

So they built the House in the Haram (2) of Mecca, where his son Ishmael lived, and built it as an example for him and for every Imam after him. The people moved toward the House, and their circling around it became likewise an example and a proof, signaling that they ought to come forward to it in every nearby or distant place; they should take refuge in it, surround it, and circumambulate it.

---
(1) In copy (e) it appears as *(shara'a)*.
(2) In version (5) it appears as *(Haram)*.

[115]

<!-- page 114 -->

About this, the Almighty said:

> "And when Ibrahim was raising the foundations of the House, and Ishmael."

The inner foundations raised here are the four pronouncements after them — namely Moses and Jesus, son of Isaac; and Muhammad and the Qa'im — these last being from the lineage of Ishmael. These four foundations are like the four limits, that is, the four pronouncements which come after them. They cut them off with a stone resting on two of its knees — and this is a sign of the interruption of prophecy from the line of Isaac after Moses and Jesus (peace be upon them), and of its continuation in the line of Ishmael. For the circumambulation, in Islam, occurs at two corners of the House which represent Muhammad and the Qa'im (may God's blessings be upon them); the other two corners, representing Moses and Jesus (may God's blessings be upon them), are not approached, not sought, not drawn near, nor circumambulated around. Rather, one circumambulates from behind the stone that was attached to them, and the two sects are kept from them and from touching them — because their command is interrupted. Circumambulation of the House remains for those whose law continues from the line of Ishmael — he who made the House an example for himself in its beginning, and for each successor (ayata) one by one after him.

He made for the House a single door for the foundation — which is the *wasiyy*, that is, the Imam — who made the House an example for himself. Around it, twelve foundations like him: the twelve captains (*nuqaba*) who are known to the Imam, each by name. They are distributors in the twelve regions, just as the inside is entered from door to door. The circumambulation around it is seven rounds, just like the *sa'i* between al-Safa and al-Marwah; this is a parable for the seven pronouncements — the seven Imams. The stone set in the corner is like the hand of the speaker, and receiving it is like shaking hands with the one who pledges allegiance to him. For this reason it came in the hadith:

> "The stone is the right hand of God Almighty. And when God took the covenant upon the children of Adam, He commanded the stone, and it picked it up. Therefore the one who receives the stone says: 'O God, I have fulfilled my trust, and made my covenant with him, that you may bear witness to me about the report.'"

After circumambulation of the House, he was commanded [p. 116]

<!-- page 115 -->

to pray two rak'ahs, which are a parable for obedience to the forerunner (*sabiq*) and the proof (*hujja*). The prayer is performed behind the station (*maqam*) — placed within the worshipper's reach — and it is not permitted to pray between the worshipper and the House. This is like the rule that one does not address the speaker except through his guardian; and the speaker does not accept the act of one who transgresses against him and rejects him, but only of one who obeys the speaker and turns toward him — because He, the Almighty, said:

> "Obey God, and obey the Messenger, and those in authority among you."

Then they were commanded to drink the water of Zamzam, and to enjoy it. This is a parable for receiving knowledge, preserving it, and seeking it. And al-Safa and al-Marwah are like the Imam and the proof. Likewise, circumambulation is like obedience to them and not going against their command — or else they part ways. The explanation of this will come in the rest of the rites of Hajj when that section is completed.

What we intended here was a notice about the House, because it gathers within itself all the principles of the Shari'ah and points to them — much as that ship gathered and bore witness; and likewise the testimony, according to what we mentioned at the time of mentioning it.

As we said: the appearance of the foundations is one thing, and their meaning is what they indicate and what they have been set as a likeness for. Whoever did not know its limits and its inner dimensions, and did not perform its rights, gains no benefit from knowledge of its appearance, and does not know the truth of what stands opposed to him. As it is narrated from 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, that he kissed the Black Stone and said:

> "By God, I know that you are a stone that neither harms nor benefits — but I saw the Messenger of God doing such a thing, and so I did it."

And the Almighty said:

> "We covenanted with Ibrahim and Ishmael: 'Purify My House for the two parties.'"

That is, the purity of the name of the Haram from every impurity. "For the sects" — meaning: the followers, that is,

---
(2) In copy (e) it is mentioned as *the appellants* (or *those who respond*).
(1) In version (e) it is mentioned as *(they are angry)*.

[117]

<!-- page 116 -->

the twelve companions of the regions, who are the sects (1) [arranged] around the Imam in the regions, just as the twelve doors of the mosque surrounded the House on every side, as we have mentioned. "And those in retreat" (*al-'akifin*) are the Imams who are the companions remaining in attendance. "And those who bow" — the foundations. "And those who prostrate" — the pronouncements. "He gave the people permission to perform Hajj" — calling them to respond.

Among what God Almighty mentioned of Ibrahim's (peace be upon him) command is His saying:

> "When he said to his father: 'O my father, why do you worship that which does not hear, does not see, and avails you of nothing?'"

Here, "When he said, 'O father,'" refers to the one from whom he had taken the knowledge of the outward — and the scholars of the outward are attributed to one's birth before the apparent. When Ibrahim came to the limit of the inner and he (his father) did not rise to it, Ibrahim called him to it. He addressed the one who had raised him up by the outward, urging him to enter into what he himself had entered into, saying:

> "O my father, why do you worship that which does not hear, does not see, and is of no use to you?"

That is: those from whom you have taken that apparent knowledge — as God says:

> "How [foolish are these idols]…"

And he said:

> "O my father, knowledge has come to me that has not come to you. So follow me, and I will guide you to a straight path."

That is, what has reached me from the stored spiritual knowledge.

> "So that I might bestow upon you my gift…"

[p. 118]

<!-- page 117 -->

That is: I will tell you about the Imam of your time, and he is the straight path.

And he said:

> "O my father, do not worship the Devil, for Satan was disobedient to the All-Merciful."

That is: do not obey, besides the master of the time, the one who disobeyed his Creator regarding what He had commanded him.

And he said:

> "O my father, I fear that a punishment from the All-Merciful will touch you, and you will become a friend of the Devil."

That is: that you will become like him in your loyalty to him.

And his (father's) saying:

> "Are you renouncing my gods, O Ibrahim?"

means: my apparent superiors and my predecessors from whom I have taken my knowledge.

> "If you do not desist, I will surely stone you. So leave me for a long while."

He says: "If you do not turn back from what you are upon, I will throw you out in disgrace, and you will be removed far from me."

> "Peace be upon you. I will ask forgiveness for you from my Lord."

That is, Ibrahim prayed for him to pay [his debt], and said: "I will ask forgiveness for you from my Lord" — i.e., I will summon him to ask Him for His favors over you.

And He said:

> "And we granted Ibrahim guidance before, and we were aware of him."

That is: We came to him to support him with the word from Us, and We taught him what he was going to do.

The Almighty also said:

> "When he said to his father..."

This means the one who had taught him the knowledge of the outward, as we have mentioned. As for the fathers in the realm of pronouncement,

[119]

<!-- page 118 -->

they are not of the same kind. The Messenger of God (peace and blessings be upon him) said:

> "The bonds of kinship and the generosity of piety…"

And the Almighty said:

> "Truly the most honored of you in the sight of God is the most God-fearing of you."

The God-fearing are the sincere believers. So Ibrahim said to his father, who had taught him the knowledge of the outward — as we have already explained, because fatherhood in the inner sense applies to both the believer and the disbeliever — and he said to his father, the latter, and to his people and the people of his region from the outward:

> "What are these statues to which you are devoted?"

That is, those who have set themselves up and imitated the people of truth, but are not among its people.

> "They said: 'We found our fathers worshipping them.'"

That is, they say: our fathers understood it this way.

> "He said: 'Have you and your fathers, then, been in clear error? Did you bring us the truth, or are you one of the players?'"

They mean: have you brought us the truth in what you say, or is what you say untrue?

> "He said: 'Nay, your Lord is the Lord of the heavens and the earth who originated them.'"

This is one of the two hadiths.

That is: He is the Creator of the outward and the inward.

> "And those who call besides Him do not possess anything, while they are empty."

That is, their inability to know the pillars and the limits of religion.

> "By God, I will plot against your idols after you have turned your backs."

He says: if you depart from the truth, I will show you how to break your idols — I mean, the people of [p. 120]

<!-- page 119 -->

falsehood, which are taken away from those who may be the most important of them under the pretext of truth.

> "So He made them fragments."

That is: when he debated with them and the argument was established against them, he divided them and scattered them.

> "Except for the largest of them, that they might return to him."

That is, their leader. He did not debate with him, but left him so that they might return to him; he broke the rest, knowing that they would understand that the leader had nothing — for, as he said, this is what the followers do above him. When they heard that the chief among them had argued against them more than the rest, most of them did not know who had done that with them.

> "They said: 'Whoever did this to our gods is surely among the wrongdoers.'"

They mean by paying their due — they claim that the oldest of them are right-owners, those whose word is heeded among them.

> "They said: 'We heard a young man speaking of them, called Ibrahim.'"

The "young man" in the interpretation is the candidate who is ready for the Imamate.

> "They said: 'Bring him before the eyes of the people, that they may bear witness.'"

So they brought him with them so that he could hear what he had to say, and they said:

> "Was it you who did this to our gods, O Ibrahim?"

> "He said: 'Rather, the greatest of them did it. So ask them, if they can speak.'"

That is: when Ibrahim came, he was asked publicly, "Was it you who broke our gods?" By his arguments, their Lord was impoverished, and he said to them: "Rather, the greatest of them."

[121]

<!-- page 120 -->

> "So ask them, if they can speak." (1)

That is: ask them whether they have an argument. When they saw that their superiors had none — that the greatest of them had no argument they could deploy (2) against the argument of Ibrahim —

> "So they returned to themselves."

That is, they returned to their elders, from whom they used to take instruction, and said to them when they saw their disconnection from any argument:

> "You are the wrongdoers."

That is, by placing the matter outside its proper place.

> "Then they reverted to their old confusion: 'You know that these do not speak.'"

He says: then they fell back upon their heads, reflecting on the breaking of their superiors' argument. And their hostility was directed at Ibrahim (peace be upon him).

He said:

> "Do you then worship, besides God, that which neither benefits you nor harms you? Fie upon you, and upon what you worship besides God! Will you not understand?"

That is: do you obey, besides God, those who declare lawful and forbid by their own opinion — declaring lawful and forbidding so as to be followed? We have mentioned this elsewhere.

The Messenger of God (peace be upon him) said to 'Adi ibn Hatim, who had been among the Arabs upon a religion and then accepted Islam — when he heard the words of God Almighty:

> "They took their rabbis and monks as lords besides God."

'Adi said: "We did not worship them, O Messenger of God."

---
(1) It was given in copy (X) as *(they listen)*. (2) In copy (S) it is mentioned as *(laughing)*.

1220.


<!-- page 121 -->
They would declare lawful for you, and you would accept what they made permissible. They would declare unlawful for you, and you would accept what they forbade. He said: Yes. He said: That is your worship of them.

And the words of the Almighty:
"They said: Burn him and stand by your gods, if you are going to do anything."

That is, their consensus was to raise his case to the authority of their patrons, to ensnare him, and to inflame them against him. This is a permissible usage in Arabic, as people say: "So-and-so burned so-and-so to the Sultan" — meaning he denounced him to him, so that his chest was inflamed against him and he became enraged at him.

"We said: O fire, be coolness and peace upon Ibrahim."

That is, the Almighty rendered their machinations and the authority they had wielded cold in his heart, so his heart was not enraged by them, nor did he grow angry at them. Rather, he looked upon him, and what he withheld from him was as follows. Allah described this when He said:

"Have you not considered the one who argued with Ibrahim about his Lord, because Allah had granted him kingship?"

Ibrahim (peace be upon him) said:

"My Lord is the One who gives life and causes death."

The king said: "I give life and cause death" — that is, "I pardon those who deserve to be killed, and I spare him, and I kill whomever I wish to kill." This is what he said outwardly. He also claimed inwardly the truth of his knowledge — that he protected from death those whom he had brought into being, and that he hastened to the death of one he wished. He broke him, plunged him into doubt and confusion, and brought him out from it, so that he would thereby die.

Ibrahim said:

"Allah brings the sun from the east, so bring it from the west."

p. 123.

<!-- page 122 -->
By "the sun" he meant the word of God, which He caused to appear from the Speaker (al-Nāṭiq) of that time. He made its setting in essence: if you are the master of the word, then another shall benefit from it.

"So the one who disbelieved" — meaning the one who was cut off and confined — "was confounded."

"And Allah does not guide the unjust people."

That is, the unjust one is he who puts a thing out of its proper place; we have already explained this earlier. Likewise, this king laid claim to what was not his and placed himself in a station that was not his — so Allah did not guide him to his right course. This is what Ibrahim (peace be upon him) said about him.

"I am going to my Lord; He will guide me."

That is, his acceptance of him with his heart and his innermost being.

"My Lord, grant me from among the righteous."

He says: O Lord, grant me first loyal respondents. "So We gave him glad tidings of a forbearing boy."

We have mentioned that the boy is the candidate for the Imamate, and that he is prepared [1] to receive the Word — and that is Ishmael (peace be upon him). "Then when he reached [the age of] striving with him" means what he sought through education.

He said: "O my son, I see in a dream that I am sacrificing you."

That is, "I shall take from you the covenant of the Imamate, and raise you up as an Imam of my Shariʿah."

"So look — what do you see?" He confirmed it to him because he knew the weight of this matter and the severity of its gravity, as we mentioned above.

[1] In copy (M) it reads "and the beneficiary."

p. 124.

<!-- page 123 -->
He said: "O my father, do as you are commanded; you will find me, if Allah wills, among the patient ones." That is, of those who bear the burdens of kingship.

"And when they had both submitted" — meaning that they both surrendered: Ibrahim by handing over the command, and Ishmael by receiving it from him and enduring it.

"And he laid him down upon his forehead" — that is, he laid him low and brought him down to the rank of acceptance from him, and Ishmael submitted to him.

"And We called out to him: O Ibrahim, you have fulfilled the vision."

That is, We made him aware of the revelation — meaning he believed in our command and submitted to him.

"Thus do We reward those who do good."

Meaning the reward for one who is best in acceptance and performance, with such dignity.

Slaughter in the esoteric sense is like taking the covenant, because slaughter brings about death — which is the stilling of bodily movements. The distinction with Ishmael was to the point of interpretation and concealment: to perform the call of the esoteric, to set its boundaries, and to maintain silence upon it. Introduction, exposition, and disputation are outward — and for that purpose Isaac (peace be upon him) was raised up, not him. Ishmael was at the foundational limit [1], and Isaac was below him at the limit of the Imamate [2]. This is the saying of Allah Almighty:

"And We ransomed him with a great sacrifice."

Outwardly, this is a ransom of a ram. The Arabs call the chief of a people who shelters them a "ram" — so-and-so is "the ram of his people." Slaughter in the esoteric, as we said, is the taking of the covenant — taken upon the Prophets, the Foundations (al-Asās), and the Imams when they are qualified for it.

[1] In copy (X) it reads "the limit of (al-Asāsiyya)."
[2] In copy (S) it reads "the front cheek."

125

<!-- page 124 -->
It is also taken from the respondents, that they may receive the limit of those above them. The Prophet and the Foundation are not taken to anything that has been given to them so that the covenant might be taken upon them in that regard. Nor does the Imam open up to the respondents the taking of the covenant upon them, until the Prophet, the Foundation, and the Imam have risen to their limits and worked their bodies in fulfillment of the oath. Their bodies then conquer the power of support, and they look out from kingship onto how small the world is and what is within it. Ishmael was lost — crushed and advanced to the rank of the Foundations — while the people of truth stood below him in the front rank. To them Ishmael called, and he answered and submitted to the command of Allah, and was patient with him in the universal matter without a degree. So Allah ransomed him for that with his patience and his submission to His command, and raised him to the rank of the Foundations, and honored him with prophethood and message — as in the saying of the Almighty:

"And mention in the Book Ishmael. Indeed, he was true to his promise, and he was a messenger and a prophet. And he used to enjoin upon his family prayer and zakat, and his Lord was well-pleased with him."

And He said:

"And when Ibrahim said: My Lord, show me how You give life to the dead. He said: Have you not believed? He said: Yes, but to satisfy my heart. He said: Then take four birds, and incline them to you, then put on each mountain a portion of them, then call them; they will come to you in haste. And know that Allah is Mighty, Wise."

In this case there are two interpretations, the first and the other. The first interpretation is that Ibrahim (peace be upon him) asked, at the start of his command, how to summon the respondents

p. 126.

<!-- page 125 -->
to the call from the death of ignorance, ignorance, and misguidance. The "vision" here is the gift and bestowal, like the saying of Moses (peace be upon him):

"My Lord, show me — that I may look at You."

That is, "Grant it to me and be kind to me." Ibrahim asked for elevation to the rank of the proof (al-ḥujja) without it, and Allah Almighty had already promised to raise him in rank before him in His saying:

"I have made you an Imam."

So this was done for him in fulfillment of the promise. It was said to him: "Have you not believed?" — that is, do you not believe in the promise, as Allah Almighty has related concerning the brothers of Yusuf (Joseph), when they said to their father:

"And you are not a believer in us."

That is, "Yes — be truthful with us, even though we are truthful."

He said: "Yes — but in order to satisfy me, tell me what this is attached to."

He said: "Four birds."

That is, "Baptize four of the authorized ones [1] through introduction (taqdīm), so that they may be yours, and teach them the limits of the captains (al-naqā'ib), and undertake yourself to open them up and educate them. If you do this and complete their order, then command each of them to extract for himself as you extracted for yourself — namely two men — and after you raise them to the limits of the captains, they will become twelve, like the twelve months of the year, of which four are sacred":

"That is the right religion."

The Sunnah of Allah has flowed in His friends.

[1] In copy (e) it reads "(al-maʾdhūn)."

p. 127.

<!-- page 126 -->
"Then place on each mountain a portion of them."

That is, place the most beautiful of them on every island of the earth — one of them, exalted by what supports him of the truth upon his mountain — for he is the one who overcomes upon it.

"Then call them; they will come to you in haste."

That is, they will come to you obedient, along with all who are upon it. "And know that Allah is Mighty, Wise."

So the call of Ibrahim (peace be upon him) spread across the diameters of the earth, and every nation acknowledged the Almighty, and acknowledged the prophet of His mercy and answered his call.

And the second interpretation said:

"Show me how You give life to the dead."

"Show me how a servant of yours rises to the rank of support (taʾyīd)."

"Have you not believed?"

That is, did not what happened to you of that happen, and did you not believe [1] it.

"He said: Yes."

"I believed him and knew him — but to satisfy my heart."

That is, "If it is from one below me, and I encompass it with him, my heart will be reassured."

He said: "Four birds."

That is, "I shall baptize four of those who are permitted to open the door — so they may be sent to you." That is, gather them to yourself by opening and nurturing; then when you have finished with them, cut them off — by breaking what you have gathered with them in exposition.

"And place on each mountain a portion of them."

[1] In copy (e) it reads "(and ratified)."

p. 128.

<!-- page 127 -->
That is, add your breaking — what you have broken against them — to your successors, one by one.

"Then call them; they will come to you in haste."

That is, if you do that, and you invite them to support you, you will see that support has appeared upon all those whom you struck with it in his heart — as though they had heard no breaking, no cutting, nor anything of that. They will answer you in haste. And when you see that, know that "Allah is Mighty, Wise" — Mighty in what He has created, and Wise in what He has wisely arranged.

And among those whom Allah mentioned in His book who were in the cycle of Ibrahim, Ishmael, and Isaac — and whose station we have mentioned, along with the words of the Almighty concerning Ishmael that he was true to the promise — is Lot (peace be upon him). He was one of the captains of Ibrahim (peace be upon him).

The story of Lot.

Lot was one of the captains (Ḥujaj) of Ibrahim (al-Maqām) on an island, where he taught many of its people. Then corruption crept upon them, and they altered the ranks of the limits that I had set, and overran the degrees that had been appointed within them. Some of them took some others into the form of interpretation and subtlety, and they broke one upon another. So Lot forbade them from this, and commanded them to adhere to their preachers, to take from them, and to conceal the knowledge of the esoteric. But they did not do as they were commanded — they broke the covering, broke the covenant, and acted on the outward course. They planted it in a place where they were born, and they abandoned their wives — those whom Allah Almighty had commanded them to take inwardly and outwardly. They were content with one another in both the outward and the subtle. This is the saying of Lot:

p. 129.
9

<!-- page 128 -->
"Do you approach the males among the worlds, and leave what your Lord has created for you of your wives? Indeed, you are a transgressing people."

That is, those who respond to the outward of the call who are prepared for acceptance.

"They said: If you do not desist, O Lot, you will surely be among those expelled."

That is, "Let us banish you from adding the invitation to you." And when they outnumbered Lot in their sermon:

"They said: Expel the family of Lot from your town; indeed, they are a people who keep themselves pure."

That is, "Who preserve the limits of the call."

The "village" here is the call, by drawing them in. They added it to themselves and made it possible for themselves. This is, from the outward, the incest which is its esoteric — that they marry one another and enter into them. They have the proof of Lot, whose wife Allah Almighty has called [his wife].

So Allah Almighty sent the angels of their destruction, destroyed them, and confined them in Tyre. The people passed by Ibrahim, and they were commanded to bring him glad tidings of Isaac and Jacob.

Allah Almighty said:

"And Our messengers came to Ibrahim with glad tidings. They said: Peace. He said: Peace. And it was not long before he came with a roasted calf."

That is, they opened to him in truth, but they gave the impression that they were from some of the respondents. So he opened to them and brought them down, in accordance with what he used to do for those whom he had permitted in the pilgrimage (Ḥajj). They had given the impression that they were among those who came for that purpose, so he slaughtered a calf for them [1] and took it, that is,

[1] In copy (e) it reads "a calf."

130

<!-- page 129 -->
he was disgraced and accused over it — but they did not extend their hands toward it. When he saw them thus, he denied them, as the Almighty said:

"And he sensed fear from them. They said: Do not fear; we have been sent to the people of Lot."

The calf, in the esoteric, corresponds to the power of opening. So he brought it to him to open them — in accordance with what he used to do for those who came to him. When they did not enter into discourse with him over it, he denied them. So they revealed to him what they had been commanded with.

"And his wife was standing, and she laughed, so We gave her glad tidings of Isaac, and after Isaac — Jacob."

His wife is the Foundation (al-Asās) with him; she was upright in what she was commanded with, and they received it from her. She caught [1] of that council and what passed in it between Ibrahim and the angels. So she became strong, and her power appeared in her, and the angels understood what had affected her. So they gave her glad tidings [2] of exaltation and elevation — and this is what we have mentioned, concerning her being transferred from the limit of the Imamate to the limit of the Foundation. They gave her glad tidings of Isaac, and that he had been ransomed for him, and they told her that Jacob would come after Isaac.

She said: "O woe to me! Shall I bear a child while I am an old woman, and this husband of mine is an old man? Indeed, this is a strange thing."

That is, "When the Speaker (al-Nāṭiq) was supporting me, helping me to labor and exert myself in the call, and I was eager to make myself acceptable to the people — he did not answer me. Today, when he holds onto me and my support has reached its limit, I have reached where I am."

[1] In copy (e) it reads "(luck)." [2] In copy (x) it reads "(and they began it)."

131


I responded, yet I was unable to receive what I was once able to answer — and now I am to have the boy.

They said, "Are you amazed at the decree of Allah? May the mercy of Allah and His blessings be upon you, people of the house — He is praiseworthy and glorious."

When the fear had passed from Ibrahim, and the good news of Ishaq and Ya'qub had reached him, he turned to what concerned him:

(They argued with Us concerning the people of Lut.)

That is, he questioned Him about the people of Lut, interceding on their behalf.

(And Our messengers came to Ibrahim with the good news. They said, "We are about to destroy the people of this town." This is a town whose people were unjust. He said, "But Lut is in it." They said, "We know best who is in it. We shall surely save him and his family, except his wife, who is to be of those who remain behind.")

By "his family" they mean those whose argument is his — they are spared with the spared, while his wife is among those upon whom the punishment will fall.

When the messengers reached the call of Lut and went in to him, his people saw them and rushed toward him. As He said:

(And his people came to him in haste.)

Yes — they hurried toward him.

(For they had long been practicing wickedness.)

They imagined that the visitors were among the seekers who had not yet entered upon their entrance, and they imagined that Lut himself was one of those seekers who had not yet entered upon their entrance. So they came to confront them. Lut feared that his people would tempt them and turn them away from him to what they themselves were upon, and so he rose to defend those who had come.

(He said, "O my people, these are my daughters.")
