That is, if you would follow them, they speak to you and address you with what you seek, and they are purer for you — if it is permissible for you to approach them; but it is not permissible to approach these guests of mine.

(So fear Allah, and do not shame me before my guests. Is there not among you one upright man?)

That is, you have learned what is upright concerning my daughters, and that you will obtain more by them. (They said, "You know we have no claim on your daughters, and you know well what we want.") — that is, what we want is to repel these to what we ourselves are upon.

(He said, "If only I had strength against you, or could take refuge in a strong support.")

He says: if only I could repel you; otherwise I take refuge in the speaker-prophet (peace be upon him).

Then the angels revealed their command.

(They said, "O Lut, we are the messengers of your Lord. They shall never reach you. So set out with your family in a portion of the night, and let none of you turn back.")

He says: depart (1) with the people of your call who have responded to you and have not changed — those who do not alter the boundaries of knowledge or the houses of explanation. He said, "in a portion of the night," meaning whoever remains of your followers, the people of the covering, who did not enter the entrance of these. "And let none of you turn back" — meaning to what was apparent to him before he entered into the truth. "Except your wife" — meaning your lining, the place of your secret, from among your suffixes; those with whom he had entered will be punished by the retribution that falls upon them for aiding them.

(Their appointed time is the morning. Is not the morning near?)

It means the manifest appearance of a speaking matter to which you are connected.

(When Our command came.)

He says: when Our matter appeared from the side of the speaker-prophet, who is Ibrahim — (We turned its upside down) — He says: We lowered the rank of the one who was uppermost in the call to its bottom, which is the apparent.

(And We rained upon them stones of baked clay in succession.)

That is, We struck them with weighty matters; through the speaker-prophet I drove them with the true subconscious before their outward destruction, lest they leave this world unveiled.

This is what befell those whose destruction was decreed: Allah destroyed them with manifest punishment outwardly, and inwardly as well, since they had deceived in both the outward and the inward. So things are completed only in their perfection: if a thing is in the inward without the outward, or in the outward without the inward, it does not stand whole. In truth, nothing is brought to completion except by its outward and its inward, and nothing exists but as inward and outward.

(1) In version (e): "go."
(2) In version (8): "non-observed people."

The Story of Yusuf and Ya'qub

Yusuf (peace be upon him) is the son of Ya'qub ibn Ishaq ibn Ibrahim al-Khalil — upon them all be prayers and peace. The Imamate ended with his father Ya'qub, and Ya'qub established his manifest call. He then (1) appointed his followers, and the people of Yusuf (peace be upon him) for his position, and his brother — to summon those of the suffixes. When Yusuf reached the boundary appointed for him, he was called by way of imagination from the support of God Almighty, so that he saw that the Imamate would pass to him, and that the Imam and his argument and his followers would submit to him and come under his authority. He was commanded to convey it to his father, and he mentioned it to Ya'qub, who said: (2)

"My father, I have seen eleven planets and the sun and the moon — I saw them prostrating before me."

Ya'qub knew that this would come to pass, and he commanded him to keep it secret from his brothers. He said:

"O my son, do not relate your vision to your brothers, lest they devise a scheme against you. Indeed Satan is a manifest enemy to man. And thus your Lord will choose you, and teach you the interpretation of narratives."

By "the interpretation" he means the interpretation of the Books that have been revealed; hence the words of the Almighty:

(1) In version (e): "I am afraid."
(2) In version (e): "he speaks."

"Allah has sent down the best of narratives — a Book whose parts resemble one another."

The interpretation of the news of the messengers and their words, which is also a narrative:

"And He will complete His favor upon you and upon the family of Ya'qub, just as He completed it before upon your forefathers Ibrahim and Ishaq. Indeed your Lord is Knowing, Wise."

Ya'qub's love for Yusuf intensified, and this affected his brothers, since they knew that the imagining of endorsement had called him, and that he would become what had been mentioned. Yusuf's brothers knew of Ya'qub's inclination toward him, and toward the brother who shared Ya'qub's followers; and the ten of them gathered and said:

"Yusuf and his brother are dearer to our father than we are, while we are a band. Surely our father is in clear error."

By "father" they mean the father of the Imamate. They meant that he had strayed from the path of the Imams in wanting Yusuf and his brother — who are the youngest of them, and the lowest in knowledge in what they have seen — to be raised, while they themselves had seen even more than him. So they envied him.

They said: "Kill Yusuf" — that is, throw him into a matter after which there would be no support left for him, and from which he would not be fit for what Ya'qub had given him — "or cast him out into some land" — that is, hand him over to one of the people's wrongdoers, who would corrupt him — "so that your father's face may be free for you, and you may be a righteous people thereafter." That is, they will describe to you the support of your father, and you will repent of this event later, and set yourselves right.

(One of them said: "Do not kill Yusuf.")

It is as if he found the matter excessive, because killing him meant cutting off the support, and that corrupts the offspring magnified for its sake. Rather —

("Throw him into the bottom of the well; some of the travelers will pick him up — if you must do something.")

What you have agreed upon. He says: hand him over to the leaders of the people of the outward, so that he will be kept from what you would throw him into, and you will not spoil the science upon him; and your words will be picked up by some of the various people of the outward who come to Ya'qub when they wish to go out to their region.

They said, "O our father, why do you not trust us with Yusuf, when we are sincere advisers to him?" — that is, we educate him and raise him up so that he may have a call. "Send him with us tomorrow that he may enjoy himself and play" — that is, that he may go out with his family upon the apparent. "And surely we will guard him" — that is, we will protect him from being humiliated by anything. Ya'qub said:

"It saddens me that you should take him away, and I fear that the wolf may eat him while you are heedless of him."

That is, you may overlook him as you draw close to him, since he is a newcomer; and the enslaved hearing — the fraudster — is one of the people of the outward, by some of what he has.

They said: "If the wolf were to eat him while we are a band, then surely we would be the losers." That is, if the deceiver reached him in that way, we would lose what we had wanted to set right.

But we wanted to train him, and for people to come to know him, and to know the realities of what they have and what they are. So Ya'qub gave them permission for that, and released him into the call, with permission. (1) That breaks the people of the apparent.

When they had set out with him, and had agreed to put him in the bottom of the well, they went on with him; they turned away from Ya'qub, and agreed to throw him to one of the chiefs of the people of the apparent — being preoccupied with him so as to ward off what he had, and to overcome him by some strength of his apparent — until he would come to be in the absence (2) of the apparent and his passions.

(And We inspired in him: "You will surely inform them of this affair of theirs while they do not perceive.")

He says: it came to him by way of imagination that they had been supporting him with their cunning, and that he would yet appear to them and rebuke all of them for what they had done. They brought him to one of the apparent chiefs, a man whose knowledge had room in it, and they said to Yusuf: "Speak to this one so that you may win him over." They also said: "Here is a man to whom a matter and a divergence from the truth have attached themselves; perhaps you may gain his reward in his returning to what came before." Then they went away and left him, and returned to Ya'qub.

"And they came to their father at night, weeping."

That is, they come to him in secret to feign grief over Yusuf.

"They said, 'O our father, we went off racing one another and left Yusuf with our belongings, and the wolf devoured him.'"

That is, we left him behind with what we had entrusted of the statement, and the wolf ate it, so we neglected the slave — to hear what you had warned us about — and so he took what he had.

(1) In versions (S) and (i): "ward."
(2) In version (X): "backbiting."

"And you will not believe us, even though we are truthful."

— even though we may be lying.

That is, they differed about him concerning a matter in which there is doubt; and this is one of the parables Allah Almighty strikes for His servants. Whoever carries it on the surface is the one who pronounced it. How can it be right to believe that the wolf eats him, when the wolf does not in fact prey on him in such a way? If a wolf did so, he would not eat all of him; and if they reached his shirt, they would have reached the rest of his body. The argument was that they were obliged to make supplication for him concerning this, and yet they did not — they did not pray, with an excuse that does not stand for them.

Ya'qub said — because he knew what had befallen Yusuf by way of imagining support:

"Rather, your selves have enticed you to a matter. So patience is beautiful. And Allah is the One whose help is sought against what you describe."

Ya'qub trusted in what Yusuf had — that he would not do what they had thrown upon him. And Yusuf stood firm when the man broke him. (1)

(And a caravan came) — that is, people who differ in appearance — to that man who had Yusuf with him; they take from him and learn from him. So they sent to him their leader in speech, and he went to the man, and found Yusuf with him. (And he let down his bucket) — that is, he posed his questions — and Yusuf opened it for him. He was struck by a gift of acceptance, so the man clung to him and went with him to his companions, and their delight in him was without bound. (He said, "Good news! Here is a slave boy!") — that is, I give you good news: here is a man who is nominated and ready for the Imamate, and I have heard from him what I have never heard from anyone before him.

(1) In version (e): "kisses."

Yusuf met with them, and conquered them, and they admired him. (And they concealed him as merchandise.) That is, they collected what they had benefited from his knowledge according to what they had been commanded; they were among the people of Egypt. So they asked him who was going with them to it, and he was permitted to go wherever he wished, so he went with them. Then they saw the man who had Yusuf — (they were of those uninterested in him) — they had no need of him, and so they did not cling to him out of fear of him.

And when they were in Egypt — which was then the city of the Copts and held their kingdom, whose chief at that time commanded their religion — Yusuf had left the borders of the Levant, in which Ya'qub was as Imam. Yusuf kept his lineage secret, and stayed with the people who had come. He asked them about it, but they denied it; so he gave them dirhams, which they desired, and they showed him to him, and brought him to him. He opened him, and loved what he had in him, and added him to his argument — which is the one Allah names as his wife — which is the words of the Almighty:

"And they were of those uninterested.

And the one from Egypt who bought him said to his wife, 'Make his stay honorable; perhaps he may benefit us, or we may take him as a son.'"

He says: perhaps we may benefit from him — that is, from his knowledge — or take him as a son — that is, we shall spend on him what we have, so that we may have a child in religion, because of the goodness he has seen in his explanation and guidance. This is the good (1) by which Yusuf was described; the king's argument took him in for himself and made him near to him, admiring what he had and magnifying him. He honored him, strengthened his side, and strengthened his command. And this is the saying of Allah, the Almighty:

(1) In version (E): "Ilahs."

(And so We established Yusuf in the land, and that We might teach him the interpretation of narratives.)

That is, its benefit comes from the science of support.

(And Allah is predominant over His affair, but most of the people do not know.)

When he reached his full strength, He said: "He had reached the boundaries of support" — meaning that the support was connected to him.

(And thus We reward those who do good. And she in whose house he was sought to seduce him from himself.)

That is, she wanted from him what she had — which is the argument of the king who is qualified for his place — that he might inform her of the ruling of the truth, because she had seen it symbolized; but Yusuf had not yet been opened to that by the apparent which is supported by the true and subconscious science. When the support came to him, he made it symbolic and brought the one she had to himself, and it was taken from her. He assured her that he would not accept it from anyone but her, nor would she accept it from anyone else aware of it. And this is what He said:

(And she closed the doors and said, "Come, you!")

That is, accept what I call you to. Yusuf said:

(Allah is my refuge — He is my Lord, and He has made my stay good.)

— with the support they gave me.

(The wrongdoers do not succeed. And she truly resolved upon him, and he resolved upon her...)


<!-- page 140 -->
That is, he wished to approach her with the true knowledge, while the illusion was that he was about to cast himself at her.

(Had he not seen the proof of his Lord.)

That is, his support was that he put the wisdom outside of its proper place and beyond its scope.

This is the interpretation of what Allah Almighty has mentioned in the story of Yusuf.

As for what the people of the apparent (ahl al-zahir) attributed to him regarding the king's wife — apparently his wife — and that he was preoccupied with her and she with him, that is, frenzy had reached them and the station of the Whisperer (khannas) had taken its seat in it: Allah preserved His friends from such a thing through divine infallibility (`isma), because it is overt fornication. And He said:

(And they raced to the doors) — meaning that each of them wished to outrace the other to a door,

to the master of that place, to tell him what had happened between them.

(And she tore his shirt from the back)

He means that she made his way of life appear ugly behind his back and slandered it.

(And they found her master at the door)

He means the king who holds the command of the da'wah of the realm and the reins of his people's religion.

(She said: "What is the recompense for one who intended evil against your wife but that he be imprisoned or a painful punishment?")

He means: what is the recompense of one who approaches your hujjah by a way other than its proper face and method, except that he be silenced from the opening of the Qur'an, or be punished by its breaking and dismantling?

(He said: "She sought to seduce me.")

He means: she desired that I open [the inner meaning] to her.

p. 142.

<!-- page 141 -->
(And a witness from her family testified)

He means: one of the witnesses of truth from the people of the da'wah.

(If his shirt is torn from the front, then she has told the truth and he is of the liars)

He means: if what was thrown to him was from the knowledge of the inner (al-batin), then she was truthful in what was mentioned about him — that he opened to her and disclosed it to her with it. But if it was from the knowledge of the apparent, she lied, and he was of the truthful. This is what He said:

(And if his shirt is torn from the back, then she has lied and he is of the truthful.)

If he had opened to her inwardly, she would have made it apparent and slandered it.

(So when he saw his shirt torn from the back)

That is, what I have mentioned concerning him is from apparent knowledge.

(He said: "Indeed, it is of your women's plan; indeed your plan is great.")

Yes, this is a scheme on your part, and it is great. And he said to Yusuf:

(Yusuf, ignore this)

He means: turn away from concealment(1) and reveal your command, and spread your da'wah. And he said to its mistress: (And ask forgiveness for your sin) — meaning, for what you sought of him when you tried, by commanding him, to bear the hatred upon him.

(And women in the city said)

He means: those authorized in the da'wah.

(1) Copy (X) reads (and reveal).

p. 143.

<!-- page 142 -->
(The wife of al-Aziz is seeking to seduce her servant; he has impassioned her with love. Indeed, we see her in clear error.)

They mean: the hujjah of al-Aziz of Egypt has called upon us, and we are what we are, and he has come from preparation and risen up as an imam to call to what he is and to lay claim to our da'wah. He is in clear error.

(So when she heard of their scheming, she sent for them)

He means: when she heard what they all said about her, she sent for them. (And prepared for them a banquet) — that is, she set up an assembly for opening and study.

(And gave each of them a knife)

That is, she gave each one a decisive argument with which she could prevail over those who held [theirs].

(She said: "Come out before them.")

He means: to Yusuf — bring forth what you have for them.

That is, when he cast to them some of what he had, they confirmed his command. (And they cut their hands) — that is, their hearts turned away from their [former] guardians and from what they had been holding to; he overcame them with it.

(And they said: "God forbid! What is this human being?")

They mean: what is this — is it the speech of a corporeal human being? This is nothing but the words of the spiritual angels (al-mala'ika al-ruhaniyyin).

p. 144.

<!-- page 143 -->
(She said: "That is the one about whom you blamed me. I certainly sought to seduce him, but he firmly refused.")

If he does not do what I command him to do, (Let them be among those debased).

He means: if he does not reveal what he has, I will cut him off from the opening, and I will bring him down(1) from his rank.

(He said: "My Lord, prison is dearer to me than that to which they invite me.")

That is, being cut off from the opening is preferable to me — I would rather bear that than release [it to] those for whom it should not be released, except by the prescribed limits.

((And if You do not avert from me their scheme, I might incline toward them))

That is, [the scheme] by which they have tried to deceive me.

(And [I might] be of the ignorant.) So his Lord responded to him and averted from him their plan.

That is, [from] whoever would have him do what he should not, and his infallibility from that.

((Then it appeared to them, after they had seen the signs, that they should imprison him for a time))

He says: it seemed to them, and to their companions, to cut him off from the opening and to bar him from it for a time, while they looked into his matter — since his story had become common among the people and they feared that he would overcome them and silence them after his signs had appeared to them and they had recognized his veracity. And two men who had answered his summons dwelt with him, [as] her people had been to be

(1) Copy (e) reads (the drops).

145

10

<!-- page 144 -->
some of the causes of that, as what the Almighty said.

(And there entered the prison with him two young men. One of them said: "I see myself

pressing wine.")

He means: I see myself [engaged] in the interpretation of the apparent and its spreading.

The other said: "I see myself carrying bread on my head, from which

the birds eat."

He means: I see myself fashioning a noble way of life for my guardian and publicizing it,

in what is a key to the locks — I mean, from the symbols and signs in the inner interpretation (ta'wil).

((Inform us of its interpretation; indeed we see you to be of those who do good.) He said to them: "No food

will be brought to you as your provision unless I inform you of its interpretation before it comes to you.")

He means: no matter will come to you and you will not gain any share of it unless you know of it

before you come upon it.

(That is from what my Lord has taught me. Indeed, I have left the religion of a people who do not believe

in Allah and who are disbelievers in the Hereafter. And I have followed the religion of my fathers — Ibrahim,

Ishaq, and Yaqub. It was not for us to associate anything with Allah. That is from the favor of

Allah upon us and upon the people, but most of the people do not give

thanks.)

So he disclosed to them his command, made known to them his lineage, and informed them that the one who possessed what he possessed of

knowledge had received it from his teacher with wisdom, and he opened for them some of the secrets.

p. 146.

<!-- page 145 -->
Then he said to them: ("O my two companions of the prison") — i.e., my two companions of the secret and concealment.

((Are diverse lords better, or Allah, the One, the Subduer?))

He means: are imams who are scattered and disagreeing — meaning the people of the apparent — better, or one imam

who carries out the command of Allah, in whose speech there is no contradiction, who is the one of his time, who commands

by the command of Allah, the One, the Subduer?

(You do not worship besides Him except names which you have named — you and your fathers — for which Allah

has sent down no authority.)

He means: "You have followed only a people whom you and your scholars have set up with your own opinions, granting

permissibility to what was forbidden to you, and you have obeyed them in that, and so you have worshiped them apart from Allah." [As in]

the words of Allah Almighty:

(They have taken their rabbis and their monks as lords besides Allah.)

And as the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said when it was said to him, "We did not worship them, O Messenger of Allah," —

by the one who said this, ʿAdi ibn Hatim — the Prophet said to him: "No, were they not

making lawful for you what was forbidden and forbidding for you what was lawful, and you took that from them?"

(Legislation is for none but Allah; He has commanded that you worship none but Him. That is the right religion,

but most of the people do not know.) So he absolved himself from [the authority of] release and seizure by what

he had affirmed against them.

Then he said:

((O my two companions of the prison))

That is, my two companions of the secret and concealment. ((As for one of you)) — that is, the one of whom he said:

p. 147.

<!-- page 146 -->
("I see myself pressing wine,")

(He will serve wine to his lord) — that is, from his close support, and the master of his secret(1).

(And the other will be crucified, and the birds will eat from his head.)

[He means] the inner knowledge of it, and he passes it on to those who are below him.

He means: he is an honored da'i, and the ma'dhun receives from him the knowledge of the chief.

((The matter has been decreed about which you both inquire.))

This matter has been decreed for the two of you, I have ordained it, and you are appointed to it.

And he said to the one of them whom he thought would be saved, "Remember me before your lord" —

that is, with his companion who would accompany him. ((But Satan made him forget)) — that is, he made him forget

the wish that had overtaken him to mention [him] to his lord, so he remained in prison

— that is, in concealment and secrecy — (several years). They said four, and they said nine.

And this corresponds to the nine hudud, [of which] four taken together — he says one, two, three,

four — these words combined add up to nine in number; this has been mentioned in full in its place.

(And the king said: "I see [in a dream] seven fat cows being eaten by seven

lean ones, and seven green ears [of corn], and others dry.

O notables, explain to me my vision, if you can interpret a vision.")

The king who ruled Egypt at that time — consider what Yusuf

(peace be upon him) cast to him, of the symbols of(2) wisdom. So he gathered the people of his retinue and his own, and said:

(1) Copy (e) reads (his sira). (2) Copy (S) reads (al-mazamir / Psalms).

148

<!-- page 147 -->
They said: I see such and such — which is what he mentioned about the matter of the fat cows.

They mean: the hujjahs of the speaker-prophet (al-natiq). ("Eaten by seven lean ones") —

he means the hujjahs of the imams who are to be taught of them, so that the fat [of the hujjahs]

belongs to the natiq. "And seven green ears" — meaning the seven imams, who are green

by [their] confirmation and clarification, unlike others who are cut off in their cessation.

("O notables, explain to me my vision, if you can interpret a vision.")

He means: if you have knowledge of interpretation, tell me of it — this was a question of testing.

It was not a question seeking benefit, because he wanted to silence them through their inability,

and to establish for them the proof from Yusuf (peace be upon him) against whoever denied his command,

when he wished to launch his da'wah and enter into his affair.

(They said: "Confused dreams, and we are not learned in the interpretation of dreams.")

They mean: this is a confusion of what we say, and we know neither its interpretation nor its meaning.

(And said the one who had been saved of the two)

He means: from the two men who were attached to Yusuf, (and remembered after a period) — i.e., after a time.

((I will inform you of its interpretation, so send me [to him].))

That is, to Yusuf. And the king sent him to bring it to them, and asked him to clarify what

he had — and it is said that he is the one who had it.

("Yusuf, O man of truth! Explain to us [the dream of] seven fat cows being eaten by seven

lean ones, and seven green ears [of corn], and others dry, that I may return

149

<!-- page 148 -->
to the people, that they may know.")

(He said: "You will plant for seven years diligently.

Whatever you reap, leave it in its ear.")

The messenger came to him, and he answered him saying: the cause of these enumerated [seven] limits is that the speaker-prophets

are seven, and they established their seven foundations to plant wisdom in their cycles in the hearts

of those who answered them; and what they had reaped — that is, they had gathered its fruit — they kept for a time, but they did not

sow it to live eternal life with it.

((Except a little from which you will eat))

He means that what the foundations had bestowed upon the imams does not pass on to them, and there comes

after that seven strenuous ones (shidad), meaning the imams between each speaker-prophet and the next.

("They will consume what you saved for them.")

That is, that knowledge becomes theirs, and they impart it to their hujjahs.

((Except a little of what you store.))

Except for what the imams favor among the hujjahs in terms of knowledge — [knowledge] that does not reach them

concerning the cycles of the speaker-prophets, the cycles of the imams, how they are, and concerning knowledge — how

((Then will come after that a year in which the people will be given rain, and in which they will press))

he moves through them.

He means that there comes after these cycles the awaited existent (al-mawjud al-muntazar), who is the existent of the time,

the one who, with his time, abrogates all the religious traditions, and brings forth what is within them of subtle meanings and knowledge.

The real one is pressed as grapes, olives, and other grains are pressed, and he takes

what is hidden within them and casts away the husks. So Yusuf opened this to the messenger, who was the companion of

150

<!-- page 149 -->
the wine, whom he had promised to be raised to this maqam — and he released him(1) and granted him permission to open it(2).

So he came to the king and his companions and told them of it, and they heard from him what had never occurred to their hearts.

And [the king] sent for him to come to him and to meet with him, after he had spread his cause among his own people,

making them aware of his bounty, lest they should turn against him as they had done to his master before.

Yusuf said to the messenger:

("Return to your master and ask him: what is the case of the women who cut their hands?

Indeed, my Lord is Knowing of their plan.")

He wanted the king to corroborate his command among them, and to argue against them so that they would have

no further dispute about it afterwards. And he turned to them with that, and to the king. So the king cross-examined them,

and asked them what they wanted from him, saying:

(He said: "What was your condition when you sought to seduce Yusuf?"

They said: "Allah forbid! We know about him no evil.")

And the wife of al-Aziz said — that is, the [bearer] of his command and his hujjah, who was paired with Yusuf —

[she] said:

(Now the truth has become manifest. I sought to seduce him, and indeed he is of

the truthful.)

He means: he was truthful in what he said at that time.

("That is so he may know that I did not betray him in [his] absence, and that Allah does not guide the plan

of betrayers.")

(1) Copy (S) reads (and I saw it).

(2) Copy (e) reads (in al-fatiha).

151


<!-- page 150 -->

"Nor do I absolve myself; the soul indeed commands to evil, except those upon whom my Lord has mercy. My Lord is Forgiving, Merciful." And he said: give me a summary of its meaning for myself.

He says: I am ready for the deliverance of my soul, and I surrender all my affairs to Him, so He brings him forth.

The king said to him:

"Today you have a safe and established position."

Joseph spoke this to the king after he had trusted him and taken a covenant from him: be over what is your right, and over what is apparent to you.

"Set me over the treasures of the land."

He means: the foundational rank that Jacob had given him, in which he had remained — in its simpler form.

He took up the da'wah, established its boundaries, and ordered it; he carried it out, and Joseph set up his deputies throughout the regions. His call spread, and his news reached his father, ending with what had been opened for him; and he became established.

This is the saying of Allah, the Almighty:

"And thus We established Joseph in the land, that he might take from it wherever he willed."

It means enabling him to issue forth from the foundations, so that he could deploy himself wherever he wished and extend his reach — knowing that he was not forbidden anything. The da'wah of Joseph went forth, and it called, and it spread, and it appeared in the form of the king's command and authority when it came to him. The da'wah of Joseph then weakened those [false claimants], and those who had followed them were cut off from what they had done to Joseph in the matter of wisdom. Those who had responded to them rejected them, and they became among the people [as ordinary folk]; and people accepted from Joseph from every side, and likewise from his brother. Whoever came to him to learn what he had and to benefit from it found his way to them.

<!-- page 151 -->

It was from him that wisdom and eloquence of speech were spread — but those [brothers] did not have it, and they did not even realize that he was the author of it. This is what He says:

"And Joseph's brothers came to him, and he knew them while they did not recognize him."

This means: he knew their rank, and they denied his rank; what had come to him in terms of support and wisdom they did not perceive, nor did they know the truth of his knowledge, and he was far removed from their own understanding.

"And when he had furnished them with their supplies."

He says: he gave them some of what he had, and what he should benefit them with — which was his brother, whom Joseph had prepared to call them with. He made them ask about their condition, until they told him their news, and that they had a brother from their father.

He said: "Bring me a brother of yours from your father. Do you not see that I give full measure and that I am the best of hosts? But if you do not bring him to me, you shall have no measure from me, nor shall you approach me."

He says: if you do not bring him to me, I will not give you any portion, nor speak to you with any wisdom.

"They said: We shall solicit him from his father; that we shall surely do. He said to his servants: place their merchandise in their saddlebags, that they may recognize it when they return to their family — perhaps they will return."

He says: respond to them in their questions, so that they will know your answer and will know the truth — perhaps they will return with their companions; this is what calls them to come back.

"And when they returned to their father" — that is, when they went to Jacob — they told him the news:

<!-- page 152 -->

"They said: O our father, the measure has been denied to us, so send our brother with us. We shall be safeguarded, and we shall protect him."

That is: send him with us to open [the measure] to us, that we may benefit — for we have received nothing of wisdom, since he forbade us from opening that door, but we will benefit through him.

We have been told that:

He said: "Shall I trust you with him as I trusted you before with his brother? But Allah is the best of protectors, and He is the most merciful of the merciful."

"And when they opened their baggage."

He means: remember what happened to them in their affairs.

"They found their merchandise had been returned to them."

That is: they found that the deputies of Joseph had given them a general answer.

"They said: O our father, what more can we desire? Here is our merchandise returned to us. We shall provide for our family, and we shall safeguard our brother."

That is: we draw from the people of our da'wah, and we protect our brother from any harm reaching him from violators — as had happened to Joseph before him.

"And we shall increase by a camel's load."

That is: we increase ourselves with the knowledge of an imam from whom it is taken.

"That is a small matter."

That is: small compared to what they had, and to what had happened to them before this discussion.

He said: "I shall not send him with you until you give me a covenant from Allah that you will surely bring him back to me, unless you are encompassed [by ruin]."

<!-- page 153 -->

— that is, unless something overwhelms you that cannot be repelled. Allah says, regarding what they would say: Allah is Witness.

"And, my son, do not enter from one gate, but enter from different gates."

He commanded them not [to approach] only one deputy as a whole, but to disperse among the deputies, so that they might learn what each of them has; and on the other hand, not to ask about a single type of knowledge, but each of them to ask about a type.

"And I avail you nothing against Allah."

He says: it is not by your affiliation with me that you receive what is given.

"And when they entered from where their father had commanded them, it did not avail them anything against Allah, except as a need in Jacob's soul which he fulfilled. And indeed he was possessed of knowledge, by what We had taught him, but most people do not know."

He says: they found that what their father told them was true — that Allah does not exchange anything for them; they would not be given anything by joining it, except what they were obliged to do.

He said:

"And when they entered upon Joseph, he drew his brother near to himself. He said: I am your brother, so do not despair over what they used to do."

That is: he drew him near to himself, and showed him what he should be aware of. He told him that he was at ease with what had been assigned to them, and that it was alright for him concerning their cunning and envy, which had been known to them in the past.

<!-- page 154 -->

"So when he had furnished them with their supplies."

It means: He gave them what they required of knowledge.

"He placed the drinking-cup in his brother's saddlebag."

That is: what came to him in the matter of da'wah, and the fortune of support without them — because he informed him of what he had not told them.

"Then a herald called out: O caravan, you are surely thieves."

It means that one of the deputies said: you have taken wisdom from where it is not within your bounds, and from where you should not take it.

"They said, turning to them: What is it that you are missing? They said: We miss the king's drinking-cup."

By the cup He means the measure of wisdom which people give in order and quantity — that is, whoever comes to him and obtains it according to his account and presents it in its proper form, has come.

"And for him who brings it is a camel-load."

[He occupies] the position of the lamb of guidance ahead.

"They said: By Allah, you have known indeed that we did not come to corrupt the land, and we are not thieves."

That is: we did not come to corrupt the limit of interpretation, nor do we steal from it what we have not been given. We are the sons of Jacob; we have come only to reclaim what has been given to us.

<!-- page 155 -->

"They said: What shall be the recompense if you are liars? They said: Its recompense is — in whose saddlebag it is found, that one shall be its recompense."

They mean: the one who has with him what he was not given — and who extends his hand to what he does not have — must yield what he had first and last, just as was the judgment in the time of Adam.

"Thus do We requite the wrongdoers."

That is: whoever puts a thing out of its place.

"So he began with their bags before his brother's bag."

He said: he asked them and queried them one by one, before his brother, but they did not bring any answer except what was thrown back at them. Then he asked his brother, who responded with what they did not have, and brought forth what was due to the fortune of support without them.

He said:

"Then he extracted it from his brother's bag."

He means: the word.

"Thus did We plan for Joseph; he could not have taken his brother by the king's religion, except as Allah willed. We raise in degrees whomever We will, and above every possessor of knowledge is one yet more knowing."

He says: We gave Joseph the guidance, to the benefit of his brother and to his support — by means of the speaker (1) — when he was in the king's authority. He took him to him and established him in the station of the supporters, may Allah be pleased with him; and Allah will grant him permission to act with the support with which He inspired him in what he did.

"They said: If he steals, then a brother of his stole before."

They mean: this one has transgressed to the limit of others, and that was not given to him; his brother (1) did the same before him, because he stole from his father — that is, [took] another.

<!-- page 156 -->

So he took her captive, and he did not yield her to them. And he said: "You are in a worse situation" — meaning regarding their false statement —

"and Allah knows best what you describe."

"They said: O Aziz."

What is dearer than what Allah has given him?

"He has a great father."

In other words: he has reached the level of the imams in wisdom, and he has the sanctity of his grandfather.

"So take one of us in his stead."

That is: either forbid him to undergo the appropriate punishment, or appoint one of us to what you wish to assign him.

"We see you indeed among the doers of good. He said: Allah forbid that we take anyone except him with whom we found our property; for then we would be wrongdoers."

That is: Allah forbid that we take the whole of this matter, except from the one whom Allah has appointed to speak in it. Otherwise we would have put the matter out of its place.

<!-- page 157 -->

"When they despaired of him, they conferred privately."

Yes, they retired and conferred. The eldest among them — meaning the most knowledgeable, and he was the one who had first signaled to them not to kill Joseph — said:

"Do you not know that your father has taken a covenant from Allah upon you?"

He means: their guarantee that they would bring him back.

"And before, you had also failed in regard to Joseph."

He means what they had done in his case, reminding them of that.

"I shall not leave the land" — that is, the place in which I stand —

"until my father gives me permission, or Allah judges in my favor; and He is the best of judges."

It means what he wills.

"Return to your father, and say: O our father, your son has stolen."

That is: he took beyond his measure, and extended his hand to what exceeds him, so I held his mind to the truth.

"And we bear witness only to what we know."

That is: this is what appeared to us, and we knew it.

"And we were not keepers of the unseen."

That is: there is something in this absent from us, which I had not memorized and we had not known.

"And ask the village in which we were."

That is: the people of the da'wah whom we were with.

<!-- page 158 -->

"And the caravan (1) in which we were."

Whatever caravan it was — and the caravans differ in appearance — that is, ask about that as well.

As for the disobedience, it is something that has appeared to us, become famous, and whose knowledge is near and far.

"And we are truthful." By doing what He had indicated to them, they said that to Jacob.

He did not accept it.

He said: "Rather, your souls have enticed you to a thing."

That is: I have told you of what is in yourselves regarding them, which is not the case in reality.

"Patience is beautiful; perhaps Allah will bring them to me all together."

That is: as a sum of support.

"He is the All-Knowing, the All-Wise."

He turned away from them — that is, cut himself off from them.

"And he said: O my sorrow for Joseph."

He says: I grieve for him; what has been cut off from me has not become his.

"And his eyes turned white from grief, and he was suppressed."

That is: he was cut off when he was contacted by the local people, and that came to belong to Joseph.

"They said: By Allah, you continue to remember Joseph until you become withered."

(1) In copy (M): "Caliber"

<!-- page 159 -->

That is: you supervise the destruction.

"Or you are of those who perish."

That is: you still remember Joseph, until what you have, and what you are in, is gone; so cease mentioning it, and accept it for yourself.

He said: "I complain of my anguish and my grief only to Allah."

In other words: I say this in relation to myself and Allah, and I do not mention it to anyone other than Him.

"And I know from Allah what you do not know."

That is: I know who has kept his command, and that even if he has been cut off from me, He has not removed him from it; Joseph has not been kept away from him.

"O my sons, go and inquire about Joseph and his brother, and do not despair of the spirit of Allah; for none despairs of the spirit of Allah except the disbelieving people."

He says: investigate the imamate — where has it become — and the babiya (1), for whom has it become; and do not despair of the benefits of His mercy. Pure despair of it is disbelief; but when they are overcome by despair, they still hope for relief, as Allah says:

"Until, when the messengers despaired and thought that they had been denied, then there came to them Our help."

The messengers did not despair of the benefits of God's mercy; if they were overwhelmed by despair, it was [despair] from the people.

"So when they entered upon him" — yes, upon Joseph —

"they said: O Aziz, distress has touched us and our family."

(1) In copy (S): "the Papacy"

<!-- page 160 -->

They mean: the lack of interest.

"And we have brought poor merchandise."

That is, weak issues that do not lead us to know what we hope for from the knowledge of truth.

"But pay us the full measure and be charitable to us; surely Allah rewards the charitable."

That is: you have favored us from the benefits, which we may not be able to ask about well, and our illusions do not end with Him.

He said: "Do you know what you did with Joseph and his brother, when you were ignorant?"

He says: have you pondered what happened to you in the matter of the Imam and his Gate, and that you committed it — that is, ignorant of their value?

"Are you indeed Joseph?"

Yes — you are the Imam.

He said: "I am Joseph, and this is my brother."

He revealed to them his rank from the imamate (1), and his brother's rank from the babiya (2). And this is the first of its appendices — "Allah has favored us" — meaning by these two terms.

"Whoever fears Allah and is patient — surely Allah does not waste the reward of the doers of good."

It means: whoever fears to follow someone else, and is patient about that, and does not long for the one above him — has not lost that in the sight of his Lord.

"They said: By Allah, Allah has surely chosen you over us, even though we were sinners."

(1) In copy (S): "Al-Imamiyah"
(2) In copy (S): "the front"


"…we have preferred you for the Imamate over us, even though we erred in what we sought when we tried to push you away from your station."

He said: "There shall be no blame upon you this day; may God forgive you" — that is, He effaces your fault from you and conceals it.

"And He is the Most Merciful of the merciful."

"Take this shirt of mine and cast it upon my father's face — he will regain his sight. And bring me your whole family."

He means: go to the rank of the Imamate with which God has clothed me, and cast that upon my father's face — the endorsement is conveyed to him, and he becomes what my uncle was over him. "And bring me your whole family" — that is, all the people of your call, return them to me.

"And when the caravan departed, their father said, 'I truly sense the scent of Joseph, even if you think me senile.'"

He says: when they came and parted from their gains, Jacob felt the support from Joseph's side.

"They said, 'By God, you are still in your old error.'"

That is, in the state he had been in before any of God's command concerning this matter had reached him.

"Then when the bearer of good tidings came…"

It means the imagination connected to him by which he came to know.

"He cast it upon his face, and he regained his sight."

He became a supporter, as he had been before.

He said, "Did I not tell you that I know from God what you do not know?"

"O father, ask forgiveness for our sins, for we have been sinners." He said, "I shall ask my Lord to forgive you; truly He is the Forgiving, the Most Merciful."

They asked him to cover them and admit them into the matter, and he promised that he would ask on their behalf — so they would not fall into regret.

"And when they entered upon Joseph, he sheltered them" — he says, they entered into his state. He showed them to himself separately.

"They said: 'Enter Egypt, God willing, in safety.'"

He says: enter into the da'wah, and have no fear of falling, God willing.

"And he raised his parents upon the throne."

That is, his parents — those who had taken up his call — for them He made a station of the degree which He had singled out, "and they fell down before him in prostration," meaning they submitted to him by acknowledging the rank of support which God had given him, and they accepted what he said.

"He said, 'O father, this is the interpretation of my earlier vision; my Lord has truly made it real.'"

That is, God has fulfilled for me what He first granted me, and I told you of it.

"And He was good to me when He brought me out of prison."

That is, out of the limit of deprivation and prohibition.

"And He brought you out of the desert."

That is, out of the state from which you had begun to take from me.

"After Satan had sown discord between me and my brothers."

I mean, what they had set in motion.

**The Story of Job (Ayyub).**

Ayyub (peace be upon him) was one of the Imams of the cycle of Ibrahim — an upright Imam — and God mentioned him in His Book, saying:

"And remember Our servant Job, when he called upon his Lord, 'Satan has touched me with hardship and torment.'"

He was concerned with the evil affliction, and Satan in his time set against him — and he was one of the victorious pharaohs. He weakened Job and overcame him, seducing the people of his call so that they inclined away from him. He pushed him out of his place and brought him low in the people's eyes. This is the saying of the Almighty:

"And Job, when he cried out to his Lord, 'Harm has touched me, and You are the Most Merciful of the merciful.'"

In the tradition, Satan was given power over him, and so he killed his children, the last of them, and took away every blessing he had — what he possessed of livestock and wealth. Then he afflicted him in his body, so that he was struck with disease and worms walked upon him. He was cast upon a refuse-heap, and no one drew near him save his wife.

The interpretation of this is that Satan is his adversary in his time, and the killing of his children is the dispersal of the people of his call. The worms (1) are like those who responded to him and then turned upon him — eating from his flesh, that is, gaining from his knowledge, though not in his form nor in his image.

In the tradition also: he used to return to himself the worms that fell from his body, saying to each of them, "Take the sustenance which God has provided for you." The interpretation of this is that he was teaching them knowledge in the hope that they would benefit from it, though it is also related that he took it back from them when they were not in the way of his righteousness.

His wife, who was patient with him and remained with him, is like the master of his secret and his Hujjah (Argument). The harm with which he was struck is like his inability to carry out the da'wah and to establish the adherents and preachers (2). The refuse-heap is like the appearance of a corrupt outward law attributed to him, from which he could not draw away — frequented by all, with no one coming near him, no one willing to accept him — so that he was unable to establish anything of the affair of his call by which he might overcome it. That was the great calamity.

When God Almighty answered his prayer, He gave him true knowledge of the matter from which his sustenance would come — which is the saying of the Almighty:

"Strike with your foot — this is a cool spring to wash in and to drink."

Any initiative to establish one of your limits to spread this knowledge washes away every defilement which has been added to the appearance of your call. So he did it, and turned toward Him.

The people of his da'wah came back to him, and others came to him as well — which is what He said:

"And We gave him his family, and the like of them along with them, as a mercy from Us and a reminder for those endowed with understanding."

So God released him, displayed him before his enemy, and his call was set straight for him.

(1) In version (E): "Worms."
(2) In copy (S) it is mentioned (and the call).

In the tradition: he washed in the water and his body became whole again, and God restored to him those of his family who had died — his son, his livestock, and his animals after they had perished.

The interpretation of this is that the people of his call returned to him, and his call was made good for him. In the tradition also: he used to take revenge upon his wife, and he swore that he would beat her. So when the affliction was removed from him, he knew that she had been good to him, and he regretted it. God Almighty said:

"And take in your hand a bundle, and strike with it, and do not break your oath."

The interpretation of this is that he had been aware that his Bab (Door) had done something to him of what was imperfect, so he swore that he would cut him off. When God released him, he regretted what had preceded — the oath he had sworn — given the Bab's preservation, his patience with him, and his repentance. So it was said to him: gather your followers, and break this oath you swore against him by placing him with those beneath him — and do not commit perjury (1); rather, keep him in the rank of the adherents. Do not overthrow him without a proven offense — instead, turn away from him and accept his repentance.

The bundle is like the rods of a plant, and that is like the gathering of the adherents.

And the saying of the Almighty:

"We found him patient."

It means the Bab upon whom we were established, and the patience of the Bab upon him.

And the saying of the Almighty:

"An excellent servant! He was ever oft-returning (awwāb)."

That is, he is given to what pleases God Almighty, and is not content with what He hates — and that he was repenting from what he had been.

(1) Mentioned in version (E) thus, not as (tahnath).

**The Story of Shu'ayb.**

Shu'ayb (may God's blessings be upon him) was in the last cycles of the role of Ibrahim. He prayed for Moses, and his prayer was answered, and he was incapacitated. We will mention this in its place when we mention Moses. Shu'ayb was in Madyan, an appointed Imam who called to it; and one of his preachers was Moses, who was in Egypt calling on his behalf. His command was what it was, and we shall mention that in its place, God willing.

Among what God has mentioned concerning Shu'ayb's affair, He said:

"And to Madyan, their brother Shu'ayb."

He means their brother by physical birth, and brothers in religion as we mentioned in the story of Hud. God Almighty did not mention this except concerning those who were among the Imams in the cycles of the messengers, attributing them to the father of that prophet, in the manner we have set down in the stories of Hud and Salih.

He said: "O my people, worship God; you have no god other than Him."

This is an invitation to all who pronounce the manifest profession by imitation.

"A clear sign from your Lord has come to you."

I mean the proof itself and his Imam.

(1) In copy (E) it is mentioned (in a city).

"So give full measure and weight."

The inner meaning of this is to fulfill what the Speaker has imposed — for it is the balance of God by which He weighs the deeds of creatures; and to accept, after accepting the apparent, the guardianship of the Bab appointed for the interpretation of the apparent, since that is the scale of God by which He has weighed wisdom for creation.

"And do not diminish people in their things."

He says: do not turn back the command of God which has come to you, so that people are diminished of their portion from it — for He will return it to you.

"And do not work corruption in the land after its setting right."

He says: do not corrupt the foundation which the Speaker has established for the interpretation of his law. In the outward, this is forbidden; in the inward, the equivalent is failure of measure and corruption upon the earth.

"And do not sit on every path…"

The path, in language, is the way; and so in interpretation it is the way of religion. What is first meant is the Speaker. God has commanded the servants to accept first His limit, which is the apparent and its profession, and then to walk upon it to the rank of the foundation, which is the subtle; so they come to Him — for the inward is an interpretation of the apparent, and the apparent must not precede its interpretation, since it is the interpretation of the interpreter and explains what has been mentioned above. One example of this is the words of the Almighty:

"It is not for the sun to overtake the moon, nor for the night to outrun the day."

The sun is like the Imam, and the moon is like the Hujjah; the Imam is the foremost.

The same applies to the Speaker and the foundation, for the foundation follows the Speaker and realizes him; and the Hujjah likewise follows the Imam and realizes him, since the Imam follows the Hujjah; and since the Speaker is attached to the foundation, and is like the apparent day — because things appear within it, and it is the limit of the sun — when it rises, it appears; just as the apparent is the limit of the Bab, and he is unified with the Speaker. The night is like the inner and the secret, because things are concealed in it, and it is the limit of the Hujjah — the unity of the foundation. The Hujjahs are like the stations on the way; and that is the meaning of the path within the adherents. Its origin is the Speaker in his time, and the Imam in his time; the adherents have their limits and their stages, just as the road to the Sacred House has.

We have set down that the Imam is like the Sacred House, the pilgrim is like the respondent, and his house is like his preacher — the one to whom the pilgrim takes refuge, and in whose words he dwells — like the house in which its dweller takes shelter, lives, and is covered. So if he wishes to rise to the rank of knowing the limit of the Imam, and to reach the rank of the righteous, the path obliges him to leave from his house — that is, from his caller. Likewise, this is the rank of the caller within the limits of the knowledge of the adherents and the verses that have been made markers and milestones. He keeps moving from one stage to another, and he is upon the way until he reaches the Sacred House — and that is the limit of the Imam. When he reaches it, he knows him, takes his stand at his limits, circumambulates him, performs his rites, and discharges his duties. Then he returns home upon the road as one delegated by him — that is, he returns to his preacher (1) and takes refuge in it. If he strays from the path, or from one of its stages on his return, he errs from his house and has no shelter, and is separated from his family — just as the one who deviates from the truth departs from the believers and is cut off from the Imam, his followers, and his material.

This is the straight path which God has commanded His servants to ask to be guided to — and the like of it is also in the inner sense.

The people of Shu'ayb used to repel the people from his preachers and followers, and from those who intended to come to him; and they would intimidate and frighten them — as He says (interpretation of the meaning):

"And do not sit on every path, threatening, and barring from the way of God the one who believes in Him, and seeking to make it crooked."

That is, you wish to divert this path by turning it aside from its limits, and from being upright upon it, until he reaches his goal in it.

The path is also in the manner of perfection: it reaches from the highest and ends at the beginning of the upper limits — and we have also mentioned them, in relation to the Prophet, then in the foundation, then in the Imam after him, then in his Bab, then in his followers, then in his preachers, then in those authorized for them — by way of the respondents. The exaltation of the respondent is by knowledge of these limits — that is, from one limit to the one above it. Each of these limits is a limit of the path for those above it — that is, the path between two stages. The path is itself and its stages and its boundaries upon which the walker descends; he takes refuge in it, dwells in it, and rests with it; and from it he obtains food and drink that revives him, sustains him, and strengthens him for his journey. So likewise, the one who departs (2) within these limits of knowledge and wisdom — they protect his soul and strengthen him to reach his goal, where he finds eternal life forever.

The likeness in sensible terms is like the traveler and what he finds at the wells (manāhil), from which he is nourished for the rest of the night of his journey, between that well and the next that follows it. So it remains, until it ends at a place where he settles — the one for whom he intended it — so that he may have its power within him, as long as he is in it.

There are many evidences, proofs, and explanations on this subject, of which we have limited ourselves to —

(1) In copy (M), it is mentioned (its walker).
(2) Received in copy (X) as (Al-Murta'a).


<!-- page 170 -->
This is what necessitates the limit we have explained regarding the boundaries of interpretation, and we have confined ourselves to the saying that mentions the path, as Allah prescribed it: the believer recites it in every rak'ah of every prayer, day and night, and at the opening of each prayer the Fatiha is recited, the chapter that contains the verse of guidance, in which He said:

(The path of those upon whom You have bestowed Your favor, not of those who have earned Your anger, nor of those who have gone astray.)

It is an exception made for them: they have no path to follow except the Imam of their time. Although they may have walked between its stages and descended into its stations, some of the people of ignorance and misguidance may have approached certain of the limits among the guardians of Allah and questioned them about some of the manifestations of their religion, and they took from them — taking from the friends of Allah just as those who were taken from Ali and after him, down to Ja'far al-Sadiq bin Muhammad (may Allah's prayers be upon them), and from those after them. They are like the common people who took from them yet do not believe in their imamate, do not intend them as imams, and do not recognize their virtue.

The same applies to those who travel toward Makkah but are not of the Ummah, or who do not intend to perform Hajj and instead seek worldly purposes such as trade and the like. They set out on the road, descended at the manahil, took shelter in them, ate and drank in them — yet their intention was not the Hajj to the Sacred House, and they did not consider its virtue, nor the virtue of its path. What Allah has decreed for them does not belong to Him as a partner.

"And there was a difference between them and the villages which We had blessed — manifest villages — and We made the journeying between them measured, [saying], 'Travel between them safely, by night and by day.'" (1)

(1) In the version (e) it came (so he said).
p. 172

<!-- page 171 -->
Then we return to what Allah Almighty mentioned in the words of Shu'ayb, in accordance with what we have mentioned. This is explained in the tafsir, which follows:

(And remember when you were few, and He multiplied you.)

That is, Allah Almighty in His response to the people says: after you were few in number and Allah multiplied you, and your multitude is what caused you to change and disobey.

(And see what was the end of the corrupters.)

I mean those who corrupted the cause of the prophets and the sinners like what you have corrupted, and what overtook them from Allah of His punishment.

"And if there is a group among you who has believed in that with which I have been sent, and a group who has not believed, then be patient until Allah judges between us, and He is the best of judges."

He says: If those of your people who are not safe have denied what you have come with, then be patient until Allah judges between us by His judgment, as He has judged in those who came before us — you will then return to your manners.

(They said, "We will surely drive you out, O Shu'ayb, and those who have believed with you, from our village.")

They mean: from this call upon which we agreed — or that you return to our nation — that is, you return to what we are upon, from the apparent meaning without interpretation.

(He said, "Even if we were unwilling?")

It means: returning back.

173

<!-- page 172 -->
"We would have fabricated a lie against Allah if we returned to your religion after Allah had saved us from it. It is not for us to return to it unless Allah, our Lord, should will."

That is: we would have spoken a lie against Allah if we denied the interpretation and falsified it.

"Our Lord has encompassed all things in knowledge."

In other words: it is not possible for us to return to the bare apparent and claim that there is no interpretation, except if Allah should will to make the corrupters appear with it — He knows best who deserves that.

(In Allah we have placed our trust. Our Lord, decide between us and our people in truth, and You are the best of those who decide.)

Then He says:

(They said, "O Shu'ayb, we do not understand much of what you say.")

By this is meant the saying of those who heard the interpretation, who responded to his call, then contradicted whatever your preachers came to us with from interpretation — strange words we do not understand.

(And indeed, we see you weak among us.)

That is, of weak argument.

(And were it not for your clan, we would have stoned you.)

If it were not for those who stand by your command — among us being among you — to throw upon you the ugliness of speech, and we have broken your words (1), but when we did that to you, we would have

(1) In the copy (S) it came (your words)
p. 174.

<!-- page 173 -->
said about them what we say about you, and they are of us, so we disagree and stand and disperse, and we do not know what will happen after that.

(And you are not of any importance to us.)

But those more important to us than you are those among us who have stood up for you.

(He said, "O my people, is my clan dearer to you than Allah, and you have cast Him behind your backs? Indeed, my Lord encompasses what you do.")

I mean: these are dearer to you than Allah — you have said about Him what you wished, denying His signs and His guardians.

(And, O my people, work according to your position; indeed, I am working.)

That is: work according to your own way from the apparent, and I am working according to my own way from it and its interpretation, with whom you raised it for him.

"You will come to know to whom punishment will come, disgracing him, and who is a liar. So await — indeed, I am with you a watcher."

He said in another place:

(And the punishment of an imminent day will come upon him.)

The Almighty said:

"And when Our command came, We saved Shu'ayb and those who believed with him by mercy from Us. And the shout seized those who had wronged, and they became, in their homes, fallen prone, as if they had never prospered therein."

(Is there no extension of religion as it has been extended?)

175

<!-- page 174 -->
He said in another place:

"So the punishment of the day of the canopy took them; indeed, it was the punishment of a terrible day."

The cry is the sounding of the argument against them with the proofs of interpretation, and the trembling of their hearts at that, and the cutting off of any argument they could raise against him — because Allah willed their destruction. The owner of the time argued against them, so that they would go out of the world tortured, deprived by the punishment of the argument, and by the apparent punishment they were destroyed. The apparent punishment of Allah came upon them, and they perished from the last of them, just as Allah (swt) mentioned the manner of their destruction outwardly and inwardly. As they were destroyed before them, that is complete destruction (1).

(1) The Imamate was carried out in succession from father to son without abnormality. But in the reign of Ibrahim this system differed, so Allah decreed that two of the speaker-prophets would be from the descendants of Ibrahim. The Imams are the well-known depositaries among the public who perform the functions of the role as they should, and their descendants will include two speakers — Moses and Jesus — and these will descend from Ishaq, while the rest of the stable Imamate continues in Isma'il and his son until the end of the great cycle, when one of his descendants will be Muhammad and the Qa'im of the Time. These are only from father to son, while the depositary Imams may transfer the imamate among themselves from brother to brother or to a cousin, provided he is from the family of Ishaq. For this reason we list the names of the depositary Imams, and then we follow them with the resident Imams.

(Ishaq) was the son of Ibrahim al-Khalil, born 100 years after the birth of Ibrahim, his mother being Sarah, from Yaqim between the Levant and Jerusalem. He was, in essence, a depositary and a veil over a stable foundation. His brother Isma'il died 280 years after the birth of Ibrahim. He lived 180 years and was buried in Jerusalem after he handed the matter over to his son Ya'qub, peace be upon him.

(Ya'qub) was born 160 years after the birth of his grandfather Ibrahim. He lived between the Levant and Jerusalem, then emigrated to Egypt with all his family members and died there in the year 307 Abrahamic. His body was transferred to Jerusalem. He lived 147 years and handed over the matter to his son Yusuf.

(Yusuf) was born in 251 Abrahamic between the Levant and Jerusalem, then emigrated to Egypt before his father Ya'qub. His story in the Qur'an is clear. He died in Egypt and was buried there. When Moses emigrated from Egypt with the Israelites to the desert of the wanderers, he transported his body.

176

<!-- page 175 -->
Joseph was with him and kept him there. After the death of Moses, Joshua ibn Nun moved him and he was buried near Nablus. His death was in 361 Abrahamic, and he lived 110 years, and handed over the matter to his son (Ephraim). We did not find his date of birth or death, but it is known that he was born in Egypt.

(Razih) — he is the son of al-Ais, that is (Esau bin Ishaq bin Ibrahim), and he received the depositary Imamate after Ephraim bin Yusuf.

(Job) is the son of Moses bin Razih bin Esau bin Ishaq bin Ibrahim al-Khalil. He resided in a place called (al-Batina) in the works of Damascus. We also did not find the date of his birth or his death, but he received the office from his uncle Razih. He was the guardian of Ephraim and handed the matter over to his son Yunus and Qadash (93 years old).

(Yunus) — his name is also Yunus, that is, Bishr bin Ayyub, and in the Qur'an (Dhu al-Nun). He was sent to the people of Nineveh in front of Mosul. The dates of his birth and death are unknown, but the matter was handed over to Shu'ayb.

(Shu'ayb) — history does not mention anything about his lineage, and the date of his birth and death is unknown. He is called in the Torah Reuel and Jethro. He lived in Madyan and died after the birth of Moses, and Moses called him. He is counted among the depositary Imams of the cycle of Ibrahim.

As for the resident Imams: Isma'il was born in the year 86 from the birth of Ibrahim, his mother being Hajar. When he was 13 years old, between Damascus and Jerusalem, his father took him to Mecca with his mother Hajar. He was about twenty years old at the time, and he married a woman from the tribe of Jurhum, and he helped his father build the House. He died in Mecca 227 years after the birth of Ibrahim, having lived 137 years, and he handed the matter over to his son Qithar; Qithar handed it to Salaman; Salaman to a daughter; the daughter to al-Humaysa'; al-Humaysa' to Mu'addad; Mu'addad to ((Adnan)) — and he completes the role of stability during the reign of Ibrahim, since he is also the father of Adnan, the resident Imam, and likewise a resident of the cycle of Moses.

177
12

<!-- page 176 -->
Chapter Four
(In which is the interpretation of the stories of Moses, Aaron, Talut, Dawud, Sulayman, Yunus, Imran, Zakariya, and Yahya, may Allah's prayers be upon them.)

The Interpretation of Musa

In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful.

When the cycle of Ibrahim (peace be upon him) ended, and the conclusion of his cycle was Shu'ayb (peace be upon him), Allah (swt) willed to send a speaker-prophet — as mentioned above in the management of His wisdom — and that was Moses (may Allah's prayers be upon him). He was one of the Children of Israel, who descended from Ya'qub to Yusuf in Egypt. They had been with Ya'qub in the Levant, and then emigrated with him to Egypt. Moses was one of those who was born there and grew up there. At that time it was Coptic; its kings ruled it, and Pharaoh was its ruler.

Shu'ayb had a call within Egypt, calling secretly to what he stood for, out of fear of Pharaoh — lest it appear in his kingdom — and because of the weakness of the matter of Shu'ayb that we have mentioned. Allah willed to manifest Moses there, and supported him with His word, sending him with the sword, the proclamation, and the fight against the Pharaoh of Egypt, and the remembrance,

178

<!-- page 177 -->
by breaking what he was upon in terms of impersonating his own call as the religion of Allah. Moses was sent with this, and was given wisdom, status, support, and strength, because he is the middle of the speaker-prophets — three before him, namely Adam, Nuh, and Ibrahim, whose stories we have mentioned, and three after him, namely Isa, Muhammad, and the Qa'im, who is the son of (i.e. Muhammad), as we will mention after this. May the prayers of Allah be upon them all.

Since Moses was in the middle of them — and the middle of everything is stronger than the two sides — Moses called as the summoner of the island of Egypt. He was under the rule of Pharaoh, keeping his faith secret, as he said in what he described as "the truth," and he had marked himself with the outward appearance, following what Pharaoh required to be pious. The time was a time of narrowness and hardship for the believers, and when Pharaoh saw their weakness he claimed the matter for himself, and he established the da'wah in his own name, attracting people to him, and turning the da'wah into his own drawing.

This is what we have mentioned in the story of Shu'ayb and the deviation of most of the people of his da'wah from him. When Pharaoh brought them to the affair of this world with desire and awe, there remained nothing but the truth — a few believers — and Shu'ayb hid himself with a debtor from the land of Hijaz, and he was cut off. This is what is mentioned in the hadith that he was blind.

When Pharaoh's command came to him, he was the one who remained in Egypt, mostly the Children of Israel alone. Some of them were called to Shu'ayb; they recognized him, and he brought them. Pharaoh came to him and ordered them to turn the invitation toward him, and Shu'ayb showed his innocence. They responded to him, and Shu'ayb permitted them to do so, so they called to Pharaoh on the apparent face of it. They used to take one by one of the respondents; then, when they saw in him the capacity for acceptance, they would establish him upon the call of the truth. When he called Pharaoh, he ordered one of them to be killed — and that is what He said:

(((They slaughter their sons and take their women.))

179


<!-- page 178 -->
The sons stand for the respondents, and the women stand for the preachers (1) who had presented themselves to him through the acceptance they showed of him and the prayers they offered for him. Moses (peace be upon him) was one of those who responded to certain preachers of Shu'ayb who were in Egypt under Pharaoh's authority and who were openly conveying the invitation to him.

When that summoner saw in Moses the power and acceptance that he saw, he informed him of Shu'ayb's command, of what had transpired before him, of what had occurred in the cycle of the prophets, of how the prophetic office was lodged in them, and of the wisdom that ought to be acted upon. He instructed him in what his ancestor possessed, and all of that he taught him and accepted from him.

When he saw in him the strength of acceptance, he informed him of the matter of the Master of the Time and counseled him to elevate him until he came of age, describing his condition.

So the Master of the Time became apprehensive about Moses's affair and feared for him from his enemy. God therefore inspired the summoner to command that the call be raised over him, that he be elevated to a particular rank, and that God would support him with His Word and dispatch him as a Messenger to His creation. That is what the Almighty said:

"And We inspired the mother of Moses, saying: Suckle him, and when thou fearest for him, then cast him into the river,
in pain (3) and fear not nor grieve. Lo! We shall bring him back unto thee and shall make him one of the Messengers."

The mother of Moses, in the inner sense, is the summoner who called him; and the inspiration came from the Master of the Time, who commanded him to do so, so the inspiration was attributed to him because he was the one inviting.

This is what He said here; in another place He said:

(1) In copy (e), "the call" is mentioned.
(2) In copy (e), "So I returned him" is mentioned.
(3) In copy (X), it is mentioned as "Aleem."

180.

<!-- page 179 -->
"When We inspired thy mother with that which is inspired, saying: Throw him into the ark."

The ark embraces what is within it, and it stands for an utterance which is the limit of support. He said:

"And their Prophet said unto them: Lo! the token of his kingdom is that there shall come unto you the ark wherein is peace of reassurance from your Lord, and a remnant of that which the house of Moses and the house of Aaron left behind. Lo! herein shall be a token for you if ye are believers."

"And cast him into the river, and the river will throw him on to the bank, and there an enemy to Me and to him will take him."

That is, take the Covenant of Prophethood upon him; then release him on the surface, so that he may dispute and act within it, and cast him to the outward extremities as far as his limit reaches.

"An enemy to Me and an enemy to him will take him" — that is, one of the enemies of religion itself will draw him forth.

So Shu'ayb directed him to that summoner, and the summoner brought him to Moses and gave him permission to declare himself outwardly under the command of Pharaoh, and to break for him those whom he found to be firmly attached to his religion. He showed him to him, the summoner reached him, and released him with permission to break.

He was permitted to make a show of complying with Pharaoh's command by way of taqiyyah, according to what he saw fit, so that whoever appeared to him acceptable — or whoever was broken by him and proved receptive — he would disclose something to him. If that man stood firm and showed himself ready for acceptance, he would dispatch the affair to him and bind it upon him.

So Moses became one of those vested with authority, and he carried the limit of support. He began at his own rank, the rank of the two authorized ones, and outwardly made a show of Pharaoh's command, observing each one carefully. Whoever showed him acceptance and the strength of certainty, he agreed with him, broke for his sake, and then cast down what he held in his hand.

When he saw that the man was firm, he disclosed to him something of the truth so that he might take charge of his affair and promote him.

181

<!-- page 180 -->
He would then promote him to his summoner — the one who had been released by permission — so that the latter could take the covenant from him as those vested with authority do, until he himself became one of the limits established at the outward extremities, firm in his command, with Pharaoh ignorant of him. He would break some of them, and one of them would come to him in response.
