So he disclosed to him some of what he held, and the man bore the news to Pharaoh and conveyed it to him to have him killed — for Pharaoh used to kill those who were in such a state. But the door of Pharaoh had already come to know Moses and spoken with him about what he was disclosing, had seen in him what he liked, and had heard from his speech what he found exquisite.

Then Moses was brought before Pharaoh's council to be killed, and Pharaoh's door questioned him about the matter and told him what he had observed of him, and of the discernment Moses had shown in their affairs. He said to him: "If he is as has been described, let us call him to what we possess, for he is a man of strength and clear speech; let him be one of us and of those of our standing."

That is what the Almighty said:

"And the family of Pharaoh took him up, that he might become for them an enemy and a sorrow."

This is the formula of an affair concerning which it is said that they "take up" a thing knowing that it will be for them an enemy and a sorrow. But they used to kill the prophets because they knew about them. The general public has said that the meaning is that they took him up although he would become for them an enemy and a sorrow — a sense of interpretation that they themselves acknowledged but altered letter by letter when pressed to make sense of it.

"Lo! Pharaoh and Haman and their hosts were ever sinning" — that is, those who brought him forth and drew out what was in him.

And the words of the Almighty:

"And the wife of Pharaoh said: A comfort of the eye for me and for thee. Kill him not. Peradventure he may be of use to us, or we may choose him for a son. And they perceived not."

Pharaoh complied with her, ordered the child to be kept with him, and invited him to what he himself had done.

182

<!-- page 181 -->
He was upon him, raising him in his da'wah, taking him to himself, and the matter reached the point where Pharaoh became apprehensive. He feared lest he be incited against him by the door of Pharaoh, who would disclose to him something of what he had been about. (1) So Pharaoh sought to seduce him by means of his own person, and dispatched a messenger of the same standing as himself — one of those who entered Pharaoh's door — to summon him and learn his state and his condition. That is what He said:

"And the heart of Moses' mother became void, and she would have betrayed him had We not fortified her heart, that she might be of the believers. And she said unto his sister: Trace him. So she observed him from afar, and they perceived not."

The door of Pharaoh accepted him, and we brought him down from him, and Pharaoh singled him out, and he persuaded him to come to Pharaoh — in front of the obligatory observance of obedience — and to come to him with adornments of speech. So he made him understand that, and gave him permission for the door of Pharaoh. Moses was on the same footing as the sincere preachers who were hidden within that era, while Pharaoh's command and acceptance appeared outwardly; he called those who came to him outwardly.

Whenever he did good to those who possessed instrument (2) and strength, he would then call them to the reality.

One day a group of the people of his da'wah gathered to him, including some who had informed him of his affairs and some who had not yet seen him. He sat with them and they conferred, and he said: "I have a great view as regards what he holds in his power" — and he had not yet informed him of his command. Moses then saw that the man who was at the command of Pharaoh had raised an argument against his master, and realized that one hundred (3) was for religion's sake, so it became an argument against him.

He interrupted him and dwelt upon it. Then he repented of his opinion and regretted it, fearing that it would appear that he had ordered him last as he had appeared first; he saw that he had gone too far and disclosed it in his council.

(1) In copy (e) it is mentioned: "and he dictates it to him."
(2) In copy (e) it is mentioned: "Places."
(3) In copy (X) it is mentioned: "Al-Hijjah."

183

<!-- page 182 -->
Many of those who followed Pharaoh's command — these are the words of God, the Almighty:

"And when he reached his full strength and was ripe, We gave him wisdom and knowledge. Thus do We reward the good."

That is, when he had reached the limits of the da'wah, knew its limits and its ruling, and his patron — and his patron was one of Shu'ayb's captains and the master of the Island of Egypt, the one with the right to put out the preachers — then God gave him this.

Then the Almighty said:

"And he entered the city at a time of carelessness of its folk."

That is, he entered upon his da'wah, while most of them were heedless of what he was about.

"And he found therein two men fighting, one of his own caste, and the other of his enemies; and he who was of his caste asked his help against him who was of his enemies."

That is, his man came to him because the argument of his opponent had compelled him, so he sought his help.

"And Moses struck him with his fist and killed him."

That is, he refuted him by his speech, by the camouflages of his sorcery, and by the infallibility granted by God the Almighty.

The door of Pharaoh saw in him no trace of acceptance — though Pharaoh accepted from him outwardly, responded to what he said, and had mentioned that — but the authorized one whom the call had sent to test the state of Moses, who was one of the special ones of Pharaoh's door and who attended everything that passed between Pharaoh and Moses — to him the da'wah singled out this duty because of his station, namely the argument of Pharaoh and his competence over it.

(1) In copy (e) it is mentioned: "Provisions."

p. 184.

<!-- page 183 -->
So the door of Pharaoh confided in him what he had observed about Moses and disclosed to him his command from a few items.

The summoner said: "He is a Hebrew, and you have preachers from among the Hebrews who are the people of his house. Some of them are so-and-so" — meaning the summoner who had dispatched him — "and you know him, and you know the truth of his belief in this matter. If you turn the matter over to him, he will set right his policy and stand up for him, because he addresses him with his own tongue and breaks him where he knows it best. He will be what you desire, and you will be relieved of his upbringing — and of whoever has followed him." So Pharaoh said to him: "I believed you, and I was right, and I did well in what I said." And he sent him along with him.

That is what the Almighty said:

"And We had forbidden foster-mothers for him before."

That is, the benefit of those who know — what was before the Shari'ah.

"His sister said…"

— that is, the authorized one who is in the same situation, and the da'wah is their father in the inner world.

"Shall I show you the people of a house who will rear him for you, and they will be his counsellors?"

"So We restored him to his mother that her eye might be cooled, and that she might not grieve."

So Moses returned to his summoner, who increased his charge over him. Seeing in him the demand and the power, he kept nothing secret from him but released him as a preacher, after he was sure that Pharaoh's door had responded to him and done well by him, and after he had counseled him to part company with the door in his calling. By his decisive argument he bound him.

He said: "This is of the devil's doing. Lo! he is an enemy, a mere misleader."

That is, no outward disclosure was made by him.

"My Lord! I have wronged myself, so forgive me. And we shall turn away from him."

He said this when he repented of his opinion, and knew that he had revealed wisdom (1).

(1) In copy (e) it is mentioned: "Judgments."

185

<!-- page 184 -->
He had no means to disclose it except at a moment when its disclosure was obligatory; his act had taken place because of that, and he had altered his stance and acknowledged that he had wronged her.

It has been suggested that "injustice" in the language means putting a thing out of its place. The place of this thing was the wisdom that had been guarding it and that had remained hidden from other people; so when it was permitted to disclose what was permissible, he asked his Lord to forgive him for that — that is, he asked Him to cover him with His mercy. That is his return to his nurse. They made him ask the Imam of his time to ask God the Almighty to forgive him.

The Almighty has said:

"And if, when they had wronged themselves, they had but come unto thee and asked forgiveness of Allah, and the Messenger had asked forgiveness for them, they would have found Allah Forgiving, Merciful."

For God does not accept forgiveness except from His guardians, so God forgave him as He said:

"He it is who is the Forgiving, the Merciful."

He said:

"My Lord! Forasmuch as Thou hast favored me, I will nevermore be a supporter of the guilty."

That is, by saying "My Lord" he addressed his forgiving time, since he had believed in migration to him and abandoned what he had been doing of aiding Pharaoh and his people by showing them the call, and also abandoned the Imam of his time after the migration to him, when he himself felt the strength.

"So he became fearful, watching in the city, when behold, he who had asked his help the day before cried out to him for help. Moses said unto him: Lo! thou art indeed a mere hothead. And he sought to lay hands upon him who was an enemy unto them both."

p. 186.

<!-- page 185 -->
He says: "From the next day on he became afraid of what he had been the day before, and he sat down."

His companion of the previous day returned, contending with another man — but this time, when he braced himself, the other one asked Moses to refute him; yet that man was the one upon the outward of Pharaoh's command.

He said: "O Moses, dost thou intend to slay me as thou didst slay a person yesterday? Thou wouldst be naught but a tyrant in the land, and thou wouldst not be of the reformers."

He is saying: You want to argue against me as you did against my friend yesterday, and so I cut him off. What you want, in my view, is to rise high over the king's argument, arrogant and overpowering the people of his call — and I do not see you wanting to set him right.

The news reached Pharaoh and his argument, and he ordered that Moses be sought out to be killed. The authorized one came to him, who had heard this from Pharaoh's door, and warned him; so Moses fled and went to the abode of Shu'ayb in the Hijaz in disguise. That is what the Almighty says:

"And a man came running from the uttermost part of the city. He said: O Moses! Lo! the chiefs take counsel against thee to slay thee. Therefor escape. Lo! I am of those who give thee good advice. So he escaped from thence, fearing, vigilant. He said: My Lord! Deliver me from the wrongdoing folk."

He went to the abode of the Master of the Time, Shu'ayb.

"He said: Peradventure my Lord will guide me in the right road."

The word *Rabb* (Lord), as the Arabs say, means a lord, a rearer, the lord of the house, the lord of the slave, an owner and a master — that He may make me one of those who call upon Him.

187


<!-- page 186 -->
Those who are the path to it from among the limits — we have already mentioned this when discussing the Path.

The same applies to the words of Ibraheem:

> "I am going to my Lord, who will guide me."

That is, "you have no command over me; raise him up wisely."

> "And he watered for them."

That is, he came to know that limit.

> "He found upon it a community of people drawing water."

He said: he found a group of preachers who were calling people.

> "And he found two women holding back."

He said: these were two of the ma'zouns who had been wronged by some of the preachers — for whom a group might be deputed, one of the respondents — while they were walking with them toward the preachers. Moses asked them about their limits, and they told him.

He said: "What is your circumstance?"

> "We do not water until the shepherds drive away."

That is, "we do not open to anyone until those who responded to these preachers have finished, and we bring them to those preachers, and then they are defeated" — meaning they are overcome by them.

So Moses, being absolute in the call, went and watered for them for a while — that is, he made a supplication for them — and brought them and opened to them, showing them that he was one of the preachers of Shu'ayb. He asked the two ma'zouns about their command, and he meant one of his doors; that is what is referred to in what he said.

Then he turned aside, saying:

> "My Lord, I am in need of whatever good You send down to me."

188

<!-- page 187 -->
One of them came to him quietly and said: "My father is calling you so that he may reward you for having watered for us." When he came to him and told him the stories, he said: "Do not be afraid; you have escaped from the wrongdoing people."

One of them said: "O father, hire him; truly the best whom you can hire is the strong, the trustworthy."

One of the ma'zouns says: "(1) In your invitation, he is a captain, strong in that." He felt secure about him, so Shu'ayb asked him to be a da'i before him, saying:

> "I wish to marry you to one of my two daughters on condition that you hire yourself to me for eight pilgrimages; and if you complete ten, that will be of your own accord. I do not wish to make things hard for you; you will find me, God willing, among the righteous."

He says: "I wish to make you a captain, and to assign you the affairs of my invitation" — and that is what is mentioned in the hadith, that he hired him to take care of (2) his sheep, because he had seen God's blessing upon him in his condition and what he deserved of the message — "provided that you give me eight of the captains, and if I complete them to ten, that will be a favor from you; no condition is needed."

> "And I do not wish to make things hard for you."

His captains had been cut off, and most of them had perished; Moses was to be taken as a captain, and was to take ten of the affiliates with him — and with him whoever took him would have two with him.

(1) In Copy (S) it is rendered (Tala'a).
(2) In Version (e) it is rendered (Control).

189

<!-- page 188 -->
Ten captains, as the Sahib al-Zaman commanded — if he found them and was able to do so. We have mentioned this above, and we shall, God willing, recall its entirety in its proper place in the future.

Perhaps the Sahib al-Zaman is weaker than this number, and it is possible that he will remain alone, or that some have been prepared for it while others were unable. More often, the Sahib al-Zaman appoints four of his doors, assigning each of them two captains; we have mentioned this above.

The four are like the four sacred months, and the eight are like the remaining months of the year.

So Shu'ayb assigned Moses to appoint ten captains for him, or eight, drawing them from among those who were fit for that. This is very difficult for those who undertake it — but because of what he knew of God's support, and what He had qualified him with from the message, Moses saw that he was able to find them, and he preferred not to leave the matter unless it was carried out for him and completed. So he answered Shu'ayb, went to that work, and established the command of his invitation. He became a hujja for him and one of the closest doors to him: at first he was outwardly a respondent, then he answered his call, then he advanced until he became a captain, and then he became a hujja before long.

Likewise, God guides His followers to the straight path, which is the second creation after the first creation — for the Almighty did not create the perfect in a single batch, but raised them up creation after creation, as He mentioned in His book. He brought them out of the earth with what it nourishes them with, until they became sperm in the loins of men; then He transferred them to the wombs of women; then He created them there as a clot, then a morsel, then bones; then He clothed the bones with flesh when He deposited souls in them; and He brought them out of the wombs as children, preparing nothing of themselves. He taught them by the hands of His servants, and likewise He transmitted them in knowledge from one degree
190

<!-- page 189 -->
to another degree. The Almighty is the Almighty, in Whose hand is the command, and to Whom is the destiny.

Moses took charge of Shu'ayb's command and fulfilled for him what he had set out to do, and he established for him ten of the affiliates. The Messenger of God (peace be upon him) was asked about which of the two terms Moses fulfilled, and he said: "The best of them, the most complete of them" — and that is the words of God, may He be exalted:

> "Whichever of the two terms I fulfill, there shall be no injustice against me."

That is, between the establishment of ten limits and eight in the period that was set for that — so he fulfilled the ten of them. God revived the call of Shu'ayb through him, and many of those who answered his call became great. Shu'ayb's (1) activity continued, and his days passed; when Moses had completed his command, Shu'ayb was taken, and Moses followed him with the people of his call in great number from the Hijaz, intending the Levant to be a stable place for him — that the people of his invitation might come down there and find it a place of fertility and abundance, because of the narrowness of the Hijaz and the scarcity of its good.

When he reached ((al-Tur)) (2), which is a mountain among the mountains of the Levant, he was called: it was the limit of the support of prophethood by God the Almighty, since he was an Imam after him at that time. Revelation came to him from God with the message; that is what He said:

> "When Moses had fulfilled the term and was traveling with his family, he perceived a fire on the side of the Tur."

A fire like the one who speaks from the light of support — meaning, he perceived the light of support in himself, and like the stage which is like the rank of the speaker, which is the very message.

> "He said to his family, 'Stay here; I have perceived a fire. Perhaps I will bring you news from it, or a brand from the fire, so that you may warm yourselves.'"

(1) In Version (X) it is rendered (criticism).
(2) In Copy (X), it is rendered (Phases).

191

<!-- page 190 -->
He says: "Stay where you are, for I have perceived the support of the message reaching me. I will come to you from it; if I am united with it, you will be illuminated by a light by which I will receive its bounty."

> "When he came to it" — that is, meditated upon it —

> "We are calling from the right shore of the valley."

He says: from the gentle rank of the speaker — because ongoing support flows from the top downward, and is divided into three sections, the best being the section of the prophets, followed by the section of the foundations, then the imams — He wished to extend the message to the highest right.

> "In the blessed spot."

This is the truth (from the tree), that is, from the limit — and all this is confirmation. Perhaps his rank was even higher, and He preferred the oath that he came.

> "O Moses, indeed I am God, the Lord of the worlds."

This is a transmission from the speaker to Moses about God the Almighty, and he added "His identity" — glory be to His word, that He revealed to him — from the limit of solitude, not in particular, because his Lord, may He be glorified and exalted, is far above being encompassed by those who encompass Him, or being called solution or self.

He said in another place:

> "When he came to it, We called out: 'Blessed are those in the fire and those around it.'"

He says: the limit of support united with it is the blessing — and whoever follows it becomes blessed; likewise the blessing spreads around it, from the preachers with the two blessed origins, from the affiliates and the wings (1). He said:

> "I am God, the Lord of the worlds."

(1) It came in Copy (e) and was rendered (and the wings).

192

<!-- page 191 -->
So the interpretation of "Glory be to God" is the purity of God Almighty — the True One — from being likened to anything other than Himself, and from being called solutions in a place without a place, or from anything that befits the contingent things being added to Him, or from anything that befits Him befalling Him. Rather, this is done by the power of His wisdom and decree, and He has no partner.

The Almighty said:

> "O Moses, I am God, the Almighty, the Wise."

That is, a report from the one who leads him about the word of the Bari — He is the Mighty, whose existence does not require caution, and who cannot be denied, even if He is unseen. Rather, He is His Word, which has become the cause of everything; those who know Him know Him by it.

> "And throw down your staff."

Like the staves — he is a sharp one of the foremost, who received from the Sahib al-Zaman of the past, so that he might throw him into what was then assigned to him in terms of knowledge — and whatever followed him became Imam of the Time, like the staves. He commanded him to establish his foundations, but the disobedient became an example for him:

> "When he saw it moving as though it were a serpent."

The first thing that came to his mind was to reveal what should be revealed — that is, that which is hidden — so he concealed it from him; and he thought that what he had was purely outward, so he broke it upon him by its outward appearance, and he said:

> "And he turned, fleeing, and did not return."

That gave him his back; and it was said to him:

> "O Moses, come forward and do not fear; you are of those who are safe."

193

13

<!-- page 192 -->
That is, "you believe that your argument is to be outwardly (1) inward, so come forward in the pure inward; we have given you news about him, and when he came to him in the subconscious, he knew that he had something therein to dwell in." This is one face of it.

In some interpretations, "the jinn is alive and not great," and he said:

> "And he turned back, retreating."

Anyone who passed and did not return to him — he wants the power of the word to suppress those who disobey him, and that his argument blows fire, and he does not open to anyone unless he has made him feel like a serpent — the deaf, who do not come to anything except to destroy it — because the Almighty said:

> "Come forward and do not fear; you are of those who are safe."

He says that when Moses saw that aura, he realized within himself that the one who leads him does not have that. So the Bari called out to him, saying, "Almighty":

> "O Moses, do not fear; messengers do not fear in My presence — except those who have wronged. Then, if one substitutes good after evil, indeed I am Forgiving, Merciful."

He says: "Whoever has been unjust and misplaced wisdom, then asks forgiveness for that — I am Forgiving, Merciful."

> "And put your hand into your bosom; it will come out white, without harm."

By "hand" He means his foundation and the owner of his secret. He says: "I see him from an apparent side, your law upon the secret of what you have come with."

> "It will come out white, without evil."

That is, when you reveal him concerning it, it comes out with a clear interpretation of the yoke of

(1) In Copy (S) it is rendered (esoteric).
194

<!-- page 193 -->
the interpretation — clear, no one doubting it, and no one pushing back against its explanation and clarification.

> "Among nine signs to Pharaoh."

He says: "You are supported with nine signs, so go as a messenger to Pharaoh and his people." The nine signs are his wealth of strength, and that which supports him from those below him; that is his limit, from the two upper origins. He limited it to the respondents, and we have mentioned this in another place.

> "They were a defiantly disobedient people."

He says: "They were in fact, and they went out of it" — and that is debauchery — as He said:

> "All prostrated except Iblis, who was one of the jinn; he turned away from the command of his Lord."

The Almighty said:

> "And We will draw strength to you through your brother — and shall grant you both authority."

The wing of the hand, which is its foundation — He says: "Join him to you in what We have supported you with; he is not afraid of the breaking of your outward appearance, for he strengthens your argument with the argument of the interpretation that he establishes."

> "Your righteousness is a sign from your Lord to Pharaoh and his dignitaries."

He says: "What comes to them from the apparent and subtle statement — you and your foundation will perform" — to Aaron.

> "My Lord, I have killed a soul from among them, and I fear they will kill me."

That is, what happened to him concerning the story with the man on whom the statement was based; (1) and he has already mentioned it, "so I fear that if I come to them on the outward side alone, they will protest against me, so that I will be

(1) In Copy (M) it is rendered (Pharaohs).
195

<!-- page 194 -->
obscured; and what happened to me is what happened to the one upon whom the argument was based."

> "And my brother Aaron is more eloquent than me in speech."

"Build the argument with him, so send him with me as support, so that he may make true his outward interpretation."

> "I fear that they will deny me."

He said:

> "We will strengthen you through your brother, and We will give you both authority, so that they shall not reach you. By Our signs, you and those who follow you will be the victors."

He says: "We will strengthen your apparent command with your brother (1)" — meaning with the interpretation that he has — "so that they will not reach you with a great deal of harm. With you are the signs of God; so you and those who follow you in that will be the victors."

So God sent Moses to Pharaoh to invite them to believe in God and to enter into the call he had been called to; He supported him with his brother Aaron, raised him up to interpret his outward, and made him a partner in the statement with him.

It was also narrated from Muhammad (may God be pleased with him) that when this verse was revealed:

> "And appoint for me a minister from my family — Aaron, my brother. Strengthen my back through him, and let him share my task."

He said: "I say, O Lord, as Moses said: 'My Lord, appoint for me a minister from my family — my brother, strengthen my back through him, and let him share my task.'"

And Moses walked with those who followed him, and those who believed in him, by the command of God the Almighty.

(1) In Version (e) it is rendered (Bakhak).
196


<!-- page 195 -->
Pharaoh and those with him made for Egypt, and Moses entered Pharaoh's court and called him to bear witness to Allah and to believe in His message (1). This is what the Almighty refers to in His saying:

"But when Moses came to them with Our clear signs, they said: 'This is nothing but invented sorcery; we never heard of this among our forefathers.'"

By "our forefathers" they mean the ancestors from whom they had received their religion, and by "sorcery" they mean the words Moses called them with. They were saying, in effect: what you bring is fraud and deception by which you only wish to draw us to your side — not by any truth, knowledge, or guidance.

"Moses said: 'My Lord knows best who has come with guidance from Him and to whom the final outcome of the Abode belongs.'"

The "final outcome of the Abode" means the consequence that falls to the messengers — for the Abode is, in itself, a station. *Dar* ("abode") taken absolutely is a past-tense verb-form; once the definite article (*alif* and *lam*) is attached, it becomes the noun *al-dar*, and the listener supposes that the dwelling-place itself is meant. But what is actually intended here is the rank united with that "abode," and this is one of the concealed signs whose meaning is grasped only by the guardians appointed by Allah. It has a long explanation in the Arabic idiom. Here the prefixed article is appropriate — it is not the normal practice to attach it to verbs — and it is acceptable because the word is functioning as a symbol. Likewise the Almighty's words "When they took refuge in the cave": He dropped the article from *kahf* ("cave"), and the meaning of cave, cavern, or village was set aside. Two readings are permissible — that the word is a noun, or that it is a denial-name (a past-tense verb from a man's "taking refuge," on the pattern of *dar*). In this lies an argument and an indication.

"Indeed the wrongdoers do not prosper."

(1) In copy (e) the word given is "in his letters." (197)

<!-- page 196 -->
We have already explained "wrongdoing," "prospering," and "deliverance" — meaning gain and victory.

"And Pharaoh said: 'O nobles, I have not known of any god for you besides myself.'"

By "nobles" he means publicly the great ones who heeded his call. The meaning of his saying is: I have not known for you, in front of anyone besides myself, the existence of any god.

"So kindle for me, O Haman, a fire over clay, and build me a tower."

He says this to his chief, who is the foremost of his preachers and the seat of his argument and his great one: make me a foundation and a base by which I may be satisfied with the proof.

"That I may look upon the God of Moses."

— the one by whom Moses is supported.

"And indeed I think he is among the liars."

As for the exotericists, who took this passage to mean that he actually undertook the work of brick-firing and built a physical tower from which he could ascend to the sky — that is impossible. It is not credible that anyone would say so, only that he was claiming it.

"And he and his hosts were arrogant in the land, without right, and they thought that they would not be returned to Us."

He says: they were arrogant in the face of the proof of Moses, demanding that the truth Moses brought be manifested to them outwardly. After they had believed the outward aspect of what Moses said, what they denied still followed from him.

"So We seized him and his hosts and cast them into the sea."

The sea here resembles the outward (al-zahir). He says: We met them at the difference of their outward show, and We forbade them to speak; so We plunged them into a manifest trial.

(1) In copy (e) the wording is "(H)." (198)

<!-- page 197 -->
There is also an interpretation of the words of the Almighty:

"Has the hadith of Moses reached you? When he saw a fire, and said to his family: 'Stay here; I have perceived a fire. Perhaps I will bring you a brand from it, or find guidance at the fire.'"

He says: Moses perceived in himself a support gentler than any support he had relied on in any prior Imam. So he commanded those who followed him to remain alone in their belief without departing from anything of his, and he indicated that he sensed an increase in himself, and that they were to follow him in that. He set a limit for himself: only when he brought them true news of what he had perceived, or had found support from the one whose gift he had been graced with, would he guide them by what he had attained.

"So when he came to it, he was called: 'O Moses, indeed I am your Lord — take off your sandals.'"

By "called," he says: the highest limit (al-hadd al-a'la), the unmediated rank between him and Moses.

"Indeed I am your Lord" —

that is, one of your educators and supporters by leave of the Almighty, since I have been set in my rank as a support for the messengers. "So take off your sandals" — he says: cast off what was outwardly upon you, other than yourself. The sandal here is like the outward, and the slipper is like the inward. From this also: the sole is named for the surface a thing rests on, and for the conduct outside. When one becomes "of the limit," it is also used for the place where he settles and takes shelter in his assembly — there he casts off his sandal or his slipper. Yet he also uses them privately and publicly, and sits, rides, walks, and prays in them; the soles are removed only in matters higher than that. So the indication given to Moses was that the Almighty had esteemed him to be sent with a renewed shari'a, abrogating the shari'a before it.

"Indeed you are in the holy valley of Tuwa."

(199)

<!-- page 198 -->
That is, you have ascended to the rank of utterance.

"And I have chosen you, so listen to what is revealed."

That is: when there comes to you, from the Almighty, His saying —

"Indeed I am Allah; there is no god but I. So worship Me and establish the prayer for My remembrance."

He says: make your worship for Allah alone, and call to His remembrance. Prayer here is like the call, and the remembrance is the Prophet — that is, call to yourself, for you are My remembrance, who reminds them of it before they remind you. This is supported by the Almighty's words to Muhammad ﷺ:

"And they say he is mad. But it is nothing but a reminder for all the worlds."

And the Almighty said:

"And We have sent down to you a Book in which is your reminder."

And He said:

"And We have sent down to you a Messenger."

This bears witness to the connection of command and questioning to the Imams from the family of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ. And He said:

"So ask the people of remembrance if you do not know"

— meaning the people of the Prophet's house, who are the Imams, the prayers of Allah be upon them.

And He said:

"Indeed the Hour is coming — I have all but concealed it — that every soul may be recompensed for what it strives."

He continues: "So let none avert you from it who does not believe in it and follows his own desires, lest you perish." (200)

<!-- page 199 -->
He gave Moses notice of the Resurrection-station and made it incumbent upon him to believe in it, so as to complete the number of those who utter belief with him.

His sisters — and he forbade him to believe those who do not believe in it and follow their desires and their sayings.

The exotericists interpreted this through the language in two ways. Some of them said: "I have all but concealed it" — that is, "I have all but shown it," since it is said of a thing that is hidden that it has appeared. They cited as witness to themselves the verse of Imru' al-Qays, where he says:

"I concealed them (1) from their watering, as if I had concealed them and struck them out of a piled cloud."

In it, the Persian-bred horse is described as charging so hard that its hooves fell upon the ground — taking shelter under its stones from the beasts and the debris — just as the torrent of rain shows them up if it falls upon them and they emerge from it. This interpretation is the inward of the report.

Allah's nearness in showing forth (2) the command of the Resurrector — peace of Allah be upon him — is because Moses is the middle one, as we have mentioned. He has passed beyond half of the era up to the Qa'im; and every thing of which one cuts off the half is near the end.

The second interpretation is: "I have all but concealed it" — that is, I have all but hidden it from myself. How then could I show it to others? The Almighty has exalted the Truth above the addition of soul (nafs) to Him, as if He were ascribing it to creatures; He added this only by way of analogy. They say it is very high — and He says of most who speak:

"Every soul will taste death."

Whatever comes by way of the addition of "soul" added to the Almighty is added in that
sense, the addition to Him being the addition of His creation. The "soul" intended is the second soul — the Tablet that has fixed —

(1) In copy (e) the wording is "Khadhafra." (2) In copy (M) the wording is "appearance." (201)

<!-- page 200 -->
in it whatever exists until the Day of Judgment; and it is called "soul" just as knowledge is a deposit in the soul.

They also claimed that the Almighty appeared to the mountain, and entered into a tree, and spoke
to some of them in the speech of human beings — Allah is far exalted above what they say. But the one who spoke them was the upper limit (al-hadd al-a'la) with which He is united, and the tree is like the limit by which He has completed Himself.

And the Almighty's words "Indeed I am Allah" mean that the limit, in his calling to Him, was calling on behalf of Allah — as one says in the language that the Sultan called such-and-such, when in fact we are calling in his name and on behalf of his command. The caller says in his call, "Whoever does such-and-such will be punished with such-and-such" — and it is the caller who said it; yet it is known that the caller proclaiming this was proclaiming on behalf of his master's command.

He said:

"And what is that in your right hand, O Moses?"

We have already said in interpretation that the right hand (al-yamin) is the limit of the speaker. It has been said to him elsewhere:

"Throw what is in your right hand."

A thing is not said to be "in" another unless it has been contained by it, or one has been included in the other. The container is gentler than the contained — and that is included by saying that Zayd is in the house. Zayd is finer than the house, and the house is denser than Zayd; therefore it is correct that Zayd be in it and that it contain him. For this reason there are analogies that require a long
explanation. And so His saying:

"And what is that in your right hand, O Moses?"

makes plain that the right hand is finer than what was asked about — as is evidenced by His saying "Throw it" — and his gripping of it in the palm of his hand, since the staff is a gentle limit among (202)

<!-- page 201 -->
the limits of support, leaned on. It is gentler than the limit of the inward, since the right hand stands for the outward, and the inward stands for the inward; and the staff is gentler still than that, because it contains it.

For this reason it was said to him: what is in your inner self upon which you have leaned?

"He said: 'It is my staff; I lean on it.'"

He says: it is the substance by which a level gentleness has been shown to him, with no crookedness in it. He describes it by the measure of what he stood upon by it. When he was asked about it, he answered with the answer of one who has been tested and is sure of his knowledge of it: "I lean upon it" — that is, he relies upon it.

"And I drive with it upon my sheep."

He says: I bring benefit from it to my community, and I make them feel well with it.

"And I have in it other uses."

That is, other benefits for myself, upon which I rely and which I work by.

"He said: 'Cast it, O Moses' — and at once it was a serpent, moving."

He says: cast it upon your foundation — that is, teach him it — so that he becomes the one who acts by it and supports it. This is the same sense as the Almighty's saying:

"They fell upon their faces in prostration"

and His saying:

"They hear the hearing."

All of this — what the Arabs would call defective speech — is not, in fact, permissible to say of any except those who

(1) In copy (e) it is mentioned ("ivory"). (203)

<!-- page 202 -->
have something thrown only from the hand. The Almighty said:

"And We have cast (alqayna) enmity and hatred between them."

This is derived from "casting" — meaning gathering — that is, between the two things from the encounter. The thing
cast (al-mulqa) is what is set forth; and what is left behind is left behind. He was told: "Take it and do not fear" —

— and "the staff bent" is, in reality, a fine science, and the path of knowledge is mentioning. So bend it back into yourself — it is a benefit, a clear argument and a sign.

The Almighty said, after mentioning the staff:

"And press your hand to your side: it will come out white, without harm — another sign."

So the staff was the first sign, and the hand the second.

"And it is named a living thing."

Yes — because of its strength, like an animal.

"He said: 'Take it and do not fear.'"

He says: attach it to yourself — that is, ascribe it to yourself, for it is before you.

"And press your hand to your wing."

The hand here is like the foundation, and the wing is like the power that is given.

"It is white, without evil"

— that is, it is to be shown forth by a clear statement of the good in which there is no worst (1).

"Another sign."

(1) In copy (e) it is stated "(none)." (204)

<!-- page 203 -->
That is: the first sign came from the Almighty, and the second was greeted to him by the power of one other than him — namely his foundation. So in the first place, it was a sign from the Almighty Allah to him, and in the second sign, it is from his foundation.

"That We may show you some of Our greatest signs."

It means the limit of the one who arises on the Day of Resurrection — that is, We will show you that at his time, so that you see him as We showed you in your own time, who has not been seen by you.

"Go to Pharaoh — indeed he has transgressed."

It is said that water "transgresses" when it rises and overflows; tyranny (tughyan) is derived from this — namely, that
he pleaded for the seizing of knowledge from Moses and his argument (peace be upon them both). From this also is the saying of the Almighty:

"A maker (bakery) from Pharaoh."

"And he is present in the earth without a word."

He said:

"Pharaoh exalted himself in the land."

This is arrogance in receiving truth from the earth.

"He said: 'My Lord, expand my chest for me.'"

It means: the support that you have given me.

"And make my affair easy for me"

— that is, in announcing it.

"And untie a knot from my tongue."

I mean: the complex contract from me, and from my foundation, when the debate is to be argued with them
by truth and by knowledge of the inward.

(205)


<!-- page 204 -->
"And appoint for me a minister from my family, Aaron my brother."

The interpretation of this has already been given, and we now return to the dialogue between Moses and Pharaoh.

He said:

"I am a messenger from the Lord of the worlds."

He also said in another place:

"So go to Pharaoh and say: We are the messengers of the Lord of the worlds."

This is said to Moses and Aaron, peace be upon them:

"Send forth with us the Children of Israel."

That is, release them from the rule of your kingdom and from your call, for they are my people, the people of my call, and the offspring of prophethood. And he said in another place: "Do not punish them." It means: do not punish them for what you call them to from your followers and the belief in your Imamate.

Pharaoh said: "Did we not bring you up among us as a child?"

He says: Were you not among those who responded to our call, and were born among us, and were raised with our knowledge?

"And you remained among us for years of your life."

"And you did the deed which you did, and you are of the disbelievers."

He means the breach he had displayed against him, and the protest he had raised against him. As if he were saying: I disbelieved when a dispute arose between us.

He said: "I did it then, when I was of those astray."

206

<!-- page 205 -->

He says: I was then ignorant of what I now support and uphold, and Allah had given me a portion of prophethood of which I was unaware, and to which I had not been guided. This is what Allah said to Muhammad ﷺ:

"And He found you lost, so He guided you."

That is, He found him astray from the path of prophethood, so He guided him by supporting it, and this is supported by the words of Moses:

"So my Lord granted me wisdom and made me one of the messengers."

"And is this a favor with which you reproach me — that you have enslaved the Children of Israel?"

He says: As for this which you describe as a favor by which you have shown kindness to me — that you enslaved the Children of Israel, and I am one of them, and you forced us into obedience to your command, and made us slaves to yourself, that is, you set yourself up before us and compelled us to obey you — this is not in truth a favor that you have bestowed on me. Because you subdued us and forced us to it, it is an ordeal, not a favor as you have claimed.

Pharaoh said: "And what is the Lord of the worlds?"

Moses is being asked: what is the Creator (al-Bari), and what are His attributes?

"He said: The Lord of the heavens and the earth and what is between them, if you are certain."

"He said to those around him: Do you not hear?"

He means: do you not listen to Moses' answer — how he answers me with something other than what I asked him about? For if I am asking him about al-Bari, what He is, and he replies to me that He is the Lord of the heavens and the earth, then Moses is ignorant of the answer.

(1) In version (e): "And the curse."
(2) Copy (e) also has: "curse."

207

<!-- page 206 -->

Moses said: "Your Lord and the Lord of your forefathers of old."

Pharaoh said:

"Indeed your messenger who has been sent to you is mad."

— because Moses answered him with something other than what he had asked.

"He said: The Lord of the East and the West and what is between them, if you would only understand."

All of this points to the self-purity of the Almighty and describes Him by His divinity.

He said: "If you take a god other than me, I will surely place you among the prisoners."

He says: If you set up a guardian other than me, those whom I forbid will not be hindered from going where I forbade them — meaning the belief in my guardianship and his invitation to return to my command — which he was displaying in order to seem pious, since he held authority.

Moses said: "Even if I brought you something manifest?"

He says: Even if I come to you in the manifest way upon which I stand, with clear proof?

"He said: Bring it then, if you are of the truthful. So he threw down his staff, and behold, it was a manifest serpent."

It means: he displayed what supports him in statement and argument, so it became conclusively convincing.

(1) Version (e) has: "Al-Fatiha."
(2) Copy (M) has: [—]

208

<!-- page 207 -->

"And he drew out his hand, and behold, it was white for the beholders."

He says: And he displayed the foundation of statement, and then a clear explanation of light beyond it. Pharaoh was shocked.

Those around him said: "Indeed this one is a knowledgeable magician, who wants to drive you out of your land by his magic. So what do you command?"

He says: He is only a man with substantial speech and a breach by which he wants to drive you out of your religion, so what do you command?

"They said: Postpone him and his brother."

That is, the last of them says: do not speak with them about anything.

"And send into the cities gatherers."

They mean: people of his call, to gather them to him.

"To bring you every knowledgeable magician."

That is, every one in such a state of skillfulness — and the magician is the one who counterfeits something with what is contrary to it, so he resists him with it and brings forth the like of what he brought.

"The magicians were gathered for the appointment of a known day."

That is, for a known time.

"And it was said to the people: Will you assemble?"

That is, those acquainted with the knowledge of Pharaoh — are you gathered?

"Perhaps we may follow the magicians if they are the victors."

"So when the magicians came, they said to Pharaoh: Is there indeed a reward for us if we are the victors?"

209
14

<!-- page 208 -->

The magicians said what they said with confidence in themselves, because they did not see anyone responding to them with any argument, and they asked Pharaoh — if they defeated Moses — that they would receive a gift and rank (1).

He said: "Yes, and indeed you will be among those drawn near."

— in calling and in rank.

Moses said to them: "Throw what you have to throw."

He said in another place:

"They said: O Moses, either you throw, or we will be the first to throw."

They say: either you throw your questions at us, or we throw our questions at you.

"He said: Rather, you throw. And lo, their ropes and staffs appeared to him, by their magic, to be moving."

It means: their words came arranged from statement, and their apparent words were such that for all (2) is apparent, and for those who are singular in what they are compelled to interpret, they take from his family an interpretation by which they interpret for themselves — and it is corrupt and incorrect, having no clarification in it for the guided contemplative. So the magicians (3) came with the apparent form of Pharaoh's interpretation based on this meaning.

"And they said: By the might of Pharaoh, indeed we shall be the victors."

They flatter themselves.

"So Moses threw down his staff."

(2) Version (E) has: "Ant."
(1) In copy (S): "Manzalah."
(3) In version (e) the word "witch" is mentioned.

210

<!-- page 209 -->

This is what he supported by way of statement, so that the statement might invalidate their interpretation. And he said in another place:

"And their ropes and staffs were imagined by him through their magic to be moving, so Moses conceived within himself a fear."

He says: he imagined that what they brought from their staffs was almost the truth, and he became afraid that it might prevail.

"Fear not, indeed you are the uppermost. And throw what is in your right hand, it will swallow up what they have made. They have only made a magician's trick."

The right hand is the inner side — for from it the thing is thrown — so the inner right is the foundation in confronting the faces of interpretation. Their outward appearance is like that of the speaker, so the grasping and the extending are intrinsically inward. And benefiting from all that it benefits from, with the integrity of its outward form against accidents, is that the inward overcomes — for the outward, in this form, lacks the inward, and the inward supports and reinforces it. The inward is also concealed by the outward (1) which is hidden in it, and the outward indicates it and bears witness to it. And it was said to him: tell your foundation to give them some of the true interpretation, as we have mentioned. He said:

"And untie a knot from my tongue."

He intended this by it, so Moses opened to them with manifest expressions, while Aaron conquered them with the esoteric, just as Moses had asked, and we have mentioned this before. So he brought them that of which they could not complain, that it was the truth outwardly and inwardly. And that is because Allah permitted Moses to display the esoteric interpretation to those who did not accept its outward form because of the intensity

(1) Copy (X) has: "object."

211

<!-- page 210 -->

of the argument. So they yielded to him, and they had no defense in that other than acknowledging submission — as the Almighty says: "So the magicians fell down in prostration."

"They said: We believe in the Lord of Aaron and Moses."

Pharaoh said:

"You believed in him before I gave you permission."

He says: You believed in him before I gave you permission, while you are within my boundaries and my call.

"Indeed he is your chief who taught you magic, so I will surely cut off your hands and your feet on opposite sides."

He says: I will cut off the substance of the two foundations, upper and lower.

"And I will surely crucify you on the trunks of palm trees."

He means: publicizing their affair among his followers, because he was making a call to delimit the Imams. He claimed the Imamate.

They said: "There is no harm; indeed to our Lord we shall return. Indeed we hope that our Lord will forgive us our sins, for we are the first of the believers."

And the Almighty said:

"And We inspired Moses, saying: Travel by night with My servants, for indeed you will be pursued."

The Isra — to travel by night — means: supporting them with the knowledge of the esoteric and the veiling. And this is a parable of night. "You will be pursued" — he says — by Pharaoh and his people. They will follow you with arguments, so support your companions, teach them, and establish them upon the grounds of the truth.

p. 212

<!-- page 211 -->

"So Pharaoh sent into the cities gatherers."

He means: Moses and those with him.

"And indeed they are a small band."

"And indeed they have enraged us."

"And indeed we are all forewarned."

It means: he gathered another group of them to argue with them, because he was enraged by what was from him and those who believed with him. So Pharaoh's companions who remained of them came with the apparent form which was with them, and this is what he said: "So they followed them at sunrise" — and sunrise is from the rising of the sun, which is the day, and is like the apparent. He says: He pursued them with the apparent.

"When the two groups saw each other."

That is, they looked at each other when they debated.

"The companions of Moses said: Indeed we are overtaken."

They say: I am not equipped with the argument, because we were dealing with the esoteric, and these people are coming to us with the outward.

"He said: No, indeed with me is my Lord, He will guide me. So We inspired Moses: Strike with your staff the sea. And it split, and each part was like a great mountain."

The sea is like the knowledge of the outward. Moses struck it with the support by which he was supported from the apparent, so he overcame (1) what they brought, divided it, cut it off against him, and distinguished between truth and falsehood from Him. Then the Almighty said:

"And We saved Moses and all those with him. Then We drowned the others."

(1) Copy (M) has: "so he digested."

p. 213

<!-- page 212 -->

It means: they drowned in their apparent arguments, so they perished in them inwardly. And they also drowned outwardly, so that they would not remain in the world — unless the argument of the people of truth was established against them — according to what the Sunna of Allah has been with those who came before them of their like.

All of this and what has preceded comes from mentioning the esoteric by way of parables. That which was apparent — parables are indications and references to that which the representation took place upon. So it was as the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "For every verse there is an outward and an inward." Thus we have stripped from this composition the mention of the subtle and the parables, and we have left the apparent to suffice with its outward appearance, since most people know about it. We have mentioned the gist of what we intended to interpret here in the book *Pillars of Islam (Da'a'im al-Islam)*, in which we have interpreted this book — and from Allah we seek help.

Pharaoh spoke the word of faith, and difference arose concerning it, and Allah did not accept it from him. This is what the Almighty said:

"Now? — when you disobeyed before and were one of the corrupters! So today We will save you in your body."

He says: We will make your affair known to the people — that what you used to claim of the knowledge of the esoteric is a false call, and is purely apparent (1) — because the likeness of the body is the apparent, and the soul is the esoteric. And the words of the Almighty:

"Then I saw the great sign."

It means: what Moses displayed to Pharaoh of what the Almighty supported him with.

"But he denied and disobeyed. Then he turned his back, striving. And he gathered and called out, and said: I am your Lord, the Most High."

(1) Copy (e) has: "Has."

214

<!-- page 213 -->

It means: he gathered his people and established the call among them for himself — that he is the Imam of creation in his time.

"So Allah seized him with the punishment of the Hereafter and the first life."

The "first" is: to expose what he displayed of the corruption of his claim, and to show what creation had been deluded by — that he was the master of the truth and the esoteric. And the "Hereafter" is that he will be punished with it without escape.

And the Almighty said:

"And We made the people who were oppressed inheritors of the eastern parts of the earth and the western parts thereof, which We had blessed."

It means: those whom Pharaoh oppressed — and his people whom Allah caused to inherit the knowledge of the Imams, and arguments — both outwardly and inwardly, to the extent of what is within their boundaries and ranks.

"And the good word of your Lord was fulfilled upon the Children of Israel, because of their patience. And We destroyed what Pharaoh and his people had made, and what they had built up (ya'rishun)."

It means: the word of Allah came forth among them from the one who spoke it, and Allah nullified the affair of Pharaoh and his people, and what they had built up in religion of weak and flimsy statement, which is like the *'arish* — which resembles a house but is not truly so.

"And We brought the Children of Israel across the sea."

He says: We raised them upon the knowledge of the apparent and the waves, and saved them from drowning in it.

Explanation of the interpretation:

"They came upon a people devoted to their idols."

215
0


<!-- page 214 -->

He says, "They passed by a people who had idols that they had raised up for themselves" — meaning they took from them the science of the apparent.

(They said, "O Moses, make for us a god as they have gods.")
That is: give us a leader who will benefit us with his counsel, and choose for us what we need, according to what they did. Moses said to them:

(You are an ignorant people.)
They are heedless of what they are in, and what they used to do is false. He says: the consequence of these is destruction.

(He said, "Shall I seek for you a god other than Allah?")
It means that the God of the worlds has sent to them, outwardly and inwardly, what He has sent — so they will be questioned about it.

After that, they returned to the opinion of the people. This is what the Children of Israel said to Moses after God destroyed Pharaoh and his people. Moses had gone with the Children of Israel toward Damascus, wishing it to be the seat of their fathers, and he took them out with him. When Moses halted with them, the science of imitation belonging to human beings — those without the messengers — caused them to ask him to establish for them someone who would teach them the science of the truth, that which is from Allah the Almighty, and which Allah revealed to him. They were, at that time, as he praised them, ten tribes (1): each tribe should have a captain who would teach them. This is what he mentioned in its entirety:

"And when Moses asked for water for his people, We said, 'Strike the stone with your staff.' And twelve springs gushed forth from it; every people knew its drinking place. Eat and drink of Allah's provision, and do not wander on the earth spreading corruption."

(1) Received in copy (E) as (Isbāṭā).

<!-- page 215 -->

The staff here, as we have mentioned, is like the support by which something is supported, and the stone is like its foundation, which belongs to it from the support that is united with it. From it, the suffixes must be appointed for each tribe — a man for each, so that they would know that he was their drinker, meaning the one from whom they benefit. Knowledge is like water, as we mentioned above.

So each tribe of them called its master, and appointed preachers for them to teach them the interpretation. They overpowered them with wisdom, after Moses had taught them the manifest message and they had not yet worshipped by his resurrection of it. And the words of the Almighty:

(Eat and drink of Allah's provision, and do not spread corruption in the land.)

He says: Eat from the statement and from knowledge as much as you can manage, one thing after another. For eating is like the eating of the weak by comparison to the able — as eating is for those who are not filled with food except after a while; likewise the one weak in strength does not contain wisdom except after a while. Drinking is like eating for the strong, as drinking is what the one who eats in his time consumes quickly. And if the strong and the weak come together when they hear, none of them can take of it except as much as he can bear, as if there came together, for food and drink, a group of different people in health and disposition — each of them taking only as much as he could bear. This differs in its outward appearance, and its inward is also different, because of the difference in human powers, for hardly do two of them come together at the same measure, such that one of them does not exceed the other except to the extent of what is lacking. This does not agree as to the appearance of the image; and even if they appear similar, there must be a difference between every two images.

When Aaron appointed the suffixes for them, and set up preachers for them to explain the interpretation and what you worshipped, Moses came and said to him: "We do not have patience for the station of interpretation alone; so ask God to speak on the tongue of your foundation that you have established, that He bring forth for us our arts —

<!-- page 216 -->

— from the apparent sciences in which you breathe, so that we can delve into the doctrines and deal with the sciences," as he said:

"And when you said, 'O Moses, we cannot endure one kind of food, so call upon your Lord to bring forth for us from what the earth grows — its herbs, its cucumbers, its garlic, its lentils, and its onions.' He said, 'Would you exchange what is better for what is inferior?'"

He said: You seek what is inferior and nearer, and you substitute it for something that is better.

(Go down to Egypt, for there you will have what you have asked for.)
He says: Go back to the apparent speaker, and you will find in him what you have asked for. Egypt here is a parable for the speaker, including the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him), "I am the city of knowledge and its door." So they were presented with the interpretation and the one who was appointed for them to perform it, and they turned to the apparent and waded in it, in the waves of its seas and the stream of its currents. They have not interpreted it, and they have gone out into the appearance of the past, and they have become a people of opinions and imitations, and of what the souls adorn for them — until they asked Moses, as God the Almighty described, that He show them aloud, and He says:

"Then the thunderbolt seized you while you were looking on."
The thunderbolt is death, and that is the death of the senses from the true knowledge by which is the life of souls. So they died from their thoughts, and they became as the Almighty said — and He is the most truthful of those who say:

(The dead are not alive, and they perceive not when they will be resurrected.)

Then Allah gave them life, and Moses commanded that the suffixes and preachers be established again for them, according to what they had been, and Aaron appointed them for them.

<!-- page 217 -->

So He revived them and brought them back to life, which is the saying of the Almighty, and He is the most truthful of those who say:

(The dead are not alive, and they do not feel when they will be resurrected.)

Then Allah commanded that the suffixes and preachers be raised up again for them, according to what they had been, and Aaron appointed them for them. So He revived them and brought them back to life, which is what He says:

"Then We raised you up after your death, that perhaps you would be grateful. And We shaded you with clouds."

He says: We have placed between you and the upper limits the barrier of the physical speaker. You take shelter from it, and you benefit from its light, safe from being burned by the kindness of the upper limits.

(And do not worry about the manna and the salwā; eat of the good things with which We have provided you.)
(And they did not wrong Us, but they were wronging themselves.)

Manna is derived from gratitude, for Allah says (interpretation of the meaning):
(Allah has bestowed favor upon us and protected us from the punishment of the scorching wind.)

He said:
(Rather, may Allah bestow favor upon you for having guided you to faith, if you are truthful.)

Whoever takes knowledge about the saints of God and their limits has received the manna and the salwā, and all good things.

The people of the apparent claimed that the manna is (al-Tarangin) (1), and the salwā is a bird —

(1) In copy (X) it is mentioned as (Trogon).

<!-- page 218 -->

— resembling a quail (1), a bird whose truth is not known. The truth is what the suffixes have done, and the upper wings have led to the knowledge with which they feed the people from their limits.

(Eat of the good things with which We have provided you.)
That is: take of what you have gained of knowledge — better than what you have been provided.

(And they did not wrong Us, but they wronged themselves.)
It means: what they have spent of what they have heard, what they have shown, and what they have left behind.

Regarding the words of the Almighty:
"And when We said, 'Enter this village and eat from it wherever you wish.'"

His interpretation is that the village means the city, and the city, as we mentioned, is like the Imam, because it is a gathering of knowledge and wisdom — like the way the city gathers good things and grace. This is what they were commanded: to accept the apparent revelation of Moses, and what was prescribed for them of the laws of religion, which is the acceptance of tradition and obedience to the foundation without argument.

(And enter the gate in prostration.)
And like the foundation chapter, as we mentioned from the saying of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), "I am the city of knowledge and its door." So they were ordered to establish the apparent and the inward, and to submit to the foundation of Moses — who was Aaron at that time. (And say, "Ḥiṭṭa.") He said: The people of the apparent take it to mean, "Put down our sins for us." But if this saying could put down sins, no sinner would be left unforgiven; rather, it is a word that indicates degeneration and submission to the limits of the speaker — that is, they acknowledged those of his time from the suffixes, and after him from the imams in —

(1) In copy (X), it is mentioned as (obesity).

<!-- page 219 -->

— the role of the speaker is to remove sins from you, as he says:
(We will forgive you your sins, and We will increase the doers of good.)
It means that the workers increase their reward after forgiveness.

(So those who wronged changed the saying to other than what had been said to them.)
Injustice, as we have said in the language, is to put a thing out of its place — meaning that they changed the name of the imamate, so that they put in it other than its people, and put its people in a position other than theirs.

And the Almighty said:
"And We appointed for Moses thirty nights, and We completed them with ten more, so the appointed time of his Lord was forty nights."

This is because he ordered the establishment of forty limits — ten of which are the upper limits, and we have mentioned them, and thirty besides them, which are the lower pure limits: the twelve suffixes, the twelve ḥujjas, and the imams — because the seventh of them becomes the speaker. These are thirty persons who worship Allah. Moses ordered them to remain without him, and Allah the Almighty completed them to forty with the upper ten that are above him. So Moses worked at their establishment, and his brother Aaron succeeded him over the Children of Israel. This is what He says:

(Moses said to his brother Aaron, "Succeed me among my people.")

When they left themselves, Moses was absent from them in what Allah the Almighty commanded him to do — the establishment of the ḥudūd. So they were tempted by some of the sons of the suffixes, and the likes of the suffixes in the subtlety of the cows, and their children were the ones who took from them and were raised by them, like the calves that —

<!-- page 220 -->

— are the calves, and one of them is the calf. So the people of Moses took a man from the sons of the suffixes and raised him up for themselves, as the Almighty said:

(And the people of Moses took, after him, from their ornaments a calf — a body that lowed.)

He says: They took from what was the ornament of faith for you — words that they had memorized — and gathered them to one of the beneficiaries of the suffixes who does not master the statement, having a belly of words but no statement in it, as is the bellow, which is the sound that comes out from the nostrils (1) and is not cut off by the tongue and lips, so that it would be clear words rather than mere expression.

And the Almighty said:
(Did they not see that it could not speak to them?)
That is: it does not speak to them the words of truth, (and does not guide them to a way) from the ways of truth.

(They took it, and they were wrongdoers.)
That is: they put it in the wrong place. We have mentioned that injustice in language is to put a thing out of its place. So they set it up in the place of Aaron, as the Almighty said:

(He said, "This is your god and the god of Moses, but he forgot.")

"At least, do they not see that it does not speak to them, and that it does not possess for them any harm or benefit?"

(And Aaron had said to them before, "O my people, you are only being tested by it. And indeed, your Lord is the Most Merciful, so follow me and obey my command.")

(1) It is mentioned in version (e) as (al-Khayāshīm).

<!-- page 221 -->

(They said, "We will not cease being devoted to it until Moses returns to us.")

When Moses had established the limits that Allah the Almighty commanded him to establish (1), he said: he does not speak of what was done above him after him — and we have mentioned them — and this is what the Almighty said:

"And We appointed for Moses thirty nights, and We completed them with ten more, so the appointed time of his Lord was completed at forty nights. And Moses said to his brother Aaron, 'Succeed me among my people, and reform, and do not follow the way of the corrupters.'"

"And when Moses came to Our appointed time, and his Lord spoke to him, he said, 'My Lord, show me Yourself, that I may look upon You.'"

This is because when Moses worked at establishing the limits — that is, at the appointed time of his Lord, the one whose time was set for him, and who is his upper limit, to benefit according to what He had specified, his appointed time for him in the place where he was met by revelation — he made Aaron his successor over his people, and set him up to perform the outward in which he was standing, and the inward, which is the limit of his foundation, Aaron.

The Samaritan envied him. He was one of those who had come to Moses and shown him acceptance outwardly, but in the inward of his command was contrary. So he appealed to the weak among the people of Moses, and showed them what Pharaoh used to impersonate, and spoke subtly about it, and longed for it in an interpretation. He set up before Aaron a man from some of the respondents who belonged to him — one who is multiplied by action, for example, as you may have mentioned earlier.

So the people of Moses were most enchanted after him, and this is what the Almighty said:

"And what made you hasten ahead of your people, O Moses?"

(1) It is mentioned in version (S) as (worship him).

<!-- page 222 -->

(He said, "They are close upon my track, and I hastened to You, my Lord, that You may be pleased.")

He said, "Indeed, We have tried your people in your absence, and the Samaritan has misled them."

We will mention this in its proper place after the interpretation of what we have already mentioned.

(My Lord said, "I am the least of you.")
From what he said, praise be to Him.

So Moses said: Here, what is meant by his Lord is his educator with wisdom — who is his upper limit, who breathed it into him by revelation from Allah, may He be glorified and exalted. This is known in the tongue of the Arabs: the owner of a matter has his Lord, as they say, "the lord of the slave," "the lord of the house," and "the lord of the garment," and similar to that — such as what Allah narrated from Yūsuf (peace be upon him) to the king who came from him:

(Return to your lord and ask him about the case of the women who cut their hands.)

He said:
(As for one of you, he will give his lord wine to drink.)

And Moses said:
(My Lord, show me, that I may look upon You.)

By this he means: looking at all that he had of knowledge, up to the last limit of knowledge — because he asked to consider the limit that is connected to him from above, and he watched. In the language, it is without the sight of the eye, as one who says to another, "be of consideration in my matter." So Moses asked for an increase in the vision of knowledge beyond what He had given him, and He specified it for him. Either Moses asked to look at Bāri' al-Barāyā, who is mentioned above, and he was of knowledge to the extent of prophecy — and this is contrary to the one who is below him in knowledge, to see —


<!-- page 223 -->

This is what is prepared for him — or rather, the question of whether it lies within the power of human beings to look upon the angels at all. For the dense physicality of human nature does not possess the power to gaze upon the subtle spiritual king, nor to hear his speech as one human being hears another, nor to be united with what is united with him. The prophets reach their upper limit among the angels only through a severe hardship that befalls them, since the strength of their nature is not equal to it. It was said that when revelation came upon the Messenger of Allah, he was overcome as though by a swoon and an anguish: sweat would pour from him, his body would grow heavy so that he could not bear it, and his consciousness would be drawn inward — so that, on the outward surface, he did not know who was present with him, nor recognize the speech of the one addressing him. For this reason, in the early days of his mission, they said of him that he had gone mad, as is alluded to in the verse:

"What does he speak from? — i.e. nothing but a revelation revealed."

(Quran 53:3–4; cf. Quran 68:51)

And if a person were addressed by some animal that he saw, or had grown familiar with, or by a tree, or by stones when he saw them and recognized them, his nature would not have the power to bear it. How then could he be spoken to about what he does not know, or know what he does not see? Therefore Allah said — and He is the truest of those who speak:

"And had We made him an angel, We would have made him [appear as] a man, and We would have covered them with that which they cover themselves."

(Quran 6:9)

And He said:

"Your companion has not gone astray, nor has he erred. Nor does he speak from [his own] desire. It is but a revelation revealed, taught to him by one of great power, of sound judgment, who became poised — while he was on the highest horizon."

(Quran 53:2–7)

— and on through His words:

"And he certainly saw him in another descent, at the Lote-Tree of the Utmost Boundary (Sidrat al-Muntaha)."

(Quran 53:13–14)

225 / 15

<!-- page 224 -->

Most of the commentators among the people of the apparent (ahl al-zahir) said that what is meant by this is Jibril, and that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ saw him twice on the night of his ascension. We have already mentioned that the Isra' was in his spirit, and most of them have said the same about how the revelation came down. Some held that he saw Jibril, but claimed that Jibril appeared to him in the form of Dihya al-Kalbi — just as those of dubious belief claimed that Allah saw al-Bari al-Baraya, the Most-Remembered. And just as they claimed that Allah Almighty descended from the heaven and entered into a tree, and that He spoke to Moses as the speech of human beings is heard — exalted and majestic is He, and high is the Almighty above what the wrongdoers say. Most of the reports on this rest on what we have already mentioned: that he (peace be upon him) heard the voice of the revelation as a sense like the clanging of a chain.

It is reported concerning Moses (peace be upon him) that he heard a sound from the tree like the sound of a cat, and similar reports — and that was the speech of the king (the angel), which is not like the speech of dense human beings. The speech of human beings is thick only because it comes out of the form of physicality, whereas the subtleties of the spiritual realm are otherwise, because what is spiritual was not drawn into a corporeal apparatus. Human speech is thicker still because it issues from the narrowness of the throat into the mouth — like the sound issuing from the narrow end of a horn¹ when it reaches its wide end, which is the equivalent of the thick mouth. So the general public claimed that Moses asked that Allah Almighty be seen — exalted and sanctified is He above what they say. Allah has kept His guardians (awliya') far from being ignorant about His power in the like of this, and from being incapable in it.

He said:

"The Word of God"

— we have mentioned that he is the upper limit, raised up by Allah Almighty; and concerning

¹ In version (e) it reads "al-Bun."
p. 226

<!-- page 225 -->

His command — blessed is His name — and His words, what is meant by him is the one who is suggested to by revelation. This is well known in the Arabic language in which the Qur'an was sent down, as they say: "the world preached to its people, addressed them concerning her sons, warned them, and admonished them" — and this is not by words coming from her.

The Almighty said:

"You will never see Me; but look at the mountain — if it remains in its place, then you shall see Me."

(Quran 7:143)

The mountain here stands as a likeness for the suffixes (lawahiq) and for the united limit (hadd) of Moses. When all things had been asked of him, Moses said in the following words:

((Show me [Yourself] that I may look upon You))

He said to him: That is what you cannot do, for it is not your limit, and your strength cannot bear it. If you wish to know that, you are one of your own followers as regards what lies above your limit — and if you see it standing firm in its place, and you yourself endure, then you will endure that from Me.

"And when his Lord revealed Himself to the mountain"

(Quran 7:143)

This expression involves a fronting and a delay (taqdim wa-ta'khir) according to what is current in the language of the Arabs. He is saying: when [the mountain] appeared to the camel — meaning, by way of explanation, that "his Lord" here is Moses's nurturer who reared him with his wisdom, and that this is what Moses (peace be upon him) did.

((He made it level))

— He is saying: you have been humbled and brought low.¹

¹ In copy (e) it came (and it was tucked).
p. 227

<!-- page 226 -->

When Moses saw this, he was struck, and he knew that had he been given what he asked for, the same would have befallen him.

"And Moses fell down unconscious."

(Quran 7:143)

— fainting from fear at what he had ventured to ask of Him, so that his state was changed.

"When he awoke, he said, 'Glory be to You; I repent to You.'"

(Quran 7:143)

So al-Bari reminded him of the duty of setting each thing in its proper place. He repented of what he had asked for, and admitted that he was the foremost in believing and affirming that there is no path for anyone to receive what is not within his limit.

"He said: 'O Moses, I have chosen you above [other] people with My messages and My words. So take what I have given you and be among the grateful.'"

(Quran 7:144)

He is saying: he is suggested to by the revelation from Allah Almighty, telling him that He supported him by the message — by the apparent and by the invitation to accept it through imitation and affirmation — and the words of the Almighty:

((And by My words))

— mean by the statement (bayan) that He confirmed, which is the interpretation (ta'wil) of what his apparent statement called for.
