This may be confirmed for the one who took it by imitation of him and by belief in it, which the Almighty named "His words" and attributed to Himself in honor of him. As most of them said:

"And know that whatever you have of any thing is from Him."

"Take what I have given you and be among the grateful."

(Quran 7:144)

And the Almighty said:
p. 228

<!-- page 227 -->

— He is saying: take what you have been given, give thanks for it, and do not seek what lies beyond it and is not for you.

Then the Almighty said:

"And We wrote for him on the tablets of every kind — admonition, and detail for everything. So take it with determination, and command your people to take the best of it."

(Quran 7:145)

The tablets (al-alwah), according to the interpretation, are the suffixes (lawahiq) that establish the foundation of the science of interpretation — we have mentioned their number and their place. The meaning is that whatever is established is within the limit of the suffixes — everything that a person needs is found there, lacking nothing of knowledge, exposition, and admonition.

"And command your people to take the best of it"

— meaning by the statement (bayan), which is the interpretation (ta'wil) by which the apparent revelation is established and becomes rooted in hearts and minds. By it the argument is proved against those who deny the rulings of the Shari'a, who contest the outward and claim that its people have worshipped it — including the People of the Bosoms (ahl al-jawhar), the heretics, and others who appeal against the Shari'a of Islam.

The esoteric interpretation (ta'wil al-batin) is what bears witness to the outward and proves its validity against the one who denies and doubts it, who is ignorant of its meanings, of what is intended by it, and of what He has made of it a proof and an example. Like the one who denies the meaning of purity by water, of prayer with water, of bowing and prostrating, of facing the qibla and turning toward the Sacred House (al-Bayt al-Haram), of the pilgrimage (hajj) to Him, the circumambulation (tawaf) around Him, and the standing in the stations and rites of Hajj¹ — and so on, of all the worship by which Allah is worshipped, of what He has made lawful for them and what He has forbidden. He has mentioned this at length, yet many have come out who do not know its interpretation.

¹ In a copy (S) it came (and his poet).
p. 229

<!-- page 228 -->

Nor did He give an example to one who denies it — when he denied it and became one of those who deny it, and did not know the truth of its interpretation from one of the scholars, while he preferred his own opinion — he has brought them out to the analogy of al-Bari with His creation, to the use of their opinions and their measurements (qiyas) and their whims in the religion of Allah, to the prohibition of what He has permitted, to lying about the Messenger of Allah, and to distorting the interpretation according to their opinions — into whatever their minds have adorned for them. This is the way of all the public.

But whoever seeks the interpretation through His guardians (awliya') — whom He has appointed for him, and to whom He has entrusted His knowledge — and learns from them what they have, has been benefited; Allah unites him with the truth of His monotheism (tawhid), denies for him any metaphor, and he comes to know the truth of how Allah Almighty is to be worshipped by His servants, what He has made lawful and what He has forbidden, and he comes to know the sound (sahih) from the unsound (saqim)¹ of the reports from the Messenger of Allah ﷺ and other matters in which people have differed. For interpretation clarifies and reveals this; it is its standard, its scale, its witness, and its very self.

For this reason, it is the best of speech (ahsan al-hadith) and the best of sciences. And Allah Almighty commanded Moses to command his people to follow it, which is what He meant by His saying:

"Follow the best of what has been sent down to you from your Lord."

(Quran 39:55)

And the Almighty said:

"Allah has sent down the best of speech."

(Quran 39:23)

And Moses returned, as Allah Almighty has said:

"To his people, angry and grieved. He said: 'O my people, did your Lord not promise you a good promise? Did the covenant seem too long to you, or did you desire that wrath should descend upon you

¹ In the copy (e) it came (al-Musaqim).
230

<!-- page 229 -->

from your Lord, so you broke your promise to me?'"

(Quran 20:86)

This was because of what they had committed after him by taking up the calf, and by turning away from Aaron and from what he had set up on the surface.

"They said, 'We did not break our promise to you of our own will'"

(Quran 20:87)

— meaning: not by our own choice.

"But we were made to carry burdens from the ornaments of the people"

— that is, from the words of Pharaoh that he had likened for us and adorned for us, which he made us carry through an interpretation he set up for us.

"So we threw it down" — meaning: we cast off those affairs once their corruption had become clear to us.

((So likewise did the Samaritan cast))

— He is saying that what the Samaritan also threw at us was [a parallel] of what was done to us; but this was the saying of those who had turned away from him, who had been shown the corruption [of his doctrine] before he came.

Moses said to them what Allah has related concerning them:

((And when [their bad deed] fell into their hands and they saw that they had gone astray))

— they kept saying: Why are we to be utterly destroyed and brought to ruin, to be among the losers?

((And Moses threw down the tablets))

— as Allah has mentioned concerning him.

"And he seized his brother by his head, dragging him toward him. [Aaron] said: 'O son of my mother, the people overpowered me and nearly killed me; do not let the enemies gloat over me, and do not place me

231

<!-- page 230 -->

with the wrongdoing people.'"

(Quran 7:150)

He said in another place:

"He said: 'O Aaron, what prevented you, when you saw them go astray, from following me? Did you then disobey my command?' He said: 'O son of my mother, do not seize me by my beard, nor by my head. I feared you would say, "You divided the Children of Israel and did not heed my word."'"

(Quran 20:92–94)

The throwing of the tablets means that he silenced the preachers and exhorters as a chastisement of his people, when they breached the covenant after him. We have mentioned that the example of these [exhorters] is like the tablets in which the sciences reside — the upper limit (hadd) in which the standard is established, which is also called the Preserved Tablet (al-Lawh al-Mahfuz), as we mentioned above. And he took his brother by the head — he seized the apparent from his hand, which was his leadership, because [Aaron] had succeeded him over it; and his beard is like the substrate that was erected for him, lest some of this be ascribed to his followers — when he cut off the invitation (da'wa) and raised the statement (bayan) for his community as a chastisement for what they had done after him. Aaron then feared that this might come to him, and so asked Moses to forgive him. That is what is said:

"O Lord, forgive me and my brother, and admit us into Your mercy. Indeed, You are the Most Merciful of the merciful."

(Quran 7:151)

— not, as the public claimed (the people of the apparent), that Moses struck the earth, according to the Torah that God sent down to him, that it was made of emerald tablets and broke when he became angry with his people, and that he took his brother's beard and his head and dragged him along the earth. God has far too high a regard for Moses to have done such an act with a book that He sent down — and likewise his brother, who is a noble prophet whom God associated in the message — even if some of them said, in a book that came down from some of their brothers, that he struck the earth with it,

232

<!-- page 231 -->

or worked with one of his slaves, and took him by his beard or by his head and dragged him to himself, so as to deny it of himself, and was ashamed and grieved to be reminded of its likeness. Yet it is easy for them to attribute this and the like of it to the saints of God whom Allah has chosen from His creation, and to His sons whom He appointed for His servants and with whom He is pleased — to suppose they could do such things. Allah has transcended this, and kept His guardians far from such ascriptions.

Then Moses said to the Samaritan what Allah has narrated of his words:

((So what is your case, O Samaritan?))

(Quran 20:95)

— that is: what is your affair that you have brought about, and by which the community was fascinated?

((He said: 'I saw what they did not see'))

(Quran 20:96)

— I saw a vision before myself other than what you (meaning Moses and Aaron) saw; and it was followed by the support that you had supported.

"So I took a handful from the trace of the messenger and tossed it"

(Quran 20:96)

He is saying: I saw for myself the strength of the message and the support, and so I claimed to act accordingly. I set up the calf for myself, called him to it, and opened the door to him by what I had asked of myself — then I renounced that, meaning: I left it.

The public claimed that the Samaritan had seen Jibril come to Moses riding on a donkey, and that he took his handful from the places where the hoof of Jibril's donkey had trodden, and made use of it, and called them to it, and threw that dust into [the calf]. It is fine for them to say this, and were it not for the length of the discourse, we would have noted with each interpretation just how corrupt is what they have brought and what they have interpreted. Yet it stands, and whoever hears the truth hears it, and it becomes clear that what they have said is corrupted by it, in sha' Allah.

¹ It is mentioned in the copy (M) (they said).
233


<!-- page 232 -->

When the Samaritan turned back from what he had been, Moses could do no more than what he did with him. This was similar to what Moses' companion (al-Khidr) did when he forbade him from opening the door, as Allah relates in His saying:

"He said: 'Go, for in this life it shall be yours to say "No touching!" And you have an appointment that you shall not fail to keep.'" (Quran 20:97)

That is: depart from our affair, for you have likened it to common people; do not speak of it to anyone, and they shall not contend with you.

"And you have an appointment that you shall not fail to keep" — meaning the appointed time of the Hereafter.

"And look upon your god to which you remained devoted; we shall surely burn it, then scatter its ashes broadcast into the sea." (Quran 20:97)

Here, the calf is what the Samaritan set up for the people of Moses in his absence. Moses had to do to it what he did. He says: We shall burn with the truth the falsehood that has been established. The outward (zahir) without its inward (batin) is like the calf, and the inward is like the sea — as we have already mentioned in its proper place above.

Moses dismantled the Samaritan's falsehood, which did not require shattering with the essence of the shari'ah; he was content to refute it on the surface, because of the weakness of that falsehood and its corruption — for that was Moses' command. Among the people of Moses were those who had not been seduced by haste and had remained obedient to Aaron. Others had been beguiled by the Samaritan, but then his corruption became clear to them, and they left him. Yet strife had already taken hold of most of them. They remained as they had been, neglecting the duties that Moses had laid upon them, and leaning toward what Pharaoh had permitted them; the matter of seditions (fitnah) took firm hold of them.

Moses saw that he should leave them to their symptoms,

(1) In version (E) the reading is "not heard."

<!-- page 233 -->

since there was nothing about them that strengthened the causes of guidance within them. So Aaron took his place among them, and Moses ordered him to set up his suffixes (lawahiq) and limits (hudud); Aaron carried that out. Then He said:

"And when the anger of Moses was appeased, he took up the tablets." (Quran 7:154)

— meaning that he restored the suffixes to them. (In its variant reading: "So I have transcribed here that Aaron transcribed from his suffixes and placed them under his limits.")

"…and in their inscription was guidance and mercy for those who fear their Lord." (Quran 7:154)

— meaning the believers who fear and obey the ruler of their time.

Moses then turned to his people, calling them to enter into a foundational matter, which is what Allah Almighty has recounted in His saying:

"O my people, enter the Holy Land which Allah has prescribed for you, and do not turn back, for then you would become losers." (Quran 5:21)

— meaning, enter into a foundational matter and my argument (hujjah); and we have already mentioned that he is like the earth. Do not turn away from him to oppose him, lest you lose what you have already done of good deeds.

"They said: 'O Moses, in it is a powerful people, and we shall not enter it until they leave it. If they leave it, then we shall enter.'" (Quran 5:22)

— meaning that those who had rallied to Aaron's command had become enemies to them. They said: "We will not be united with them in a single matter at all."

(1) In copy (X) the reading is "and they swore allegiance."

<!-- page 234 -->

"Two men from among those who feared, upon whom Allah had bestowed His blessing, said: 'Enter upon them through the gate; for when you enter it, you will surely be victorious.'" (Quran 5:23)

The gate here is Aaron, as the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "I am the city of knowledge, and Aaron is its gate."

"When you enter it, you will be victorious" — that is, you will overcome them because of your great numbers, and the rank and station will be yours. This is because they refused to enter into the matter of Aaron, and they did what they did. They are the very ones who, at the time and place appointed for them, had no gathering on their side.

"And put your trust in Allah, if you are believers." (Quran 5:23) — that is, make your reliance upon Allah, if you are truthful.

"They said: 'O Moses, we shall never enter it as long as they are in it. So you and your Lord go and fight; we shall sit here.'" (Quran 5:24)

They say: "Go, you and the Lord (rabb) whom you have raised up for your people" — meaning Aaron. So they set him up as a contention against those who disagreed with them, since they relied on themselves because of their great numbers; while few of the believers from Moses' people followed Moses.

"He said: 'My Lord, indeed I have no power over any but myself and my brother, so distinguish between us and the wicked (fasiq) folk.'" (Quran 5:25)

He said: Do not join us together with those who have committed corruption, that is, those who have turned away from Your command. Moses said this because none of his people remained firm upon his command except his brother; there was no one else left for them. He said that he had no power over any but himself and his brother. And this is the same Moses who said to his people:

<!-- page 235 -->

"And when Moses said to his people: 'O my people, you have wronged yourselves by taking the calf.'" (Quran 2:54)

— meaning, you have placed it where it does not belong, if you obey the one whom Allah has not commanded you to obey.

"'So repent to your Maker and kill yourselves; that is better for you in the sight of your Maker.'" (Quran 2:54)

He says: Overcome them — that is, your souls (nufus) — in what they have called you to of falsehood; and conquer them in favor of the truth, so that you make them dead to falsehood. Allah Almighty sent down upon them the trembling that shakes hearts, so that Moses had mercy on them, hoping they would turn back from their misguidance, as the Almighty says:

"And when the trembling seized them, he said: 'My Lord, if You had willed, You could have destroyed them before, and me along with them. Will You destroy us for what the foolish among us have done? It is only Your trial by which You lead astray whom You will and guide whom You will. You are our Protector, so forgive us and have mercy on us; You are the best of forgivers. And ordain for us in this world good and in the Hereafter; indeed, we have turned to You.' He said: 'My punishment — I strike with it whom I will; but My mercy embraces all things. So I shall write it down for those who are God-fearing and pay the zakat, and those who in Our signs believe.'" (Quran 7:155–156)

— meaning what they did in his time. "And me too" — meaning the error he made when he said: "My Lord, show me, that I may look upon You" (Quran 7:143) — for that was what they took from him.

<!-- page 236 -->

"…those who follow the Messenger, the unlettered Prophet whom they find written with them in the Torah and the Gospel; he commands them to good and forbids them from evil, makes the good things lawful for them and the impure things unlawful, and removes from them their burden and the shackles that were upon them. Those who believe in him, honor him, support him, and follow the light that has been sent down with him — those are the successful." (Quran 7:157)

Allah Almighty informed Moses, in the end, that He will have mercy on his followers only on those who reach the time of Muhammad ﷺ, believe in him, and believe in his signs — those Imams being his Imams.

"And follow the light that has been sent down with him" — this is the exposition of the interpretation (ta'wil) by which he enlightens, and to whom he has entrusted it.

"Those are the successful" — that is, those who succeed and are saved from torment, from among the people of Moses and those who believe in the signs before him, who are the Imams of Moses and his argument.

Then Allah Almighty mentioned His cursing them and making them defiled, and the punishment by transformation (maskh) that befell them. Then He recounted these in different places in the Book of the Almighty:

"Enter the gate prostrating" (Quran 4:154) — He said:

"Do not transgress on the Sabbath" (Quran 4:154)

(1) In copy (E) the reading is "their order."

<!-- page 237 -->

— that is, do not transgress what is forbidden to you. As the Almighty says:

"And We took from them a solemn covenant." (Quran 4:154)

— meaning the covenant taken upon them. And the words of the Almighty:

"Because of their breaking their covenant…you do not (forget the companions of the Sabbath)." (Quran 4:155 / 2:65) — He said:

"And (because of) their hearts being hard, they distort the words from their places." (Quran 5:13) — He said:

"And We made some of them apes and swine, and the worshippers of the taghut." (Quran 5:60)

"And you have known of those of you who transgressed on the Sabbath, and We said to them: 'Be apes, despised.' So We made it an exemplary punishment for those before them and those after them, and an admonition to the God-fearing." (Quran 2:65–66)

I mean by their being transformed into apes the reversal of their faces — those faces they used to depict in religion (i.e., in their interpretations) — so they turned into images of disbelief, which is the ugliest of forms, just as apes and swine are the ugliest of images among animals. Many of those upon this (false) interpretation are like a swine in the form of a man.

Then Allah removed from the people of Moses the foundational virtue and the explanation (bayan) within it. The interpretation of the words of the Almighty:

"And it is forbidden for them; for forty years they shall wander in the earth." (Quran 5:26)

— that is, they shall be in doubt, doubting the foundation; and Allah seized Aaron from among them.

<!-- page 238 -->

The matter of interpretation and explanation was cut off, and they wandered in the earth — as Allah Almighty had already decreed that the Imams are not established except from the descendants of the foundation. Aaron left no son fit for that, and the one who would have succeeded him was not suitable, being a child. Moses' patience was long.

Statement and foundation were not established. They came to know the merit of what they had been forbidden, and they blamed themselves for what they had done. They were dealt with accordingly, and Allah commanded Moses to command them to choose from among themselves a man fit to be the argument (hujjah) of Moses among them, as He said:

"And when Moses said to his people: 'Allah commands you to slaughter a cow.' They said: 'Do you take us in mockery?' He said: 'I seek refuge in Allah from being among the ignorant.'" (Quran 2:67)

In the interpretation (ta'wil), the cow is like the arguments (hujaj), and slaughtering is like taking the covenant — that is, choose a man from among you upon whom the covenant of arguments shall be taken, and an argument shall be established for you. We attribute the slaughter to them because they were the ones who performed it.

"They said: 'Do you take us in mockery?'" — meaning, do you mock us when the nation is establishing arguments?

"He said: 'I seek refuge in Allah from being among the ignorant.'" — that is, were I to do this on my own opinion, I would be among the ignorant; but Allah commanded it. He made that available to you, even though his (true) reference was to the son of Aaron afterward — for Allah Almighty had appointed him to establish that for him, and for his son after him.

"They said: 'Pray for us to your Lord that He may make clear to us what she is.'" (Quran 2:68)

— that is, show us the man who is the argument over you in your life, and your guardian (wali) after your death. Ask Allah to show us in his qualities, so that we may stand upon him and know whom we are choosing for this matter.

<!-- page 239 -->

"He said: 'Indeed He says that she is a cow neither old nor virgin, but middling between the two. So do what you are commanded.'" (Quran 2:68)

He says: Neither old nor a young heifer — meaning, she is not from those who have become weakened in supporting (the faith) with knowledge, nor from anyone newly hadith (i.e., new) to it, but middling between the two extremes.

"So do what you are commanded" — meaning, what is the course of the words of this man whom we choose, and the description of his statement?

"'He says that she is a yellow cow, bright in color, pleasing to the beholders.'" (Quran 2:69)

He says: He is a follower of a fair statement, not tainted by a bad one, and there is no change in him.

"They said: 'Pray for us to your Lord to make clear to us what she is, for cows look alike to us, and indeed, if Allah wills, we shall be guided.'" (Quran 2:70)

They say: We have multiplied the description, so that whoever is fit to be an argument is suspected; we shall be guided by the statement of what we are charged with, if Allah wills.

"He said: 'Indeed He says that she is a cow not subjected to plow the earth nor to water the field; one of no blemish, of one color (with no other).' They said: 'Now you have brought the truth.' So they slaughtered her, but they hardly did so." (Quran 2:71)

(1) In copy (e) the reading is "cow."

<!-- page 240 -->

He says: He is an argument that does not humble himself to the people of the apparent (zahir) by speaking with them when they have no rank.

"Nor water the field" — meaning, he does not approach them with any statement.

"To plow the earth" — that is, ploughing it; he says, he works with the interpretation of the foundation and sets his affair in order.

"So they slaughtered her, but they hardly did so" — because of that.

Moses then entrusted him and appointed him the successor of Aaron's son until he should reach the age fit for the Imamate, when the matter could be handed over to him. That was when Moses was brought close to his death; and it is not necessary that the people should remain without a guardian, so Joshua son of Nun was made the executor of the will and the caliph.

Then He said:

"And when you killed a soul and disputed about it, but Allah brings out what you were concealing. So We said: 'Strike him with part of it.' Thus Allah revives the dead and shows you His signs, that you may understand." (Quran 2:72–73)

He meant by His saying "You killed a soul" — that is, the Imam: they pushed him away from his right, which is Aaron (peace be upon him), and they wronged him. We have already mentioned above that injustice (zulm) is like killing. He says: You pushed his right aside, and you set up your own appointee in his place; you forbade him from setting up the suffixes and from publishing the statement and the interpretation. You made this a covenant among yourselves, and he was prevented.

<!-- page 241 -->

You kept him from the weak of the nation, and you deceived them into thinking that he is the foundation by right.

"And Allah will bring out what you were concealing." (Quran 2:72) — Concealing is suppression. It has been said that some of them had turned away from the Samaritan's command when they saw his shame, and that a group of them were obedient to Aaron — residents who did not follow anything of the Samaritan's order, and they are the fewest of the enemies. As for those who followed the Samaritan: the people of obedience denied what they had done and established the argument, but they did not accept it. That was because of Aaron's restraint with them, and his having given them permission. He said:

"And he had already said to them: 'O my people, you have only been tried by it, and indeed your Lord is the Most Merciful; so follow me and obey my command.'" (Quran 20:90)

Their answer was as Allah Almighty has told us:

"They said: 'We will not cease to be devoted to it until Moses returns to us.'" (Quran 20:91)

So they pushed him (Aaron) aside from his right, and they pushed those who obeyed him from their ranks and stations. He said:

"Strike him with part of it" (Quran 2:73)

— that is, they defended (themselves). For this is what happened between them and those who were powerful in knowledge. As for the weak and the ignorant, they kept it secret; and there is no right for falsehood, as the Almighty has told us:

"And Allah will bring out what you were concealing." (Quran 2:72)

— meaning, it is the right of the Imam. And this was the way of the nation of Muhammad (his progeny)…


<!-- page 242 -->

This rests on his command and the foundation he laid down for me, as he (peace be upon him) said: "You shall follow the ways of the nations before you, sole for sole and foot for foot, so much so that even if they entered the hole of a lizard, you would enter it after them." The foundation is the soul, because its place is from the speaker. So the Messenger of Allah (may the prayers of Allah be upon him) said: "I am the city of knowledge and Ali (1) is its gate" — because knowledge, too, resides in the soul, just as the knowledge of the true speaker does, which is the esoteric interpretation of what the outward revelation indicates. That knowledge resides in the foundation, and from him it is transmitted to the imams, and each imam is set in his own argument differently, since place, circumstance, and times all differ in that regard.

Among the messengers and imams (may Allah's prayers be upon them all), some are prepared in their own time and able to establish their argument — their followers, their proofs, their preachers, and their admonishers — across all matters belonging to their call in every island of the earth. Others are prepared and able in some regions but not in others, or are able to maintain some of their hudud but unable to maintain others, and still others live in times in which they are not prepared to establish any argument or proof at all. We have already mentioned the situation of some of them in that respect, and how some of them at certain times did not act.

What was set in motion by the people of Moses with the affair of the calf was the cause of what happened afterward — the killing of the prophets — and Allah the Almighty attributed this back to them, saying:

> "Say, 'Why then did you kill the prophets of Allah before, if you were believers? And Moses had certainly brought you clear proofs. Then you took the calf in worship after that, while you were wrongdoers.'"

Whoever establishes a foundation, and a matter arises from it, the good and the evil of it belong to him and accrue to him.

(1) In version (m): (verb).
(2) In copy (X): (and above).

<!-- page 243 -->

This is what the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) meant when he said: "Whoever sets a good sunnah and acts upon it, and others act upon it after him, has for himself its reward and the reward of those who work by it after him, without diminishing anything from their wages. And whoever sets a bad sunnah and acts upon it, and others act upon it after him, has its burden upon him and the burdens of those who work by it after him, without diminishing anything from their burdens."

The servant will be held accountable on the Day of Resurrection and questioned about it. He will be asked even about bloodshed and will say: "By Allah, I never shed blood." Then it will be said to him: "You spoke such-and-such a word, and from it the matter rose until blood was shed because of it, and so you are charged with it."

"Strike him with part of it" — that is, strike him so that Allah may bring the dead to life and show you His signs, that perhaps you might understand.

He says: strike the dead — meaning the dead of ignorance among you, each striking the other. The cow that he likened them to is the argument they were given, telling them that every person dead to the truth, if struck on his ear and on his heart by the interpretation of the foundation, becomes alive through what he gains from it. It is well established that Allah likens death to ignorance in more than one place in His Book, as He says:

> "They are dead, not alive, and they do not perceive when they will be resurrected."

And He says:

> "O you who have believed, respond to Allah and the Messenger when he calls you to that which gives you life."

— that is, to revive you through clear statement.

> "And He will show you His signs"

— that is, He will reveal to you, through whoever does that, some of His guardians.

<!-- page 244 -->

> "That perhaps you will understand"

— meaning their deeds, those who answered them.

Then the Almighty informed about the people of Moses who went astray after that. He said:

> "Then your hearts became hardened after that, being like stones or even harder."

That is, their hearts did not move to accept knowledge and wisdom; they were like the dead from among visible stones. Then He said:

> "And indeed, there are stones from which rivers burst forth."

That is, He is striking parables. Allah struck the stone as a parable for the foundation, for his steadfastness (1) and his firmness in his religion and conviction, and from him flow the ethnic suffixes — that is, the ten — and we have mentioned the interpretation of that above.

> "And there are some of them that split open and water comes out."

That is, among the preachers there is one who has solidity in religion, and from him the revival of knowledge is brought forth.

> "And there are some that fall down from fear of Allah."

He said: there may be one among the believers who does not reach the rank of the hudud, but who has firmness in his religion and strength, an officer submitting to a higher level out of fear of Allah's greatest remembrance.

(1) In copy (e): (for his aunt).

<!-- page 245 -->

The Story of Talut:

The imamate in the cycle of Moses ended with Talut, and this is what Allah the Almighty said:

> "And their prophet said to them, 'Indeed, Allah has sent to you Talut as a king.'"

— meaning as an imam. And among these is the saying of Allah the Almighty:

> "Or do they envy the people for what Allah has given them of His bounty? But We had already given the family of Ibrahim the Book and wisdom and conferred upon them a great kingdom. They said, 'How can he have kingship over us while we are more worthy of kingship than him, and he has not been given any measure of wealth?'"

He said: this is because of what they saw at that time of the suffixes — meaning hudud — and some of them held that he was the least learned of them. That is what they meant by their words: "And he has not been given abundance of wealth" — that is, knowledge that has not expanded for him as much as it has for us, so we are more deserving of the imamate than he is.

> "He said, 'Indeed, Allah has chosen him over you'"

— that is, He has selected him.

> "'And has increased him abundantly in knowledge and stature, and Allah gives His kingdom to whom He wills, and Allah is All-Encompassing, All-Knowing.'"

<!-- page 246 -->

He informed them that Allah had increased him in knowledge — and He made plain here that knowledge is wealth in the inner, hidden sense, while the body is the outer, apparent sense; that is, He widened them both in him together.

Talut was the imam of his time, and the one who claimed the imamate from among the people of rebellion (1) was Goliath. He and Talut were both prepared to argue which of them had the greater right to the front. So each of them gathered his people for the debate. And David was one of Talut's commanders — the one who walked with him, as the explainers said it appears that he had married Talut's daughter, and that David said: "Carry me with you." So David took three stones and put them in his pouch and walked with Talut.

His marriage to his daughter is that he joined some of his followers and family to the testament — as Shu'ayb son of Moses had done, and we have already mentioned this — and the three stones are three issues by which he countered Goliath and his companions. When Talut went out toward those he had chosen from among his callers, he informed them of what Allah the Almighty was about to test them with, and this is what He says:

> "And when Talut set out with the soldiers, he said, 'Indeed, Allah will be testing you with a river.'"

— that is, he is testing you with a knowledge that he conducts to you on the tongue of my speaker.

> "'So whoever drinks from it is not of me, and whoever does not taste of it is indeed of me — except one who takes a sip with his hand.'"

He said: except the one who has been blessed with the explanation, so that he knows it. This applies to those who are in genuine need of being prepared for the knowledge of the debate.

Goliath and his companions passed through that, and not one of them sought it from someone who was prepared for the debate. They asked it from another face — from their family and from others — and that is what afflicted them, and they were warned against it.

(1) In copy (S): received from (Ahl al-Taqbal).

<!-- page 247 -->

They took it only from the side of those preachers of theirs to whom the benefit of the first hands had been lost. For this reason the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade slaughtering an animal at the water — which is that the drinker drinks from it foolishly as an animal drinks — and he commanded drinking with the hands and with vessels, which are like the preachers. He said: "If you do not find them" — that is, the vessels — "then drink with your hands, for that is better for you." That is, if you do not find the preachers, then take the suffixes and the arguments directly, for they are better for you.

So Talut commanded his followers from among the believers not to take the knowledge they sought, by which to prepare themselves for the debate, except by means of his commanders, and he forbade them to take that from before the public. But only a few of them accepted it from him.

> "So they crossed it, he and those who believed with him. They said,"

— that is, those who turned back from him and did not accept from him, among those who disobeyed him —

> "'There is no power for us today against Goliath and his soldiers.'"

— that is, because when they disobeyed their guardians and took knowledge from one whom they had been forbidden to take from, they could not prevail (2) against him, though they had thought they would be victorious.

> "Those who were certain that they would meet Allah said,"

— meaning those who obeyed their guardians and took nothing except by their command, taking it from him —

> "'How many a small company has defeated a large company by the permission of Allah, and Allah is with the patient.'"

(1) In copy (e): the Kerr was retrieved.
(2) In version (E): (Bata'il).

<!-- page 248 -->

By "the few" they mean the few of their own party, and by "the many" the companions of Goliath. And the Almighty said:

> "And when they appeared before Goliath and his soldiers, they said, 'Our Lord, pour patience upon us, set our feet firm, and give us victory over the disbelieving people.'"

That is, they emerged for the debate after they had held back from advancing, because the one who had failed had broken ranks and disobeyed the command of the guardian of the time. He mingled with the rest and took from the one he had been forbidden to take from, and so they fell behind and perished. They were the majority of Talut's companions, as Allah mentioned about them:

> "So they drank from it, except for a few among them."

It is reported that the companions of Talut were four thousand, and three thousand of them were defeated and killed, while a thousand stood firm and defeated the companions of Goliath. He said:

> "So they defeated them by the permission of Allah, and David killed Goliath."

— with what David had prepared for him: he cut him down by it and overcame him, and overcame those who supported him. That is why it is reported in the traditions that he struck him with a stone and finished him with it — yet a stone does not do that. Rather, it means that he cut him down with the argument, and two men of his company suffered defeat through him and looked on at him.

<!-- page 249 -->

The Story of David:

The imamate passed to David after Talut (peace be upon them), and this is what Allah the Almighty said:

> "And Allah gave him kingship and wisdom."

That is, David encompassed the knowledge of the outward and the inward, and his son Solomon was entrusted by him with the matter of the inward, as He says:

> "And We gave David and Solomon knowledge, and they said, 'Praise be to Allah, who has favored us over many of His believing servants.'"

And the Almighty said:

> "And David and Solomon, when they judged concerning the field"

— the field is like cultivation —

> "when the sheep of the people grazed at night within it"

— that is, the people of the call partook of him at night, eating without respecting their proper bounds —

> "and We were witness to their judgment."

> "And We gave understanding of it to Solomon"

— that is, We made for him the knowledge of the judgment in that case, because the ruling on calling and preaching belongs to the argument without the imam.

<!-- page 250 -->

> "And to each We gave wisdom and knowledge."

Knowledge belongs to the speaker, and judgment belongs to the imam, to argue by his command for what is to be done.

The owner of the field has been assigned to him, which is the cultivator — that is, the one who is authorized (the ma'zun) to educate the believers. And the owner of the sheep is the preacher in one aspect, who in another aspect is other than the da'i. So the ma'zun mentioned that the people of this da'wah interacted with his companions who have permission to act as preachers in their upbringing, and they listened to them on the interpretation and corrupted them.

So Solomon told the preacher who opened himself to friends outside his own people that he is met by the people of his call to the extent of the people who corrupted him by drawing near to them. They go out of his call and turn to this one who corrupted his companions and ruined him by doing so, because he should have surrounded them and prevented them from opening the door, since they are within his sanctuary — even if they open it outwardly, for it is no concern of his, and the ruling on the outward agrees with this, by what we have said.

In the hadith it is narrated about the owner of the field and the owner of the sheep that the sheep grazed by night and that grazing at night is the evening meal — Solomon said: the people of the walls must take precaution with their walls during the day; if the people's sheep escape upon them, without their having released them in it, then they bear no responsibility — as we have mentioned regarding the responding ones approaching outwardly, who bear nothing of it if they do it of their own accord. He said: the owners of the livestock guard them at night; if they escape and ruin a thing, their owners guarantee the damage — and this is like the responding ones approaching in the inward sense, and the judgment upon them is by what we have mentioned, as well as what is outwardly evident.

It is also mentioned in the hadith that Solomon ruled in favor of the owners of the field by giving them the sheep that escaped

<!-- page 251 -->

to them at night, and the seedlings are managed for the people of the planting like them, to be paid as a fine — and this is the ruling acted upon in this matter to this day, both outwardly and inwardly. And the words of the Almighty:

> "And We subjected with David the mountains, exalting and the birds."

The mountains are like the proofs (hujjats), and the birds are like the preachers, and their exalting is their orientation toward those who respond to the call, educating and responding to David — that is, their harnessing to the call, which they are guided by him to.

> "And We taught him the making of garments to protect you from your might. Will you then be grateful?"

By this He meant what He taught David of the explanation and the argument, and commanded him to teach this to those who respond to his call, so as to immunize them from their strength and to defend them from their stabbing and to throw them with their arguments — this is like what the shield does in war by warding off blows and the stabbing of enemies.

And the Almighty said:

> "And We certainly gave David from Us a bounty. O mountains, exalt with him, and the birds."

We have already mentioned the interpretation of the mountains and the birds.

> "And We softened iron for him."

He says: walk with him where he walked, and repent — walking is biased toward the rider — and it was not that the mountains and the birds were walking outwardly with David where he walked. So the saying about this is the reality in the inward sense.

> "And iron was made for him."

That is, We made it easy for him — for it is hard to talk of, but iron is on the surface, even if it was made


Of an armor (1) that you did not have in the form it now takes, and people have continued to make armor (2) just as Dawud made it down to today. He was not the only one capable of that, and yet the Almighty said:

"To work it as you wish."

The limits of complete and wide-reaching conduct are set, and our age is complete in accordance with knowledge and wisdom. The people of your law are forbidden from stabbing those who turn to them in appeal, as we have mentioned before.

"And measure in the weaving."

The measuring and proportioning in the weaving — perfecting it without inconsistency — applies likewise to his affair: he must establish his law, his Sunnah, and his conduct in moderation, with nothing differing, nothing varying, nothing contradictory in it. It is also said that to measure in the weaving is to make the loops of the chain proportionate — neither so tight that the chain breaks, nor so loose that it falls apart. The meaning of this is that speech composed with extreme precision is understood by only a few and only with effort and cost, while speech that is loose is unpleasant to hear and dries on the hearts. It should rather be intermediate between the two.

And the Almighty said:

"And remember Our servant David, the man of strength."

That is, the one who has strength in the matter of his religion.

"Indeed, he was oft-returning."

(1) In copy (S) this is given as (al-Dawa'a).
(2) Also in copy (S) it appears as (al-Adara'a).

That is, he returned to his Lord in all his affairs.

"If they are content with it, they are immersed in walking and in radiance."

This refers to the moment of handing over from the past to the next, and the next's accepting what is delivered: they take charge of the one to whom the command has now come, they call upon him, and they cleanse the Creator of any taint his creatures might attribute to him.

(And the birds, gathered) — we have already given the interpretation of the mountains and the birds.

(Each one with him) — returning to his order.

(And We strengthened his kingdom) — that is, "Our hand is in front of him" — and we gave him wisdom: that is, the true knowledge.

(And the discernment of speech) — meaning the judgments that separate one matter from another. He is among those who judge by it, and that is the knowledge of the inner and the knowledge of the outer.

And He said:

"And has the news of the disputants come to you, when they scaled the wall of the chamber?"

"When they entered upon David, he was alarmed by them. They said, 'Do not fear — two disputants. Judge between us with the truth.'"

That is: judge by the truth in the inner. "And do not transgress" — that is, do not be unjust.

"And guide us to the even path."

That is: guide us by your judgment to the justice of what stands before us.

"This is my brother. He has ninety-nine ewes, and I have one."

He said, "Entrust her to me, and overpower me in the argument."

That is: he is strong in argument.

He said, "He has wronged you in demanding your one ewe in addition to his own. Indeed, many partners wrong one another, except those who believe and do righteous deeds — and they are few."

When they said this to him, he answered them as he answered them while they were before him, then he looked and saw no one. He knew that this was a trial from Allah, and that is what he said:

"And David thought We had tried him, so he sought forgiveness from his Lord and fell down bowing, and turned in repentance."

He says: when David saw them, he had been unaware that they were angels appearing to him in human form. Then he understood what they had presented to him, and Allah forgave him. The general public claim, in their interpretation, that David's case was this: Satan was made to appear to him in the form of a beautiful bird unlike any he had seen, and it fell into his hands. He moved to take it, but it slipped from him slightly, then dropped not far off. He rose and went up to the roof, climbing toward it, and from there he looked down upon the house of Uriya ibn Hanan. Some of his own household and his men were with him. When his wife had purified herself, she let her hair (1) flow down abundantly, and she covered herself with it. Dawud was fascinated by her, so he sent for her husband, Uriya ibn Hanan, and placed him in front of the coffin, in a position where there was no place to stand. He was thus exposed to be killed so that David might marry his wife. He was killed, and then Dawud married her, though he already had ninety-nine other women while Uriya had only this one. They say that the two angels gave him this parable of what he had done.

But Allah has cleansed his saints and purified them from this and from anything like it among the great sins of the past, although the people heard the story in this form — as a parable — and carried it on its outward face (1). The truth of the matter is in the inner.

(1) In copy (E) this is given as (her feeling).

That truth is this: David had ninety-nine authorized representatives — as we mentioned — who prayed to him and listened to him. He raised them up to match the number of the names of God, which are ninety-nine names. Uriya ibn Hanan was one of his preachers, and he had one ma'zoun whom David would raise up to respond to his call. One of the ma'zouns whom Dawud had set up died, and Dawud wished to raise another in his place so that the lute he had chosen would not be broken. Something pleased him, and he asked who was fit for the role; he was told of some of those whom they trusted and whose beliefs they accepted. He may also have hit upon the bird as the example I mentioned. The popular account is that the bird fell into David's hands and that Satan was made to appear in its form — but it is not as they said. It is as they heard, but they did not know its true meaning. That is why it was said to be among the finest birds Dawud had seen. When he wanted to take it, what he wanted was to set up a successor for the deceased ma'zoun, joining him to that station — and the bird is what guided him to the ma'zoun of Uruya ibn Hanaan, as mentioned. The bird being carried into David's hands signified the showing-forth of Uriya's wife and what they recounted about her.

The ascent to the surface is his Orientalism in the selection, signifying the true upper knowledge. His Orientalism is not from the path of mere guidance and opinion; he distinguished it by the good statement of the man who manifested it for him, by his creed, by his folding him in, and by his doing what David wanted in support of him.

What they recounted about Dawud's gaze upon the woman of Uriya ibn Hanan — his contemplation of her while she bathed naked, that she pleased him and fascinated him, and that when she saw him he was contemplating her while she was naked in her hair (2) — Allah has invalidated his prophets and dismissed them from any rank like that. If such a thing had been done by an ordinary man, it would have been a deficiency and a stigma upon him in his religion.

Rather, what David did was to look into the man's affairs — to read through his deeds — and they pleased him.

(1) In copy (E) this is given as (his back).
(2) In copy (X) this is given as (her feeling).

[The passage now repeats with slight variation across the manuscript witnesses.]

He said, "Entrust her to me, and overpower me in the argument."

That is: he is strong in argument.

He said, "He has wronged you in demanding your one ewe in addition to his own. Indeed, many of us as partners wrong one another, except those who believe and do righteous deeds — and they are few."

When they said this to him, he answered them as he answered her while they were before him, then he looked and saw no one. He knew that this was a trial from Allah, and that is what he said:

"And David thought We had tested him, so he sought forgiveness from his Lord and went down crying out."

He says: when David saw them, he had been unaware that they were angels appearing to him in human form. Then he understood what they had presented to him, and Allah forgave him. The general public claim, in their interpretation, that David's case was this: Satan was made to appear to him in the form of a beautiful bird unlike any he had seen, and it fell into his hands. He moved to take it, but it slipped from him slightly, then dropped not far off. He rose and went up to the roof, climbing toward it, and from there he looked down upon the house of Uriya ibn Hanan. Some of his own household and his men were with him. When his wife had purified herself, she let her hair (1) flow down abundantly, and she covered herself with it. Dawud was fascinated by her, so he sent for her husband, Uriya ibn Hanan, and placed him in front of the coffin, in a position where there was no place to stand. He was thus exposed to be killed so that David might marry his wife. He was killed, and then Dawud married her, though he already had ninety-nine other women while Uriya had only this one. They say that the two angels gave him this parable of what he had done.

But Allah has cleansed his saints and purified them from this and from anything like it among the great sins of the past, although the people heard the story in this form — as a parable — and carried it on its outward surface (1). The truth of the matter is in the subtle.

(1) In copy (M) this is given as (her feeling).

That truth is this: David had ninety-nine authorized representatives — as we mentioned — who prayed to him and listened to him. He raised them up to match the number of the names of God, which are ninety-nine names. Uriya ibn Hanan was one of his preachers, and he had one ma'zoun whom David would raise up to respond to his call. One of the ma'zouns whom Dawud had set up died, and Dawud wished to raise another in his place so that the lute he had chosen would not be broken. Something pleased him, and he asked who was fit for the role; he was told of some of those whom they trusted and whose beliefs they accepted. He may also have hit upon the bird as the example I mentioned. The popular account is that the bird fell into David's hands and that Satan was depicted in his image — but it is not as they said. It is as they heard, but they did not know its true meaning. That is why it was said to be among the finest birds Dawud had seen. When he wanted to take it, what he wanted was to set up a successor for the deceased ma'zoun, joining him to that station — and the bird is what guided him to the ma'zoun of Uruya ibn Hanaan, as mentioned. The bird being carried into David's hands signified the showing-forth of Uriya's wife and what they recounted about her.

The ascent to the surface is his Orientalism in the selection, signifying the true upper knowledge. His Orientalism is not from the path of mere guidance and opinion; he distinguished it by the good statement of the man who manifested it for him, by his creed, by his folding him in, and by his doing what David wanted in support of him.

What they recounted about Dawud's gaze upon the woman of Uriya ibn Hanan — his contemplation of her while she was naked and playful, that she pleased him and fascinated him, and that when she saw him he was contemplating her while she was naked in her hair (2) — Allah has invalidated his prophets and dismissed them from any rank like that. If such a thing had been done by an ordinary man, it would have been a deficiency and a stigma upon him in his religion.

Rather, what David did was to look into the man's affairs — to go through his readings and his deeds — and they pleased him.

(1) In copy (E) this is given as (his back).
(2) In copy (X) this is given as (her feeling).

He did not see anything in him to its contrary. When the man learned of this from David, he concealed it outwardly. It is like the poetry they recited about Uriya's wife covering herself when Dawud looked upon her while she was naked: when David saw the man's inner state and disclosed it to him, the man drew a veil over it for him — appearing humble, lowering himself — because Dawud saw him as bearing what he was bearing in good faith. It is impossible that Dawud took this man from Uriya, with his guardian's leave, and gave him command until he had promoted him to this station, all without the care and adornment Dawud had received from him, and the knowledge he had taught him. Indeed, Dawud raised Uriya to the rank of those gathered close when he saw the goodness of his rising and his discipline. He brought him near, established him at his hands — and this is what they describe as his "placing him in front of the coffin." They heard the outward of this and did not know its inner. The coffin is the outward sign of the body of the Imam in the inner. Of this the Almighty said:

"Their Prophet said to them: 'Indeed, the sign of his kingship is that the coffin will come to you, containing tranquility from your Lord and a remnant of what the family of Moses and the family of Aaron left behind, borne by the angels.'"

The coffin is what we have mentioned. The tranquility is the Imamate, and the remnant of the family of Moses and the family of Aaron is what they preserved of knowledge and wisdom for those who would act upon it — entrusting it to those who succeeded them and inherited it: Imam from Imam, from what the angels carried from God to the Messenger and which, through him, came to be theirs.

So David saw that he had rewarded Uriya for his good rectification, and given him even better — raising him further and authorizing him in his own self, lifting him above his prior rank. He did not mention this to Uriya, nor tell him what he was supporting him with, nor consult him; for he believed himself to be the first of his nation, and that it was permissible for him to do with them what he had done, and to direct their affair as he wished without consulting any of them. Then it fell into the heart…

(1) In copy (M) this is given as (Arqala).


<!-- page 259 -->
Uriah did not mention anything to David — since David himself had not spoken of it, nor placed his hands upon him — and he kept silent about the matter. He showed nothing of it outwardly, though by the right he held with God his quest could not go to waste. His just compensation lay in God's raising up the very man whom David had elevated, in the best assessment and extraction of his worth, and in not cutting off his due. It was incumbent that this be done by David's own command and through his own hands, so that the fulfillment came from him.

God therefore gave David hope and reflection, took him to task for what he had done, and warned him about what he had overlooked from Uriah — through what he showed him by way of the command of the two kings (1), whom He portrayed to him as two adversaries. By this David came to know what he had been concealing from himself, and he asked God's forgiveness, as the verse says:

((And he turned back and said))

— meaning the humility of Uriah and the command of his companion were returned to David, and he became obliged to do what was obligatory upon him. So God forgave him, as the Almighty said:

((Indeed, We have made you a successor in the land, so judge among the people in truth, and do not follow desire, for it will lead you astray from the path of God. Those who go astray from the path of God will have a severe punishment for what they forgot on the Day of Reckoning.))

For David was certain of what he had ruled, and that he had not knowingly followed his own whim. If such was his right, then it is in this manner that God Almighty reproaches His prophets and disciplines them — that they err in matters where they do not pause to speak with care. Yet if some of them are charged by the common people with immorality and major sins, God has acquitted them; God is pleased with that and has saved them from such accusations. His words are:

"So judge between people with the truth."

(1) In copy (e) it is mentioned (the Mamluks).

259

<!-- page 260 -->
This applies to everyone who is tested and tried in the affairs of all people — in speech, in reproach — in that he stood in the command of those entrusted with wisdom, who are the foundation of his call from among his followers and captains, his preachers and his admonishers. To each of them belongs his right, and none may surpass that right.

Do not follow your love for them, but follow what you have been commanded — both regarding those around you and those who came before you, and those who will come after you of your own kind. God's rule is one and His way is one, in the first and in the others. There is no change in it, nor any substitution, as the Almighty said:

((And you will never find any change in the way of God.))

Regarding His saying:

"He will keep you away from the torrent of God"

— that is, concerning the Master of the Time. David was the Master of the Time in his own age, yet the Master of the Time after him intended to follow his own desire among his people and in the command of his call, not to judge among them according to what their rights required of them. As for those whose deeds and entitlements fell short, he went astray from knowing the one truly worthy of his station after him. Whoever strays from knowing the Imam of the Time is the one whom God promises His punishment (1) — and that occurred with David before Solomon had been established in the place of his proof. For had Solomon already been so established, he would have considered the matters of those in charge of the call and of the subordinate proof. But David was still examining matters; he had not yet appointed his minister. Then God Almighty granted Solomon to him and set him up as the proof for the command of the call and the summoning to it. This is the meaning of the Almighty's words:

((And to David We gave Solomon — an excellent servant; indeed, he was one who repeatedly turned [to God].))

(1) It is mentioned in copy (M) (His promise).

260.

<!-- page 261 -->
The Story of Solomon:

When God Almighty willed David's passing and his departure from this world, He raised up Solomon — peace be upon him — and the Imamate passed to him. He inherited from David the Imamate, the kingship, and the rule. That is the saying of God Almighty:

((And Solomon inherited David.))

He said:

"O people, we have been taught the speech of the birds, and we have been given of all things. Indeed, this is a manifest favor."

And the saying here:

((O people))

— addresses the people of his call, those acquainted with his wisdom, telling them of the great blessings of God upon him.

He said:

((We have been taught the speech of the birds.))

The birds, on this reading, are like the angels — those of the upper ranks who descend by the command of God to His prophets, and likewise the preachers of the lower ranks who call to the Imams. Those who report concerning them did not intend by "the speech of the birds" anything other than the speech of knowledge and wisdom — which is the speech of the birds — and the matters that pass from this in the way of the angels, from God (swt) to His messengers and to the successors of His messengers, the Imams of His religion. From them the people of their call quote it for all who respond to them.

261.

<!-- page 262 -->
This is the speech of the birds that Solomon mentioned, that he had been taught — not in the sense the common people claim, that he spoke with birds and birds spoke with him, by which they mean the visible bird. Rather, God Almighty has singled out human beings with articulate speech and rational language. Animals possess only sounds that express the conditions they are in — like the cawing of one bird at the sound of another, or what passes between them when they fight or compete, and the rest of the animals in the same manner — and likewise (1) the sounds a mother makes to her young, and the like, which is recognized in every case.

As for speech — articulate utterance and language used for purposes, conveying reports and the other arts of intention — God has singled out human beings with this and favored them over each other by it. The saying:

"We have been given of all things"

— and he did not say "everything," because that uniqueness belongs to the Creator alone. His servants receive from Him only as much as they have need of, when He entrusts them with it. This is the same as His saying:

"And We have indeed struck for the people in this Qur'an from every parable."

And He said:

"And they ask you about Dhu al-Qarnayn; say, 'I will recite to you a remembrance of him. Indeed, We established him on the earth and gave him a means to everything.'"

There are many such instances in the Qur'an.

He said:

((And Solomon gathered for him his soldiers from the jinn, mankind, and the birds — and they were arranged in ranks.))

(1) It is mentioned in version (E) (and its admonition).

262

<!-- page 263 -->
That is, the gathering of those entrusted with his call, who hold fast to it (1) and protect it. The jinn here, in the inner sense, are those who carry the knowledge of the unseen — meaning those you do not see, yet they follow him. The humans here are the people known by his wisdom, his captains and preachers. "Arranged in ranks" means dispatched in formations, each pressing the other and competing in good deeds — the lesser among them pressing forward by his good deeds to rise toward the rank of one above him, without envy between them, for they compete only in the meanings of matters and the highest of stations. As the Almighty says:

"Until, when they came upon the Valley of the Ants —"

— and the ants here are like those authorized among the preachers, those permitted to break ground among the people of the outer sense, and to point those whom they have prepared toward the one who guides them, by educating those whom he has invited and taught. We have mentioned before that their likeness is the sheep who feed and raise their young — sheep being the believers, who hear what they ought to do.

One of the ants said:

((O ants))

— meaning: O you who have been permitted to enter —

((enter your dwellings.))

That is, return to those among whom you dwell, your preachers from whom you have taken your knowledge; take from them as much as you can hold, and then withdraw.

((Lest Solomon and his soldiers crush you while they do not perceive.))

He says: you have heard what you can bear within your own limits; now go away and rely upon your prayers, before the speech of Solomon and his followers and companions exceeds what you can carry and thus destroys what you are — while Solomon and his companions do not perceive what is permissible for you. That is, do not seek to hear the kind of speech you cannot bear. The one who said this was from the authorized ones, knowing who was among them, fulfilling them in knowledge, and aware of their obligation.

(1) In version (M) it is mentioned (yathibun — "they cleave to it").

263

<!-- page 264 -->
He feared that the words of the high-ranking and the captains would continue, and that they would not perceive the limits of his companions, so that some of them would be unable to bear it, not having reached its station.

"So Solomon smiled at what he said."

That is, he was pleased with what the man said, and approved of it; he rose in admiration of his intelligence and his alertness.

He said: "My Lord, inspire me to be grateful for Your favor which You have bestowed upon me and upon my parents, and to do righteousness of which You approve, and admit me by Your mercy into the company of Your righteous servants."

This was when he saw from the man what he saw of discernment and good discrimination, and that the man recognized the lower limit. Solomon recalled the favor that God Almighty had granted him out of His bounty — He had raised him to praise Him — and so he asked to be aided in giving thanks for the grace He had bestowed upon him and upon his parents, meaning those before him in his own time, when he was called and when his proof was raised. So he turned to himself and gave thanks for himself, that he might be saved by it. He did not intend the thanks itself to be apportioned among them; rather, he intended that what God had bestowed upon him, and what He had bestowed upon them, be distributed — as God said concerning them:

"And admit me by Your mercy into Your righteous servants."

— meaning those who had gone before him among the Imams, who obeyed God and were pleasing to Him when they made themselves right. He asked to be joined to them, sealed with their station, that he might enter into their company.

The Almighty said:

(1) It is mentioned in version (M) (imtiyaz — "distinction").

264

<!-- page 265 -->
((And he inspected the birds and said, "Why do I not see the hoopoe — or is he among the absent?"))

The bird here, in the interpretation, is like those who call from the upper limits — the messengers — and the like of the callers from the lower limits. That is the saying of God Almighty:

((Originator of the heavens and the earth — He makes the angels messengers, with wings of two, three, and four; He increases in creation what He wills. Indeed, God is over all things competent.))

He said, regarding the mention of the callers:

((Then take four of the birds and incline them to yourself, then place upon each mountain of them a portion; then call them — they will come to you in haste.))

We have mentioned the interpretation of this in the story of Abraham, when he said:

((And he inspected the birds))

— with two interpretations. The first is that he meant the upper limit connected to him. The second is that he meant one of his lower limits. The name "hoopoe" (al-Hudhud) is derived from "guidance," meaning that he is a guide and shows the way to others — and he may have intended both together. So God Almighty informed them of this with a single word; one of the two meanings may be intended without the other, if the one is absent in regard to its connection with him.

He said:

"I will surely punish him with a severe punishment, or I will slaughter him —"

— if he meant his upper limit connected to him, then he intended to punish him —

265.

<!-- page 266 -->
— by holding him to his question (1), because he reckoned within himself that the messenger had been delayed before him; he would slaughter him and cut him off, so that another could be brought into connection with him. That was like the delay of the Messenger of God ﷺ when Gabriel was slow to come — he thought it was from his own side, until God sent down to him:

((And we do not descend except by the command of your Lord.))

If he meant the lower limit attached to him, then his punishment would be: barring him from receiving the original support and aid, and his anger directed at renewing the covenant upon him and resuming with him. Or the matter would be like the doing of one humbled. Then he repented and said:

((Or he must bring me a clear authority.))

That is, with a strong argument for the reason of his delay. The two interpretations are joined when he said:

((But the hoopoe did not stay long, and said, "I have encompassed what you have not encompassed, and I have come to you from Sheba with certain news.))

Knowledge of what one had not penetrated — knowledge of what leads to it and had not been informed of — may be of either the upper or the lower range. If the hoopoe saw something he had not seen, from above him and from below him, and brought him news of it — something which had not yet reached him, nor been reported to him — then he brings it to him and conveys it to him likewise. His upper limit informs him of what he had missed.

He said:

"I found a woman ruling them"

— meaning there is none of those who follow him, nor those who preceded him among them, who has a right to that rule —

((And she has been given of all things))

— meaning of knowledge — so she calls them to herself.

(1) Received in copy (X) (sticking).

266.

<!-- page 267 -->
((And she has a magnificent throne))

— that is, a great summons.

"And I found her and her people prostrating to the sun rather than to God."

This means that they suppose the Imam to be the Creator — God Almighty above what they say of him — that he is a man, and that his guardians act with the authority of God concerning what the wrongdoers attribute to them. Such a thing has been believed and said by a number of nations regarding the accused, when they exaggerated their station, altering and changing what they had been commanded, and Satan adorned their deeds for them — that is, those who turn away from their guardian are called devils.

(((Satan) has turned them away from the way, so they are not guided))

— and "the way" is the guardian of the time. He turned them away from him when they invited them to themselves and to what they had invented, and established for them in the place of the Imam, and the Imam in the place of the Creator Almighty — God has kept his parents far from such utterance, or from calling himself by it.

He said:

((So that they do not prostrate to God, who brings forth what is hidden in the heavens and the earth.))

— meaning, to the Creator, before whom and through whom come the benefits — the proofs and the captains, the foundations before them, are all connected to Him.

((And He knows what you conceal))

— meaning in the inner self.

((And what you reveal))

(1) Contained in copy (M) (Z).

267


<!-- page 268 -->

That is, what manifests outwardly does not conceal what the speaker reveals — what he casts forth by way of teaching to those beneath him. And Allah, the Most High, after all of this declares:

> "There is no god but He, the Lord of the Great Throne."
> (Quran 27:26)

The meaning is that the Almighty is the Originator of the great daʿwa that has spread from the top of the upper boundary down to the very lowest boundary, and He is its Lord — He alone governs it. Know that the Imam is in need of one who calls on his behalf from the upper hudud, who serves as the intermediary between him and the Almighty, so that he is not pressed upon directly and his name is not arrogated.

He said:

> "We shall see whether you have spoken the truth or whether you are of the liars."
> (Quran 27:27)

This is a saying that does not properly apply to the upper hudud of the caller except by way of metaphor — meaning, we shall inquire about them: if they persist in what you have said, then your report about them and your judgement of them is true; and if they turn back to the truth, they have given you the lie. The statement is actually addressed to the lower hadd, the one beneath him, on the apparent level. The point of the metaphor follows what we have already explained: in the case of trust placed in him, we wished to clarify the saying in the two aspects already presented.

Then he said:

> "Go with this letter of mine and deliver it to them, then turn back from them and see what they return."
> (Quran 27:28)

The interpretation of Allah's Book is His Messenger esoterically, and whoever among the Imams establishes it after him is one who, after the Messenger, becomes the Book; and the Imam is the one who applies it, executes it, and conveys it.

268

<!-- page 269 -->

In its esoteric interpretation: He sent to them a caller to invite them to himself and to make known to them his standing with his Lord, and that he is the Master of the Time to whom the command has reverted:

> "She said, 'O chiefs, indeed a noble letter has been cast to me.'"
> (Quran 27:29)

The meaning is that this later figure who summoned them to himself — when there came to him from Solomon what came, and he recognized the bounty of the support attached to him from Allah — gathered the people of his daʿwa to him (1), those who had answered what he called them to, and informed them of all that, and that there had come to him a noble messenger (peace be upon him) honoured with knowledge and wisdom by Solomon. This is what is meant by his words:

> "It is from Sulayman, and it reads: In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful."
> (Quran 27:30)

That is, what the letter indicates concerning the hudud.

> "Do not exalt yourselves against me, but come to me in submission."
> (Quran 27:31)

He is saying: do not show pride, for I am your guardian — submit to my command and consult the people.

In this regard he said:

> "She said, 'O chiefs, advise me in my affair; I do not decide a matter until you bear witness for me.' They said, 'We are possessors of strength and possessors of great might.'"
> (Quran 27:32–33)

That is, we possess knowledge, wisdom, and decisive proofs to use against those we argue with.

> "But the command is yours, so see what you will command."

> "She said, 'Indeed kings, when they enter a town, ruin it.'"
> (Quran 27:34)

He is saying: if the Imams take over the people of a daʿwa and the people of that daʿwa respond to them, they corrupt whatever those people held in their hands of their prior teaching and shift them to where they themselves stand.

(1) In copy (e) it reads "the sinners."
(2) In copy (S) it reads "and they saluted."

269

<!-- page 270 -->

> "And they render the dear ones of its people abased. And thus they do."
> (Quran 27:34)

That is, they aim to bring back those who had held headship in knowledge and advanced standing within his school — to re-educate them from the beginning, so that he becomes one beneficiary among all the others who benefit.

> "But indeed, I will send to them a gift and see with what the messengers return."
> (Quran 27:35)

I shall send them some of the knowledge that I possess — the benefits of which, if they accept, they will understand they are in need of what I have. And if they do not accept, you will know that you should return, profiting from them their abasement at their hands.

> "So when [the messengers] came to Solomon, he said, 'Do you provide me with wealth?'"
> (Quran 27:36)

He is saying: do you wish to enrich me? — when what Allah has given me is better than what He has given you. It is better than what you have been given, given the corruption you mix with what is in your hands.

> "Return to them."

He says to his messenger:

> "We will surely come to them with soldiers that they will be powerless to encounter, and we will surely expel them from there in humiliation, while they are debased."
> (Quran 27:37)

He is saying: I shall send to them preachers against whom they will have no argument, until he draws them out of the daʿwa they had corrupted. And he did that to them. Then he said:

> "Which of you will bring me her throne before they come to me in submission?"
> (Quran 27:38)

He is saying to his own arguments and followers: which of you knows the science of their daʿwa and what they have adorned it with — whatever they hold as proof? — for I know that.

> "Before they come to me in submission" —

(1) In copy (S) it reads "you will reason."

270

<!-- page 271 -->

— I do not yet know about them, and I shall address them concerning it from where I do know. It may happen that the Master of the Time himself is the one who pilots the sciences and the doctrine-sciences of the people, their sayings, and the way they mimic the differences in their proofs — that knowledge being what Allah, the Almighty, extends upon that walī's tongue.

> "An ʿifrit from the jinn said:"
> (Quran 27:39)

That is, a mighty one among the preachers.

> "I will bring it to you before you rise from your place, and indeed, I am for this trustworthy and strong."

He is saying: I am strong in the knowledge of that, and I am trustworthy with him — neither to alter nor to be altered.

> "I will bring it to you before you rise from your place" —

that is, before you occupy yourself in demanding it and leave the station Allah has set you in. May Allah, the Almighty, grant the power to execute His command and to consider the true knowledge He has chosen for you.

> "He who had knowledge from the Book said:"
> (Quran 27:40)

That is, his proof who reached him by his knowledge.

> "I will bring it to you before your gaze returns to you" —

i.e., before the hadd that brings you support from your Lord comes back to you — and so he mentioned all of that in its proper place.

> "When he saw it placed before him" —

that is, in the one who accepted him, took up his cause, and was established for his station after him, who knew what he possessed of the arts of knowledge.

271

<!-- page 272 -->

> "He said, 'This is from the favour of my Lord to test me whether I will be grateful or ungrateful. And whoever is grateful — his gratitude is only for the benefit of himself. And whoever is ungrateful — then indeed, my Lord is Free of need and Generous.'"
> (Quran 27:40)
