He is saying: whoever gives thanks for the grace of Allah which is with him, it is for him; and whoever disbelieves in — i.e., covers up — that grace and does not display it by thanking him, Allah is without need of his thanks, generous in what He bestows on His servants whether they thank Him or not.

> "He said, 'Disguise her throne for her; we will see whether she will be guided or will be of those who are not guided.'"
> (Quran 27:41)

This is after he had sent his preachers in reply to what the one who had claimed that station for himself had sent — and he knew that she would come to him submitting, with her companions, and that they would deny the daʿwa she had claimed. They were to present it to her: if it came to her with such falsehoods as hers, then it follows from her claim and her arguments.

> "We will see whether she is guided or whether she is of those who are not guided" —

we shall look at whether she perceives the truth in this and draws near, or whether she persists deeper in the falsehood she clings to.

> "When she arrived, it was said, 'Is your throne like this?'"
> (Quran 27:42)

This is a summary statement of the matter — that he knew what she was calling to and what she hoped for from whoever called him, and acted on that knowledge without asking her about it. He knew, and Solomon's companions knew, what she was calling to and what she was doing. Then he represented it to her inwardly in a way that exposed what was in her hands and likened her to it — and she was told: "Is this not what you were calling to of falsehood and vanity?" — like that with which she was represented from the mirage (1) and the foam (2):

(1) In copy (e) it reads "drink."
(2) In copy (e) it reads "and the butter."

272

<!-- page 273 -->

— as if he were the one who had legitimized it and founded it.

> "She said, 'It is as though it were that very one. And we were given knowledge before her, and we have been Muslims [in submission to Allah].'"
> (Quran 27:42)

He is saying: there is a story regarding Solomon's companions when they overcame that later substitute. They told him, by way of their excuse, that they had knowledge before her, and that she had no knowledge, and that they were Muslims — i.e., submitting — to their walī.

> "And that which she used to worship besides Allah had averted her, for she was from a disbelieving people."
> (Quran 27:43)

That is, she had been turned away from the guidance of those who follow him by what she had been worshipping besides Allah — namely, the people of falsehood. "She was from a disbelieving people" — that is, the truth shall be seen, and disbelief shall cover the matter over.

> "It was said to her, 'Enter the palace.'"
> (Quran 27:44)

The word ṣarḥ in Arabic means a high palace. From it is the saying of Allah, the Almighty:

> "And Pharaoh said, 'O Haman, build for me a lofty palace.'"
> (Quran 28:38; or Quran 40:36 in the related passage)

It is reported in the interpretation of the general exoteric account that Bilqis's father was from the jinn, and that the jinn were afraid that Solomon, if he saw her and found her pleasing, would marry her — and if he married her, they would expose their secret. They said: when the son is from a jinn through a human, his leg is like the hoof of a donkey. They reproached her for this trait which she carried. He wished to know whether this was so from where she could not see that she was being tested — so he sat her on a bed in a palace, made a courtyard of water and covered it with glass. When she entered, she took it to be water and bared her legs, and he saw her feet.

The meaning in the esoteric interpretation is as follows:

> "It was said to her, 'Enter the palace.'"

273
18

<!-- page 274 -->

That is, in the knowledge of the speaker, the Messenger of Allah (may peace be upon him) said: "I am the city of knowledge and ʿAli is its gate."

When she saw it, she looked into it — and the latter one disclosed to her something of Solomon's reasons by his true knowledge, and the beginning of its interpretation, of what must be begun with from the bāṭin which has a thin veil covering it from the ẓāhir, of which there is no doubt that it is the pure inward. So he disclosed to her its inner side, and the water in its interior is like the science. The meaning of their saying that it was covered with glass is what stands in place of the thin veil — so she supposed it to be the underlying base.

This is what he said:

> "She thought it was a pool and uncovered her shins."
> (Quran 27:44)

That is, the root of the bāṭin. From this is also the saying of Allah, the Almighty:

> "The Day a shin shall be uncovered."
> (Quran 68:42)

He said:

> "It is a palace paved smooth with slabs of glass."
> (Quran 27:44)

It was said to her: it was not a pure inward (1), but a thing hidden beneath the subtle outward appearance. When she learned this, she was astonished at the greatness of what she had heard, and her awe of it — when she was told that this was the lowest of the hudud among the hudud of knowledge. So she acknowledged her wrongdoing and submitted to the command of Solomon when the proof had been made clear to her.

This is what the Almighty said:

> "My Lord, indeed I have wronged myself" —
> (Quran 27:44)

— i.e., by the denial and the alteration you had committed against him.

> "And I submit with Solomon to Allah, Lord of the worlds."
> (Quran 27:44)

It is reported in the hadith that Solomon married Bilqis when her Islam was made good, while he was in —

(1) In copy (S) the word is mentioned.

274

<!-- page 275 -->

— the subtle. That is, after she had submitted to the command of Solomon, entered into his daʿwa, and answered his command, her state improved, her residence in his house was secured, and they are his consorts in the inward.

And Allah, the Almighty, said:

> "And to Solomon We subjected the wind, its morning a month and its afternoon a month."
> (Quran 34:12)

It means that He granted him the benefits of wisdom and knowledge — for there is no mercy from Him for the believers more than this. By it He raises them, nourishes them, and gathers benefits for them — just as the wind does in gathering the clouds and driving them along until they pour out water. In it are decisive proofs that overthrow the people of falsehood, just as the wind contains punishment and severity. And his saying:

> "Its morning a month and its evening a month" —

morning is the dawn of the day, and evening is the dawn of the night. Allah, the Almighty, perfects [the comparison] when one follows it outwardly and inwardly.

He said:

> "And We caused to flow for him a spring of molten brass."
> (Quran 34:12)

That is, We gave him knowledge of the dense outward, of which people do not know the inward — so that We made it flow like a current of molten metal that lets one see what is within because of its purity and its emergence from the limit of inanimate matter. So He opened the outward to him from his inward.

And the Almighty said:

> "And among the jinn were those who worked before him by the permission of his Lord. And whoever deviated among them from Our command — We will make him taste of the punishment of the Blaze."
> (Quran 34:12)

The jinn in esoteric interpretation take their name from janna, which is concealment — they are the people of the inward realm who conceal him. Here, then, he means by them his proofs and his followers.

275

<!-- page 276 -->

> "They made for him whatever he willed —"
> (Quran 34:13)

— meaning, they appointed preachers for him who guide creatures, who themselves are guided because they have a touchstone —

> "— and mihrabs" —

— meaning, what they utter of allegories in their speech to people in their daʿwa, explaining to them the parables of the Qur'an —

> "— and statues" —

— meaning the same as the above; what they say in proverbs.

> "And basins large as reservoirs" —

— that is, bowls the size of mahid in capacity. These are the authorized ones who establish the partition, the statement, and the disclosure — represented by the mahid because the guides take benefits from them just as people eat from plates of food.

> "And vertical cauldrons" —

— meaning the standing pillars, fixed from one side and following them. They are settled on the side of their walī like the steadiness of pots anchored in place. So Allah, the Almighty, has established the earth from His proofs, His followers, His preachers, and His arguments — those who establish His daʿwa and bear the command of those who respond on his behalf, who give them the answer and bestow on them knowledge and wisdom, and deduce for them from that what nourishes them. He means by that, and acts upon it, without him; and whoever does not do that from them tastes —

> "— the punishment of the Blaze" —

— that is, the cutting off of substance and reconciliation from him, and his being afflicted with ignorance.

And it is by Allah's favour upon His prophets and the people of His religion that He gives them helpers (1) who establish for them the reasons of their daʿwa, who carry its burden on their behalf, and who do for them their hudud and their reasons — though some among them do not complete it and do not themselves suffer it — for what Allah, the Almighty, wills of the perfection of recompense and reward for them, and Allah is the most generous in bliss and grace. And this is the saying of Allah, the Almighty:

> "And of the devils were some who dived for him —"
> (Quran 21:82)

— and they perform an action that is not that. And he says:

(1) In copy (e) it reads "Objects."

276


<!-- page 277 -->
"And the devils, every builder and diver, and others bound together in chains —
this is Our gift, so bestow it without reckoning or withhold it without reckoning."

The meaning is that He placed at his disposal everyone with him, and apart from him the other imams, those of his followers who dive for him and his summoners across the spectrum of knowledge — they extract its fine particulars for him, expound its keys to the people, and unlock its hidden meanings. All of this is what He casts down upon them out of the totality of the wisdom whose burden they bear with effort of thought and toil (1) in clarifying and explaining it. This was sustained for him by what was sustained before him through a teaching from God Almighty connected to him. Of this is his saying: "The Messenger of Allah taught me a chapter of wisdom and knowledge that opened for me a thousand doors, and each door opened for me another thousand."

Jabir said: The guardian of guardians — that is, Muhammad ibn Ali ibn al-Husayn, may the prayers of Allah be upon them — informed me of about a thousand matters, each matter opening a thousand more. Thus the guardians of Allah are reinforced from the wisdom appropriate to their stations and to what is required of each of them. Some among them probe and deduce, and explain and expound to the people according to their capacity, their knowledge, and what Allah has granted them of the matter, so that they may carry from His guardians what is theirs to carry. For no human being has the strength to bring about anything without a helper, and He alone is unique by this attribute, the Almighty. He is remembered, and all His creatures are powerless before Him — a sign of His power, His oneness, their inability, and their weakness. If, then, the bounds of the causes of the guardians of God are established as necessary, and their belief, their intentions, and their argument are preserved, then in that lies safety and success from God. They have discharged what they bore, and they have agreed upon the truth in their words and deeds, and they have rendered it back to the Almighty.

(1) In copy (e) it is mentioned as "the Khawarij."
p. 277.

<!-- page 278 -->
— the duty and the discharge of their own affairs and the affairs of their summoners among those who respond and those who guide. But if they grow self-admiring and arrogant against the guardians of God, and claim for themselves something they have seen for themselves, and ascribe it to a stratagem or strength of their own, they have robbed themselves of success. They have entrusted themselves to themselves alone, the supply of God Almighty has been cut off from them, and they have therefore distorted speech from its proper places, altered it, and perished. Those who clung to them and followed their command have perished — those who heard this from them and saw in them his own imagination — and before that, those who perished among the past nations perished by the same path. Of this is the saying of Allah Almighty:

"And whoever among them deviates from Our command, We shall make him taste the punishment of the Blaze."

And the Almighty said:

"And they followed what the devils recited concerning the kingdom of Solomon. Solomon did not disbelieve, but the devils disbelieved" — and they made what is plain into what is obscure — that is, the falsehood that they make resemble the truth. When they do that, they have gone astray and led others astray, as Allah Almighty says:

"And they have indeed led many astray, and they themselves have strayed from the right way."

That is, they have strayed from the guardian of their time and abandoned him, and others have strayed from him by what they reported concerning him — the falsehood they attributed to him and to those who summon on his behalf. That, however, does no harm to the guardians of God: what the devils said about Solomon and ascribed to him did not harm Solomon, and Allah Almighty is not harmed by anyone who lies about Him; the liar lies only to himself. Likewise, it does no harm to those who hold fast to the command of the guardians of God, if they disown whoever does this; rather, it harms only those who say it and those who follow them. He came to know this — some among them by what he saw of what they did — and he diverged from them in the very foundation of what he was called to:

the covenant of Allah that is taken upon the servants. That is the first thing the responders hear (1)

(1) In copy (X), "the responders hear."
p. 278.

<!-- page 279 -->
and is taken from them, regarding the guardians of Allah — in which lies the foundation of all that they claim. The taking of the covenant is itself the argument of His guardians. Whoever holds to it and takes it from him, holds firm; and whoever breaks anything from it and contravenes it has destroyed himself. Whoever follows him is destroyed with him. May Allah preserve all His believing servants from destruction and guide them to what holds within it deliverance (1) and protection from error.

As for the words of Allah, the Almighty:

"Every builder and diver" —

the meaning is those who construct the house of wisdom in which the guided take refuge, who are the summoners established by the arguments and given authority. And His saying:

"And others bound together in chains" —

means that some of those who have not been permitted to open the door — among those who have been kept back — have been restrained by their covenants and pacts:

"This is Our gift, so bestow it or withhold it without reckoning" —

that is, you are not bound either to favour the one who deserves to receive from you, or to withhold from the one who does not deserve to be granted:

"And indeed, he has with Us a place of nearness and a fair return" —

meaning that Solomon, peace be upon him, has nearness and a goodly return in the Hereafter, in proportion to what he did by His command.

As for the words of the Almighty:

"We did not decree death upon him, but only the creature of the earth, eating his staff, indicated his death."

(1) In copy (e) it is mentioned as "deliverance" (al-najat).
279

<!-- page 280 -->
"To them the masters ate, and the jinn realized — had they known the unseen, they would not have remained in the humiliating torment."

The common people have explained that Solomon, peace be upon him, was standing over the jinn and at their work, and they took him to be alive, until the woodworm ate his staff and he fell after a long stretch of time, only then did they realize he was dead. This is itself proof of the corruption of their interpretation. How can a dead man be propped upright on his staff? How can the death of one who is being looked upon be concealed? On their account, the jinn were hidden away from him — yet he had family, companions, kin, and those who tended to his food, his drink, and his bed, and they saw that he neither took shelter nor moved from his place day and night, until his staff was eaten away. And his limbs and his body — surely they would decay before the staff — with many further signs of the corruption of this account that we have left aside for brevity.

In truth, this is one of the subtleties — one of the parables Allah Almighty has struck in His book — of which He says:

"And these parables We strike for the people, and none understand them except those who know."

He said:

"When We decreed death upon him."

He says: when his end approached, We moved him and decreed for him to hand over what was in his hand to My guardian after him. He did so, and the matter took hold of him, and no one of those who followed him perceived it.

"Nothing indicated his death to them" —

that is, nothing they could point to in argument.

"Except the creature of the earth"
280

<!-- page 281 -->
— that is, the one who stood after him, whom he had set up.

"Eating his staff" —

and "staff" in the language of the disobedient and the like is, in one mode of interpretation, the support upon which the one appointed by Allah Almighty depends. That is, when they looked at what had appeared in the one who supported him, they took this to indicate that he was still in his station — yet only the saying about him remained.

"The creature of the earth," then, is the one who takes up the matter after the shifting (1) of the master of the time, owing to the intensity of his secrecy and concealment, since scarcely anyone perceives his command in the lifetime of the Qa'im except those whom he has informed. He likened his life to the crawl of an ant upon the earth, which scarcely anyone sees or senses — none but those who meditated upon him in order to draw near to him from among his peers, those who suppose him worthy of it; and he supposes, too, that if there is anyone among them in that station, then it could not have been otherwise. They were all then acknowledging the merit of the one who appeared in the lifetime of the Qa'im, the guardian, and they followed him. This is what many of them came to know.

Sulayman was among those who came to know this from him, and assumed the matter in the lifetime of Dawud — and he had no peer who could displace him from his station. This is the saying of Allah, the Almighty:

"And Dawud and Sulayman, when they were judging concerning the field — when the people's sheep strayed into it by night — and We were witnesses to their judgement. So We gave Sulayman understanding of it, and to each We gave judgement and knowledge."

We have explained the interpretation of this above. So He tells us that Sulayman's rule was carried out in the lifetime of Dawud, and that there is no opening for the one who comes after him, no rightful claim for him; he therefore concealed it during his lifetime, out of fear of him and of those who

(1) In copy (X) it is given as "transfer."
281

<!-- page 282 -->
must remain in concealment for that reason. This is the saying of Allah concerning this community:

"And when the word falls upon them, We shall bring forth for them a creature from the earth, speaking to them, because the people were not certain of Our signs."

This means that one of the successors of the Qa'im at the end of time will appear before his appearance, and the matter will fall to interpretation of what is established in secret and concealment until the one who emerges does so. And the Almighty said:

"Then when he fell, it became clear to the jinn that had they known the unseen, they would not have remained in the humiliating torment."

He says: when Sulayman departed unto the one he had raised up — that is, made his command manifest — and had they known the unseen kept from them before that, they would not have lingered for that span:

"In the humiliating torment" —

meaning the doubt they had concerning the affair of the one he had raised up, since they saw the imagination of support in him, and before the truth of his matter was unveiled to them. The meaning of the news is submission and obedience (1). Submission, that is, is the saying of Allah Almighty in the story of Yusuf, peace be upon him:

"And he raised his parents upon the throne, and they fell down before him in prostration."

He has already explained this. And He said:

"They prostrated themselves before him."

The believers are meant — they submitted in obedience (2) to their guardian, and the foregoing indicates that

(2) Likewise in version (5) it is given as "obedience."
p. 282.

<!-- page 283 -->
And the Almighty informs us, in what He related of the affair of Sulayman, that those who succeeded after the caliphs were unable — even those who drew near them — to do what they did. None drew near the guardians of God to know any of their affairs except by what they themselves showed and taught them; for they do not know any of the unseen, which is the interpretation and the truths of the unseen, except what they grant them, and what the guardians of God teach them of it.

Of this is the saying of the Almighty concerning those who summon Sulayman from his arguments and his followers, his summoners, and their causes:

"Had they known the unseen, they would not have remained in the humiliating torment."

And the Almighty said:

"And We tested Sulayman."

He says: We informed him of the trial.

"And We cast upon his throne a body" —

meaning that one of the people of the lower realm prevailed against him by summoning to him a body in which there is no soul of true life, as Allah Almighty said of the disbelievers:

"Dead, not alive." "Then he returned."

That is, Sulayman repented of a sin that had caused his predicament:

"He said: 'My Lord, forgive me, and grant me a kingdom that shall not belong to anyone after me. Indeed, You are the Bestower.'"

So Allah destroyed his enemy and gave him the kingdom he had asked for:

"It shall not belong to anyone after me" —

meaning the Imamate will not pass to anyone else during his lifetime; rather, it will be after me — only after he hands it over to me, and as long as I am alive, no — since this had not yet happened
p. 283.

<!-- page 284 -->
at his death; for Sulayman was not ignorant that Allah Almighty does not leave His earth without an imam whom He raises up. And he asks of Allah Almighty what He does not do — except that when he was afflicted by what was cast onto his throne by way of the one who had overcome it, he asked Allah Almighty that, should his kingdom be returned to him along with the family of him who overcame it, He should never afflict him again with the like of it. As for His saying:

"And We granted Dawud Sulayman. What a fine servant! Indeed, he was ever turning in repentance. When there were displayed to him at evening the swift, well-trained horses, he said: 'I have preferred love of good things over the remembrance of my Lord' — until they disappeared behind the veil. 'Bring them back to me!' Then he began to stroke their legs and necks."

The common people claim that he was presented with horses, and he was occupied with them until the time of the afternoon prayer passed, until the sun set, and that the horses were slaughtered for that reason. But had one of them done such a thing, they would have been deemed ignorant for his sake. What is the cause for striking the legs and necks of horses — several times (1) — for the sake of Allah, without any sin that had been committed, given the assumption of sin which they alleged of him, namely that he neglected the prayer? The face of the matter, in this interpretation, is like that of Allah Almighty striking him by the well-trained ones — for *al-Safinat* in the language are horses, and horses are likened to horses; he is here likened to the inner arguments that were presented to him, what is going on in their summons, and he was pleased with that, and he sought help from them.

He said: "Indeed, I have preferred love of the good for the remembrance of my Lord" —

and by his Lord he means here the previous Imam before him, who taught him, was beneficial to him, and commanded him to love them. The "good" here, like horses, is also in its interpretation what the common people interpret from the saying of the Messenger of Allah (may Allah's prayers be upon him): "The horse is tethered to goodness in its forelock until the Day of Resurrection."

The inner interpretation of this is the arguments, as we have mentioned. So He tells us about them when they presented him with what they had

(1) In copy (e) it is mentioned as "I returned."
284.


<!-- page 285 -->
They followed him in the da'wa, and he was pleased with them because of his love for them.

(Until she was concealed by a veil)

That is, he did not mention this until they had risen from his presence and departed, and a veil was drawn between him and them.

(So bring them back to me)

They returned them to him, and he opened wisdom to them, increased his support of them, and anointed them with it.

Their shanks, which represent their interior, and their necks, which are their outward aspect — that is, he wipes them wisely.

The mention of the shank, which signifies the disclosure of the inner, has been advanced, because the shank is hidden.

It is a parable for the inward, while the neck is outward and is a parable for the outward; so he increased them in knowledge and clarity.

And in support of what the people of the apparent break upon, act upon, and command,

through their followers and subordinates, they have surpassed (1) in its degree and its causes, and it is a limit that has not been reached.

They will report to him, and he will speak to them about it; and when he is pleased with their deeds and with what befell them in

their call, and with their compliance with what he commanded them to do without changing it, increasing it, or detracting from it,

and nothing of it being lacking, he rewarded them for it, after praising them and describing them as being within his love.

So he gave them the greatest rank — and that is what the guardians of God do to those who have done well by them.

He desires their obedience and the obedience of those who follow them, whether near or far.

They raise those who do this from one degree to another, above what they had already attained.

They have many ranks, and the faithful believers continue to be elevated

within it as long as those above them are satisfied with them, throughout the days of their lives. May God grant all of them from that

what pleases Him, what lies in their fortune and happiness, and the satisfaction of His guardians with His might and power.

(1) In the version (X), this word is mentioned.

<!-- page 286 -->
The story of Yunus:

Yunus (peace be upon him) held the position of the sahib al-waqt (master of the age), and he was from the cycle of Moses (peace be upon him). He had established its boundaries, dispatched its preachers, and his command had been set straight for him. Then

the people of his time corrupted matters, transgressed against his command, deviated from much of his obedience, and he could not restrain them

or order them to be set right; he was unable to do so, his breast was constricted, and he did not succeed,

for God had not granted him that. So when he was within his presence and his dwelling of hijra, it became corrupted, and he abandoned it

and fled from them to an island where he had a strong call regarding the matter of

his soundness, and where he had a successor among them who managed their affairs. So he himself turned away to him. This is what the Almighty said:

(And indeed, Yunus was one of the messengers, when he fled to the laden ship.)

Al-fulk in language is the ship, and in the inner sense it is the da'wa (1); an explanation has already been given.

He related this in the story of Noah (peace be upon him), including the words of the Almighty:

"And he departed in anger, supposing that We would not have power over him."

That is, against his people when they corrupted matters and refused to obey him — and that was a fault on his part,

for he was obliged to be patient and to trust in God Almighty and to know that He is able to

repair what has been corrupted and to set straight what has become crooked for him. As if he had despaired, the Almighty said:

"He supposed that We would not have power over him."

(1) In Copy (M) it is mentioned as (al-Da'wa).
286

<!-- page 287 -->
God (swt) tested many of His guardians in this way, and they were patient until

the help of God came to them. This is what He said:

"And messengers before you were certainly denied, but they were patient over the denial and the harm they suffered

until Our help came to them. And none can alter the words of God."

He says: God does not replace His guardians with other enemies whom He has appointed against them

and who would overcome their command. But Yunus did not have patience as they had, and he supposed that his enemy would prevail.

So he fled from his hand and took refuge with someone who came after him, to complain to him about what had befallen him and to ask his help

in his affair; he placed himself beneath him, while God Almighty had raised him above him

and given him the highest of his rank. God Almighty wished to show him and to make clear to him what he had done wrong —

that he did not have patience until His help came to him — and when he came to that da'wa, he fell into

dispute (1) and disagreement within it.

In the hadith, when he took shelter in the ship, it was disturbed, swayed, and stood still — it would not

run, though the wind was favorable. The navigator said: "This is nothing but the sin of a sinner among us."

The people of the ship did not know who that guilty one was, so he ordered them to cast lots, and the lot

fell upon Yunus. That is the saying of God, the Almighty:

(So he drew lots and was among the losers.)

The navigator is the master of this da'wa, and he is one of the followers of Yunus to whom he had taken refuge.

When he saw that his da'wa had been disrupted and all his preachers and means had been thrown into disarray

within it, he made him inquire about the causes of the corruption that had occurred in his da'wa and from where

it had entered upon it and how it had come to be in this state. They discussed it until they brought him to Yunus

(peace be upon him), and that this was because he had abandoned the matter and fled from his hijra,

(1) In the version (X) it is mentioned (Diaspora).
287

<!-- page 288 -->
his da'wa, and had fallen under one who was beneath him, and that doubt had entered for that reason

upon the one to whom he had come. He looked into the causes of each of them and found him innocent of

being anything other than the da'wa. They saw, and Yunus saw, that for the sake of setting things right

he should depart from their midst and conceal himself from the people of the apparent until God Almighty should reconcile

his affair, as His guardians had promised. This is what is mentioned in the hadith: that they cast him into

the sea — and the sea is like the people of the apparent — and we have explained this in detail above.

When he came out from among them, he was met by one of the ma'dhūn who was among the people of the

apparent who had no da'wa. That ma'dhūn sheltered him and surrounded him, and he became all blessings.

Thus he became worse off than he had been, as He said:

(So the whale swallowed him while he was blameworthy.)

Yes, he is to blame for what he did. Among the reports mentioned is that

when they took him to the edge of the ship and threw him from it, the whale from the sea received (1) him

and took him. The ship was then drawn forward and set straight. So Yunus (peace be upon him) became certain of his having fallen into

sin, and he repented and turned to God and confessed his sin, so God turned to him in mercy and made manifest

his command in his proper direction, and answered him through his family, and he was honored through it.

He took it as a place of hijra, and matters were set straight for him. That is the saying of God, the Almighty:

"Had it not been that he was of those who glorify, he would surely have remained in its belly until the Day

when they are raised up."

He says: were it not for the praise of God by anyone and his deliverance from those who are beneath that limit —

and that is the perfection of tawhid and purity, which means that he accepted that and was obliged

to give every possessor of a right his right, and to take what was not his — among that

He said:
288.

<!-- page 289 -->
"There is no god but You; glory be to You.

Indeed, I was among the wrongdoers. So We answered him and saved him from distress, and

thus do We save the believers."

It is said in the hadith that he called upon his Lord in this way while he was in the darkness of the night and the darkness of

the sea and the darkness of the whale's belly. These are like the darkness of night, of concealment and secrecy, since he had become hidden

and concealed after God Almighty had established him as a place of manifestation and support. The darkness

of the sea is the knowledge of the apparent, abstracted from the bāṭin and from the ta'wīl that its people claim. There is no knowledge

others have understood in the darkness of ignorance of this matter, and they drank of it salty until it was filtered and ascended.

It punishes him and deposits its salt and burns him — for sea water, when placed upon a fire,

what rises from it rises fresh, while the salt water remains at the bottom; likewise what is within it.

Counterfeit is made of gold and silver, which is an inanimate object that perishes; when he is tested by that, his counterfeit is removed.

The darkness of the whale's belly is concealment, and it is that he came under the rule of that ma'dhūn who surrounded him.

That is, he called toward that tawhid, and God saved him from his grief and distress, and made manifest

his command, supported him with His victory, and overwhelmed him with His mercy, so he returned to what he had been. Among that

He said:

"And We sent him to a hundred thousand or more, and they believed, so We gave them enjoyment

for a time."

So God Almighty replaced him with those who had disbelieved, disobeyed His command, and corrupted

his call, with those who repented to him — for one who effects punishment upon those who are loyal to Him among His guardians,

as He stated in His Book when He said:

(And He gives victory to the righteous.) And had it not been that God Almighty had turned to him by his calling upon Him,
289
19

<!-- page 290 -->
he would have remained hidden and humiliated under the rule of the ma'dhūn to whom he had taken shelter and had come

under his charge — through the weakness of the matter of the one for whom there is no da'wa but who is only permitted to some

of the preachers. As for His saying:

((So We cast him onto the open shore while he was sick))

That is, weak because of the trial that had befallen him, and he became a man who knew

nothing of the knowledge of the bāṭin. And His saying:

"And We caused to grow over him a tree of yaqtīn (gourd)."

The yaqtīn in language is every tree that spreads along the earth and does not stand upon a stem, like

(1) gourds, watermelons, melons, and the like. So too in the tafsir concerning

the general public: that when the whale swallowed him, he remained in its belly for three days; then God commanded the whale

to cast him forth, and he was thrown from its belly onto the open ground, and he came out naked, finding nothing to shade him

from any tree or anything else. Then God Almighty caused, from His Secret, a gourd tree to grow and stretch out,

which clothed him. And in the subtle interpretation: he found a man who had called to some

of his arguments, so he took a little knowledge from him which he did not like, and he took it as an argument for himself and spread out from it

the da'wa that had been concealed; and the one mentioned by God Almighty responded to him, as has been mentioned above.

Thus.

"So I am going to allow them to enjoy for a time."

That is, they enjoyed what they benefited from of knowledge and wisdom until the appearance of the Qa'im

(peace be upon him).

(1) In the version (e) it is mentioned (al-Aqra').
(2) In Version (E) it is also mentioned (Al-Aqra').
290.

<!-- page 291 -->
The story of Zakariyya:

Zakariyya (peace be upon him) was an Imam in the last cycle of Moses (peace be upon him). He

knew that he would not reach the cycle of Jesus (may God's prayers be upon him), and that Imran was the sahib al-waqt

before him. Imran had not prepared anyone for the establishment of an imam from his da'wa, so he established Zakariyya, who had no

da'wa of his own. He added to him a man from his da'wa whom he supposed would assume the Imamate after him,

but he did not give him the strength to do so, so he joined him to Zakariyya, who was called upon by God Almighty.

It was narrated of Maryam (peace be upon her) that she became a hujja after that. The Almighty said:

"When the wife of Imran said: 'My Lord, indeed I have vowed to You what is in my womb,

consecrated, so accept this from me. Indeed, You are the All-Hearing, the All-Knowing.'"

That is, the hujja of Imran knew that he preceded the Imam in departing from this world,

and that God would put in his place and make Imam after Imran

the one whom, when he tested him, it became clear to him that he could not lead the

Imamate — there was nothing in him valid except that he be a hujja. That is what he said:

"And when she gave birth to her, she said: 'My Lord, I have given birth to a female,' and God knows best

what she gave birth to."

That is, he knew that before he said it.

"And the male is not like the female."

(i.e., the one fit for the Imamate is not like the one fit to be a hujja.)
291.

<!-- page 292 -->
"And I have named her Maryam, and I commend her and her offspring to Your protection from Satan,

the accursed."

I have fulfilled my vow regarding her and delegated my command to you, as a piece taken from the schemes of

the slave.

(So her Lord accepted her with a good acceptance.)

That is, that man after Imran and his hujja — and he is Zakariyya (peace be upon him).

That is, with the acceptance of knowledge and wisdom.

((And caused her to grow a good growth.))

Yes, he raised her well in that.

"And Zakariyya was made her guardian," that is, he placed her under his hand, his care, and his oversight.

"Whenever Zakariyya entered upon her in the sanctuary, he found with her provision.

He said: 'O Maryam, from where is this to you?' She said: 'It is from God.'"

He says: whenever he engaged her and spoke with her about some matter of the Imamate, he found that she had knowledge of

that which was finer than what he himself did.

"God provides for whom He wills without reckoning."

That is the support of God Almighty, and what came to be was only with His knowledge beforehand.

Zakariyya (peace be upon him) had become weak in his command, and his esoteric da'wa had grown feeble.

This is what He said:

"A mention of the mercy of your Lord upon His servant Zakariyya, when he called out to his Lord

secretly. He said: 'My Lord, indeed my bones have weakened, and my head has flared with white.'"
292.


<!-- page 293 -->

"And never have I been in my supplication to You, my Lord, deprived."

This was when he had reached the age at which he saw that the Imamate had been transferred away from him, and still he had not begotten a child.

"And indeed, I fear my kinsmen after me."

That is: I feared that the Imamate would, after my passing, revert to those of the call who preceded me.

"And my wife is barren, (1) so grant me from Yourself an heir."

I have not received, from the call of my hujja, anyone fit for the Imamate — and Maryam is the one I petition for.

"Grant me from Your presence a guardian."

Apart from me, she is the very one I fear losing.

That is, responding to my supplication: "who inherits me" — meaning the inheritance of the Imamate.

"And he shall inherit from the family of Yaqub; and make him, my Lord, well-pleasing."

"O Zakariyya, We give you good tidings of a boy whose name is Yahya; We have not assigned to any before him a namesake."

By this I understand: a respondent fit for the Imamate, with none above him in virtue — and from this also:

He spoke in this way when he saw the support given to Maryam, and Zakariyya called upon his Lord saying:

"My Lord, grant me from Your bounty good offspring; indeed You are the Hearer of supplication."

"The upper limits benefited him" — meaning the upper limits supplied him with the knowledge of this.

"And he was praying in the prayer niche" —

(1) In copy (M) the word "Amir" is given.

293.

<!-- page 294 -->

— that is, he was within the rank of the Imamate.

"Allah gives you good tidings of Yahya, confirming a word from Allah."

This is a word from God that is made manifest to the servants through him — and "master" means Imam.

"And he shall not take a woman and bring her to himself, because that has already been done before by Allah, the Almighty."

It fell upon Imran that Maryam be a hujja without his appointing her so, and it is —

knowledge had been granted to her from two Imams before him, yet she did not accept any of them for —

the Imamate. But Allah Almighty made clear to him that He Himself had taken charge of the affair of 'Isa —

peace be upon him — and that it stands within the rank of authenticity, without being set up before its time. So God preserved him —

through Maryam, and named him by her name, because he is the mother of 'Isa peace be upon him from the side of the birth of religion —

the inner side — just as his mother Maryam was from the side of physical birth. He was therefore named after her, and she —

stood for him; she was the one intended by the mention of conception and birth, while he himself was unmentioned. Otherwise —

Allah Almighty would have told him about the affair of 'Isa peace be upon him outright; and we will mention this in —

its proper place (1), insha'Allah.

The same was the case with Yahya peace be upon him, who is the cousin of 'Isa from —

the side of outward and inward birth alike, his mother being the sister of Umm 'Isa by descent —

just as it was with 'Isa, who was called by his mother Maryam's name. And that was because —

Zakariyya, peace be upon him, when he wished the Imamate to remain in his descendants, asked God to grant —

him a servant fit to be Imam; he was the best of those who had been seen.

If he had a hujja with him, and he was the one who named him Maryam, the seat of his hujja, then he protected him —

peace be upon him — from the call of the hujja which Zakariyya and 'Isa had inherited from the call of the one for whom that is intended.

(1) In copy (e) the reading is "its subjects."

294.

<!-- page 295 -->

— through Maryam, and it was from the hujja of Zakariyya and from the call of 'Imran. But Zakariyya raised him and took charge of him —

after him, and wished the Imamate after him to remain in the one he had established from —

his own line, and his son Yahya was from him. So Allah Almighty informed him that Yahya would be an Imam —

but that there would be no Imam after him; and Allah Almighty singled out the one named Maryam, whom —

Zakariyya guaranteed, by making the Prophethood and the Imamate part of his call for what had already been done.

Al-Fadl (1) — and He did this for him without his being an Imam, nor in contact with the order of —

the one who would be Imam, like the Imam, like the male; and the hujja like the female. He assigned that to him —

by God's design in this manner, and it is the hujja of any verse for him, and the competence which He has assigned to him. So when God Almighty took him to Himself,

and Zakariyya passed, the Imamate after him fell to his son Yahya, while 'Isa peace be upon him was born —

and Allah Almighty singled him out for the support that we shall mention in its place. He lived —

knowing his own merit in the lifetime of Zakariyya, and from this came the hadith which has been narrated:

each of them was in his mother's womb, and Yahya prostrated himself to 'Isa while still in the womb —

of his mother. The subtle meaning of this is that they were within the limits of upbringing, and each of them —

stood with one of Zakariyya's hujjas, after the name of Maryam had been given. We will mention —

how that came to be in its place. Yahya saw in 'Isa a grace and a strength —

of knowledge and wisdom that were not in himself, so he submitted to it and acknowledged its excellence.

The Imamate passed to Yahya peace be upon him, who obeyed 'Isa and fell under his rule and entered —

among the people of his call — including the hadith in which it is mentioned that 'Isa came —

to Yahya to be baptized, and Yahya said to him: "How can I undertake that, when you are my master and lord?

You have changed me" — because he knew of it, and that he would be a speaking prophet. Then —

'Isa, peace be upon him, said: "But today you are my master and the master of others, and I cannot —

(1) In copy (e) the reading is "Al-Fadil."
(2) In copy (e) the reading is "his curiosity."

295.

<!-- page 296 -->

— do anything except enter into your affairs. So baptize me." And he plunged him into the lake of education — that is, to take the covenant.

He gave him for himself, and gave him of knowledge what he was meant to give to those like him. When 'Isa peace be upon him reached —

the measure of the message, Yahya handed the matter over to him and brought out for him what was in —

his hand, and fell under his rule. And from the grace that Allah Almighty singled out for 'Isa —

was the next event: 'Imran left behind, under Zakariyya's sponsorship, the one named Maryam, of whom it is said:

"And when the angels said: 'O Maryam, indeed God has chosen you and purified you, —

and chosen you over the women of the worlds. O Maryam, be devoutly obedient to your Lord and prostrate —

and bow with those who bow.'"

This means that the upper limit is supported by a support other than that of her caretaker, who —

had guaranteed her a specialty from God Almighty for what we have mentioned. So He revealed to him that God —

the Almighty had chosen her over all other hujjas, purified her, and commanded her to perform qunut and prostration —

for her caretaker — that is, not to raise herself against him with anything other than what he assigned her, namely Zakariyya —

and to direct her call to him and submit to his foundation, while she is protected until what comes from God Almighty arrives.

As for the words of the Almighty:

"And you were not with them when they cast their pens, as to which of them should be the guardian of Maryam."

That was during the era of 'Imran. He gathered his followers to see which of them —

was worthiest to be a hujja, so they all vied for this. He ordered each of them to —

display what he had of clarity, so that the support and strength in him might be seen. Each one then cast forth —

what he had of that, and this is the meaning of "their pens" in the interpretation.

The hadith says that they cast their pens into a flowing river, and whoever's pen went first would have the verdict in his favor.

In the interpretation, however, they cast what each one had of clarity into the knowledge of the master of the time —

296.

<!-- page 297 -->

— so that he might know what Allah had assigned of knowledge, which of them was most advanced in it, and which was stronger than the rest.

He saw that this was found in the one called Maryam after he tested him and found him sound.

The clarity is within the rank of the hujjas; and it is not fitting for him to be an Imam. So Zakariyya stood before him —

and attached him to himself as a hujja, until he should be ready to receive the rank of the Imamate, while Zakariyya tested him —

— and Zakariyya wished that this remain among the people of his call, as we have already mentioned.

That is the interpretation of the words of the Almighty:

"And you were not with them when they cast their pens, as to which of them should be the guardian of Maryam."

He also said:

"When the angels said: 'O Maryam, indeed God gives you good tidings of a word from Him.

His name is the Messiah, 'Isa ibn Maryam, eminent in this world and the Hereafter, and among those drawn near.

He will speak to the people in the cradle and in maturity, and he is of the righteous.'"

The angels say: "O Maryam, God gives you good tidings of a word from Him, whose name is the Messiah, 'Isa —

ibn Maryam." Maryam is the hujja of Zakariyya. Their saying "'Isa ibn Maryam" means —

his mother in the outward sense; and their saying "a word from Him" means that 'Isa peace be upon him is among the prophets of God —

and His saints, who are His words: with them He addresses His creation, and with them He shows them what He wills, just as words show —

what the speaker wills. Allah Almighty does not resemble His creation, nor is He described by their attributes.

Their saying "eminent in this world and the Hereafter" means he comes with prophecy and message in this world —

and in the Hereafter through contact with the upper limits, and being one of those drawn near to those limits, and speaking to —

the people in the cradle — that is, in the rank of education, with the wisdom by which a child is reared and moved —

just as the rank of joining with wisdom is once approached and once departed, as he acts —

297.

<!-- page 298 -->

— like the boy whose cradle moves him. He is said to speak wisdom and to address people with it. He is —

in childhood — that is, in the rank of education — and in adulthood — that is, after he reaches the rank of the one who calls to prayer.

We have already mentioned the meaning of the angels' saying to her: "O Lord."

The fourth speaker, Musa, was supported by his brother Harun; but Harun died during the lifetime —

of Musa, who was forced to install Yusha' ibn Nun as the guardian of the son of Harun.

The Imamate after him followed the known order: Talut, Dawud, Sulayman, Yunus,

'Imran, Zakariyya — peace upon them — and he is the last Imam of the cycle of Musa.

The speaker is the son of 'Imran ibn al-Yashamaa ibn Amihuz ibn La'Adan ibn Nahas —

ibn Ta'la', son of Rashif ibn Rafi' ibn Buraiah ibn Ephraim ibn Yusuf ibn Ya'qub ibn Ishaq —

ibn Ibrahim al-Khalil. He was born in the year 425 Abrahamic and died in 545 Abrahamic, living 120 —

years. He was born on the seventh of March in Egypt and died in the Sinai desert.

Harun was the brother of Musa, born in 442 Abrahamic in Egypt and dying before Musa's death —

a little while, in the desert of the wandering, that is, forty years before the Israelites left Egypt. Yusha' —

ibn Nun, the cousin of Musa and Harun, was born in 463 Abrahamic in Egypt and died in 28 —

Musawiyya — that is, after the death of Musa — and he was essentially his successor and the guardian of the son of Harun.

After Musa died, the Children of Israel crossed the Jordan river from the desert of wandering in three days —

on the tenth of April of the year in which Musa died. After that —

he besieged the town of Jericho for seven days, took it, killed those within it, and then marched —

to Nablus, then to the king of the Levant; his care for the Children of Israel lasted twenty-eight years, and he was buried —

in Kafr Haris at the age of 110. As for Talut — we did not find in the Ismaili manuscripts —

any mention of Talut among the Imams; only the name of Samuel is given, and perhaps it is Talut, who was —

born in 442 and died in 495 Musawiyya. Dawud is the son of Bashar ibn Awfaid —

ibn Boaz ibn Salmon ibn Ghashon ibn Aminudab ibn Reem ibn Hazrun ibn Yahudha ibn Ya'qub.

He was born in 419 Musawi and lived in Hebron, then moved to Jerusalem and conquered the country.

He died in 535 Musawi, living 119 years. Sulayman is the son of —

Dawud; he was born in 523 Musawi and received the Imamate at the age of 12. He built the —

holy house, beginning in 539 and completing its construction in 546. He also built a house of his own —

in Jerusalem, finishing it in 547. He died in Jerusalem in 575 Musawi, living 52 years.

298.

<!-- page 299 -->

Chapter Five

(In which is the interpretation of the story of 'Isa, may God's prayers be upon him)

In the name of God, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful.

When the cycle of Musa ended, the last Imam of his cycle being Yahya — upon them be peace — Allah Almighty willed to send (1) a fifth messenger, who was —

'Isa, may Allah's prayers be upon him. The mention of Maryam has already been made in the fifth chapter.

She is the mother of 'Isa from the educational standpoint, and one of the hujjas of Imam Zakariyya. Before that —

she was one of the hujjas of Imam 'Imran, who came before Zakariyya, and who handed her over to him and included her among the —

Imams: Yunus, then 'Imran, then Zakariyya, then Yahya — who is John the Baptist, son of Zakariyya.

In 1716, six months before the birth of 'Isa, Herod was killed by the king of the Children of —

Israel in 1746, thirty years after the birth of the Messiah. He was the last Imam of —

the cycle of Musa, and he is the one who delivered to 'Isa the teachings of the inherited prophecy. These are the Imams —

the Trustees. As for the stable Imams from the descendants of Isma'il ibn Ibrahim, they are: Adnan, Ma'ad —

ibn Adnan, Nazar ibn Ma'ad, Mudhar ibn Nizar, Elias ibn Mudhar, Madrakah ibn Elias —

Khuzaymah ibn Madrakah is the resident Imam of 'Isa, and the Imam is the perfect Imam.

(1) In copy (S) the reading is "Missions."

p. 299.


<!-- page 300 -->
Zakariyya, in answer to his arguments, named her Mary, because he did not see in him sufficient strength to receive the Imamate. So Zakariyya established an Imam without his invitation, and the truth was that his proof was through Mary. He set her up as a second argument, and from her would come the one who would carry the matter forward — because her caretaker, who is her mother, was among the people of his da'wah, so that the matter would continue through him after him.

Now we wish to speak of the birth of Jesus (peace be upon him) in the inner sense — that is, the birth of the call, not the outward birth, which the people of the apparent took as the only birth. They did not require themselves to know him truly, and they did not know him.

This is because, when Zakariyya decreed the matter to Yahya, he also wished that his proof should come from his da'wah. God Almighty wanted ʿImran to fulfill what he hoped and longed for, making him a prophet after his da'wah, after he had answered the call of Zakariyya (peace be upon him). He gave him protection, as He said in His Book, and made the Imamate for him after him. Then He extended after ʿImran the one who was called Mary — she is the mother of Jesus in the inner world.

She is the one whom ʿImran set up and whom Zakariyya guaranteed for him. Zakariyya did not remain merely to protect; he also hoped that the matter would continue through his successor.[^1] His people called her, and the matter had already been transmitted before by God Almighty — that she was later named Mary without Zakariyya or Yahya knowing of it. And his proof, who was called Mary, remained at her old rank among the ranks of the followers; she had no part in the exposition up to the rank of the preceder, and she remained in her degree.

Then the upper limits called upon her, and the Maker, the Almighty, gave her good news of what God had assigned her of virtue and selection[^2] over the followers. They commanded her to believe in the Imamate of Zakariyya — submission to him, not deviation from obedience to the Imam of the Time — as the Almighty says:

> "And when the angels said, 'O Mary, indeed God has chosen you and purified you.'"

[^1]: In copy (m) it is given as "its aftermath."
[^2]: In copy (e) it is given as "disappearance."

300

<!-- page 301 -->
> "And chosen you above the women of the worlds."

By this is meant the followers.

> "O Mary, obey your Lord" — that is, give your devotion to the Imam of your time.

> "And prostrate and bow down" — that is, humble yourself to your principle.

> "That is from the news of the unseen which We reveal to you."

He says this to Muhammad (peace be upon him): that is, He informed him of that inner matter. Then He confronted him with the angels' announcement that she would call upon a man who would respond to her and become a prophet speaking by the law after him, and that the prophethood thereafter would be from the offspring of his da'wah — as the Almighty says:

> "When the angels said, 'O Mary, God gives you good tidings of a word from Him, whose name is the Messiah, Jesus son of Mary, honored in this world and the Hereafter, and one of those brought near.'"

So He told her his name and his mother's name on the surface, even though his mother was the one being addressed. The people of the apparent claim that mentioning her here had no meaning, because the address to her did not require mention of her name — for if a woman is told that she will give birth to[^3] a male servant called so-and-so, then mentioning her by saying "son of so-and-so" would be impossible, since the news to her is that she gives birth to him, and it would be redundant to tell her that he is her son: she who gives birth to him is his mother, and she knows this.

By His saying "a word from Him" — news that he would be a prophet. The prophets of God are His words, because they prophesy of Him by His command to His servants. From this it is said that the Qur'an is the words of God, because the Prophet spoke it and explained to people about God in words, as he sees of Himself from Himself and from other human beings. And God has likened His creation to a great exaltation, and said:

[^3]: In the version (s) the word is "birth."

301

<!-- page 302 -->
The name "Messiah" means that he wipes away what is visible and what is hidden, and the anointing reveals the thing. From this it is said to the sick, "May God wipe away your harm" — that is, may He reveal it from you and remove its misfortune from you. So Jesus anointed those who responded to him from the sickness of religion, in both their outward and inward command — and for this reason he was called the Messiah, because he himself was anointed by it as well.

And his saying "true in this world and in the Hereafter" — that is, his reward in both of them: in this world it is prophecy and the message, and in the Hereafter it is communion with the upper limits.

> "And of those brought near" — that is, near those ranks.

> "And he speaks to people in the cradle" — in the state of education before puberty, by the exposition of one who has reached that rank, calling toward the limits of the Opening.[^4]

> "And in maturity" — that is, he does this also after puberty. So he will lead in exposition in the state of childhood in a manner unlike what the angels perform, and after puberty in a manner like what they perform — for the followers are described by the quality of exposition, knowledge, and wisdom.

> "She said, 'My Lord, how shall I have a child when no human being has touched me?'"

That is, directly before the time of his release to me.

In another verse: "And I have not been unchaste" — and I do not wish for it to happen without His command.

> "He said, 'Thus God creates what He wills.'"

He says to her: the upper rank that addresses her says, not whenever he is created by God Almighty — as I have claimed — by what His way has been in most matters, meaning the creation of religion: that this is only through an Imam and a proof, but God Almighty does it through whomever He wills.

[^4]: In copy (e) it is given as "al-Fatihah."

302

<!-- page 303 -->
> "When He decrees a matter, He only says to it, 'Be,' and it is. And He will teach him the Book and Wisdom."

That is, He will then introduce him to the Imam of the time, and he will be elevated. "And Wisdom" — that is, the knowledge specific to him, the one who speaks. "And the Torah" — meaning the apparent. "And the Gospel" — meaning the inner.

> "And a messenger to the Children of Israel."

Which is his guardianship; and then He gives it to those who responded to Israel's call from the turn of Ibrahim (peace be upon him) to his time.

> "Indeed I have come to you with a sign from your Lord."

It means himself and the one who succeeds him after him.

> "Indeed I design for you from clay the likeness of a bird."

He says: I raise up for you those of you who have responded to me, and they are the believers.[^5] From this is what Muhammad, the Messenger of God (peace be upon him), did with Ali — calling him Abu Turab when he established him and told him that he would be the father of the believers after him, that is, Imam. And water is like knowledge: when it mixes with dust, it becomes mud. So he said: "I am most useful by the knowledge that is responded to."

And the bird is like the caller: when he becomes such, there is breathed into him from a soul of life, which is the science of support given to the preachers:

> "Then it becomes a bird" — that is, He sends him as a caller.

[^5]: In copy (e) it is given as "the respondent."

303

<!-- page 304 -->
> "By God's permission" — that is, by what God has permitted me.

> "And he heals the dumb and the leper."

That is, I see with wisdom the one who was blind to her, and the blind man is the ignorant. From this the Almighty said about the disbelievers, when He described them:

> "Deaf, dumb, blind — so they do not understand."

The leper is the one mixed with doubt, misguidance, and the like.

> "And I revive the dead, by God's permission."

He says: I bring back the disbelievers by calling them, so that they become believers if they respond. For disbelief, in the inner sense, is death, and the dead are inwardly the disbelievers.

> "Dead, not living."

He said:

> "And you were trusted, so I will revive [them] for you."

He says: I do that by the permission of God Almighty, and not by my own initiative.

> "And I inform you of what you eat and what you store in your houses."

He says: I teach you, from knowledge, that by which your souls live, just as your bodies are nourished by what you eat from food. And so too we revive your souls with knowledge and wisdom.

> "And what you store in your houses."

That is: for the preachers and proselytizers, it is provision for those who deserve it — the respondents who rise to the degrees of merit. The "houses" are those who lack them, and they take refuge in them.

304

<!-- page 305 -->
> "Indeed in that is a sign for you, if you are believers."

That is: in what I have told you is a clear sign, if you are among those who believe.

> "And believing, I did not see my hand among the lights."

That is: I believe in the apparent and command it, and I do not say it inwardly without it.

> "And I will make lawful for you some of what was forbidden to you."

He said: I will release, from the knowledge of the inner, some of what was forbidden for you to hear.

So He gave good news to the follower of what would be the command of Jesus (peace be upon him), and told him of this — so that it would be more likely that he would have a call without being released before its time, and that there might come such a thing as God Almighty had mentioned by His permission, as He did with Adam. He said:

> "The likeness of Jesus before God is as the likeness of Adam: He created him from dust, then He said to him, 'Be,' and he was."

He, the Almighty, told that he was given over to a believer like him, and was then raised up[^6] without any human being interceding to the rank of prophecy. And when God Almighty wished to do what He had promised, He did it. That is the next stage of Jesus' command: to retire the people of the call — in which he was Zakariyya's call — so that they would believe in his Imamate before the time, and to withdraw to his followers and conceal himself from them. This is what the Almighty said:

> "And mention Mary in the Book."

God Almighty says that to the extent that it leads to Muhammad (peace be upon him) — that He mentions her and informs him of her concealment ("Mary," that is, the later one).

[^6]: In copy (e) it is given as "Armah."

305

20

<!-- page 306 -->
> "When she withdrew from her family to a place toward the east."

He meant the owner of the time, and she rejected his followers.

> "So she took a veil from them."

He says: I withheld him from them and concealed what he wanted, and waited for what I had promised.

> "So We sent to her Our Spirit."

It means the trustworthy spirit, who is connected to the prophets by God Almighty:

> "The trustworthy spirit descended upon your heart, that you might be of the warners."

He said:

It means Ali and Muhammad (peace be upon them).

> "And he appeared to her as a perfect man."

So the angel manifested himself to the later one and commanded him, on behalf of God Almighty, to take from Jesus the covenant, and to seek concealment[^7] for the one who follows this matter — because that does not make it lawful for the caller to hear it, since that is not part of his rank. And He said:

> "She said, 'I seek refuge in the Most Merciful from you, if you are God-fearing.'

> "He said, 'I am only the messenger of your Lord, to give you a pure boy.'"

That angel says that, by the command of God, He brought him to confirm this to her when she was in a state of distress. He repeated to her what he had said to those who had preceded him, and that was when he said:

> "She said, 'How shall I have a boy when no human has touched me, and I have not been unchaste?'"

This has already been explained. And the boy is the one who deserves the Imamate.

[^7]: In version (E) it is given as "Fastrap."

306

<!-- page 307 -->
> "He said, 'Thus has your Lord said.'"

The angel tells her that this is by the command of God.

> "'It is upon Me, and I have brought you the one who is before you, and you have not yet come.'"

That is: I have raised you up with support, without mediation before you.

> "And let us make him a sign for the people and a mercy from Us, and it is a matter decreed."

That is: God judged him and ruled by him, so he was certain of the matter and knew Jesus, and so he called him. So he responded to him and took the covenant, and began to raise him with knowledge and wisdom. The mention of Yahya has already come earlier — and his upbringing through the proof of Zakariyya for him, and his submission to Jesus (peace be upon him) when he saw his exposition and the strength of support in him; and that was in the era of Zakariyya (peace be upon him), as we have mentioned.

Zakariyya was arrested, and the matter passed to Yahya after him, and Jesus reached the rank of support. The follower then believed that it was his duty to raise him to the point of maturity and to nurture him to do that on his own. He saw nothing but to manifest his command and to designate one of the arguments that protect him — peace be upon him — fearing that he would attack him with the matter. So he confided to him what he had been commanded, and his grace was revealed for him. This is what the Almighty says:

> "So the pains of childbirth drove her to the trunk of the palm tree."

The "labor" is what happens at birth, and in interpretation it is the time of revealing the one who has been raised to the point of puberty; and "pregnancy" in the inner sense is the period of raising up; and the state of revealing the one raised to the point of puberty: when that later woman, called Mary, felt the strength of support from Jesus, she resorted to the next of Yahya's followers before his time and informed him of his matter — that this should pass through Yahya. She apologized to him and showed him grief and sadness over it, as the Almighty said:

307

t

<!-- page 308 -->
> "She said, 'Oh, would that I had died before this and been forgotten and made forgotten.'"

So the follower Yahya was informed of this, and told of the matter of the follower — that nothing was said in him but the truth, in what he had seen of support from Jesus and what he believed concerning the strength of [his rank]. He showed him the contact of the upper limits with him while he was in the state of upbringing — and this is what is mentioned in the hadith, where he said: "I saw a white dove upon his head, and while I was looking at it, it sank into his head and entered it and disappeared, and then I knew that the Revelation had touched him." So he greeted him with peace through his wife, and that later one sent word to the follower who had come, in a letter, telling him that he was pleased with him, and apologized to him, and that he had extended to him the knowledge and support he had, so that he might lead him to it. And I command him to keep that — whoever lives is alive — and that is what he said:

> "He called to her from below her."

That is, without her in rank.

> "Do not grieve; your Lord has placed beneath you a stream."

That is, He has provided you with knowledge from Me, and brought it to you.

> "And shake toward you the trunk of the palm tree; it will let fall upon you fresh, ripe dates. So eat and drink and be comforted."

Ask him about what he gives you — when shall I give it to you? You will obtain from him what your eyes desire, and know that this is with His consent, and that he has accepted what was with you.

> "And if you see any human being, say, 'I have vowed to the Most Merciful a fast,

> "'so I will not speak today'"[^8]

[^8]: In copy (e) it is given as "Taisha."

308


<!-- page 309 -->

This means that he concealed it and did not disclose it to anyone among the people of the apparent. He then commanded Jesus, and Jesus came forward to safeguard him, peace be upon him. Yahya came to him, and Jesus asked him about the baptism.

This is what is mentioned in the hadith: that Jesus came to Yahya while Yahya was on the Sea of Galilee baptizing the people, and Jesus said to him, "Baptize me." Yahya said to him, "How can I undertake this when you are my master, and it is not fitting for me to undo your secrets?"

Jesus said to him, "Even so, today you are my master. Baptize me." So he baptized him, and Jesus then commanded him in this matter.

The latter manifested his command and his call without mentioning what had occurred between him and his predecessor — for Allah had not yet made the command public. So he did this, as in the verse:

"And her people brought him (the child) to her, and they said, 'O Mary, you have brought a strange thing. O sister of Aaron, your father was not a wicked man, nor was your mother a prostitute.'"

They were saying to her, "You have come with a grave matter."

By "O sister of Aaron" — Aaron was one of the deputies attached to him, possessing virtue. They meant: "You have done this, while your brother Harun has standing among us. Your father was not a wicked man, and your mother was not a prostitute, so how did you do this, and what was the imam and the argument by which you acted?"

For one like her would not act outside the bounds, nor do such a thing except according to what had occurred to her — that is, the divine custom. "And she pointed to him," that is, by command of the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, that he should answer them.

This is the linkage of the higher substance to him, the submission of the master of the time to him, the recognition of his right, and the handing over of his affair to its rightful holder.

"They said, 'How can we speak to one who is in the cradle, a child?'"

<!-- page 310 -->

The cradle, in the inward sense, is the level of nurture. They were saying: how can we converse with one who is at the level of nurture? — for whoever is at this level, his nurturer draws him near by what is opened to him of knowledge, and shields him from it at times when there is fear that he cannot yet bear it. This is just as one who rocks the cradle of a child draws him close at one moment and pushes him away at another, so that the child may speak.

Jesus addressed them with prophecy and called them to himself, saying:

"He said, 'Indeed, I am the servant of Allah. He has given me the Book and has made me a prophet.'"

He says: He has given me the imamate and the prophethood. "And He has made me blessed wherever I am" — that is, wherever I am within the bounds of the call.

"And He has enjoined upon me prayer and zakat as long as I am alive."

This means: establishing the call, laying the foundation, and constituting the Shari'a. "And dutiful to my mother" — that is, the one who summoned Maryam.

"And He has not made me arrogant and wretched."

That is: I do not compel those beneath me, when Allah has given me of His bounty.

"And peace be upon me" — meaning, support.

"The day I was born, the day I die, and the day I am raised alive."

That is: the support does not leave me in any of my states, for I used to say that Allah Most High —

"That was Jesus, son of Mary, the word of truth about which they are in dispute."

— that he should take from the affection of the Most High.

<!-- page 311 -->

He exalted Himself above having a son, as the disbelievers attributed to Him. He and the ignorant are far above that.

Jesus carried out the message, greeted his deputy, who followed him and believed in him, and called his people. They rejected him, except for a few, so he turned away from them, withdrew, and triumphed over those who believed in him.

He said:

"When Jesus perceived disbelief among them, he said, 'Who will be my helpers toward Allah?' The disciples said, 'We are the helpers of Allah. We have believed in Allah, and bear witness that we are Muslims.'"

He asked them to testify to what they had done.

"'Our Lord, we have believed in what You have revealed, and we have followed the Messenger, so register us among the witnesses.'"

They asked to be with the imams in their company, to follow them. So they followed him and believed in him — the disciples, who were his followers. It was said in the narrations that they were hunters, and that this was because they hunted out the call from those who had turned away from the truth. It was also said that they were dyers, and all of this means that they turn people from misguidance to guidance and from disbelief to faith, just as dyers and clothmen change garments and goods of color.

He said this to them by way of example, and the common people took it according to its apparent meaning, attributing to them that outward sense.

As for the words of the Most High:

"When the disciples said, 'O Jesus, son of Mary, can your Lord send down to us a table from heaven?' He said, 'Fear Allah, if you are believers.'"

That is because they asked him to bring forth for one of them something material like what he himself had been given. So he commanded them to fear Allah and to take from those whom He had appointed for them.

<!-- page 312 -->

They said, "We wish to eat from it and have our hearts assured, and to know that you have spoken to us in truth, and to be among its witnesses."

They meant: if the matter comes to them from the higher limits without intermediary, they will know the truth.

"Jesus, son of Mary, said, 'O Allah, our Lord, send down upon us a table from heaven that will be a feast for us — for the first of us and the last of us — and a sign from You. And provide for us, for You are the best of providers.' Allah said, 'I will send it down to you, but whoever disbelieves afterward among you, I will surely punish him with a punishment such as I have never inflicted on any of the worlds.'"

He called them to this and said:

"And when I inspired the disciples to believe in Me and My Messenger, they said, 'We have believed, and bear witness that we are Muslims.'"

It is said that this was what appeared in the image of Christ to them after he had left them. Again and again it benefited them in what their hearts needed, and none believed in it except the disciples. Others disbelieved in it and said:

"This is clear magic." So they did not believe, despite what he had brought them by His command, and they turned away from him, as the Most High says:

"Allah said, 'O Jesus, I am taking you.'"

That is: I am moving you from the station of conveying the message to the station of overtaking them.

<!-- page 313 -->

"And raising you to Myself."

He says: I am drawing you near to the limit of support from me, ennobling you by extending the means of support, so that between you and Me there is no intermediary except some of them.

"And purifying you from those who disbelieve."

That is: when they have disbelieved in what you have brought them, before Me, I do not bring them close. I deprive them of your bounty and sever between you and them, as a punishment for them and a reward for you.

"And making those who follow you" — that is, those who have believed in you —

"superior to those who disbelieve until the Day of Resurrection."

That is, until the last, who is the Master of the Resurrection, with whom Allah gathers the servants. They will be rewarded by Him, and He will reward the believers and punish the disbelievers.

"Then to Me is your return, and I will judge between you concerning that wherein you used to differ."

That is: the return to the abode of the Hereafter.

"As for those who disbelieve, I will punish them with a severe punishment in this world."

This is the doubt, confusion, and misguidance they were in. "And the Hereafter" — they will be in His abode according to what Allah has promised them.

"As for those who believe and do righteous deeds, He will give them their reward in full."

That is, the reward for what they did in this world from their acknowledgment of monotheism, their belief in the Messengers, and their faith in the Imams.

"And Allah does not love the wrongdoers" — meaning those who put the matter out of place.

"That is what We recite to you of the verses and the wise remembrance."

<!-- page 314 -->

He says this to Muhammad, peace be upon him, informing him of the news of those who have passed before him from the Messengers. The wise remembrance is the knowledge of the interpretation of this and of the parables it has struck.

This is the conclusion of what is said in the story of Jesus, peace be upon him, and what was the origin of his Shari'a — for the matter of the cross, which he commanded those who followed him to take with him, has already been spoken of, and the explanation of its interpretation has been given above; there is no need to repeat it.

(1) After the fifth speaker, Jesus Christ, the bequest was passed to Simon al-Safa, his cousin, Simon ibn Yunus, who was nicknamed al-Safa because of his serenity; he was also called Peter the Prophet, and was one of the disciples of Jesus — that is, one of his followers. The matter then came to seven imams who were the deposit-holders: Marqus, Filib, Stephens, then Marwa the monk, then Herkel, and after him his nephew Jeremiah, then Girgis, who is the lake-monk, in whose time the sixth speaker Muhammad gave the call and took from him the deposits and documents that had been preserved from the time of Moses.
