By his death, the prophecy and the message returned to the children of Isma'il ibn Ibrahim, and the imamate likewise, which they bore — this was called al-Mustaqarra. The imams from the sons of Isma'il in this cycle are listed in the genealogical tree of the imams as follows: Kinana ibn Khuzaymah, al-Nadr ibn Kinana, Malik ibn Kinana, Fihr ibn Malik, Ghalib ibn Fihr, Lu'ay ibn Ghalib, Ka'b ibn Lu'ay, Murrah ibn Lu'ay, Hashim ibn Murrah, 'Imran ibn Hashim (Abu Talib), and 'Abd al-Muttalib whose name is Shaybah al-Hamd. As for 'Imran, he is the resident imam of the sixth speaker, Muhammad.

<!-- page 315 -->

## Chapter Six

### (In which is the interpretation of the story of Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him)

In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful.

When we intended to compose this book — which is the book *Asas al-Ta'wil* (The Basis of Interpretation) — and to expound in it what we had set forth in the book *Da'a'im al-Islam* (The Pillars of Islam) concerning the mention of monotheism, the knowledge of Islam, faith, prophethood, imamate, knowledge, scholars, halal and haram, and the issues and rulings with which the one who responds to the call of the guardian of the time should begin — so that he may be set right in his outward worship of Allah, manifesting his command, performing acts of obedience, and taking that from the direction of him — we mentioned that this is comparable to what should be done for the one born in the outward sense, who should be tended to first by setting right the outward form of his body: by being wrapped and adjusted, swaddled with bands, and by cutting his umbilical cord and severing him from what is not part of him — the placenta that was upon him and emerged with him — which is like the outward affiliations that the respondent assumes apart from his guardian. If his outward state is set right and corrected of its distortion and the disorder of creation that comes upon him if left untended, then he is received into nursing.

When we published the book *Da'a'im al-Islam*, which represented the setting right of the outward of the newborn for us, we enabled him to estimate what he hears,

<!-- page 316 -->

from believers and respondents, in what they do over two whole years. Then we composed this book to explain the inward of what is in the book *al-Da'a'im*, so that the respondent should come to know the apparent truths of what is in the book *al-Da'a'im* — the obligatory actions — and should come to know the realities of knowledge and rulings from the Imam. Thus his outward is set right; then he is prepared by what he hears, and is advanced in his knowledge of what is in the book *al-Rada' fi al-Batin* (Breastfeeding in the Inward) to accept the advanced evening lesson, his knowledge of which is apparent from what is within the bounds of this book. He becomes aware of that — in belief and in knowledge of the truth of the apparent knowledge that has been imposed upon him and of the rulings by which he worships. He persists in it, performs what he is to worship from its residence, and then rises to the levels of the limits of knowledge and wisdom, in proportion to his acceptance and merit, one limit and degree after another.

When we mentioned the imamate in this book — which we had set forth in the book *al-Da'a'im* — we devoted a chapter to mentioning whether it is the axis of the religion on which it revolves, or not, and that the deed is not rewarded and not accepted until the imam of the time is known. This book is its explanation and interpretation, so we needed to begin the account from Adam. We began with him, mentioned his story and the cycle of each speaker after him, and what occurred in it, and what Allah Most High narrated to Muhammad, peace be upon him, from their reports in His book that He revealed to him — and the inward of that, and the imams whom Allah Most High named among those who were in the cycles of the prophets, those whom Allah Most High singled out for prophethood and message to the people of their time when they had changed and their states had been corrupted by the law of the speaker who was in his cycle. In his law are seven imams; the cycle ends with the seventh of them, who is called the completer of the sixth — that is, the elucidation is made, and after him there is no elucidation; then the seventh comes forth in the elucidation, and the power of support is manifested in him, if he is prepared to be a messenger, even if a cycle is reigned over.


<!-- page 317 -->
The spokesman before him served as the Speaker, and if that arrangement was not in place, it was carried out cycle after cycle so that the conditions might be prepared. God Almighty sealed the message and the Prophethood with Muhammad (peace be upon him), and He kept the Imamate as his succession, ordaining it to continue cycle by cycle, so that the seventh of them might come.

He confines himself to declaring the proof, which is the seventh of the Imams; and the six before him display the speech of the Speaker, while the seventh delivers the speech and the proof of what manifests its power and support. They also play the role of Muhammad (peace be upon him), as occurred with every Speaker in his cycle — though none of them is a prophet or messenger, because God Almighty sealed prophethood and the message with Muhammad (peace be upon him), favoring him above those who would abrogate his Sharia with another Sharia or message brought by another Messenger. With Muhammad, God Almighty gathered the truth and made plain in him the obligatory matters,(1) the rulings, the lawful, and the forbidden, and He ratified what he brought; so none of the Imams of his cycle may turn from it, diminish it, substitute it, or come with anything other than it.

This is unlike the Imams of the Speakers' cycles before him, who could do so because the revelation of God Almighty came to them. With the elevation of Muhammad (peace be upon him), revelation was withdrawn and the messengership concluded, while the Imamate continued in its fullness, according to the Sunnah of God Almighty established within it. This is the saying of Ja'far ibn Muhammad (God's prayers be upon him): "We have the same obedience that the Messenger of God had, except that we do not permit or forbid anything other than what was already permitted and forbidden."

To another end in the cycle of Jesus (peace be upon him): God Almighty willed to abrogate his Sharia with the Sharia of Muhammad (peace be upon him) and to send a prophet who would speak after him, having already preached to his people — as God Almighty told him in His Book, saying:

"And [recall] when Jesus, son of Mary, said: 'O Children of Israel, indeed I am the Messenger of God to you, confirming what came before me of the Torah and bringing good tidings of a messenger to come after me, whose name is Ahmad.' But when he came to them with clear proofs, they said: 'This is clear magic.'"

(1) In Copy (5) "Petitions" is mentioned.

317

<!-- page 318 -->
Likewise, every Speaker preaches the Word that comes after him and warns his people of his cycle, just as Jesus (peace be upon him) in his cycle gave good tidings of the Messenger of God,(1) Muhammad (peace be upon him) — in what the People of the Torah and the Gospel read in their Torah and their Gospels, according to what they read after they distorted and changed it.

(1) A comparison of what is written in this book shows that there are differences between the Torah and the Bible in wording, and sometimes in sentences. I believe the reason is that this transmission — or rather that al-Nu'man — took the Bible verses from a copy written in a language other than Arabic and translated it, so it came as it is and the difference appeared. For example, the word "Baraclete" in the Bible refers to "Muhammad," and the translator of the Gospel of John rendered it with the word "the Comforter," and the translator of the Gospel of Matthew rendered it with the name "Elijah." The sentence that came from David's mouth — "O God, send the one who makes the six (?) so that people may know that he is a human being" — we have not found in other books, yet it is established because al-Nu'man saw it, even if he had not seen it when he wrote. Here we quote the verses as they were narrated:

"So Sarai humiliated her — that is, Hagar — and she fled from her face. An angel found her at the spring of water in the wilderness, the spring which is on the way to Assyria, and he said: 'O Hagar, where have you come from, and where are you going?' She said: 'I am fleeing from the face of my mistress Sarai.' The angel of the Lord said to her: 'Return to your mistress and submit under her hands.' The angel of the Lord said to her: 'Behold, you are pregnant, and you shall give birth to a son. You shall call his name Ishmael, for the Lord has heard your humiliation; and he shall be a wild man, his hand against every one and every one's hand against him, and he shall live in front of all his brothers.'"

It is stated in chapter 17, verses 18–21:

"Abraham said to God: 'Would that Ishmael might live before You.' And God said: 'Your wife Sarah shall bear you a son, and you shall call his name Isaac, and I have established an eternal covenant with him and with his descendants after him' — which is a Greek word and its meaning is 'the Holy Spirit,' or 'the Comforter,' or 'the Lawyer.' It is mentioned in the Gospel of John three times, in chapter 14 and in chapter 16, verse 7. The meaning of the verses there is as follows: 'And I will pray to the Father that He may give you a Comforter,' and in verses 16, 17, and 26: 'that he may remain with you forever — that he is the Spirit of truth, and the Comforter, that is, the Holy Spirit; the Paraclete whom the Father will send in his name, will teach you all and remind you of all that I have said to you. Truly, I say to you: it is good that I go, for the Comforter will not come to you unless I go; but if I go, I will send him to you.'"

318

<!-- page 319 -->
As God Almighty said, Muhammad (the prayers of God be upon him) gave good tidings of the Resurrection after him, and of the Mahdi before him, and warned against lying about him and denying him, and so forth. He said:

"Indeed, We have sent you as a witness, and a bearer of good tidings, and a warner."

We shall mention the matter of the Qa'im, the Mahdi, and the other Imams — may God's prayers be upon them — God willing.

When Jesus's afternoon turn was complete, may God's prayers be upon him, the seventh — who is the awaited one — was not prepared to appear, and the transmission of the perfection had been attended to before that. This may occur in some cycles: it is the period mentioned by God Almighty in His Book. Thus, the last week of Jesus's cycle came to pass before the appearance of Muhammad, may God's prayers be upon him.

And the earth was not devoid of God's proof within it; for when the orphan was not prepared for the appearance of the seventh in his time, the believers held fast to the guidance of those past, themselves lying in concealment, awaiting the rising of the seventh — since his rising had come and his time was due. From that derives the inner interpretation of His saying, the Almighty:

"And those of you who die and leave wives behind, they shall wait by themselves for four months and ten."

He means: if the world remains before the appearance of the seventh, the survivors hold fast to the allegiance of the four foundations and the ten branches, which we have already mentioned — that is, to believe in the Unity of the Creator and what relates to the intermediary between Him and the prophet; and to believe also in acknowledging the prophet and his foundation, and the Imam and his proof, who are the mediators between Him and the servants; and the seven Imams and the seven Speakers; and to believe that they know and acknowledge it.

319

<!-- page 320 -->
And they wait until the seventh rises, which is for them the time of concealment. That is His saying:

"There is no blame upon them for what they do with themselves."

I mean: from showing wisdom and joining the Master of the Time — as the women whose husbands have died do, when their time has come and they have completed the waiting period until they present themselves again for marriage and become wives once more — so that the community may, during the interval, not be cut off from obedience. That is the saying of God, the Almighty:

"Those who disbelieved among the People of the Book and the polytheists were not to be parted from their ways until the clear evidence came to them."

That is, the speech of the Master of the Time.

"And where are the disbelievers among the People of the Book?"

These are the ones who saw the matter of the Imam after they had known him. "And the polytheists" are those who associated others with the guardianship to which they had no right. When God sent Muhammad, he summoned to him the survivors from the cycle of Jesus (peace be upon him), who revealed to him what they had and saluted him. We shall mention them later, as we have stipulated regarding the remembrance of the messengers — the good tidings of the messengers, those who acknowledge it and those who deny it among the Jews and Christians, from what is in the books in their hands, from what they have acknowledged and where they mention a verse from the Torah and the Gospel, in addition to what they took away of what was in it concerning him (peace be upon him).

When Abraham(1) called upon Ishmael, He said to him:

"I have heard your supplication concerning him; behold, I have answered him, I have blessed him, and I have made him exceedingly great. I shall give him a kingdom, and I shall make him a great nation."

320

<!-- page 321 -->
That is Muhammad — and the twelve great ones are his limits, the captains in every age. In this book: when Hagar fled from Sarah, a king appeared to her and said to her:

"O Hagar, a nation of masters — return to your mistress and submit to her, for God will multiply your descendants so that they cannot be numbered when you are with child. You shall give birth to a son and call him Ishmael, for God Almighty has heard your supplication. His hand shall be above the hand of all, and the hands of all shall be extended to him in submission."

This concerns the Messenger who comes after the prophecy. The king was born, and Isaac was born before him; then God Almighty turned things, and the kingdom in Ishmael came to be as promised.

And of what He says:

"God came from Sinai and shone forth from Sa'ir, and rose from the mountains of Faran; He shall come from the hills with the trampling — at His right hand is the wicked one."

They said: He meant that He came from Sinai when He sent Moses — when the Torah was revealed to him at Mount Sinai; and the shining from Sa'ir is when He sent Jesus from there, and he lived in a village called Nasareth which is in the land of Galilee; and likewise, the rising from the mountains of Faran is when He sent Muhammad — and Faran is Mecca — by the tongue in which God revealed the Torah. Thus we remind, and we make known that in its mountains the news of God's Muhammad was revealed, and his book was revealed to him, and he was one of the people of Jerusalem — the appearance of the Resurrection. And the fire that is at his right is the revelation of the inner meaning of the Sharia and its interpretation; we shall mention his story in its place, God willing. He said to Moses: "I shall raise up for

321
21

<!-- page 322 -->
the Children of Israel a prophet from their brothers, like you; I shall place My words in his mouth, and he shall speak only by My command." And the brothers of the Children of Israel are the sons of Ishmael, and the prophet Muhammad is from them, in the Sharia which Moses commanded by God.

Among what they mentioned is the saying of the Messiah in the Gospel to the disciples: "I am going, and the Holy Spirit will come — the Holy Spirit will come, not of himself, but as it is said: he says what bears witness against me; and you bear witness for me, because you are with me before the people. And everything that God has prepared for you, He has prepared for your good."

In another account, John said about Christ: "The Baraclete will not come to you unless I go; and if he comes, he will rebuke the world for sin, and shall not speak of his own accord, but shall give praise to it and speak to you, and shall whisper to you about the truth, and tell you of accidents and the unseen."

In another account: "The Paraclete, the Spirit of truth whom my Father will send — He will send him; for he teaches you all things." And He said: "I ask my Father to send you another Paraclete, who shall be with you forever — who teaches you everything." I mean by his saying that "he shall be with you forever" his Sharia, which remains to eternity.(1)

In another account: "The human being is going, and the Paraclete comes after him. He comes to you with secrets, and confesses all things to you, and bears witness for me as I bore witness for him. I brought you parables, and he brings you their interpretation."

When Yahya ibn Zakariyya was imprisoned and about to be killed, he sent his disciples to Christ and said to them: "Tell him: are you the one who is coming, or do we await another?" They told him this, and Christ said to them: "Truly, with certainty, I tell you that he has not risen,"

(1) "As for Ishmael, I have heard you: behold, I have blessed him, and I shall make him fruitful, and shall multiply him exceedingly; twelve chiefs shall he beget, and I shall make him a great nation." It says in chapter 21, verse 14: "So Abraham rose early in the morning, took bread and a jar of water, and gave it to Hagar, and put them on her shoulders, with the child; and he sent her away. She departed and wandered in the wilderness of Beersheba, and when the water ran out of the bag, she threw the boy under one of the trees. She went and sat opposite him, far away — about a bowshot's distance — for she said: 'Let me not look upon the death of the boy.' So she sat opposite him,"

322


A better one than Yahya bin Zakariya — while the Torah and the books of the prophets recited prophecy and revelation one after another until Yahya came. As for the human, if you wish to accept it: the Baraclet (the Paraclete) is going to come after me; so whoever has ears to hear, let him hear what I am truly saying.

And among what they mentioned is that the Psalms say: "Praise the Lord. Praise the righteous who built it to make Israel rejoice in its Creator, and the houses of Zion — because God has chosen a nation for Himself and granted it victory, and has rewarded the righteous, some of them with dignity. They rest upon their beds and grow up for Him with loud voices. In their hands are double-edged swords with which God takes vengeance on the Gentiles who do not worship Him, and with which they bind their kings with chains and their nobles with shackles." This was for none but Muhammad.

And in another Psalm: "He shall have dominion from sea to sea, and from the rivers to the ends of the earth. The peoples shall run before him on their knees, and his enemies shall lick the dust beneath his feet. Kings shall bring him offerings and prostrate before him, and nations shall owe him obedience and submission — for he saves the wretched and persecuted from the one stronger than him, and rescues the poor who have no helper, and has compassion on the weak and needy. He shall give of the gold of the land, and prayer shall be offered upon him at all times, and he shall be blessed every day, and his remembrance shall endure with the remembrance of Allah Almighty forever."

And from what David (peace be upon him) said: "O God, send the one who shall make the sons of men know that he is a human being."

And among what they mentioned is, from the words of Isaiah, he said concerning God Almighty: "My chosen servant —

— and she lifted up her voice and wept, and God heard the voice of the boy, and the angel of God called to her from heaven and said to her: 'Hagar, do not be afraid, for God has heard the voice of the boy where he is. Get up, lift up the boy and hold him firmly by the hand, for I will make of him a great nation.' And God opened her eyes, and she saw a well of water, and she went and filled the skin with water and gave the boy to drink. And God was with the boy, and he grew up and dwelt in the wilderness, and he became an archer with the bow, and he dwelt in the wilderness of Faran (Paran), and his mother took for him a wife from the land of Egypt." [Genesis 21:14–21, continuing the citation.]

— upon whom my soul shines, with whom my soul is well-pleased. My justice shall appear among the nations, and he shall commend her with the commandments. He shall not laugh, nor shall his voice be heard in the markets. He shall open blind eyes, hear deaf ears, and protect anxious hearts. What I have given to him I shall give to no other — Ahmad. Praise be to God, a new praise that comes from the farthest reaches of the earth. Its elders and its inhabitants are awed by it. They acclaim Allah Almighty in every honor and exalt Him upon every banner that does not weaken nor is overcome, that does not bend with the wind nor humble the righteous who are like a bruised reed, but rather strengthens the two friends, which is the corner of the humble — and it is the light of God which is neither extinguished nor concealed, so that His argument may be established in the earth and excuse cut off by Him through His Torah, and humankind and the jinn within it may be led by it as by the Torah."

"And I made you a light to the nations and a covenant for the peoples, to open the eyes of the blind and rescue the captives from the darkness that has overcome them — authority shall rest on his shoulders, the sign of prophecy."

"So look at what you see, and tell me of it." I said: "I saw two riders, one of them coming on a donkey, the other on camels. And one of them said to its owner: 'Babylon and its carved idols have fallen.'" By the owner of the donkey he means Isa (Jesus), and by the owner of the camel he means Muhammad — and the fall of Babylon and its idols at the hands of the Persian king came to pass.

And he said: "He shall fill the desert and the cities and the palaces built of clay with praise; and from the tops of the mountains they shall call to those who turn toward God in honor, and shall affirm His praise on land and sea, and raise for them a banner for all nations."

In Deuteronomy 18:15 it says: Moses said to the children of Israel: "The Lord your God will raise up for you a prophet from among you, from among your brothers, like me — to him you shall listen, according to all that you asked of your God at Horeb on the day of the assembly, saying: 'I will no longer hear the voice of the Lord my God, nor will I see this great fire again, lest I die.' The Lord said to me: 'They have done well in what they have spoken. I will raise up for them a prophet from among their brothers, like you, and I will put my words in his mouth, and he shall speak to them all that I command him. And it shall be that the person who does not heed my words that he speaks in my name — I shall require it of him.'"

"From the far ends of the earth they shall come swiftly, and they shall build a Ka'ba — they are the ones born of Ishmael, and the banner raised is the Messenger of Allah Muhammad (peace be upon him)."

And from the words of Habakkuk in the time of Daniel: "God came from Teman (Yemen) and from Jerusalem and from the mountains of Faran (Paran)" — meaning Mecca. This is that Allah Almighty sent Muhammad (peace be upon him) from there, and the earth was filled with the praise and sanctification of Ahmad, and that land lay beneath His right hand, and the necks of the nations shall submit to him to illumine the earth, and his horses shall carry him into the sea.

And from his words: "And you shall stride forth with your bow, and you shall draw the arrows by your command, O Muhammad" — this is revelation in his name (peace be upon him). This is what they have acknowledged and confirmed, beyond what they have altered and exchanged, as Allah informed us concerning them — and most of His remembrance and the manifest one whose banner is the Prophet's holds a secret and an evidence.

And among those who reported news of his prophecy before his time, in the period mentioned above, was a group of Abyssinian Christians who were sent. They saw him being carried at midday by the woman who had nursed him in the desert and who was bringing him back to his mother in Mecca. They saw upon him the sign of prophecy from what had been told to them, and they understood that they should take him from the woman and carry him off to their country. She was not free of them except after great effort, and after he had overcome them and those who were with her from among her people had come to her aid.

And among such accounts is his story with Bahira the monk. He was between Mecca and the Levant, when his uncle Abu Talib took him with him to the Levant. He camped beneath a tree, and Bahira looked from his hermitage and saw what appeared to be a cloud shading him from the sun, and saw the branch of the tree leaning over to shade him from the sun. He knew that this was so. He prepared food, then summoned the people to it and brought him along with them. When they had eaten, he asked about him.

In Deuteronomy chapter 33, Moses said: "This is the blessing with which Moses, the man of God, blessed the children of Israel before his death. He said: 'The Lord came from Sinai, and rose upon them from Seir and shone from Mount Faran (Paran), and came from the hills of Jerusalem, and from His right hand was the fire of the law for them.'"

They told him about him, and they said: "Muhammad bin Abdullah." He said: "And who is he?" They said: "He is with his uncle." "And where is his father?" They said: "He died, and his mother died, and his grandfather took charge of him and then he died, and his uncle took charge of him." This was among what he knew of his signs. So he took him aside and said to him: "O my son, I ask you about al-Lat and al-Uzza — do not conceal what I ask you about them." Muhammad said to him: "What can I tell you of al-Lat and al-Uzza? By Allah, there is nothing more hateful to me than they." This further increased his certainty in a striking way, and he said to him: "I ask you by Allah." He said: "You have asked me by a great matter." So he asked him about some of his conditions, and Muhammad told him of them, and he gave him his proofs. Then he took Abu Talib aside and said to him: "Guard this nephew of yours from the Jews, and do not show him to them — they are his enemies and the enemies of one like him before him. So beware of them concerning him." He had hoped to reach his time, but he died before that.

Khadija bint Khuwaylid had wealth and used to trade with it, placing goods in the hands of men. When the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) reached manhood, the virtues that emerged in him — purity, honesty, and trustworthiness — became known. She sent money and goods with him to Damascus, and sent with him a servant of hers to serve him. He returned to her with great profit, and the boy told her that whenever the heat intensified, two great birds would shade his head. He also told her that one day he came down and slept under a tree, near which was a monk in a hermitage. When the monk saw him, he came down to him and saw him sleeping. The boy asked about him, and the monk told him that no one had ever slept under this tree except a prophet.

Khadija had been widowed by her husband Abu Hala, and Waraqah ibn Nawfal — the son of her uncle — had been engaged to her and was at odds with her, while he was on the Christian religion. So she told him what

Gospel of John, chapters 14:15, 24, 25:
Jesus said to his apostles: "If you love me, keep my commandments, and I will ask the Father, and he will give you another Comforter to remain with you forever." And his saying: "He who does not love me does not keep my words. And the words that you hear are not mine, but the Father's who sent me. By this I am with you. But the Comforter, the Holy Spirit, whom the Father will send in my name, he will teach you all things and remind you of all that I have told you."

the boy had told her about him. And he said: "I hope that he is the prophet of this nation, for the time of his appearance has come, and we know him and find his description in our scriptures." So Khadija — may Allah have mercy on her — sent to him and offered herself to him when she learned of the virtue in him, and he married her. Waraqah ibn Nawfal awaited his prophethood and asked Khadija about his condition, and she told him. He said: "He is, by God, the prophet of this nation, and there are well-known poems of his concerning it." But he died before Muhammad (peace be upon him) was sent with the message, fearing his summons to do so. The people of knowledge from those remaining in the final period of Jesus (peace be upon him) used to come to him; and he called those who remained among them, and they gave him what they had. Then Allah honored him with prophethood and sent him as a messenger. This is what most of us say.

He is the one whom Allah sent to the believers, asking him to recite to them His verses, and to purify them, and to teach them the Book and wisdom, even though they had been before in clear error — and to others of them who had not yet joined them. And He is the Mighty, al-Hakim (the Wise). That is the bounty of Allah which He grants to whom He wills, and Allah is the possessor of great bounty.

The ummi (illiterate ones) are the people of truth among the believers. They are called ummi because they are linked to the argument of the speaker of their time, to whom belongs the inner call. He is, in the inner world, their mother, and the spokesman is their father. They also relate what the higher or the lower boundary mentions, in the position of the mother — and the higher as the father — and those who respond to them as children. So He sent him as a scholar.

In Gospel of John 15:26–27 it is said: "And the Comforter whom I will send to you from the Father — the Spirit of Truth which proceeds from the Father — he will bear witness of me, and you also shall bear witness, because you have been with me from the beginning."

And to those who followed him from the final period of Jesus (peace be upon him) — they are the ummi people whom He mentioned, and the others who did not follow them are the polytheists. And I sent him as a messenger to all the worlds — and this is what the Almighty says: "That bounty is bestowed upon whomever He wills, and Allah is the possessor of great bounty."

As for the sons before him, they were sent to particular nations — and the remembrance of Allah Almighty (sent Muhammad to all mankind) is by His saying: "Say: O people, I am the Messenger of Allah to you all." And the saying of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): "I was sent to the red and the black." Allah Almighty made him an argument against all His creation, sealed the prophethood with him, and made no prophet after him.

The "worlds" (al-'alamin) here are the believers at the time of the period, in order that they may belong to the speaker of their time. Among the arguments of his argument is that Allah Almighty said: "The Prophet is closer to the believers than themselves, and his wives are their mothers" — and in some of the readings: "and he is a father to them" — and his wives, in the inner sense, are his arguments, the first parents: the father, then the son, then the brother — and the wife on one side only.

It is mentioned in Gospel of John 16:6–11: "But I have not told you these things until now, lest sorrow fill your heart. But I tell you the truth: it is better for you that I go. For if I do not depart, the Comforter will not come to you; but if I go, I will send him to you. And when he comes, he will rebuke the world for sin, for righteousness, and for judgment: for sin, because they do not believe in me; for righteousness, because I am going to my Father and you do not see me any more; for judgment, because the prince of this world has been condemned." He also said: "I have many things to tell you, but you cannot bear them at present. But when the Spirit of truth comes, he will guide you into all truth, for he speaks not of himself, but whatever he hears, he speaks, and he tells you the things to come. He glorifies me, because he takes what is mine and tells you. All that the Father has is mine — that is why I said: he takes what I have and tells you."


Her husband, and she shall be the mother of her children — except for Maryam, whose story stands apart.

The "unlettered" in the language of the Arabs, in which the Qur'an was revealed, are those who do not read the Book and do not write. So too were the believers in that period, who lived in the final cycle of the Messiah until the rise of Muhammad (peace be upon him). None among them was acquainted with any of the knowledge of the Imam who would accept him, and so he remained, peace be upon him, until Allah singled him out for prophethood by His might. This is the meaning of the words of the Almighty:

"The unlettered Prophet"

And He said:

"And you did not recite before it any book, nor did you inscribe one with your right hand."

For the inscription is the noblest of things, yet these are the signs of the verses in the breasts of those who have been given knowledge.

The truth here is like the truth of the Imam of the Time, who says: you were never standing before any book, nor did you establish a foundation or compose a law, until Allah singled you out for that — and you, O My Prophet, did not know it. Had you known it, those who lay in wait around you would have doubted, and would have said that you had foreknowledge of it. His claim is among the miracles that human beings are unable to perform and cannot bear except with the support of al-Bari. By these verses he proves that Muhammad was a Messenger sent to a people whose limit was only what we have described — then Allah raised them up and elevated them, and that is what Allah Almighty intended.

In Matthew, chapter 11, verses 11–15, it is stated:

"Truly, I say to you, among those born of women there has risen no one greater than John the Baptist, yet the least in the kingdom of heaven is greater than he. From the days of John the Baptist until now, the kingdom of heaven has been seized by force, and the forceful seize it. For all the prophets and the Law prophesied until John, and if you are willing to accept it, he is Elijah who is to come. He who has ears to hear, let him hear."

The transmission of the prophethood from the son of Ishmael, peace be upon them, came in this interval so that none would be tested with being compelled to submit to one weaker than himself. Allah Almighty did this out of mercy for His creation and compassion for His servants, and it was He who appointed the successor. Jesus, peace be upon him, as we have mentioned, summoned the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) when his own matter had ended and his work had ceased. He made his command manifest to him, took his covenant, and led him and those who came after him to the successor. Their reasons reached both Arabs and non-Arabs, and he was the appointed one when Allah Almighty singled out Muhammad for the Message, honored him with prophethood, and called his people.

Some of them lied and said: rather, this knowledge of Muhammad's is what a non-Arab teaches him — the one who used to instruct him and call him. Such is the saying that Allah, may He be exalted, refers to:

"And they said, 'These are legends of the ancients which he has written down.'"

And He said:

"And We certainly know that they say, 'It is only a human being who teaches him.' The tongue of the one they refer to is foreign, and this Qur'an is in a clear Arabic tongue."

The way of Allah Almighty has been carried out in all those He has sent among His messengers: that the Speaking Messenger establishes the manifestation of the Shariʿa and the revelation, and appoints a foundation from among the people closest to him — whoever responds to his call, he tests him, and is satisfied with him, to perform the subtle interpretation.

It is stated in Psalm 72 of our master David:

"O God, give Your judgments to the King, and Your righteousness to the king's son. May he judge Your people with justice and Your afflicted with right. May the mountains bring peace to the people, and the righteous judge for the poor of the people, save the children of the needy, and crush the oppressors. May they fear You as long as the sun and the moon endure. May he descend like rain upon the mown grass, and like showers that flow upon the earth. May righteousness flourish in his days, and abundance of peace, until the moon is no more. May he rule from sea to sea, and from the River to the ends of the earth. Before him the desert-dwellers shall bow, and his enemies shall lick the dust. The kings of Tarshish and the isles shall bring offerings, the kings of Sheba and Seba shall present gifts. All kings shall worship him, and all nations shall serve him, because He delivers the needy."

The Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings of Allah be upon him) established the manifest Shariʿa and set its boundaries, which he set up for them to observe, in accordance with what Allah had revealed to him. As the Almighty said:

"And We have sent down to you the Reminder so that you may make clear to the people what has been sent down to them."

He thus disclosed some of its statement to those whom he had appointed and set up, before he established his foundation, and he informed them that he was appointing him. Some of them grew greedy on account of this, and I had to pray to Allah, who made them few. And Allah sent down to Muhammad (peace be upon him):

"Do not move your tongue with it to hasten it. Indeed, upon Us is its gathering and its recitation. So when We have recited it, then follow its recitation. Then upon Us is its clarification."

He thus taught him and his family that he should not have disclosed it of himself — for the clarification belongs only to Allah Almighty, who commands the Prophet to set up the one for whom it is to be set up.

And the Almighty said:

"And warn your nearest kin."

So he gathered Banu ʿAbd al-Muttalib — we have already mentioned the matter of gathering them, how he gathered them, and what he presented to them of its symbols, in the book "Daʿaʾim al-Islam" (Pillars of Islam) — and it is well known that many of the common people narrated that he (peace be upon him) gathered them with the thigh of a sheep and a goblet of milk. They ate until they were satisfied and drank until they were sated, though they were forty men, most of whom would each consume a whole leg of mutton and a great quantity of drink. So too, inwardly, with the knowledge he conveyed to them.

"He has mercy on the poor and the wretched, and he saves the souls of the poor from injustice and abduction. He redeems their souls and honors their blood in his sight. He shall live, and the gold of Sheba shall be given to him; men shall pray for him continually, and bless him all the day. May there be abundance of grain in the land, on the tops of the mountains; may its fruit wave like Lebanon, and may men blossom from the city like grass of the field. May his name endure forever; may his name continue as long as the sun. May all nations be blessed in him; may all the earth bless him."

And wisdom — he warned them of it, and that it was but a little, yet they did not bear it, nor were they guided to its knowledge. In their minds, their ears, and their dreams they could not carry or learn knowledge beyond that, and so they were unable to grasp what the Prophet gave them. He then informed them of what he wished to set up as his foundation, and presented to them the one whom he had taught. All of them were unable to accept this, and he held to him by the prayers of Allah upon him. He set him up in their presence, and I bear witness to that. Those who attended him were among those who would set them up for the limits of the manifest Shariʿa — even greater than that for their believers and their disbelievers, except those who are infallible by Allah.

When the believers saw that they were themselves more deserving of that than he, this was the first arrogance — and it was the polytheism and hypocrisy of those who are called Muslims. We have mentioned their saying to Abu Talib: "We congratulate you, your son has come to you" — and when they went away mocking, this weighed heavily upon the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), upon his obstacles and his sorrows. His chest tightened, and he kept silent before the rest of the people out of fear of them — until Allah Almighty sent down upon him, on his return from the Farewell Pilgrimage, saying:

"O Messenger, convey what has been sent down to you from your Lord. And if you do not, then you have not conveyed His message. And Allah will protect you from the people."

So he made Ghadir for the guardianship (wilaya) of ʿAli (may Allah's prayers be upon him), and the report of that is well known, narrated by the public and the private. We have mentioned it in the book "Daʿaʾim al-Islam" (Pillars of Islam).

Psalm 149, verses 1–8, says:

"Hallelujah! Sing to the Lord a new song, His praise in the assembly of the godly. Let Israel rejoice in his Maker; let the children of Zion rejoice in their King. Let them praise His name with dancing, making melody to Him with strings and instruments. For the Lord takes pleasure in His people; He carries the meek with salvation. Let the godly rejoice in glory; let them sing for joy on their beds. Let the high praises of God be in their mouths, and a two-edged sword in their hand, to execute vengeance on the nations and punishment on the peoples, to bind their kings with chains and their nobles with iron fetters, to drag them — the written judgment — this is honor for all His godly ones. Hallelujah."

This weighed heavily upon the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings of Allah be upon him), who said:

"We did it not except with the truth."

"And We have not created the heavens and the earth and what is between them except in truth."

The heavens are like the utterance, and the earth is like the foundations — meaning, what we have established from:

"And indeed the Hour is coming."

I mean: the Resurrection will indeed be raised.

"So forgive with gracious forgiveness."

That is, what harm is it to you in the hatred of those who oppose its raising?

"Indeed your Lord is the All-Knowing Creator."

Meaning the One who has determined that by His knowledge.

"And We have given you seven of the often-repeated."

Meaning the seven Imams after him from his descendants, whose excellence ends with the seventh of them — the sixth of them being prevented from the disclosing statement, in order that the seventh be the one who gathers the affairs of the servants.

"And the Great Qur'an."

I mean: the foundation that he established.

It is mentioned in the words of Isaiah, in chapter 42:

"Behold, My servant whom I uphold, My chosen in whom My soul delights; I have put My Spirit upon him, that justice may come forth to the Gentiles. He will not cry out, nor lift up his voice, nor cause it to be heard in the street. A bruised reed he will not break, and a smoldering wick he will not quench. He will faithfully bring forth justice. He will not grow weary or be discouraged, until he has established justice in the earth, and the coastlands shall wait for his law. Thus says the Lord, the Creator of the heavens and the One who stretches out the earth and its produce, who gives breath to the people upon it and spirit to those who walk on it."

"Do not stretch out your eyes toward what We have given for enjoyment to pairs among them, nor grieve over them."

I mean: those who took refuge in denying what he did in establishing his foundation.

"Of the disbelievers and the hypocrites."

And they did not prevent him from continuing.

"For a determined period."

And that the punishment not be hastened upon them.

"And lower your wing to the believers."

Meaning those who are content with that and submit to his command.

"And say: indeed I am the clear warner."

"As We sent down upon those who divided into parts, those who have made the Qur'an into portions."

Meaning those who wanted it to be among them.

"By your Lord, We will surely question them all about what they used to do. So proclaim what you are commanded, and turn away from the polytheists. Indeed, We are sufficient for you against the mockers."

"In him is a Spirit. I, the Lord, have called you in righteousness; I will take you by the hand and protect you, and make you a covenant for the people, a light for the nations, to open the eyes of the blind, to bring out the prisoners from the dungeon, those who sit in darkness. I am the Lord; that is My name. My glory I will not give to another, nor My praise to graven images. Behold, the former things have come to pass, and new things I now declare; before they spring forth I tell you of them. Sing to the Lord a new song, His praise from the ends of the earth, you who go down to the sea and all that fills it, the coastlands and their inhabitants. Let the wilderness and its cities lift up their voice, the villages that Kedar inhabits; let the inhabitants of Sela sing for joy, let them shout from the tops of the mountains. Let them give glory to the Lord and declare His praise in the coastlands. The Lord goes forth like a mighty man, like a man of war He stirs up His zeal; He cries out, shouts aloud, and shows Himself mighty against His foes."

I mean those who mocked his action in establishing his foundation.

"Those who set up with Allah another deity — they are going to know."

"And We already know that your chest is tightened by what they say."

"So glorify the praise of your Lord and be among those who prostrate. And worship your Lord until there comes to you the certainty."

So he shares it with those who set it up, those of the Imams among his descendants, and those who stand at the end of time from his descendants. And he consoled him with what was bringing him up, and his chest was straitened by the rebuffing of them away from the one he had set up, as the Almighty said in the story of Moses:

"The Samaritan led them astray, and they took the calf as a god besides him."

The Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings of Allah be upon him) therefore said: "You will surely tread the paths of the nations before you, span by span and cubit by cubit — even if they entered a lizard's hole you would enter it."

He says: if those before you answered the call of a beast, you would answer the call of such a beast like them, and you would enter it — meaning the one in whose downfall and folly there is no doubt. So the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was consoled with the consolation of Allah, presented to those whom he had been commanded to be patient in turning away from them, and accepted what Allah commanded of him. He set up his foundation, and feared for him, until his command appeared, as we have mentioned, on the day of Ghadir. He revealed what he revealed, as Allah Almighty had confirmed to him, and I cited him so that he could establish the argument of Allah against the one who disobeyed His command. When he did that, he presented the one he had left behind, and Allah gave him good tidings, as He sent down to him, saying:

It is also mentioned in chapter 21, verses 6–10:

"For thus the Lord said to me: 'Go, set up the watchman; let him declare what he sees — riders of donkeys, riders of camels.' So he listened intently, and then cried out like a lion: 'Lord, I stand continually upon the watchtower by day, and I stand at my post every night. Behold, here come riders, men in pairs of horsemen.' And he answered: 'Babylon has fallen, has fallen, and all the carved images of its gods are shattered to the ground.'"


<!-- page 336 -->
"Indeed, We have granted you a clear conquest."

That is: We have opened for you what was closed in your Sharia by way of declaring the position of the one upon whom you rest your foundation.

"That Allah may forgive you what preceded of your sin and what is to follow."

It means: what you have left of the declaration ("and what is delayed"), that is, what you take up afterwards.

"And that He may complete His favor upon you."

That is, by the appearance of the one who rises from among your descendants at the end of time.

"And guide you to a straight path."

That is, He guides you to the establishment of those of his descendants.

"And that Allah may grant you a mighty victory."

It means that He makes it manifest to every nation, as the Almighty said:

"That He may make it prevail over all religion."

It means: that one of his descendants is the one who rises. And the words of the Almighty are as follows:

"We have opened for you a manifest conquest."

That is, We have established a foundation for you. We have mentioned in what is above this — and elsewhere — that, from among the borders, it may not be possible to establish it through the guardian of the time, but he must do what is necessary by himself.

It is mentioned in the words of Habakkuk, chapter 3:

"God came from Teman, and the Holy One from Mount Paran. His majesty covered the heavens, and the earth was filled with His praise. And a brightness like the light had rays from His hand, and there He hid His power. Before Him went the plague, and at His feet came forth fever. He stood and measured the earth; He looked and made the nations tremble; the everlasting mountains were crushed; the ancient hills bowed low. Eternity belongs to Him."

<!-- page 337 -->
And concerning what Allah opened for the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): Allah then raised him to the world of His kingdom, showed him the limits of His heavens, taught him the knowledge of His unseen, and thereby preferred him over all His Prophets and brought him into proximity to the upper limits. This is what the Almighty says:

"Glory be to the One who took His servant by night from al-Masjid al-Haram to al-Masjid al-Aqsa, whose surroundings We have blessed, that We might show him of Our signs. Indeed, He is the All-Hearing, the All-Seeing."

He said:

"The Almighty is the One who took His servant by night."

Glory be to the purity of the Creator above the purity of His creation, and the heavens of His righteousness.

"And His servant" — here this is Muhammad (peace be upon him).

"Took him by night," that is, He caused him to travel by night; He took him by night and departed.

In the language of the Arabs they say "so-and-so took such-and-such by night," meaning he traveled with him by night and the secrets of the journey.

Night, and night in interpretation, are like concealment and secrecy in the inner meaning.

It refers to his eminence and his biography in the knowledge of the esoteric, between him and the completion of his role; and he is the sixth of the Imams, and the seventh after him is the one prepared for the task. We have mentioned that, and we will continue to speak about it perfectly.

Speaking of it in its place later on, insha'Allah: al-Masjid al-Haram is like the speaker of his time, whether he was a prophet or an imam, and al-Masjid al-Aqsa is the figure of the end. And he, the sixth, is forbidden to open the mosque. Al-Masjid al-Haram is outwardly the mosque of Mecca, and within it is the house to which one goes on pilgrimage. Al-Masjid al-Aqsa, outwardly, is a mosque in the holy place; pilgrimage is made only to it, and there is the circumambulation around the house. So the completion is that no one approaches him except his proof whom he establishes after him; and after him, he is the seventh of

<!-- page 338 -->
the Imams to whom the chain ends. Therefore it is mentioned in the report that he was taken by night from Mecca to Bayt al-Maqdis: this means that he is superior in knowledge between it and the completion of the previous role, and he has gathered the knowledge and wisdom contained in them concerning what passes through their affairs and how their limits stand — as they are — from the upper limits that he saw by the Holy Spirit. This is the saying of Allah the Almighty:

"The heart did not lie about what it saw. Will you then dispute with him about what he saw? And indeed he saw him in another descent, at the Lote-Tree of the utmost boundary, near which is the Garden of Refuge."

He said:

"He has indeed seen of the great signs of his Lord."

I mean by all of this the upper limits which he saw with a vision that did not falter, while he was injuring

The pure soul is from distress, so it was narrated from some of his wives that she said of

The night of his being taken by night: "By Allah, there was nothing between my body and his body." And it was said in the report that

When he reached Bayt al-Maqdis, Gabriel came to him with a riding-mount unlike a camel, and on the back of the animal he was called

al-Buraq, with his knees. In the interpretation, this is the shining and resplendent banner, which is the declaration

And the banner of the later one, and through it, the knowledge of the Imam and his riding upon it is his grasp and ascension

To the heavens — in interpretation, his knowledge of its kingdom and the knowledge of what is in it — including his saying:

The Almighty in the story of Abraham (peace be upon him):

"And thus did We show Abraham the kingdom of the heavens and the earth."

"And that he might be among those who have certainty."

It is also mentioned in the report that he prayed, gathering the Prophets, and he prayed with them in secret.

<!-- page 339 -->
His call to all nations, that he was sent to all of them, as we have mentioned, while the other prophets in turn

were each sent to a particular people, and he said:

"Some of Our signs."

That is, one of the signs of Allah the Almighty that I show is His limits which He has set

Between him and his children and the angels — and he saw a great sign from among them. That is what He said:

"He has indeed seen of the great signs of his Lord."

And the Almighty said:

"He is of great strength, possessed of soundness, who appeared on the highest horizon. Then he drew near, and came down, and was at a distance of two bow-lengths or nearer, and revealed to His servant what He revealed. The heart did not lie about what it saw. Will you then dispute with him about what he saw? And indeed he saw him in another descent, at the Lote-Tree of the utmost boundary, near which is the Garden of Refuge — when there enveloped the Lote-Tree that which enveloped it. The sight did not turn aside, nor did it transgress. He saw of the great signs of his Lord."

I mean by all of this the upper limits which he saw with the clear and insightful eye of his heart, and

he heard with his ear that He said:

"Indeed, He is the All-Hearing, the All-Seeing."

He said:

"To al-Masjid al-Aqsa."

We have mentioned that it is like the one who is forbidden, and He said:

"Whose surroundings We have blessed."

<!-- page 340 -->
Blessing is support and opening. That occurred among those who were before him and after him.

He said:

"That We might show him of Our signs."

This is because He showed him the upper limits and established for him a lower limit corresponding to them.

So he (peace be upon him) and his instrument, from that knowledge which he brought back to its foundation, were directed to what should be done:

He leads him to it, teaches him, then entrusts him to lead, from that, the one who leads him

to himself with his secret, and establishes him after him, with what he should bring, and transfers it likewise from one to one,

just so, as well as the knowledge of the apparent Sharia, and commanding him to perform it on his behalf for the servants, and what

he needs from him. Then He said — and He is the most truthful of those who speak:

"It is He who sent down tranquility into the hearts of the believers, that they might increase

in faith along with their faith."

I mean by "the believers" here the Imams. Tranquility is the support by which the hearts dwell

in the knowledge of the truth, so that you may be able to bear what you persist in, if you are guided by support for it. The believer in

the authentic language: Allah the Almighty said in a story about the brothers of Yusuf (peace be upon him):

"And you are not going to believe us, even though we are truthful."

"You will not believe us" — and if we believe, this is a name that falls on every believer. He said,

God Almighty:

"The Messenger believed in what was revealed to him from his Lord, and so did the believers. Each one believed in Allah, His angels, His Books, and His Messengers, [saying] 'We make no distinction between any of His Messengers.'"

He said, in a story about Moses (peace be upon him):

"Glory be to You, I am the first of the believers."

<!-- page 341 -->
The Prophet (peace be upon him) is called a believer because he believes in Allah, and the Imam is called a believer because he believes

in Allah, in the prophet, and in the believer; he is a believer because he believed in Allah, in the prophet, and in the prophet of the time. What confirms

this among the words of Allah concerning the Imams is:

"And those who believed in Allah and His Messengers — they are the truthful and the martyrs

with their Lord."

The martyrs are the Imams and the righteous as well. This is the saying of Allah the Almighty:

"And the prophets and the martyrs were brought, and judgment was made between them with truth, and they were not

wronged."

And the saying of the Almighty:

"So how then when We bring from each nation a witness, and We bring you as a witness against these?"

He said:

The Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings of Allah be upon him) said:

"Beware the insight of the believer, for he sees by the light of Allah" — meaning the Imam. And his saying:

"That they might increase in faith along with their faith,"

means that He sent down tranquility (1) into their hearts, while the matter of the imamate has come to rest with them.

"And before that they were believers, and they increased

in the rank of imamate."

And the Almighty said:

"And to Him belong the soldiers of the heavens and the earth."

(1) In the (S) version, "al-Sakun" is mentioned.

<!-- page 342 -->
The soldiers of heaven are the upper limits, and the soldiers of the earth are the lower limits.

Among them is the saying of the Almighty:

"And if they were to seek aid, they would be aided with water."

And it was said to them: "A soldier will destroy them through the prohibitions of Allah, (1) with their hands, their tongues, and so on."

They plant from knowledge and wisdom in the world as the soldiers throw it forth — those who he is from and who establishes them.

Then the Almighty said:

"We have sent you as a witness."

I mean: as a witness over those who are in your time of creation, and whoever has answered you among them, you were

as a witness for him; and whoever does not love you, you are a witness against him. This is what the Almighty says:

"How then when We bring from every nation a witness, and We bring you against these as a witness?"

These are witnesses.

Then He said:

"And a bearer of good tidings and a warner."

It means that he is, in essence, a human being, and the Imams are from his descendants before them.

"And a warner" — for he warns the one who rises from among his descendants, and what is allowed to the disobedient against him,

the punishment for it in the Hereafter. Then He said:

"That you may believe in Allah and His Messenger."

We have sent this Messenger so that you may believe in what he has brought to you from his Lord.

"And honor him and revere him and glorify Him morning and evening."

(1) In version (8) it is mentioned as "shocks."

<!-- page 343 -->
20,150

I mean: glorify Allah, exalt Him, and praise Him, in some respect outwardly in words and beliefs, and in

the limit of truth with knowledge and certainty, to unite Him with the rightful unification — from the spiritual and the physical —

who created him. Then he mentioned what he commanded concerning the pledge of allegiance and the taking of the covenant and the compact, which

his Sunna was carried out in the first two and the last, and his Messenger ordered him to perform it in

his Sharia. And he said, "The Almighty said":

"Indeed, those who pledge allegiance to you actually pledge allegiance to Allah; the hand of Allah is over their hands.

Whoever breaks his pledge only breaks it against himself, and whoever fulfills that which he has covenanted with Allah,

He will give him a great reward."

He says: Whoever takes the pledge of allegiance, the covenant, and the compact, and takes it upon himself, then

he pledges allegiance to Allah, who commanded you to do it.

"The hand of Allah is over their hands."

I mean: when he made the pledge of allegiance and gave the attribute by shaking hands, because the hand of the taker

is by the command of Allah, it is the hand of Allah who placed it in that place and set him up for him as a way

of attribution — as one says in the tongue of the Arabs concerning the one who raises him as a watcher: "my eyes"; and concerning whom

he raises him to listen for him: "my ear"; and whoever he establishes to take and give, his hand; and whoever defends

him: "my sword, my spear," and the like. So Allah the Almighty addressed the Arabs in

this through their tongue, by which they understand what they hear from speech. He said:

"Whoever breaks" — that is, this pledge, and the origin of its contract and conclusion is that

he is not against you, because he is the one who punishes that deed.

"He will give him a great reward" — that is, He will reward him with a great reward and hasten for him what He hastens, and delay what He delays.

Then His Majesty said:

<!-- page 344 -->
"It is He who sent His Messenger with guidance and the religion of truth

— all of it — even though the polytheists may dislike it."

It means that He is the Almighty who sent Muhammad (peace be upon him) with guidance, which is the declaration that

the believers are guided to the truth, "and the religion of truth" — by which is meant what He has prescribed.

His Sharia: "to manifest it" — He says: to make it prevail (1) over every religion, in purity and victory.

"Oppression" is also said to come from it: "We have turned our backs on the enemy, and Allah has shown us, and He has shown it."

Glory be to Him: over every religion. Its promise is fulfilled with the appearance of the one who rises at the end

of time, from his son, who is established by his Sharia. Allah the Almighty makes it manifest to every religion and every

nation. His word is exalted, and the people of every law and religion suffer oppression and victory. From that

He said:

"And We have written in the Psalms, after the Reminder, that the earth shall be inherited by

My righteous servants. Indeed, in this is a message to a worshipping people."

And the Almighty said:

"Indeed, We will help Our Messengers and those who believe, in the life of this world and on the Day when

the witnesses arise."

The Almighty said:

"Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah, and those with him are forceful against the disbelievers, merciful

among themselves."

"Those who are with him" are those who followed him in truth, believed in him, and accepted him outwardly and inwardly.

(1) In version (e) it is mentioned as "by flipping."


<!-- page 345 -->

They carried out his command in his lifetime and after his death — those who were among his causes during his time, and the Imams who came after him stand with him by following him, adhering to his command, and calling in his name, because they are in one system with him. The connected God grasped his side in Allah's hand and his side in the hand of the servants, as the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) described. The Prophet is the upper end of the rope in this lower world, and the Foundation is connected to him, and the Imams are each connected to one another in turn. The lower end, which is in the hands of the servants present in every time who hold onto him, is whoever has clung to the rope of Allah. Each of them in his own time is the most trustworthy handhold, which cannot be severed — like a chain, each loop of which is connected to the next.[^1]

Whoever holds onto the lowest of them holds onto all of them and to each of them. This is the saying of Allah Almighty:

> "Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah, and those with him..."

They are the Imams. We have shown elsewhere that the name of faith falls upon the Messengers, the Foundations, the Imams, and all the believers who are connected to them — a connection that continues as long as time remains. His law is not interrupted, is not abrogated or changed, and is not broken except by the breaking of the world itself. Those who adhere to it become the reality of adherence to it until the eternal Hereafter is established. So the good of this world reaches them together with the good of the Hereafter.

The polytheists said that Muhammad had no offspring, that his successor would not come, and that his command had been interrupted by his death. So Allah Almighty informed them of what would be — the survival of his law in his creation and his community, their fulfilling of the matter of his community, and the connection of his causes by description — and He said:

> "Merciful among themselves"

meaning their causes that are connected to them.

[^1]: In copy (e) it appears as "connected."
[^2]: In copy (E) it appears as "Al-Bidiya."

345

<!-- page 346 -->

> "You see them bowing and prostrating"

that is, they are subject to the Speaker and his Argument.

> "seeking the bounty of Allah and the good pleasure of Allah; their marks are on their faces from the trace of prostration"

By this is meant obedience to the Imams.

> "That is their likeness in the Torah"

That is, on the outward face: that they submit to their Imams, obey them, and remain loyal to them. Then He said:

> "And their likeness in the Gospel"

namely:

> "like a sown crop that brings forth its shoots..."

In the language of the Arabs, the "sown crop" refers to the shoots that grow from the original stem. It is said that the seed brings forth shoots — meaning that if one of them rises up, there will be a successor from among them.

> "and strengthens them"

— and argues —

> "so they become stout and stand firm"

by supporting

> "upon their stalks"

— and the stalk is the plural of leg, meaning that he establishes his followers and his causes; he equates them with the highest rank in support.

> "delighting the sowers"

meaning the successors and the preachers who sow wisdom in the hearts of the believers.

> "to enrage by them the disbelievers"

that is, to enrage the disbelievers who imagined that Muhammad's[^3] command would be cut off — by what they saw in those among them who had seen him and were certain that his command was connected.

[^3]: In version (8) it appears as "Muhammad."

346

<!-- page 347 -->

— and in whoever takes them up, and what they see from them at all times.

> "Allah has promised those who believe and do righteous deeds"

meaning all of them,

> "forgiveness and a great reward."

This refers to what they obtain from the reward of the immediate and the appointed, like the words of the Almighty:

> "Indeed, We have granted you al-Kawthar. So pray to your Lord and sacrifice. Indeed, he who hates you — he is the one cut off."

It is said that 'Amr ibn al-'As said to the disbelievers of Quraysh: "Be patient with what you are suffering at the hands of Muhammad. He has no son, and if he dies, his remembrance and command will be interrupted." Word of that reached the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and grieved him, so Allah Almighty revealed to him this Surah, al-Kawthar. It has been said in the commentary that al-Kawthar is a river in Paradise — like the great river — which is what Allah Almighty granted him of the knowledge of subtle interpretation.

> "So pray to your Lord and sacrifice"

— that is, establish the call to God inwardly, which is the inner aspect of prayer, and establish it outwardly as well, not the outward without the inward.

> "and sacrifice"

— that is, take the covenant of the Foundation upon your foundation and establish it for the statement; your inward descendants will be called, and those who respond to your call will be multiplied, and[^4] cut off.

He said this to him, and it was as Allah promised him. The slaughter (nahr) is only for camels, which are like the Imams; the slaughter (dhabh) is for sheep, which are like the believers; and the cows are likenesses of the Arguments. So He struck the parable of Abraham with the ram, the foundation of Moses with the cows, and the foundation of Muhammad with the camel. As for what he mentioned of the saying of Ibrahim concerning it — that is Ishmael:

[^4]: In copy (X) it appears as "and amputated."

347

<!-- page 348 -->

> "I see in a dream that I am sacrificing you."

But that was the taking of the covenant upon him first, by which he ruled himself to obedience.

Moses said to his people:

> "Allah commands you to sacrifice a cow."

This is the establishment of the Argument, as we have mentioned. And Muhammad (peace be upon him) was commanded to sacrifice — that is, he was commanded to take the covenant of the foundation upon the prayers of Allah upon him.

> "Did We not expand your breast for you?"

He meant: to clarify the manifest thing that was in his limit, by establishing its foundation to explain it.

> "And We removed from you your burden"

meaning what you were carrying of the outward without statement.

> "which had weighed down your back"

meaning that you were burdened with what you were conveying to the respondents without statement.

> "And We have raised high for you your remembrance"

through the highest mention with what you remember in it.

> "For indeed, with hardship comes ease"

He says: with the outward revelation comes an inner statement that clarifies it and makes it easy for those who would otherwise be unable. He commanded him to deliver the statement, which is the interpretation.

> "Indeed, with hardship comes ease"

He says: that with the outward call comes an inner call in which there is clarification and facilitation.

> "So when you have finished, stand up..."

348

<!-- page 349 -->

He says: put yourself to work, and strive hard to establish the foundation and to establish the call of the inward.

> "...and to your Lord direct your longing."

That is, I want Him and ask Him for help in that, and for the turnout of the respondents to him.

One of the symbols of the supplication to Him is the words of the Almighty:

> "Call to the way of your Lord with wisdom"

He says: Call to your foundation which You have raised up,[^5] and which you have established by the command of your Lord, and you have made a path that is meant by the wisdom entrusted to him, which is the statement.

> "and good instruction"

This is what he preaches to those who would not accept it and would turn away from it and reject it. He wished to do so, since he thought that he was qualified for it.

> "and argue with them by that which is best"

He says: their proofs and arguments — which of the two ways is better, the one that I have set up for them, or that which they wanted?

> "Your Lord knows best who has strayed from His way"

meaning, who has departed from the one whom He has raised up.

> "and He knows best those who are guided"

meaning the Muslims who come to him for his command. Another such instance is the words of the Almighty:

> "O Prophet, indeed We have sent you as a witness, a bringer of good tidings, and a warner — and one who calls to Allah by His permission, and an illuminating lamp."

[^5]: In copy (E) it appears as "and its position."

349

<!-- page 350 -->

It appears that He sent him as a witness to his nation — those whom he saw and who were in his era — with what they had of obedience, disobedience, disbelief, and faith in what he had brought them; and in his inwardness, a witness to those of them who were obedient to those whom he commanded them to obey, and to those of them who disobeyed his command. The obedient among the people will be rewarded; (and a warner) who warns the disobedient among them of His punishment.[^6]

> "and one who calls to Allah by His permission"

that is, he is commanded to call people to obey him and to do his command.

> "and an illuminating lamp"

meaning that he is a guide in the darkness of ignorance, and one who sees by the light in the darkness of the night. In the depths of that, He has shown him the number of those whom He appoints in the community in their ranks. The "witness" means the Speaker, who is the Messenger (peace be upon him) in his era; and the Imam of every time after him will be in that rank, a witness to the people of his time. "And one who calls to Allah by His permission" is the Foundation in the era of the Prophet, and the Argument in the era of the Imam. In this rank, he gives good news to those who respond to his call, accept his interpretation, are guided by it, and do what he commands outwardly and inwardly — to win, to survive, and to be happy in this world and in the Hereafter.

"And a warner" — that is, the one who follows the Arguments in every island. Each of them, in this rank, warns the people of his island, those who preach within it, of God's punishment for those who fail to respond to it. The ma'dhun is the sixth among the prohibited imams; he must open to someone other than his Argument, who will be the seventh Imam after him. The people of his time warn him of his stay, and of what he expects from the end of the credit reaching him and the completion of the matter in him — from being completed upon his hands so that they rush to him. And the caller is —

350

[^6]: In copy (e) it appears as "with his disability."

<!-- page 351 -->

— the one who is called the owner of each island, and they are the preachers; each one of them is in this rank.

> "and an illuminating lamp"

is the permission that the caller gives to him to break through. Whoever sees his breaking-through and shows him the way to it is likened to the lamp by which one is guided in darkness to the place of need.

These are the five lower limits that God Almighty has commanded and established in the earth for His servants, corresponding to the five upper limits that are in heaven. The statement on this was mentioned at the beginning of this book. So when it is complete in the era of a prophet or an Imam, and the time helps him and the community obeys him, and he finds within it those who are qualified for these ranks, he is commanded; and if he likewise exists and is prepared to reside in all the islands of the earth — which are twelve islands, to be addressed later — and in each region of preachers and ma'dhuns there are several, or more than that number (they will be mentioned in their place), until the people of the earth respond[^7] to the seventh — in the last cycle of the seventh Imams from the descendants of the Messenger of Allah, willingly or unwillingly, by oppression and victory — and the religion will be as Allah Almighty said: "all is for Allah." His promise to Muhammad will be fulfilled:

> "(complete images) with the appearance of his religion over all religion, even if the polytheists hate it"

— that is, the receptors, as they were, until they are overcome and enter under the rule of the owner of that time. The matter happening among them is as we will mention, if we come to its place, God willing.

Perhaps the Speaker of his time was not prepared for the establishment of these limits, in which case he assessed what was prepared for him and was enabled to do so with the help of time and what is unfolding through him by the grace of Allah Almighty — for the servants in any age and time He wills to do it, as He sends the rain when

[^7]: In copy (E) it appears as "in their entirety."

351

<!-- page 352 -->

He wills, and waters the earth once, and once again leaves it dry; and we find good things in our region and they reach us, and sometimes we are in distress and sometimes in satisfaction. But all of this is the grace of Allah over the servants — He gives it to them if He wills, and it is a punishment for some of them and a trial and reward for others.

If this is done to them, then the guardians of God in every age — whether in hardship or in prosperity, in grace or in calamity — have the bounty that Allah Almighty has made for them. They do not lack the symptoms of the worshippers from among them; if any present something to them, their acceptance of it does not increase what they accept. But they love it when Allah brings them the grace, compassion, and mercy upon the servants — that the servants accept what is in their own happiness and goodness, that their command is fulfilled, and that they strive in it. They spend in it what they hope for of the reward of Allah in that for which He has used them.

By Allah Almighty — out of their goodness, they melt themselves and consume their own bodies, and they report of it as much as they are able, according to what they have been assigned, commanded, and used for.

In this is what the Messenger of Allah said to Ali: "That Allah should guide a single man through you is better for you than that upon which the sun has risen or set," and in another wording: "better for you than the red-furred camels (i.e., the choicest of blessings)."

Among what Allah Almighty commanded the believers — that they follow the outward law of Muhammad, that is, they believe him and believe in his message — He says to them: "Act: if you believe in the outward appearance, you have been commanded to do it and to act upon it":

> "Alif Lam Mim. That is the Book about which there is no doubt, a guidance for those conscious of Allah — who believe in the unseen and establish prayer"

meaning the outward and the inward.

> "and from what We have provided them, they spend"

meaning, from the outward, they spend of wealth what is obligatory in it; and from the inward, they spend of knowledge.

[^8]: In copy (M) it appears as "and they are corrected."

352


<!-- page 353 -->
Knowledge must be practiced and taught to those who deserve to learn it, for this is the mark of the pious — and it is a single sentence in which all the obligatory duties, outward and inward, are gathered together, just as Allah Almighty described the pious by these very qualities.

Since Allah Almighty has commanded *taqwa* in His Book, *taqwa* is what He intends here. This is one example of the conciseness characteristic of the Arabs whom the Qur'an addressed in their own tongue. He says here to those who believe in the outward (*zahir*) of the Prophet: fear God so as to gather all of this together. And His saying "and believe in His Messenger" means: believe him in what has come from the inner substance (the *batin*), and take from him what he has appointed for inner performance, just as you have taken from him outwardly. Carry out the duties of the inner and reflect upon them, just as you have learned and reflected upon the outward duties.
