"He will grant you two shares of His mercy" — a share that is the reward of your faith and works in the outward, and a like share for the inward. "And He will appoint for you a light by which to walk" — that is, knowledge and proof by which you are guided. "And He will forgive you, and Allah is Forgiving, Merciful." Forgiveness is concealment: He covers you with His mercy from His punishment, and guides you to cover what He has commanded you to cover, so that He may turn to you in mercy.

This is confirmed by the words of the Almighty: "And an announcement from Allah and His Messenger to the people on the day of the greatest pilgrimage, that Allah is free of the polytheists, and so is His Messenger. If you repent, it is better for you; but if you turn away, then know

<!-- page 354 -->
that you cannot frustrate Allah — and give tidings of a painful punishment to those who disbelieve."

This was, on its outward face, a warning at the time of the Messenger of Allah to the polytheists. In the report, the Messenger of Allah commanded Abu Bakr to go out to Mecca at the season of pilgrimage and warn them of it; and Surat Bara'ah was written for him and entrusted to him. Then Allah Almighty sent down to him that no one shall deliver it for him except one who is of him, who is the witness after him — as the Almighty said: "He was upon clear proof from his Lord," and as He said: "and a witness from Him recites it" — meaning Ali, peace be upon him. So he sent for him, and Ali overtook Abu Bakr, took the writing from him, and conveyed it as Allah had commanded.

This is the outward. The inward operates in the same way — as the night and the day, the sun and the moon, and all that is in the Book of Allah of commands, prohibitions, promises, and warnings, of good news and the rest, all continue. For the Qur'an endures, and the creatures worship by what is in it. Even if a particular verse was revealed concerning a particular man or people or matter at the time of the Prophet, its ruling does not pass away with the passing of those persons, nor does its obligation fall away with their disappearance. The whole Qur'an is the same in this respect: it turns in every period of time and over every century of centuries, just as the sun and the moon turn and run in their courses, and as the night and the day pass. He addressed those present in his own time with the obligations of prayers, *zakat*, and the rest — and those obligations are likewise addressed to all who come after them, until the Hour is fulfilled. The same is true of everything in the Qur'an. So we say here:

<!-- page 355 -->
"And an announcement from Allah and His Messenger" — meaning an act of informing and making known, just as the muezzin announces and makes known the time of prayer, and as Allah Almighty said: "Their ears were assailed by a hard hearing"; and as He said: "to the people" — meaning, in the inward sense, those acquainted with wisdom, who are the believers and the responders. That is to say: tell them that he and his Messenger are acquitted of the polytheists, who are all those who associate others with the *awliya*' of Allah, or who take a *wali* from outside their proper ranks.

"And on the day of the greatest pilgrimage" — the speaker and the hearers here are the *asas* who goes to him, and before him the *natiq* who is its foundation, and before the foundation its *hudud*, and before the *hudud* the responders ranked according to their stations and the measures granted to each of them concerning him. As for the manifest pilgrimage of the Imam — the Almighty intended by this announcement to inform all the people who are His proof at that time, and those who come after them in the cycle of Muhammad, peace be upon him, from the people of his *shari'ah*, from the first of them to the last, warning against *shirk* in Him and in His *awliya'*, both the known kinds of it and the great. We have mentioned what has been mentioned above within the limits of knowledge and its aspects. And he said, may the prayers of Allah be upon him: "*Shirk* is more hidden than the creeping of a black ant upon a black stone in a dark night."

The whole point of this is that a person may suppose that someone among them does not deserve a station that

<!-- page 356 -->
God has appointed for him, or may deny something that God has established for him, or may take some matter of his religion from one whom God Almighty has not appointed, or accept it from someone other than those whom He has designated for it. All of this is *shirk*. And to give everyone his right concerning that, and to take from whomever has been commanded to be the one taken from, is the very monotheism of Allah Almighty.

We have already mentioned sentences and reports from the accounts of Muhammad, Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and a brief discussion of his source and the origin of his obligatory law from what is mentioned in the Book of Allah. If we were to track down everything in the Qur'an bearing on this, the discussion would have run beyond the limits of this book. But we have kept it brief, as mentioned, in order to interpret in detail what we have abbreviated here in the book *Da'a'im al-Islam*. When we came in that book to the Bab al-Imamah (the chapter on the Imamate), we judged that it was enough to say only a little there, mentioning its root and its branch — for we then realized that to recount it in full from Adam to Muhammad, the prayers of God upon them, would be a long undertaking, even though we abbreviated and refined our speech in it. We shall, God willing, mention each matter in the Qur'an bearing on this or that, within the limits of knowledge, with the help of Allah, His support, His granting of success, His recompense, and the substance He has set in relation to His *awliya*' and their measures in His servants.

When Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him, had established his *shari'ah* and all that God commanded him to deliver, and the time of his passing drew near — within months, as we mentioned — Allah Almighty commanded him to inform his community of the succession to his testament, and to set up his successor in his own place, and to tell them that he is the *wali* of those whose master he is. And Allah Almighty sent down: "Today I have perfected for you your religion, completed My favor upon you,

<!-- page 357 -->
and chosen Islam for you as a religion." The Messenger of Allah, peace and blessings be upon him, responded — and so did those who were with him. And Allah sent down: "When the help of Allah and the conquest come, and you see the people entering the religion of Allah in multitudes, then glorify the praises of your Lord and ask His forgiveness; indeed, He is ever Accepting of repentance."

By this, God intended for him to know that his end had been drawn near. He had transmitted his *shari'ah*; God then appointed him, by His command, to set in his place the one who would succeed him — and this is what is meant by "When the help of Allah and the conquest come." This was the help and conquest by which God strengthened him through the establishment of his foundation, his minister and brother, Ali ibn Abi Talib, may the prayers of God be upon him; through what God opened for him with him and at his hands; through the outward conquest accomplished by his hand and his sword, and the inward conquest accomplished by his tongue and his knowledge, which God sent down to him by the command of his Lord — that is, the *ta'wil* of His *shari'ah*, the exposition of the inner sense of what the Prophet brought, his inclusion in that station, and his fulfillment of the duty assigned to him in it.

So Allah Almighty showed him a sight by which his eye was comforted and his soul set at ease and his heart steadied — because he saw, in his lifetime, a creation after him just as he had seen it before him in his brothers among the prophets and their nations, and he saw him likewise from among his Imams down to the last of them. These are the gifts of Allah Almighty to His *awliya*' in their lifetimes — gifts that do not afflict them nor grieve them, as we mentioned the trials of those who lived before them and those who will appraise it after them. And this does not diminish their merit. Had the people responded, as we mentioned, what God brought to him would have been still better; had each *ummah* received its imam properly, may God have mercy upon them all, the benefit at his hands would have been greater.

He says (interpretation of the meaning): "So glorify the praises of your Lord." He says: take, O Muhammad, the right of praise for what He has given you, and given you, and given you — concerning the attributes of His creation — and do not associate anyone else with Him in that. Should you see that one of the *hudud* of the Alid line stands between you and Him — that you give preference to him over yourself, "and I will save the glory" — give thanks for that by acknowledging that it is from Him, without denying the right of the right-holder

<!-- page 358 -->
from among them, nor reducing what is due to him — as we mentioned, in the bound of *tawhid*, that this is *shirk*.

"And ask His forgiveness" — that is, ask Him to cover with His mercy what you have been commanded to keep concealed in your *shari'ah*. "Indeed, He is ever Accepting of repentance" — meaning, toward the one who has done that and remained loyal to him for his own sake. Then Allah Almighty took him to Himself when He willed his honoring, and brought him to the dwelling of his safety and his reward for what the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, had accomplished.

When Muhammad's departure drew near, Allah Almighty commanded him to declare his testament for Ali ibn Abi Talib openly. But the Prophet feared the people and their hypocrisy in opposing him after him, and his breast was constricted. So Allah commanded him to say: "O Messenger, deliver what has been sent down to you from your Lord regarding Ali. If you do not, you will not have delivered His message — and Allah will protect you from the people."

That was when he left the Farewell Pilgrimage. When he reached Ghadir, he ordered that those who had gone ahead be brought back, and that those who were behind catch up. He had the *dawhat* (the spreading trees of that place) cleared for him, and stones piled up like a frame, like a pulpit, and he gathered his followers, his supporters, and the responders to his call. There he stipulated the *wilayah* of the Commander of the Believers, may the prayers of God be upon them both. He stood him at his side. Then, after he had praised Allah, he said: "Am I not more entitled to you than you are to yourselves?" They said, "Yes, O Messenger of Allah." He said, "O Allah, bear witness to their answer." Then he repeated it a second time: "Am I not more entitled to you than you are to yourselves?" "Yes, O Messenger of Allah." He said, "O Allah, bear witness." Then he repeated it a third time, and they said, "Yes, O Messenger of Allah." He said, "Whoever I am his master, Ali is his master. O Allah, befriend whoever befriends him, oppose whoever opposes him,

<!-- page 359 -->
help whoever helps him, and forsake whoever forsakes him, and turn the truth with him wherever he turns."

He handed over to Ali his books, his weapon, and the inheritance of the prophets, just as those who had come before him from among them had handed over to their successors. Yet his arguments stirred envy in the envious — just as Iblis envied Adam, and just as Iblis was followed in his envy by many of the angels. As the Almighty said: "And when your Lord said to the angels, 'I am placing a caliph upon the earth,' they said, 'Will You place therein one who will work corruption in it and shed blood, while we glorify You with praise and sanctify You?' He said, 'I know what you do not know.' And He taught Adam the names, all of them; then He presented them to the angels and said, 'Inform Me of the names of these, if you are truthful.' They said, 'Glory be to You — we have no knowledge except what You have taught us. Indeed, You are the Knowing, the Wise.' He said, 'O Adam, inform them of their names.' And when he had informed them of their names, He said, 'Did I not say to you that I know the unseen of the heavens and the earth, and that I know what you reveal and what you have been concealing?' And when We said to the angels, 'Prostrate to Adam,' they prostrated, except Iblis."

So Allah commanded the angels to prostrate to Adam, and they did so after they had displayed their disagreement and disputed with their Lord. But Iblis raised himself up in his tyranny and in disobedience to his Lord, and in fanaticism for his own kind, and he was proud over Adam by arrogance and by ascribing himself to a substance of fire. He said: "I am better than him — You created me from fire and You created him from clay."

<!-- page 360 -->
So Allah Almighty cast him out of Paradise by his deed as one disgraced, and by his ruling on his disobedience as a devil. He described his rank and lowered his station: "Descend from it; you have no right to be arrogant in it. Get out — you are among the debased."

So he was struck down by his arrogance and his standing by the One who compelled him. Adam, however, still did not yet know whom God would appoint as his testament and his successor after him. So Allah Almighty commanded that Cain and Abel each draw near with an offering — for Abel was his appointed *wali*, as the Almighty said: "And recite to them the news of the two sons of Adam in truth, when each offered a sacrifice, and it was accepted from one of them and not accepted from the other. He said, 'I will surely kill you.' He said, 'Allah only accepts from the *muttaqin*. If you should stretch your hand toward me to kill me, I shall not stretch my hand toward you to kill you — for I fear Allah, Lord of the worlds. Indeed, I want you to bear my sin and your sin, and so be among the companions of the Fire — and that is the recompense of the wrongdoers.'"

"Then his soul prompted him to the murder of his brother, and he killed him, and he became one of the losers."

Satan exaggerated in his disobedience and persisted in it, and continued in his obstinacy. In the same way overlap the *lawahiq* (the successors-by-attachment) of Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him — and the *lawahiq* do not interfere with the angels, because the *lawahiq* are angels in potential. If they do not leave this physical world and pass over to the spiritual world, they become angels there in actuality. For by their works they ascend to the world of permanence, and their works are their dwelling — the *da'wah* and the publication of the *bayan* (the exposition) among its people.

When Muhammad concluded his covenant with his *wali* concerning the *imarah* of the believers, and handed over to him the inheritances of the prophets, in his presence his envier followed him in envy — as we have mentioned of the envy of Iblis


<!-- page 361 -->
just as the angels envied Adam (peace be upon him), and as Cain envied his brother Abel (peace be upon him) and killed him. So too the followers of Muhammad (peace be upon him) said to one another that Muhammad had favored Ali because he was close to him. He told them so, and Allah revealed to him:

Say: "Have you considered: if it is from Allah, and you disbelieve in it, while a witness from the Children of Israel has testified to its like — and he has believed while you have grown arrogant — (1) indeed, Allah does not guide the wrongdoing people."

The interpretation of this is: have you considered, O companions of Muhammad and his arguments, that if this designation of the guardian is from Allah by His command, and you disbelieve in it — meaning that you will be honored by his rank, the rank Allah has brought him to and chosen for him — and Moses testified to its like, for he commanded the Children of Israel, and they acknowledged the one who succeeded him over them. Then envy overtook them, and they took a calf — a body with a hollow sound — which has no truth and is not firm in the minds. When the Messenger of Allah was absent, you saw the rank of his foundation — may the prayers of Allah be upon him — and you suppressed the explicit designation of the Prophet and his appointment of allegiance, the allegiance they had pledged at Ghadeer Khumm. You followed Satan, Cain, and the Samaritan, treading sandal-step in sandal, footstep in footstep. You sat in his council and called by his name, claiming his station of caliphate and command of the believers. You clung to the outward and dismissed it.

So the Foundation — may the prayers of Allah be upon him — established his argument by the Qur'an that had been revealed to Muhammad (peace be upon him), when he gathered it and brought it to them, and they said, "We have no need of this; Allah has no need of us for what you have." So he took it and turned away from them, finding no supporter or helper, and the ordeal grew severe upon him. They harmed him so greatly that they conspired to kill him during his prayer.

For the first opponent ordered Khalid ibn al-Walid, if he prayed with them in the front row, that the first one would say, "Peace be upon you," and Khalid would strike him while he was praying in his prayer-niche and kill him: "Then you will be a master in it." But when he prayed, the first opponent thought about the power of the Banu Hashim, and he said, "Perhaps it will not be done.

(1) In version (e) it is mentioned (and he was arrogant).
361

<!-- page 362 -->
Khalid will kill him, and the people will disagree with us, and they will retract their oath of allegiance, and so he will be killed." So he sat for a long time before completing the salutation, until she was about to look up at him. Then he said, "Khalid, do not do what I ordered you." He raised his voice, then made the salutation, and said to him — peace be upon him — "Khalid, woe to you, would you have done it?" And he stretched out his hand to his collar and held him so that none could free him from his right hand, until they swore by Muhammad (peace be upon him), and Khalid swore to him, and so he released him. And his ordeal increased until the first opposition had passed.

Yet they kept coming to him with every difficulty that befell them — dilemmas (1) and matters of judgment — and he would find a way out for them. He did not relax his striving until he had established his arguments, his call had spread, and he had a house of migration just as the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) had, and his patience over the harm of the polytheists. He did with his command as the Prophet had done, and showed patience as he had shown patience, until he had a house of migration. He established his limits in the lower world and took up the sword of interpretation, killing the apostates, the murderers, and the rogues. He called the upper limits, and he was a scholar.

The Divine Intellect is the world of contentment, subsistence, and bliss, and he established its foundation under him over its counterpart in the world of the soul. So the Speaker becomes the manifestation, in the world of the soul, of the Universal Intellect's spiritual reality, and in the light of the world of subsistence and contentment they live and do not die, because their substance is of subsistence — namely the Universal Intellect — by following in the spiritual world, and likewise in the world of composition. None of the laboring seekers reaches knowledge of the truths of the parables of the Shari'ah and its symbols, and the arbiter who interprets it, except through the call of the inner Foundation, who corresponds in the spiritual world. From him one ascends to the world of the spiritual Soul.

So the Speaker is, for example, like the Universal Intellect in the world of command (2), and the Foundation is, for example, like the Universal Soul, the speaker through the wisdom of interpretation that displays the virtue of the Speaker and what he signifies. The Imam is the product of the Speaker and the Foundation, just as Idea is the product of Intellect and Soul. Idea

(1) It is mentioned in Version (e) (Misleading).
(2) Contained in Copy (X) (Education)
362

<!-- page 363 -->
displays the virtues of Intellect and the world of divinity, and displays the virtues of Soul and its dispositions in the spiritual world without annihilation. Likewise the Imam (peace be upon him) displays the virtues of the Speaker, revealing his symbols and parables in the outward of his revelation and his Shari'ah, and he interprets the call of the Foundation and the inner workings of his wisdom.

When the Speaker is absent and ascends to the spiritual world, his Foundation rises to his rank and inherits his station, establishing himself in the place of his predecessor. He establishes the Imam, who is the repository under him, as the successor in the world of the Soul. When the Foundation is absent — may Allah's peace be upon him — the Completion (1) has risen to the level of the Foundation, and the Imam has been established and guided. The Foundation hands over to him what was in his hand from the deposit of the inheritance of the prophets and imams, and he becomes absent.

The Imam (peace be upon him) was elevated to the station of the Speaker and met the rank of his predecessor, so that he becomes the Intellect of all that is in the world of composition, and establishes the argument under him by exposition concerning him over its counterpart in the world of the soul. The argument of the holder of the island of the call comes under him, just like the establishment of the next Speaker and his call for the previous one by the next, and so on.

The rank of the dai under the argument of the holder of the island of the dawah is like the rank of the self-speaking under the Foundation of the Speaker, and the rank of the argument under the Imam is like the rank of the Soul under the Intellect. The Prophet (peace and blessings of Allah be upon him) pointed to the station of his guardian and successor and said: "I am the city of knowledge, and Ali is its door."

The apparent meaning is: he said that no one among the limits of the limits below the Speaker, and his roots, can claim the wisdom of revelation and the Shari'ah except from the side of his guardian, who is the gate to the City. And the City, in interpretation, is what the world owes from the apparent revelation and the parables that the Speaker erected, like a fortress for the city, so that one can only reach the city through its gate. In the city there is buying and selling and merchants, the owners of trades in the markets, and the wall surrounds the city, so that what is inside it can only be reached through its gate. As Allah Most High says:

(1) It is mentioned in Copy (e) (Resident)
363

<!-- page 364 -->
"So a wall will be put up between them, with a gate. Inside it will be mercy, and outside it will be punishment.

The hypocrites will call out to the believers: 'Were we not with you?' They will reply: 'Yes, but you tempted yourselves, and waited, and doubted, and were deluded by false desires until Allah's command came. The Deluder deluded you about Allah.'"

Medina — the city — is the law of the Prophet, which Allah made resemble the fortress of a city. Its goods are like the outer and inner of the Shari'ah, and the markets (1) are parables of the arguments of the holders of the islands. The merchants in the markets are the preachers. The buying and selling is like the one who takes the pledge of allegiance and pledges allegiance to the Imam of his time, and buys his own self from the Imam of his time, as the Almighty said:

"Indeed, Allah has purchased from the believers their own selves and their wealth in exchange for Paradise."

In Medina there are also castles, which are like the hidden limits, by which the Shari'ah may be veiled — the inner call has limited itself to knowing its limits through them — and Allah Almighty said:

"And keep yourself patient with those who call upon their Lord morning and evening, seeking His countenance. Do not let your eyes pass beyond them, desiring the adornments of the worldly life. And do not obey one whose heart We have made heedless of Our remembrance, who follows his own desires, and whose affair is ever in excess."

So Allah Almighty commanded His Prophet (peace be upon him) to hold himself with them and not to leave them, nor to let his eyes pass beyond them. They are the Imams — may the prayers of Allah be upon them — those whom the people of

(1) In the copy (M) it is mentioned (Al-Asaboo)
364

<!-- page 365 -->
the Shari'ah have failed to recognize, and whose houses they have not known. All of this is in the city of knowledge, with its gate over it and the outward form of the Shari'ah, so that no one reaches the truth of what is apparent in the religion of Allah and what is subconscious in it except through his inner call — not through the one who is the gate of Medina — and through him one is led to the knowledge of what the Prophet (peace and blessings of Allah be upon him) brought and symbolized and veiled from the gate, in which there is mercy, while outside the wall is the outward punishment.

He says to the people of the outward: "Were we not with you in the law of the Prophet? But you tempted yourselves with what you erected, like the calf of the Samaritan, (1) and you acted by it just as those before you did — like sandal-step in sandal, footstep in footstep — and you turned away from the call of the Foundation and his secret, who called you to it; you turned away and concealed yourselves from him."

The Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings of Allah be upon him) said in another report that confirms that they will not reach what he brought except through the side of his guardian, in his saying: "I am the city of knowledge, and Ali is its gate; whoever wants knowledge, let him come through the gate."

The expressions "the prayers of Allah upon them" refer to the houses which Allah willed should be raised and His name be remembered in them. To praise Him in the morning and evening — and the origins of the verse mean the apparent and the invisible. The Almighty said:

"It is not righteousness that you enter houses from their backs, but righteousness is in one who fears Allah. So enter houses through their doors. Whoever is mindful of Allah, fears, and is in the home of our fathers."

Muhammad (peace be upon him) is the best house, and his gate is the best gate; whoever enters through it is safe. Allah Almighty said: "Its inner door contains mercy, and its outer

(1) In the version (M) it is mentioned (Samarra)
365

<!-- page 366 -->
before it is punishment." Whoever violates the call of the inner Foundation and dwells on the outward is under the outward punishment, and the prayers of Allah are upon him.

The best gate is the limits of Allah, who are the pronouncement, and the wisdom of Allah is kept hidden in His houses, and the best of His houses is Muhammad (peace be upon him), and the best gates of his houses are his foundations. So he informed the world of what is in the depths of the hearts, for he is the informer of the unseen, that what he has obscured the Pharaohs do not reach, nor do they know it:

"In a hidden book, none can touch it except the purified."

The hidden is what is veiled and concealed, so that none knows it because of its concealment and hiddenness. The Book — that is the Foundation, upon whom was written the exposition of the interpretation of his Shari'ah and its parables — what he conceals and veils, none can touch but the purified, who are the Imams of his descendants. We will mention a story for each of them in its place, Allah willing.

And the killing of the second opponent was more severe. He left the matter to six men: the Commander of the Believers, Uthman ibn Affan, Suhaib al-Rumi… (he said: I shall gather the four through the fifth, and the sixth disagreed with them; let the five kill him). So (peace be upon him) went to his house and did not seek it, and the people pledged allegiance to the third, Uthman. They left Ali aside.

Uthman ibn Affan arose and ate the Muslims' wealth from zakat, tithes, and charity, and forbade Aisha what her father had been paying her, and Umar after him. The Muslims took revenge upon Uthman for these reasons we have mentioned. He favored the non-Arabs and abandoned the Arabs. And Ali, peace be upon him, despite all this, was busy building his inner call — which is the limit Allah Almighty had commanded him to do, and to establish through the agency of the Prophet (peace be upon him).

The people spoke to Uthman and went to Aisha and complained to her about what he was doing — that Uthman favored the non-Arabs and abandoned the Arabs. And she said: "Kill the squirrel, may Allah kill him!
466

<!-- page 367 -->
He has changed the religion of Allah, first and last." So the Muslims killed him: they confined him to his house for three days, fighting him day and night. And on the prayers of Allah upon him be the one who fought him and those who followed him and answered his call.

When it took long, Uthman was certain he would be killed, and he wrote a letter to Ali in which he said: "O Commander of the Believers, the flood has reached the peak and the belt. If you are a man of resolve, then come to me; otherwise, understand me." When the letter reached him, he addressed it to his son al-Hasan to prevent what he had grasped — but only after they had already entered the house. Al-Hasan was held back until they broke through his defense, and Uthman was killed.

The people came to the Commander of the Believers, and he was the first to extend his hand to pledge allegiance to him. Talha and al-Zubayr shook his hand; he said: "The hand of paralysis does not preserve a matter, and it shall not be done." The people pledged allegiance to him and multiplied around him. Aisha went out after that to perform Umrah, and the Commander of the Believers undertook the affair. Talha and al-Zubayr came to him, each asking for a grant, and he gave them as a Muslim slave gives. They said to him: "Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman had rewarded us for something, so we should be rewarded with the like." He said to them: "I have guided you according to the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah; the people are together in it." They found this against him, and they kept their hypocrisy from him and held it in.

Talha and al-Zubayr left for Umrah, asking Ali's permission, and they went away on the matter. When they met Aisha, Ali went to his house of migration to fulfill what Allah Almighty had commanded and to spread His call in interpretation. His journey to Kufa was like a house of his inner migration, in which the people of Muhammad's law (peace be upon him) were content, and his migration from the cave of Taqiyyah.

Aisha walked with Talha, al-Zubayr, and a group of the Muhajireen and others to Basra, and she fought him. So he — may the prayers of Allah be upon him — killed most of them, and the rest were defeated, after Talha and al-Zubayr had been killed. Aisha entered Basra, and Ali — may Allah bless him — sent her to her house, guarded by a hundred women dressed as men.

As for what came of his affair — it is not known to this point. The words and the exposition end here, and peace be upon the messengers.
367


<!-- page 368 -->
Praise be to Allah, Lord of the Worlds.

(1) After the office of the sixth Speaker, Muhammad ibn Abdullah, the divine wisdom decreed that the affair pass on to the final cycle. The role of the Imams was assumed by the Commander of the Faithful, Ali ibn Abi Talib, who was born on the 13th of Rajab in the year 604 AD and died on the 19th of Ramadan in the year 40 AH in Kufa.

He was succeeded by al-Husayn ibn Ali, who was born on the 5th of Sha'ban in the year 4 AH in Medina and was killed on the first of Muharram in the year 61 AH in Karbala.

He was succeeded by Ali Zayn al-Abidin, who was born on the 16th of Jumada al-Thani, a Friday, in the year 38 AH in Medina, and died on the 10th of Safar in the year 94 in Mecca.

He was succeeded by Muhammad al-Baqir, who was born on the 3rd of Safar in the year 57 AH in Medina and died in 117 AH.

He was succeeded by Imam Ja'far al-Sadiq, who was born on the 17th of Rabi' al-Awwal in the year 83 in Medina and died on the 10th of Shawwal in the year 148 in Medina.

He was succeeded by his son Ismail, who was born in the year 101 AH and died in 158 AH in Basra. (This is one of the historical Ismaili sources that contradict the other sources.)

He was succeeded by Muhammad ibn Ismail, surnamed al-Habib and al-Maktum, who was born in 121 AH in Medina and died in 193 AH in the town of Palmyra.

After him came his son Abdullah al-Radi, who was born in 179 in Muhammadabad and died in the year 212 in Salamiyya.

He was succeeded by his son Ahmad al-Wafi, who was born in the year 198 in Salamiyya and died in the year 265 in the town of Masyaf.

Then his son al-Husayn al-Taqi took over after him; he was born in the year 219 in Salamiyya and died in the year 289 in Salamiyya.

After him came his son Ali al-Hadi al-Mu'al, who was born in the year 237 in Salamiyya and died in the year 275 in Salamiyya.

After him came his son Muhammad al-Qa'im, who was born in the month of Muharram in the year 280 in Salamiyya and died on the 18th of Shawwal in the year 334 in al-Mahdiyya.

After him came his son Ismail al-Mansur Billah, who was born on the 1st of Jumada al-Thani in the year 303 in al-Mahdiyya and died on the 3rd of Shawwal in the year 341 in al-Mansuriyya.

After him came his son [al-Mu'izz li-Din Allah], who was born on the 11th of Ramadan in the year 317 in al-Mahdiyya and died on the 11th of Rabi' al-Awwal in the year 365 AH in Cairo.

After him came his son Nizar al-Aziz Billah, who was born on the 14th of Muharram in the year 344 AH in al-Mahdiyya and died on the 28th of Ramadan in the year 386 AH in Cairo.

After him came al-Hasan al-Hakim bi-Amr Allah, who was born on the 23rd of Rabi' al-Awwal in the year 375 in Cairo and died on the 27th of Shawwal in the year 411 in Cairo.

After him came Ali al-Zahir li-I'zaz Din Allah, who was born on the 6th of Ramadan in the year 420 AH in Cairo and died on the 15th of Sha'ban in the year 427 in Cairo.

After him, his son Ma'add al-Mustansir Billah took over the imamate. He was born on the 6th of Ramadan in the year 420 AH in Cairo and died on the 8th of Dhu al-Hijja in the year 487 AH, also in Cairo.

We do not wish to continue tracing the branches of the tree after the Fatimids here, because we intend to make a detailed and accurate study of that subject in the near future, God willing.

Index of Book Topics

Investigator's Introduction — From page 1 to page 24

The reasons that moved the investigator to publish the book *The Basis of Interpretation* (*Asas al-Ta'wil*); a discussion of the subject of hermeneutics in esoteric philosophical studies; a comparison between *tafsir* (interpretation) and *ta'wil* (esoteric interpretation); the reason for placing this work in this series, who was the first to speak about it, and a glimpse of the life of al-Nu'man ibn Hayyun al-Maghribi al-Tamimi, the author of the book — how he came into contact with the Fatimid Imams in the Maghrib, with a review of the works he wrote both in the Maghrib and in Cairo. A glimpse of the life of the Fatimid Imam al-Mu'izz li-Din Allah and the flourishing of science and literature in his era; his encouragement of scholars and his participation with authors in composition and investigation; and finally a review of the intellectual life that prevailed in Islamic society at that time and the teachings of the Liberated Mind of the Qur'an. The reason for naming the Imams from the descendants of Ismail ibn Ja'far al-Sadiq "Fatimids" rather than "Ismailis"; and finally, how the book was prepared and the number of copies against which the text was collated.

Author's Introduction — From page 25 to page 32

The author introduces his book with an extensive opening in which he contrasts *tafsir* and *tanzil* (revelation), the apparent and the hidden, the body and the soul, and the book *The Pillars of Islam* (*Da'a'im al-Islam*), which represents the apparent, with *The Basis of Interpretation* (*Asas al-Ta'wil*), which represents the hidden. He supports his statements with Quranic verses and practical proofs to confirm interpretation, and finally moves on to clarifying the meaning of *iman* (faith) and *islam* in their outward and inward aspects as set forth in *The Pillars of Islam*. He explains the testimony "there is no god but Allah" and confirms it with the clear verses, before moving on to the interpretation of the functions of the ranks (*hudud*) of the world of religion, grounded in the Holy Qur'an.

369   24

<!-- page 370 -->

Chapter One — From page 33 to page 75

The number of Speakers (*nutaqa'*); the meaning of the word "Speaker"; the beginning of the universe, or what is called the religious cosmos; the doctrine of the descent of Adam; the cause of the descent; Satan's stand; the sin that took place in it; Adam and Eve and their return after repentance; the reason for Adam's creation from clay; his will to his son Abel; Cain's envy; Seth's assumption of the central position after Abel's death; the meaning of the major and minor cycle; the meaning of the *Resident* (*Muqim*), the *Completer* (*Mutimm*), the *Foundation* (*Asas*), and the *Deposit* (*Mustawda'*) and the *Stable* (*Mustaqarr*). The Quranic verses cited in this regard, explained in the margin. The number of Imams who passed through, hidden, from Adam until the appearance of the second Speaker, Noah, along with the names of their callers (*du'at*), investigated against the heavenly books and written sources.

Chapter Two — From page 76 to page 106

Statement of the appearance of the second Speaker, Noah, in the second cycle, with mention of his callers Hud and Salih; the reason for the building of the ship in the esoteric sense; the story of his son's holding back and his refuge on the mountain, and Noah's disowning him; an explanation of the ship and those who rode it; Hud taking up the call, and then Salih after him. A statement of the Quranic verses received in this regard, and finally, in the margin of the first chapter, an explanation of the number of Imams of the second cycle who were hidden through the office of the second Speaker, Noah, until the appearance of the third Speaker, Abraham.

370.

<!-- page 371 -->

Chapter Three — Page 107

The appearance of the third Speaker, Abraham, in the third cycle, and his taking charge of the affairs of the mission; the meaning of the covenant he took from his son Ishmael; the meaning of the sacrifice from the interpretive (*ta'wil*) point of view; the story of Lot and the meaning of the sodomy of his people; the story of Jacob and his sons; Joseph and his going down to Egypt and the wife of al-Aziz; then Job and Shu'ayb, with mention of the Quranic verses cited in this regard. In this cycle, a statement of the division of the Imams after Abraham into *Deposited* (*mustawda'*) and *Settled* (*mustaqarr*) — God decreed that Isaac ibn Ibrahim hold the *Deposited* imamate and that two Speakers, Moses and Jesus, come from his descendants, while Ishmael held the authentic *Settled* imamate, with Muhammad and the Qa'im among his descendants. In the margin, a statement about the *Settled* and *Deposited* Imams from the office of the Speaker Abraham until the fourth Speaker on the fourth cycle, with an explanation of the meaning of *Deposit* and *Settled* in Ismaili belief.

Chapter Four — From page 179 to page 298

The story of the appearance of the fourth Speaker, Moses, on the fourth cycle, and his carrying out the affairs of the message; his going to Midian to meet with Joshua; then the story of his struggle with Pharaoh, which is the struggle of falsehood with truth; a statement about the supporters of his covenant, namely Talut, and how Goliath claimed the imamate after him; and the story of David, Solomon, Jonah and the Whale, Imran, and Zechariah and his son [John], with mention of the Quranic verses revealed in this regard. In the margin, a statement about the number of Deposited and Settled Imams from the offices of Isaac and Ishmael and the son of the Speaker Abraham until the start of the fifth cycle, which begins with Isa ibn Maryam, with mention of the Quranic verses revealed on this subject.

371

<!-- page 372 -->

Chapter Five — From page 299 to page 314

The story of the appearance of the Speaker Isa ibn Maryam and his rising to the message without progressing through the ranks — that is, without a spiritual father to give him the pledge and teach him; this is what is known as spiritual fatherhood and birth without a father. Then the story of Mary — who they were, and whether the birth was physical or spiritual, and what is meant by being born without a father; and what was the position of Joseph the carpenter relative to Mary; then the baptism of John for Jesus, and the baptism of Jesus for John, with mention of the Quranic verses cited on this topic, alongside some of what is mentioned in the Bible. In the margin, a statement about the number of Deposited and Settled Imams who passed, hidden, during the period of the first cycle.

Chapter Six — From page 315 to page 368

The story of the appearance of the last Speaker and the seal of the messengers, Muhammad. The author mentions his migration, his story with the monk Bahira, Abu Talib's protection and sponsorship and pledge to him, his marriage to Khadija and his reliance on her and taking her as a base for the call, the revelation of the Qur'an to him, the details of his life and his death, al-Saqifa, the inauguration of the first caliph, the will of Ghadir Khumm, the inauguration of the second caliph, the death of the third caliph, the war of the Camel, and so on — at which point the author stops following the incidents. In the margin he mentions the lineage that occupied the cycles of the imamate after Muhammad according to the Ismaili imamate tree, until the last Fatimid Caliph in Egypt, namely al-Mustansir Billah. And here the book ends — its subject and its margins.

372.

<!-- page 409 -->

**APOLOGY AND CORRECTION**

We offer our strongest apologies for several typographical errors that occurred inadvertently in the book *Asas al-Ta'wil* (The Foundations of Ta'wil), particularly in the diacritical markings of the Quranic verses. The reason was a difficulty that prevented us from examining the final edition. In any case, these are minor errors in themselves; they do not affect the substance, and they are not hidden from the honorable reader.

Aref Tamer

<!-- page 411 -->

…controversy. By this means, Islam awakened reason — engaging it in its mission and strengthening the intellectual faculties so that the individual could rely on himself and freely express his own opinion.

What follows is therefore a brief summary of the theory of *Ta'wil* set out by Nu'man ibn Hayyun al-Tamimi in his work *Asas al-Ta'wil* — a theory we have examined in every detail, drawing on our Ismaili conceptions for the necessary themes, and inspired exclusively by the Ismaili creed, which we regard as the sole possible means by which seekers may come to know the mysterious theories of the *batin*.

We hope that the task we have undertaken will be of some service to scholarship; we have thus fulfilled a duty toward our history, our religion, and our Arab philosophy.

Aref Tamer
Beirut — Lebanon
1960

<!-- page 412 -->

…itself, and which represents the highest faculty of the human being. One may also affirm that Islam was in reality nothing other than a moral rule that forbids the doing of evil and enjoins the doing of good — a gnosis reinforced by an all-powerful faith; it is likewise the conscience that governs every person of integrity, together with the practice of exemplary and virtuous works.

In any case, the sacred Quran is there to demonstrate that the conception Islam brings is in no way contrary to reason; it is, moreover, inadmissible that it should be opposed to it. If this conception were not coherent, it would not keep pace with reason — all the more so since the Muslim religion, from its inception, is a religion capable of evolution.

If we read the verses of the Quran attentively, and if we analyze its precepts in the light of reason and reality, we conclude that the human being must reason and act, observe and meditate, consider and remain vigilant. Islam is a universal and general conception that guides the human being in his life and helps him to acquire, for himself and for humankind, a state of high spiritual, moral, and material perfection.

Thus, "knowledge," in the religion of Islam, conditions faith. Whoever believes blindly does not believe freely; true belief is that which is grounded in arguments, in understanding, and in freely chosen consent. This allows us to affirm the following:

Islam is a revolution directed against static reason; it is a combat against backward theories, fanaticism, and traditionalism. It broke the bonds that restrained liberty, allowing thought to take flight and to spread. Liberty thus acquired a particular value. Muslim principles were established on the basis of reasoning and testimony, not by violence and traditionalism, and these principles, illuminated by reason, remain the object of vigilant attention.

It is therefore no longer possible for the human being to be an inert thing, accepting everything without discernment. Islam thus liberated human intelligence from the grip of traditions; it gave its impulse to sound reason; in this it was radically distinguished from the religions that preceded it, principally in matters of inquiry and…

<!-- page 413 -->

2° Recourse to the divine writings and the sacred books, by the method of gnostic *ta'wil* — "free will, promises, fulfillments."

It can therefore be said that the intellectual method had as its foundation a profound knowledge of philosophy. It implies a system of beliefs supple in essence, thirsty for additional knowledge. It refuses to grant the slightest credit to the concepts of foreign traditions, however intelligible they may be.

Religion was, and has not ceased to be, enclosed within a powerful fortress whose access is rendered possible only by the practice of a system founded on rational certainty, and which forms, by its very conception, a coherent whole: it is obviously not a question of relying on glittering appearances or on superficial knowledge — even if time has later transformed them into tradition. Every concept that does not emanate from reason and does not belong to its domain is naturally destined to disappear in short order.

The verses of the Quran were revealed in an immediately accessible form; they are not, however, devoid of gnostic significance, just as every existing thing has such significance. Let us note that the text of the Quran and its interpretation give rise to many controversies. By contrast, *ta'wil* — the discovery of the gnostic signification — constitutes a coherent method, not subject to variations, which leads to rational truth and which adapts itself to every milieu.

We have said that *ta'wil* is "knowledge," and that it lay within the competence of the imam and his entourage. It is for this reason that we see the Prophet Muhammad recommending to his Companions the attentive pursuit of this "knowledge." This proves that the literal "knowledge" is easy to acquire, whereas *ta'wil* is acquired only after arduous research, after passing through a series of stages, and after attaining an intellectual discipline called "Testament, Covenant, and Promises."

In a general way, one may affirm that God has revealed his religion to humanity, leaving it free to choose the surest path. He manifested his justice by granting the human being this faculty of using the lights of the perfect intelligence which he himself…

<!-- page 414 -->

…that they were masters in the interpretation of the precepts of Islam. They spoke of the *batin* and of its necessity, just as they also spoke of the *zahir* (the evident). In other words, the *zahir* is inconceivable without the *batin*, just as the *batin* is useless without the *zahir*, because the *zahir* and the *batin* are like body and soul.

For this reason we hold that the two books *Asas al-Ta'wil* and *Da'a'im al-Islam*, edited by Nu'man ibn Hayyun, present two ideas and two directions intimately linked — namely, the *batin* and the *zahir*. The first is considered the foundation of *batini* philosophy. The second is considered the basis of *fiqh* and of the *shari'a*.

This is why we are entitled to conclude that the Ismailis do not employ only realistic interpretation; they interpret the *shari'a* and the Quran allegorically and gnostically, drawing on sources worthy of trust. This manner of interpreting represents, in their eyes, the primordial reason — the *nous*. In this case we can say of the Ismailis that they are rationalists, since they ground their religion on this basis alone. The Ismaili movement is a movement of worldwide scope, or to speak more learnedly, it is an intellectual discipline destined to overturn the political order that reigned in the Muslim world; and its principal aim was to revolutionize thought and religious conceptions.

Assuredly, this intellectual discipline imposes precisely upon the adept the recognition of the principles of the *zahir* and of the *batin*. These two principles, closely linked, constitute the very spirit of religion, and are obligatory for every adept and every believer. The *zahir* is a general concept that encompasses the directives concerning religious life. And the *batin* is the very spirit of religion; it is hidden from view; it belongs to the domain of the elite. This is why the Ismaili apostles propagated their theories in two manners and preached their intellectual discipline under two aspects:

1° That which concerned the prophets and the utility of drawing from them examples, edicts, and precepts, by the literal method, calling the world to rally by means of "force and tradition."

<!-- page 415 -->

…the prophets, as one finds them in the three inspired books: Bible, Gospel, and Quran. All of this constituted an absolutely secret theme, in that it surpassed the limits of the general comprehension of the popular classes, who, it was thought, had only a superficial idea of culture, and only an appearance of knowledge.

It is clear that *Ta'wil*, in the sense the Ismailis effectively attribute to the word, differs from *Tafsir* in the true acceptance of that term, as the other Islamic sects have conceived it. *Tafsir* signifies clarifying any obscure term whose sense escapes the reader. If, for example, to the question "What is the *Tafsir* of the word 'tree'?", we respond, "It is a transplanted seedling that develops and ramifies into branches and twigs, which clothe themselves in leaves; in spring, they bear flowers that soon fructify into delicious fruits, etc.", that is *Tafsir*. But to the question "What is the *Ta'wil* of the word 'tree'?", we respond, "Interpretation is the prerogative of the one directly responsible for *Ta'wil*."

He may say that it is a stone, or an ox, or a rock, or anything that may correspond to truth, to reality, and to reason. And this interpretation will not seem implausible or unreasonable. *Ta'wil* is the profound, symbolic sense, which expresses the essence of the object; it is a truth hidden by definition behind an expression that does not unveil it. It is for this reason that the ideological precepts of the Ismailis assigned the power of *tafsir* to the Prophet — the *Natiq* — but the power of *ta'wil* to the imam. The first was regarded as representing the *shari'a* and the concrete law; the second represents the truth, the *ta'wil*, the philosophy, and the hidden law.

And this brings us to the city of Alexandria and its philosophical atmosphere — to the accounts of Philo and his disciples, who attempted the *ta'wil* of the Bible, though their gnostic *ta'wil* was not crowned with success; just as St. Augustine, his disciples, and his school attempted the gnostic *ta'wil* of the Gospel, yet did not succeed in realizing their design, for several motives on which one cannot elaborate here. Then came the Ismailis, who spread their dogmas, and the precepts of *ta'wil* were the first precepts they put into practice and proclaimed. It is therefore clear that they fertilized the doctrine with their ideas, and that they introduced into it the rational *ta'wil* which forbids the passive acceptance of the narrative. Of course, they proved to the Muslim world…

<!-- page 416 -->

**INTRODUCTION**

I hesitated long before sending this book to press; for in truth I wished to leave it in the shadows of *Taqiyya* — in the secret of Ismaili traditions, sheltered from profane curiosity, among the other Ismaili manuscripts whose hour of publication has not yet come. Furthermore, the information that it is indispensable to obtain from this projected book is not yet sufficient; in addition, there exist other manuscripts whose disclosure is more urgent. But although the value of this information is of lesser importance, it nevertheless constitutes an introduction to our work.

And now, when I reflect on *Ta'wil* (secret and mystical interpretation), of which we are speaking, I understand it through *Asas al-Ta'wil* (The Foundations of Ta'wil), for this is the only book in the collection of Ismaili manuscripts that treats exclusively of *Ta'wil*. The fundamental idea of this science is to obtain a logical and rational representation; to expose in a meticulous and detailed manner each phrase, and to project light upon it so as to render it accessible to the mind.

*Ta'wil*, at the time of the appearance of the Ismaili doctrine, was the foundational project of every *batini* (gnostic) philosophical idea; it was the tree that grew to give birth to different branches; more precisely, it was the base upon which the foundations of this doctrine were raised; it was the nourishment that sustained *batini* philosophy, giving it wisdom, logic, and eloquence. For all these reasons, this book has been classed by the Ismailis among the books beyond price — the precious relics whose doctrinal explanations demand mystery and non-disclosure to anyone who does not belong to the Ismaili community. This book is regarded as the secret and the key of the doctrine, all the more so since it furnishes the mysterious interpretation of the history of…
